# Changelog

Pre-release. Work is tracked by milestone (Mn) following the roadmap in `DESIGN.md` §4.10.
Versioning and the stability tiers are defined in `STABILITY.md`; `g2g-core` is the
semver-covered surface, the plugin/binding crates are provisional or experimental.

## Unreleased

- M664: `AudioMixer` PTS-based alignment. The summing fan-in no longer aligns by arrival (which drifts when inputs arrive out of step and ignored buffer PTS entirely); it places each input buffer on a shared output sample-frame timeline at the position its PTS maps to (`pts_ns -> sample_rate`). Overlapping ranges sum, a PTS gap within an input mixes as silence, and a buffer whose PTS is at or behind the input's own coverage is treated as continuous and appended (covers zero / duplicate PTS). A span emits once every open input has covered it; an input at EOS stops driving the timeline while the others continue, its place mixed as silence. Sample-rate / channel-layout reconciliation stays upstream (`audioresample` / `audioconvert`), matching gst `audiomixer`, so the mixer keeps no resampler. The i16-summing core (`accumulate` / `clamp_to_bytes`) is now shared between the timeline path and the unit tests. `m664_audiomixer_pts_align` drives the element through `process` for the overlap-sum, gap-silence, early-EOS, and continuous-append cases.
- M663: `H265Parse` framerate from the VUI `timing_info`, validated on a real libx265 stream. The SPS walk continues past the conformance window through the whole tail (bit depths, sub-layer ordering, block sizes, an optional scaling list via a new `skip_scaling_list_data`, PCM, the short-term RPS list, SPS long-term refs, TMVP/smoothing flags) into `vui_parameters()` down to `vui_timing_info`, yielding Q16 fps as `vui_time_scale / vui_num_units_in_tick` (per-picture ticks, so no H.264-style field factor). Best-effort by construction: any tail the walk cannot cross leaves geometry refined and the rate `None`, never a parse failure. The RPS crossing cannot be a lean skip (the predicted-set derivation drops zero-delta entries, so `NumDeltaPocs` needs the real derivation): `H265ShortTermRps` + `parse_h265_short_term_rps` moved from the gated `vulkanvideo` module to `h265parse` (re-exported), so the parser and the Vulkan decoder share the one driver-validated implementation. `m663_h265parse_real_stream` closes the other open `H265Parse` item: ffmpeg/libx265 encodes a B-frame Annex-B stream (real RPS sets in the SPS) and the re-framing parser recovers 320x240 + 25 fps in one `CapsChanged` with one `DataFrame` per access unit.
- M662: FLV codec-config side channel, both directions, ffmpeg-oracle-validated. The pure parser (`flv::FlvDemuxer`) retains the sequence-header tags as the side channel (`video_config` = the `AVCDecoderConfigurationRecord`, `audio_config` = the AAC `AudioSpecificConfig`) and reads the video tag's signed composition-time offset, so units now carry PTS and DTS (`pts = dts + cts`, B-frame-ready). `FlvDemux` uses them the way the MP4 demuxers do: AVCC -> Annex-B re-framing honouring the `avcC` length-prefix width (a new `length_prefixed_nal_units` in `annexb`), SPS/PPS prepended in-band to the first access unit (re-armed on flush so a seek resume is decodable), raw AAC ADTS-framed from the ASC, and the concrete channel layout / sample rate announced via `CapsChanged`, so both extracted elementary streams decode standalone. The single-track `FlvMux` element is now the honest inverse (previously it wrote the input bytes verbatim, an unplayable FLV): like `FlvMuxN` it captures the config in-band from the first access unit (parameter sets from the IDR -> `avcC` sequence header, first ADTS header -> ASC), re-frames video Annex-B -> AVCC with the keyframe flagged from the IDR NAL, and writes audio de-ADTS'd, which is also what `RtmpSink` publishes. Shared helpers moved to ungated homes so the `no_std` FLV elements reuse them instead of duplicating: `parse_avcc` / `starts_with_param_set` / `prepend_param_sets` / `split_annexb` / `nalu_type` / `is_keyframe_nal` / `parameter_sets` / `avcc_sample` / `avcc_record` into `annexb`, `asc_from_adts` / `strip_adts` / `adts_from_asc` into `aacparse` (re-exported from their old modules). Validated against ffmpeg as the reference peer in `m662_flv_config_interop`, now a CI conformance oracle recording `Oracle` evidence for `flvdemux` + `flvmux`: ffmpeg encodes a real H.264+AAC FLV and then decodes both g2g-extracted elementary streams standalone; ffprobe + ffmpeg read back the g2g-muxed FLV.
- M661: heap-free YUYV->I420 video convert + STM32H743 Ethernet/RTP harness (drafted). `g2g-mcu::videoconvert::YuyvToI420` is the MCU twin of the host `VideoConvert` (M23, which is `alloc`-based and so cannot enter the heap-free pipeline): a `no_std` `StaticTransform` that converts one packed YUYV 4:2:2 frame (the order a DCMI/DVP camera like the OV2640 emits) to planar I420 4:2:0 (what `HwH264Enc` wants) in place through a `StaticLendRing` slot, closing the `camera -> H.264 encode` gap. Chroma is vertical 2:1 averaging (YUYV is already 4:2:0's horizontal resolution); geometry is checked (`yuyv_len`, even width), and all access is bounds-guarded so no panic path enters the no-alloc subset. Host tests (`m661_videoconvert`) assert the Y/U/V plane layout on a hand-computed vector, reject a mis-sized frame, and run a `camera (YUYV) -> convert` pipeline over `GrabberSrc`; the output is exactly `i420_len(w, h)`, the size `HwH264Enc::new` accepts. A full-chain integration test (`m661_camera_h264_rtp`) then drives `camera (YUYV) -> YuyvToI420 -> HwH264Enc -> RtpSink` as one static pipeline (fused with `Chain`), tracing a tag byte stamped at the camera all the way to the RTP payload and asserting the RTP header (V2, PT 96, sequential, SSRC), so convert (M661) + encoder seam (M660) + RTP egress (M643) are proven to compose. Also added: `examples/g2g-stm32h743`, the STM32H743 (Cortex-M7) on-device harness that runs the flagship audio graph and egresses its RTP over the H743's on-chip Ethernet via a pure-Rust `embassy-net`/smoltcp stack; the g2g-specific bridge is `EmbassyNetSender: PacketSender`, mapping the RTP egress seam one-to-one onto an embassy-net `UdpSocket`. It **compiles for `thumbv7em`** (verified, `embassy-stm32` 0.2 + `embassy-net` 0.7), kept out of CI only for embassy's build weight; only runtime config (RCC/clock, RMII pins, RTP destination, marked `VERIFY`) needs the board. This is a pure-Rust network path (no C), unlike the P4's C6/esp-idf WiFi.
- M660: hardware H.264 encoder seam + C bridge (ESP32-P4 Tier-2 groundwork). `g2g-mcu::hwh264` adds the `H264Encoder` peripheral contract (feed one raw I420 frame, the silicon emits one Annex-B access unit and reports its byte count + keyframe flag) and `HwH264Enc`, the heap-free `StaticTransform` that owns the logic around it: I420 geometry validation with checked 4:2:0 sizing (`i420_len`, rejecting odd/zero dimensions), output sizing against the reported count, the ring lend, and fault surfacing, the encode twin of M640's `HwJpegDec`. `g2g-mcu::cffi::CH264Encoder` bridges it to a C `EncodeFn` callback, so the ESP-IDF (or i.MX/STM32 VPU) hardware encoder driver *is* the peripheral, alongside the existing `CFrameGrabber`/`CPacketSender`. Host tests (`m660_hwh264`) replay the encoder contract through both a Rust mock and a real `extern "C"` callback (byte-identical output proves the C seam is transparent), reject a mis-sized capture before any peripheral traffic, check the keyframe cadence, and run a `camera -> HW-H.264 encode` pipeline end to end over `GrabberSrc`. On-device validation on real ESP32-P4 silicon (plus the MIPI-CSI camera + C6 WiFi C drivers) stays the silicon-gated remainder.
- M659: banded display streaming for large panels (ESP32-P4 Tier-1.5). `SpiDisplaySink::with_stripe(rows)` switches the sink from one whole-frame blit to horizontal-band streaming: each frame is one `width x rows` band written to the next vertical sub-window, the cursor wrapping at `height`, so the pipeline ring holds a single band (a 240x16 band is 15 KB) instead of a full framebuffer (240x240 RGBA = 230 KB, impossible on an MCU). The window addressing is generalized (`set_window(row0, rows)`) with the same checked/saturating geometry; whole-frame mode (`stripe = 0`) is byte-identical to before, so every existing proof is unchanged. `noalloc_pipeline::run_display_banded_with` is the board-agnostic full-panel runner (240x240 in 16-row bands, generic over the embedded-hal seams), and `examples/g2g-esp32p4` now drives it. Tests: `m629_spi_display` gains banded cases (successive-window addressing + wrap, a full 240x240 refresh tiled from a tiny ring with exactly one write per pixel, mistiled-stripe / wrong-size rejection); a host test drives the runner end to end. Footprint after the added branch stays within budget (video 4180 B ROM / 1404 B stack ARM, 3848 / 1360 RISC-V).
- M658: ESP32-P4 (RISC-V) Tier-1 board harness, drafted, plus a board-agnostic display runner. The heap-free display pipeline (`camera -> transform -> SpiDisplaySink`) is now driven through `noalloc_pipeline::run_display_with`, generic over the `embedded-hal` 1.0 `SpiDevice` / `OutputPin` / `DelayNs` seams, so a real HAL's peripherals slot in exactly where the proof stub bus did; `run_async` (every no-alloc / panic-free / footprint / QEMU proof) now delegates to it, and a new host test drives the generic entry and asserts the wire is bit-identical to the pinned display protocol (also the first Rust host check of the video checksum, previously only verified by the C harness + QEMU). `examples/g2g-esp32p4` is the drafted on-device harness: esp-hal `#[main]` init + SPI2/GPIO ST7789 wiring on the ESP32-P4-EYE + a call into `run_display_with`. It is excluded from the workspace and not built in CI because esp-hal's `esp32p4` support is on the esp-hal git `main` branch only (no published crate exposes an `esp32p4` feature as of esp-hal 1.1.1, and cargo validates dep features eagerly), so it is a faithful draft against esp-hal 1.x with the GPIO map / driver calls marked to verify on the board; when esp-hal ships a released esp32p4, switching the git dependency to that version makes it a normal buildable example. On-device execution stays the silicon-gated remainder.
- M657: RISC-V footprint model completed for the flagship audio graph. On RISC-V, rustc encodes that pipeline's stack frame as a constant too large for `addi`'s 12-bit immediate, so it materializes the size into a register (`lui`+`addi`) and does `sub sp, sp, <reg>`, which the M656 stack model refused rather than under-report. `tools/footprint.py` now tracks per-function compile-time constants in GPRs (the `lui` / `li` / `addi` / `slli` / `add` / `mv` materialization chain) and resolves `sub sp, sp, <reg>` to its exact constant, still failing hard if the register is ever not a statically known constant (the register-materialized frame release, `add sp, sp, <reg>`, is recognized as an epilogue). So the RISC-V audio graph is budgeted exactly like the others (measured 10852 B ROM / 0 B static RAM / 6432 B worst-case stack, within the ARM audio budgets), added as a fourth `footprint-report.sh` row. Closes the one modeling follow-up left from M656; both proof pipelines are now footprint-budgeted on both ISAs.
- M656: RISC-V, a second ISA for the heap-free guarantees (Tier 0 of ESP32-P4-class support). The `g2g-core` no-alloc subset and `g2g-mcu` build unchanged for `riscv32imafc-unknown-none-elf` (the ESP32-P4 class), because the static element model is ISA-agnostic pure Rust (only the QEMU harness bins carry ARM startup / `wfi`). The machine-checked guarantees now cover both ISAs: `tools/noalloc-check.sh` builds the `g2g-noalloc` pipeline archive for **both** `thumbv7em-none-eabihf` and `riscv32imafc-unknown-none-elf` and asserts zero allocator symbols and zero panic symbols on each, so the heap-free + panic-free claim is proven cross-ISA, not an ARM accident. `tools/footprint.py` gained a RISC-V stack-frame + call model (`--isa riscv`: the frame is a single `addi sp, sp, -N`, calls are `auipc`+`jalr` with the target symbol annotated on the `jalr`, indirect calls are register `jalr`/`jr`), keeping the same never-under-report discipline (any unmodeled `sp` write is a hard failure), and `tools/footprint-report.sh` reports the RISC-V video-pipeline footprint (measured 3718 B ROM / 0 B static RAM / 1328 B worst-case stack, within the same budgets as the ARM build). Both scripts add the RISC-V target themselves, so CI proves it with no workflow change. Not yet done: on-device execution (needs real ESP32-P4 silicon + an esp-hal harness) and the esp-hal peripheral adapters. (The flagship audio graph's RISC-V stack, deferred here, is budgeted in M657.) This is the portability thesis, pure-Rust media core across ARM and RISC-V, made machine-checkable.
- M655: certification artifacts, a structured, evidence-backed safety case for the MCU path (the down-payment MISRA / functional-safety adoption needs on top of the heap-free + panic-free guarantees). The centerpiece is a **machine-checkable requirements traceability matrix** (`docs/safety/REQUIREMENTS.md`): 15 safety requirements across memory, timing, faults, concurrency, input validation, and data integrity, each stating a property, its verification method, and the evidence that verifies it, a proof script, a named test, or a CI job. `tools/traceability-check.sh` (a stdlib-only Python checker, `traceability-check.py`) parses the matrix and fails if any cited evidence does not exist (a renamed test, a deleted proof script, a removed CI job) or if any cited proof script is not actually wired into a CI workflow, so the matrix is a *checked* claim that cannot drift from the code that satisfies it (the validation-first posture applied to the safety case), and it runs in CI like every other proof. `docs/safety/SAFETY_MANUAL.md` is the companion conditions-of-use document: scope (the no-`alloc` static configuration only), the safety-relevant properties and the assumptions each rests on, the `unsafe` inventory (application code needs none; the framework's is localized to the lending primitives with documented contracts), a summary of integrator responsibilities (build no-`alloc`, wire a hardware watchdog to the `Watchdog` seam, honour the SPSC contract, keep HAL adapters panic-free and fault-reporting), and an honest limitations section (emulated not silicon, pre-1.0, not certified, a safety-case input rather than a certificate). `tools/qualification-kit.sh` runs the full proof set (no-heap/panic-free, footprint, timing, on-target execution across executors, the codec/sensor oracles, and the traceability check) and prints a consolidated requirement-to-evidence-to-result report, gracefully reporting SKIP for on-target proofs when their toolchain is absent so it runs anywhere. Closes the certification-artifacts wedge item; the remaining wedge work is the silicon-gated on-device `Hardware` rows.
- M654: peripheral-catalog breadth, widening the MCU element set from capture / display / audio / RTP into the I2C sensor and UART transport a real product also needs (with real, datasheet-anchored driver logic, not stubs). `g2g-mcu::sht3x` is a driver for the Sensirion SHT3x temperature + humidity sensor over the portable `embedded-hal` 1.0 `I2c` seam: `Sht3xSrc` is the heap-free `StaticSource` that issues the datasheet single-shot measurement command (`0x2C06`, clock-stretching high-repeatability), reads the 6-byte result, validates both CRC-8 check bytes (`crc8`, polynomial `0x31` / init `0xFF`, the datasheet's `0xBEEF -> 0x92` worked example is a test vector) and rejects a mismatch as a bus-integrity fault, converts to milli-units per the datasheet transfer functions (`raw_to_millicelsius` / `raw_to_milli_rh`, the `-45 + 175*S/2^16` and `100*S/2^16` maps, widened to `i64` so the `175000*65535` product does not overflow), and lends an 8-byte reading downstream. `g2g-mcu::uart` adds the UART transport: local `SerialTx` / `SerialRx` seams (embedded-hal 1.0 keeps blocking serial in the separate `embedded-io` crate, so these follow the `PacketSender` / `PacketReceiver` local-seam pattern), `UartSink` (a `StaticSink` writing each frame's payload as a byte-stream egress, telemetry / console), and `UartSrc` (a `StaticSource` reading fixed-size frames, short reads retried until a whole frame assembles, a drained link a clean EOS only at a frame boundary), the two round-tripping over a link. Host-tested (`g2g-mcu/tests/m654_peripherals.rs`): the datasheet CRC vector, the transfer-function endpoints and a hand-checked midpoint, the sensor source reading + converting + rejecting a corrupt CRC, the UART sink/source round-trip, and an I2C-sensor-to-UART telemetry pipeline. On-target proof (`examples/g2g-qemu`'s new `sensor` bin, run by `tools/qemu-check.sh` in CI): a mock SHT3x returns a datasheet response and the `Sht3xSrc -> UartSink` pipeline streams each converted reading out a mock UART, the emitted bytes asserted equal to the datasheet conversion, so I2C read + CRC + conversion + UART egress all run on the Cortex-M ISA (`g2g-sensor: uart-bytes=32 OK`). Both elements are `Recover`-capable for the M652 supervisor. Narrows the remaining wedge gap to certification artifacts (and the silicon-gated on-device rows).
- M653: the receive direction on-MCU, the inverse of the capture-to-egress flagship (the TX chain shipped; the RX path, ingress + jitter buffer + decode, was the gap). The load-bearing new element is a heap-free RTP jitter buffer. `g2g_core::rtp::RtpHeader::parse` is the wire-tolerant inverse of `to_bytes` (handles a CSRC list, a profile extension header, and payload padding a real sender may set; every offset folded with checked arithmetic and bounds-checked, so a malformed or truncated datagram returns `None` rather than panicking, the demuxer discipline), in the no-alloc subset; the std H.264 depayloader (`g2g-plugins::rtpdepay`) now shares it instead of its own hand-rolled offset math. `g2g-mcu::rtprecv` adds the `PacketReceiver` ingress seam (one datagram in per `recv`, the lwIP `recv` / Zephyr `recvfrom` shape, plus a `reset` for supervised recovery) and `RtpSrc`, the heap-free `StaticSource` that receives a datagram, parses it, and lends the payload downstream zero-copy as a `Frame` whose `sequence` is the RTP sequence number (so the jitter buffer can reorder it) and whose PTS is the RTP timestamp mapped through the payload `MediaClock`; a stray non-RTP or filtered-payload-type datagram is skipped and counted, a payload larger than the ring is a sizing `CapsMismatch`. `g2g-mcu::jitter::JitterBuffer<N, BYTES>` is the reorder element (a `StaticTransform`): a fixed `N`-slot reorder window absorbs arrival jitter and reordering, emitting the next-in-sequence packet once a prime depth is buffered, and handles every reception hazard explicitly and countably, reorder (buffered and played in order), duplicate (dropped), late (below the play cursor or out of window, dropped), and loss (when a packet more than `depth` sequences ahead has arrived the missing head is declared lost and the cursor advances, so one loss never stalls the stream; packet-loss concealment is a documented future refinement). The output frame borrows the buffer's own slot zero-copy, sound under the single-frame-in-flight discipline (the same argument as `SpscFrameRing::borrow`). These compose into the RX flagship, `RtpSrc -> JitterBuffer -> G.711 decode`, validated on mock peripherals (`g2g-mcu/tests/m653_rx.rs`): fed a reordered, duplicated, or lossy RTP wire (built from `RtpHeader::to_bytes`, whose layout is separately ffmpeg-validated in M643), the chain reconstructs the ordered decoded PCM byte-for-byte, drops duplicates, and leaves a clean gap on loss, with the jitter counters asserted. On-target proof (`examples/g2g-qemu`'s new `rx` bin, run by `tools/qemu-check.sh` in CI): the RX chain reconstructs an ordered PCM stream from a reordered wire on the Cortex-M4, proved by an order-sensitive rolling hash equal to an independent in-order decode (a plain checksum sum is order-insensitive and would not catch a reorder bug), `played=14 reordered=3 lost=0 OK`. `RtpSrc` and `JitterBuffer` are `Recover`-capable for the M652 supervisor (the source re-opens its socket, the buffer flushes and re-syncs). Closes wedge track item #2 (the receive direction half).
- M652: runtime fault recovery, the supervisor the safety / cert MCU market needs on top of the static heap-free path. Until now the static runners propagated a returned fault (`PoolExhausted`, `Hardware(Peripheral)`, an overrun) straight out: the first glitch ended the pipeline. `g2g_core::supervise` adds the opposite default, a bounded, deterministic recovery layer, in the no-alloc subset (it links with no allocator). A `FaultPolicy` classifies each fault into a `Recovery` action, `Retry` (re-drive a transient fault), `Skip` (drop the frame and keep cadence, degraded mode), `Reset` (re-initialize the stages), or `Escalate` (give up); the supplied `RetryThenReset` (retry, then reset, then escalate) and `SkipBounded` (degrade a bounded number of frames, then escalate) cover the two canonical patterns and both escalate in finite steps for a persistent fault. `Recover` is the per-stage re-initialization seam (default no-op, so a stateless stage opts in with `impl Recover for Foo {}`, and a stage with peripheral state, `GrabberSrc` via a new `FrameGrabber::reset`, `RtpSink` via a new `PacketSender::reset`, `SpscCaptureSrc` which flushes stale buffered frames so real-time capture resumes from live data, overrides it), so a supervised pipeline declares each stage's recovery behavior. `Watchdog` is petted only on real forward progress (a delivered frame); a wedged or escalated pipeline stops petting, so a hardware watchdog fires and resets the chip, and `g2g-mcu::watchdog` supplies the `WatchdogTimer` HAL seam (embedded-hal 1.0 dropped its watchdog trait) plus the `SupervisorWatchdog` adapter. `SupervisorReport` is the fault accounting (frames / faults / retries / resets / skips / escalation) the safety case wants for traceability. `step_supervised` (a C superloop / RTOS task owns the loop) and `run_supervised` (run to completion) drive it, and `step_supervised` is bounded by a hard `MAX_ATTEMPTS` cap so even a buggy never-escalating policy cannot hang the supervisor. On-target proof (`examples/g2g-qemu`'s new `supervised` bin, run by `tools/qemu-check.sh` in CI): a `capture -> G.711 -> checksum` pipeline recovers a mid-stream latched capture fault (retry, then reset via the `FrameGrabber::reset` seam, then continue: all 64 frames delivered, wire checksum equal to a clean reference run, the watchdog fed once per frame) and then escalates a dead peripheral within its bounded retry/reset ladder without hanging, the watchdog never fed (`delivered=64 resets=1 wd=64 escalated=4 OK`). Host tests (`g2g-mcu/tests/m652_supervised.rs`, `g2g-core/src/supervise.rs`) cover transient recovery, the reset ladder, degraded-skip, immediate escalation on a structural fault, the watchdog-pet accounting, and the hard-cap backstop. Closes wedge track item #2. Also made `GrabberSrc`'s frame limit count delivered frames, not attempts, so a supervised retry does not consume the budget.
- M651: the interrupt/DMA-driven capture concurrency model, the piece a real MCU media pipeline needs that the synchronous single-context model did not cover. Real capture runs in interrupt context (a DMA-completion ISR marks a buffer ready) while the pipeline runs in the main/task context; the two must hand frames across that boundary lock-free, heap-free, with bounded back-pressure. `g2g_core::SpscFrameRing<N, BYTES>` is that hand-off: a fixed-capacity single-producer / single-consumer FIFO of frames. The producer (`produce`, called from the ISR) fills the next free slot and publishes it; the consumer (`borrow` / `release`) drains it in capture order, zero-copy (the frame borrows the ring slot). It uses only atomic load/store (no compare-and-swap), so it builds on Cortex-M targets without atomic CAS (e.g. `thumbv6m`), and back-pressure is explicit and non-blocking: a producer in an interrupt cannot wait, so a full ring drops the frame and bumps an overrun counter the consumer reads, rather than stalling the ISR. `g2g_core::SpscCaptureSrc` is the consumer-side `StaticSource` (the concurrent twin of the synchronous `GrabberSrc`): it drains the ring into the pipeline and, while the ring is empty, calls a caller-supplied idle hook (`cortex_m::asm::wfi` on hardware, so the consumer sleeps until the capture interrupt; a yield in a host test) and retries. On-target proof (`examples/g2g-qemu`'s new `isr_capture` bin, run by `tools/qemu-check.sh` in CI): a SysTick interrupt handler is the producer, running in genuine interrupt context on the emulated Cortex-M4; the main-context pipeline drains the ring through `SpscCaptureSrc -> G.711 mu-law encode -> checksum`, sleeping on `wfi` between frames. The wire checksum must equal the same pipeline run with synchronous delivery, so every interrupt-produced frame is proven to reach the pipeline in capture order and uncorrupted (`captured=64 overruns=0 OK`). Host tests (`g2g-mcu/tests/m651_isr_capture.rs`) exercise the hand-off under real thread concurrency: a producer thread feeds the pipeline lossless and in order when paced, and a fast producer over a slow consumer drops-and-counts frames without reorder or corruption. Heap-free throughout (the bin links for `thumbv7em` with no allocator).
- M650: C seam ABI, the zero-Rust driver-integration path for the MCU/RTOS wedge. Where `examples/g2g-freertos` links the whole g2g pipeline as a static library the C app calls into, this is the inverse a C shop with a large driver investment actually needs: C code IS the peripheral. `g2g-mcu::cffi` adds `CFrameGrabber` and `CPacketSender`, adapters that implement the `FrameGrabber` capture seam and the `PacketSender` egress seam over C function pointers (`CaptureFn` / `SendFn` + an opaque `ctx`), so a board registers its existing C DMA/capture routine and C network stack and g2g calls them back each frame, no Rust adapter hand-written. `g2g_core::staticelem` gains `step_source_sink` (+ the `Step` enum), a frame-at-a-time runner that runs one frame and returns control to the caller, so a C superloop (or an RTOS task) owns the loop and interleaves the pipeline with other work; compose a processing tail with `SinkChain` and it steps any linear graph. Proof (`examples/g2g-cffi`, run by `tools/cffi-check.sh` in CI): a `no_std` staticlib exposes `g2g_audio_egress_init` / `_step` / `_reset` (a `capture -> G.711 mu-law -> RTP` pipeline driven from C callbacks) plus a C header (`include/g2g_cffi.h`); it links for `thumbv7em` with ZERO allocator symbols and ZERO data-panic symbols (bounds / overflow / unwrap / slice), and a real C caller (`harness.c`) supplying C capture + send callbacks steps the pipeline and reproduces the pipeline's own Rust reference wire byte-for-byte, proving the C seams are byte-transparent. (A `g2g-mcu` integration test proves the same transparency in pure Rust for CI portability.) The one-frame-step future leaves a single benign, runtime-unreachable async re-poll guard the run-to-EOS runners discharge; the check permits only that guard and nothing else, so a real data-panic or heap use still fails.
- M649: brought the public docs current with the heap-free MCU wedge. README.md gained an "Embedded: heap-free pipelines on a bare-metal MCU" section (alloc-optional core, static element model, the machine-checked no-alloc / panic-free / footprint / QEMU / timing proofs, one graph across four executors, `g2g-mcu` peripherals, the flagship deterministic-audio graph, and the general `g2g-mcugen` compiler), an updated portability table (heap-free MCU + four-executor RTOS rows), and the `g2g-mcu` / `g2g-mcugen` crates in the workspace table and layout. docs/index.html (last touched at M585, ~two months and the entire M623+ wedge behind) is caught up: alloc-optional hero + pillar, the dissolved `g2g-enterprise` card removed and `g2g-mcu` / `g2g-mcugen` added (its `TensorBatcher` folded into the `g2g-ml` card), two new embedded feature cards, and the heap-free MCU + four-executor portability cards. Keeping both public surfaces current is now part of every milestone, like CHANGELOG / DESIGN.
- M648: generalized the host graph compiler (`g2g-mcugen`) beyond audio into a general MCU graph compiler with a second (video / display) catalog, proving "one declarative graph compiles to a bounded static build" is not audio-specific. Frame geometry became a sum of audio (rate / width / channels) and raster (pixels / bpp), `grabbersrc` captures either by its props (`sample-rate` vs `width-px`/`height-px`/`format`), and a new `spidisplaysink` element (ST7789 / ILI9341, RGBA-in) joins the catalog with its geometry contract (bpp and panel dimensions must match). Codegen gained a per-sink `SinkPlan`: the entry's seams, setup, and return vary by sink kind, an `RtpSink` takes and returns a `PacketSender`, an `SpiDisplaySink` takes an SPI bus + D/C pin + delay bound on `embedded-hal`, emits the panel `init()` before the run, and returns unit. Proof (`examples/mcugen-graphs`, renamed from `mcugen-audio`, run by `tools/mcugen-check.sh`): the compiler now regenerates and drift-checks *both* flagship graphs, the generated `camera -> SPI display` pipeline (`g2g-mcugen/examples/display.yaml`) is driven with the same stub panel bus as the hand-written display reference and reproduces its panel wire byte-for-byte (`EXPECTED_CHECKSUM`, the reference's byte no-op transform makes camera->display equivalent), alongside the existing audio equivalence, and both build heap-free for `thumbv7em`. The reference's video mock peripherals (`PatternGrabber`, `StubBus` with `spi()`/`dc()`/`checksum()`, `NoDelay`) are exposed from `noalloc-pipeline` so the generated display graph is driven by the exact same peripherals the reference uses, not lookalikes. Mis-wires stay compile errors (a display fed RGB565 or a 4x4 camera into an 8x8 panel are rejected with a diagnostic before any Rust is emitted).
- M647: consumable Zephyr packaging, promoting the M637 hand-linked proof into a reusable Zephyr module (`examples/g2g-zephyr-module`). A Zephyr shop now lists the module in its west manifest (or passes it via `ZEPHYR_EXTRA_MODULES`) and gets the g2g static pipeline library plus its C header wired into the build automatically: the module's `zephyr/module.yml` + `CMakeLists.txt` import the prebuilt archive (`zephyr_link_libraries`) and expose `include/g2g.h` (`zephyr_include_directories`), so the application declares nothing about the library, no staticlib path, no include directory, no `target_link_libraries`, it just `#include <g2g.h>` and calls `g2g_noalloc_run()` / `g2g_audio_run()`. `examples/g2g-zephyr` is converted to consume the module (its CMakeLists drops the old `-DG2G_NOALLOC_LIB` hand-link) and `tools/zephyr-check.sh` points Zephyr at both the module and the prebuilt archive (`G2G_STATICLIB`); the same on-target QEMU Cortex-M3 boot + checksum banner now proves the packaged integration, not just the app-links-a-lib path. The prebuilt-staticlib recipe (build the `no_std` Rust archive for the board's ISA, then hand its path to the module) is documented in the module README.
- M646: host graph compiler (`g2g-mcugen`), the codegen resolution of the "develop-and-test on Linux, ship a bounded static build to the MCU" tension. It reads a declarative audio graph document (YAML/JSON) and emits the monomorphized static MCU pipeline, the same six-element `capture -> convert -> resample -> mix -> encode -> RTP` shape `noalloc-pipeline::audio` wires by hand, but with every ring sized from the graph's frame geometry (rate x period x width x channels) instead of hard-coded, plus a total ring-memory budget report. A small element catalog (`grabbersrc`, `pcmconvert`, `resample`, `mixer`, `g711enc`, `rtpsink`) carries each element's role and geometry rules, so a mis-wired graph (an encoder fed 32-bit slots, a mixer whose two inputs disagree, a rate/period that is not a whole sample count) is rejected with a diagnostic before a line of Rust is emitted. Supported topologies match what the static runners provide: a linear chain or two source branches joined by one fan-in then a linear tail; the emitted entry is generic over the peripheral seams (capture grabbers + RTP sender), so a board supplies HAL impls and a proof harness supplies mocks. The schema is deliberately its own, not the dynamic `GraphSpec`: it adds the frame geometry a static build needs and drops the dynamic-only escape hatches (launch-string, tee/demux, backpressure) that cannot monomorphize. Proof (`examples/mcugen-audio`, run by `tools/mcugen-check.sh` in CI): the compiler regenerates the checked-in flagship graph (drift is a hard failure), the generated crate builds heap-free for `thumbv7em`, and, driven with the reference capture peripherals, its RTP wire output equals the hand-written `AUDIO_EXPECTED_CHECKSUM` byte-for-byte, so the compiler is proven to reproduce the ffmpeg-and-DSP-verified reference graph, not merely to emit Rust that compiles.
- M645: per-frame timing / jitter report for the flagship audio graph, the timing sibling of the footprint report (wedge item: publish worst-case execution and jitter like the memory numbers). `TimedSumSender` in `noalloc-pipeline::audio` stamps every emitted RTP packet with a caller-supplied clock read (fixed array, heap-free); `examples/g2g-qemu/src/bin/timing.rs` provides SysTick (25 MHz emulated system clock) and reports `first` (the one-time negotiation + resampler warm-up frame) and steady-state min/max/jitter over semihosting with a hand-rolled decimal writer (no `core::fmt`). `tools/timing-report.sh` boots it under `-icount shift=0,sleep=off`, where virtual time is a pure function of the instruction stream: two boots must report byte-identical lines (asserted), so the numbers are budget-enforceable in CI (new step next to the QEMU proof). Measured: steady-state worst case 19093 ticks (~764 us of a 10 ms frame, ~7.6% of an emulated 25 MHz core), jitter 9 ticks (~360 ns, the G.711 encoder's amplitude-dependent segment search); budgets 24576/24576/256. The same binary without icount reports ~1400x the jitter (host scheduling noise), which is the point: emulated instruction timing is not silicon timing (the deferred on-device `Hardware` row's job), but it proves the pipeline's execution cost is bounded and data-stable, and CI catches any regression that grows it.
- M644: the flagship composed demo graph: `capture -> convert -> resample -> mix -> encode -> RTP` as ONE static heap-free pipeline, executed and checksum-verified on every proof target. New machinery, all reusable: `SourceChain` / `SinkChain` in `g2g_core::staticelem` (fuse a transform onto a source / sink, the static `bin` analog, so the M642 const-arity fan-in runner drives arbitrary linear branches), and `g2g-mcu::PcmConvert` (the `convert` stage: left-justified 24-in-32 I2S/SAI capture slots -> S16LE, keep-top-16 via the free `s32_slot_to_s16`). The graph itself lives in `noalloc-pipeline::audio`: a DMIC-shaped 8 kHz S16 capture (1 kHz tone) fans in with a SAI-shaped 48 kHz 32-bit-slot capture (2 kHz tone) -> convert -> resample 48 -> 8 kHz -> Q15 mix -> G.711 mu-law -> `RtpSink` (PCMU, one 10 ms packet per frame), generic over the M643 `PacketSender` so hosts inspect the wire and proof targets checksum it; the mix link negotiates `Caps::Audio` (black-boxed intersect), putting the audio caps arm under the symbol proofs alongside M636's tensor arm. Host validation (`noalloc-pipeline/tests/flagship.rs`, run by noalloc-check.sh): RTP structure, DSP semantics against an independent f64 reference (both tones recovered at their mixed amplitudes by least-squares projection, residual SNR > 30 dB), and the pinned wire checksum. Proofs: the archive keeps zero allocator + zero panic symbols (the resampler needed `.max(1)` divisor discharges; the example profiles move `opt-level` z -> s because "z" stopped inlining the grown archive's async state machines, reintroducing panic paths, and "s" is smaller anyway: video 4286 -> 4096 B ROM, 1508 -> 1388 B stack); the audio graph gets its own gc-sectioned ELF + budget row (measured 10572 B ROM / 0 B static RAM / 6504 B worst-case stack, budget 12288/8192/0); and the SAME pinned checksum is re-verified on-target on QEMU Cortex-M4 (bare + Embassy, whose task arena grew to 16 KB for the ~7 KB future) and Cortex-M3 (Zephyr, second ISA flavor), plus FreeRTOS (task stack 4 -> 12 KB) via the C ABI (`g2g_audio_run` / `g2g_audio_expected`), making the fixed-point chain's cross-target bit-exactness machine-checked on all four executors. DESIGN_TODO wedge item 1 (reference audio chain) closes.
- M643: RTP egress seam, completing the reference audio chain's element set (capture -> convert -> resample -> mix -> encode -> RTP). First the de-dup the milestone rode in on: the RFC 3550 fixed header had five hand-rolled writers (`rtppay`, the ST 2110 -20/-30/-40 and JPEG XS cores) plus eight copies of `RTP_HEADER_LEN`; all now come from one place, `g2g_core::rtp::RtpHeader` (`const fn to_bytes`, heap-free subset), behavior-preserving under the existing 559 g2g-plugins unit tests. On the MCU side, `g2g-mcu::rtp` adds the `PacketSender` seam (one datagram as a header + payload scatter-gather pair, so an lwIP pbuf chain / Zephyr `sendmsg` adapter stays zero-copy; blocking is the network back-pressure, like `PcmWriter`) and `RtpSink`, the heap-free `StaticSink`: one frame = one packet (an over-MTU or empty payload is `CapsMismatch`, never silent fragmentation; format-specific fragmentation like FU-A stays with the std packetizers), RTP timestamp = frame PTS through `MediaClock` (the ST 2110 mapping), marker on the first packet only (RFC 3551 talkspurt start), caller-seeded sequence/SSRC (no entropy source on an MCU). Real-peer validated: G.711 encode -> RtpSink over loopback UDP into ffmpeg's RTP demuxer reproduces our payload stream byte-for-byte (PCMU, PT 0, SDP session); wired into the CI conformance job's interop step, persisting peer-tagged Oracle evidence for `rtpsink`.
- M642: static fan-in + the Q15 mixer, the `mix` stage of the deterministic reference audio chain. `g2g_core::staticelem` grows its first const-arity multi-input surface: `StaticFanIn2` (a heap-free 2:(0 or 1) stage, `process2(a, b)`) and the `run_sources_fanin_sink` runner, the fan-in analog of `run_source_transform_sink` (lockstep pull, `a` first, EOS when either source ends, `Ok(None)` drops the pair; fully monomorphized like the linear runners). `g2g-mcu::mixer` implements it: `mix_q15` is a free `const fn` (`sat(a*ga + b*gb)`, gains Q15, round-half-up), with the accumulator widened to i64 because two `i16::MIN` products sum to exactly 2^31, one past `i32::MAX`; `Mixer` wraps it over the ring-lend model (via `lend_slot`, factored beneath the codecs' `lend_converted`), rejects unequal or torn payloads as `CapsMismatch` (a silent shorter-input policy would hide a rate bug), and inherits timing from input `a` (the timing master). Oracle is an independent i64 reference over the full 65536-sample axis plus the distinguishing corners (both saturations, the i32-overflow pair, exact 0.5+0.5 identity, exact equal-and-opposite cancellation).
- M641: fixed-point polyphase resampler (`g2g-mcu::resample`), the first stage of the deterministic reference audio chain (capture -> convert -> resample -> mix -> encode -> RTP; the strategy-review wedge). Mono S16LE over the telephony rate set {8, 16, 48} kHz: Q14 integer MACs over generated Blackman-windowed-sinc tables (`tools/gen-resample-tables.py` -> `resample_tables.rs`, checked in; every phase branch sums to exactly unity, so DC gain is exact at every phase, no periodic ripple), streaming state carried across frames (fixed history window + fractional position: chunked processing is byte-identical to one-shot, no drift on long streams). No bit-exact external reference exists for a resampler, so the oracle is analytic: table invariants, exact DC, in-band tone SNR by least-squares sine fit (measured ~86 dB, asserted > 55), alias rejection when decimating (measured ~120 dB, asserted > 50), chunk-invariance. `Resampler` rides the ring-lend transform model; same-rate is zero-copy pass-through.
- M640: hardware-JPEG codec peripheral seam, `g2g-mcu::hwjpeg`. `JpegDecoder` is the STM32H7-shaped contract (feed one complete JFIF stream, the silicon parses the header and reports width/height/subsampling, then emits MCU-block-ordered YCbCr); `HwJpegDec` owns everything around it: SOI/EOI framing validation before any peripheral traffic, the MCU-tiling output-size cross-check (`decoded_len`, checked math over header-derived dimensions: 8x8/16x8/16x16 tiles for gray/4:4:4/4:2:2/4:2:0), the `StaticLendRing` output lend, fault surfacing (a peripheral whose write count contradicts its own header report is `HardwareError::Peripheral`, not trusted), and `info()` for downstream wiring. Datasheet-tested on a scripted mock (`m640_hwjpeg`); the output stays the silicon's native block order on purpose (raster conversion is a separate stage). What a mock cannot prove, that real silicon matches its datasheet, is the deferred on-device `Hardware` conformance row (STM32H747), which with M638-M640 is now the only open item on the MCU codec track.
- M639: IMA ADPCM fixed-point codec (WAV / DVI4 block layout, mono) in `g2g-mcu::adpcm`, the 4-bits-per-sample sibling of M638. `ImaState` sample arithmetic uses the multiplicative reconstruction ffmpeg uses (`(2d+1)*step >> 3`), not the bit-serial approximation (they differ in truncation); `encode_block` / `decode_block` stream nibbles directly between frame payloads (no block-sized sample buffer on the MCU stack); the encoder carries the step index across blocks and frames like the reference. Validated bit-exact against ffmpeg in all three directions (our encode == ffmpeg's stream byte-for-byte, our decode of its stream == its own decode, and ffmpeg reconstructs *our* stream to exactly our reconstruction), persisted as Oracle evidence in the CI conformance job. `AdpcmEnc` / `AdpcmDec` ride the ring-lend transform model via a shared `lend` helper (factored out of the G.711 elements, one copy). `AudioFormat::ImaAdpcm` added (wire tag 7, `audio/x-adpcm`).
- M638: G.711 (mu-law / A-law) fixed-point codec, the first MCU-fit codec, in `g2g-mcu::g711`. Pure-integer `const fn` sample conversions implemented once for any consumer; encode quantizes to the *nearest* reconstruction level in the 14-bit domain, and the whole codec is validated **bit-exact against ffmpeg over the entire domain** (all 65536 encoder inputs + all 256 decoder codes, both laws), persisted as `Oracle` conformance evidence in the CI conformance job (mu-law's two zero codes collapse on re-encode exactly as the reference peers do). `G711Enc` / `G711Dec` are the first payload-*producing* static transforms: companding changes the byte count, so they lend output from a `StaticLendRing` (the capture source's model; safe `'static`-ring ctor + `unsafe with_ring`, `PoolExhausted` on exhaustion, `CapsMismatch` for torn samples / undersized slots) and inherit the input frame's timing. `AudioFormat::{Mulaw, Alaw}` added (wire tags 5/6, `audio/x-mulaw` / `audio/x-alaw`). No runtime zero-alloc test on purpose: `g2g-mcu` has no `alloc` crate in its build, so a heap-needing path cannot compile.
- M637: Zephyr executor proof, the fourth leg of the executor matrix (bare single-poll M628, Embassy M632, FreeRTOS M633, Zephyr M637; all running the same proven pipeline with the wire checksum verified on-target). `examples/g2g-zephyr` is a normal Zephyr CMake application (`find_package(Zephyr)` + `target_link_libraries(app libg2g_noalloc.a)`, `main()` calls `g2g_noalloc_run()` from the main thread), so beyond the C-call shape M633 already proved, this proves the *build-system* integration a Zephyr shop actually uses. No west workspace: `tools/zephyr-check.sh` clones the pinned Zephyr tree (`v4.2.0`) plus the CMSIS module revisions its own manifest pins into the gitignored target dir and hands them to CMake as `ZEPHYR_MODULES`, builds with the GNU Arm Embedded toolchain, and boots QEMU's lm3s6965evb Cortex-M3 (the `qemu_cortex_m3` board: thumbv7m soft-float, so the staticlib is also proven on a second ISA flavor next to the other proofs' Cortex-M4F). In CI (`features-linux`) after the FreeRTOS step, reusing its qemu + arm-gcc installs.
- M636: fixed-rank `TensorShape`, closing the M623 carve-out: `Caps::Tensor` is now part of the no-alloc MCU subset like every other caps kind. `TensorShape` stores up to `MAX_TENSOR_RANK` (6) dims inline (`Copy`, no heap) instead of a `Vec<u32>`; constructors are the compile-time-rank-checked `TensorShape::new([1, 3, 224, 224])` (a post-monomorphization guard, so no runtime branch and no panic path in the no-heap archive) and the fallible `from_slice` for runtime dims (a model's reported shape, a wire-decoded rank), which rejects rank 0 / > 6 instead of panicking; the wire decoder now bounds the attacker-controlled rank field the same way. The proof pipeline (`noalloc-pipeline`) negotiates `Caps::Tensor` on its transform link (intersect at build, per-frame byte-size validation), so the no-alloc + panic-free symbol proofs, footprint budgets, and QEMU run now cover the caps algebra including the full un-inlined `Caps::intersect` (budgets re-measured: 4286 B ROM / 0 B static RAM / 1508 B stack; the `dims()` accessor clamps rank so the optimizer discharges its bounds check). `m636_fixed_rank_tensor_caps` adds the runtime complement (counting-allocator proof that tensor caps negotiation is heap-free). Dynamic *negotiation* is unchanged (DerivedOutput closures, mid-stream `CapsChanged` re-emission, ONNX dynamic batch dim); only rank is now bounded, matching `TensorView`'s existing `MAX_TENSOR_RANK`. Fixing the call sites surfaced pre-existing bitrot in the never-CI-built `ort` feature (missing `#[non_exhaustive]` wildcard arms in `OrtInference::process` / `DetectionDecode::process`, the M561/M635 pattern), now fixed.
- M635: dissolved the `g2g-enterprise` crate. Its reason to exist was an AGPL/commercial boundary that no longer does (the crate went LGPL like the rest of the workspace), it held a single element, and its other role (the only crate depending on both `g2g-ml` and `g2g-plugins`, hosting the CUDA<->wgpu e2e tests) was stale: `g2g-ml` has had an optional `g2g-plugins` dependency since M220's `cuda-wgpu` feature. `TensorBatcher` moved to `g2g-ml::batcher` (std-gated) with its unit + runner integration tests; the `cuda_wgpu_{scaffold,e2e}.rs` GPU tests moved to `g2g-ml/tests/` behind a new `g2g-ml/cuda-wgpu-e2e` feature (forwarding `g2g-plugins/cuda` + `ffmpeg` exactly as before). The move surfaced pre-existing bitrot in the never-CI-built `cuda-wgpu` path: `CudaToWgpu::process` lacked the M561 `#[non_exhaustive]` wildcard arm for `PipelinePacket` (fixed: forwards unknown control packets, the pass-through-transform convention). Crate tables in README / DESIGN / STABILITY / AGENTS updated; one less crate, no behavior change.
- M634: `forbid(unsafe)` application posture. An application on the g2g MCU surface now needs no `unsafe` at all, proven by `m634_forbid_unsafe`: a test crate under `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]` (a hard error even for `#[allow]`d unsafe) builds and runs a complete camera -> display pipeline. Two enablers: `StaticLendRing::new` is now `const` (associated-const array-repeat, the MSRV-1.75 pattern), so the DMA ring lives in a `static` and `GrabberSrc::new`'s safe `'static`-ring constructor applies; and the single-poll noop-waker executor is promoted to a safe `g2g_core::staticelem::drive_ready` (returns `None` on `Pending`, which a noop waker could never wake again), de-duplicating the five hand-rolled copies (noalloc-pipeline, m624, and the three g2g-mcu test files). Footprint gotcha found by the budget guard: taking the future by value across the crate boundary linked a 1.6 KB `memmove` for the state machine; `#[inline]` on `drive_ready` restores in-place polling. Budgets re-measured: 3067 B ROM / 0 B static RAM / 1468 B worst-case stack (+178 B ROM vs M632, the cost of the const-init ring + safe executor).
- M633: FreeRTOS executor proof, completing the executor matrix (bare single-poll M628, Embassy M632, FreeRTOS M633, all running the same proven pipeline with the checksum verified on-target). `examples/g2g-freertos` is a plain C FreeRTOS application (kernel `V11.2.0`, fetched pinned, not vendored; CM4F port; **static allocation only**, so no FreeRTOS heap is even compiled, keeping the whole image consistent with the g2g no-heap guarantee) that links `libg2g_noalloc.a` and calls `g2g_noalloc_run()` from a task: the C-shop integration path, deliberately thin. `tools/freertos-check.sh` builds the staticlib, cross-compiles with `arm-none-eabi-gcc`, boots QEMU MPS2-AN386, and asserts the banner + semihosting exit code (gotcha: raw semihosting `SYS_WRITE0` lands on qemu's stderr, unlike the Rust examples' `SYS_OPEN(":tt")` path). In CI (`features-linux`) via the distro `gcc-arm-none-eabi` + `qemu-system-arm`.
- M632: Embassy executor proof. The proof pipeline is now exposed as a plain future (`noalloc-pipeline::run_async`; `run` wraps it with the single-poll executor) and a new `examples/g2g-embassy` bare-metal binary awaits it from a real Embassy task (`embassy-executor` 0.7 thread-mode on Cortex-M, `#[embassy_executor::main]` plus one `.await`, no adaptation layer: the static element model is executor-agnostic by design) on QEMU's MPS2-AN386, with the wire checksum verified on-target. `tools/qemu-check.sh` now builds and boots both the bare-executor (M628) and Embassy variants in the same CI step. The symbol proofs survive the extra async layer (still zero allocator and zero panic symbols); footprint budgets re-measured at 2889 B ROM / 0 B static RAM / 1460 B worst-case stack.
- M631: audio render seam, `PcmWriter` + `PcmSink` (`g2g-mcu`). The I2S/SAI-shaped contract: `write(&[i16])` renders one block of interleaved samples (a real adapter feeds the peripheral's DMA ring and awaits space, which is the pipeline's natural audio back-pressure); `PcmSink` decodes a frame's S16LE payload through a fixed 64-sample stack buffer (no second copy of the audio frame) and rejects torn sample-frame payloads (`len % (2 x channels) != 0`) as `CapsMismatch` before anything reaches the peripheral. Panic-free by construction like its siblings (slice patterns, `get`-based slicing, saturating math). `m631_pcm_sink` asserts bit-exact sample reconstruction (negative values, `i16::MIN`/`MAX`), chunk-boundary streaming (64+36 split with order preserved), framing rejection, and failure propagation.
- M630: camera capture seam, `FrameGrabber` + `GrabberSrc` (`g2g-mcu`). The DCMI/CSI-shaped contract: `capture(&mut self, buf) -> bytes-written` fills a lent `StaticLendRing` slot (a real adapter arms the peripheral's DMA at the slot and awaits the completion interrupt); `GrabberSrc` owns the ring/lease/sequence/PTS logic and publishes each capture downstream zero-copy, with an exhausted ring surfaced as `PoolExhausted` (a sizing bug, not silently waited out) and an oversized capture claim rejected as `CapsMismatch`. The safe constructor takes a `'static` ring (the MCU idiom, StaticCell); a borrowed (stack) ring is the `unsafe with_ring` variant inheriting `publish`'s outlives contract. `m630_grabber_src` covers sequence/PTS flow, the zero-copy witness (`ring.contains` on the payload pointer), ring exhaustion, contract violations, failure propagation, and a full camera -> SPI-display pipeline on mock peripherals. The proof pipeline's hand-rolled source is replaced by the real `GrabberSrc` + a stub pattern grabber, so all four proofs (no-alloc, panic-free, footprint: now 2881 B ROM / 0 B static RAM / 1348 B stack, QEMU on-target checksum) cover the real camera element too.
- M629: first MCU peripheral element, `SpiDisplaySink` (ST7789 / ILI9341 SPI TFT), in a new `g2g-mcu` workspace crate (`no_std`, no `alloc`). Elements there are heap-free `staticelem` elements written against `embedded-hal` 1.0 trait seams (`SpiDevice` + D/C `OutputPin` + `DelayNs`) instead of chip registers, so the real driver logic is host-testable: `m629_spi_display` records the wire traffic on mock peripherals and asserts the DCS init sequence (opcodes, parameters, D/C phases, datasheet reset/wake delays), CASET/RASET window addressing with panel offsets, streaming RGBA8888 -> big-endian RGB565 conversion (through a fixed 128-byte stack chunk buffer, so an MCU never holds a second framebuffer), geometry validation (`CapsMismatch` before any bus traffic), and SPI-failure surfacing (new `HardwareError::Peripheral`). The element is panic-free by construction (slice patterns instead of indexing, checked geometry math) and joins the proof pipeline: `noalloc-pipeline`'s sink is now the real `SpiDisplaySink` over a checksumming stub bus, so the no-alloc + panic-free symbol proofs, the footprint budgets (now 2661 B ROM / 0 B static RAM / 1300 B worst-case stack, the ST7789 driver costing 581 B of ROM), and the QEMU Cortex-M run all cover an actual peripheral element end to end, with the wire checksum (init parameters + windows + pixel stream) verified on-target.
- M628: emulated Cortex-M execution proof. The heap-free pipeline had linked for `thumbv7em` but never executed on the ISA; now `examples/g2g-qemu` (a bare-metal `cortex-m-rt` binary) boots it on QEMU's MPS2-AN386 Cortex-M4 and verifies the checksum on-target (64 frames, sum 2016), reporting the verdict as the semihosting exit code plus a static banner (no formatting machinery on top of the pipeline). The pipeline definition moved to a shared `examples/noalloc-pipeline` rlib consumed by both `g2g-noalloc` (the M625/M626 symbol-proof staticlib, which must stay `staticlib`-only: adding `rlib` silently disables fat LTO and un-eliminates core's panic/fmt machinery) and `g2g-qemu`, so both proofs cover one definition. Made `RingSlot` carry its slot/lease references instead of a stored ring index (`g2g-core::staticpool`), so the panic-free property is structural rather than relying on the optimizer rediscovering the `idx < N` invariant across crates (found when the split reintroduced a bounds-check panic path; the symbol check caught it). `tools/qemu-check.sh` (in CI via apt `qemu-system-arm`) runs the proof; `$QEMU_SYSTEM_ARM` overrides the emulator binary for hosts without one.
- M627: build-time worst-case RAM / stack / ROM report for the heap-free pipeline. `tools/footprint-report.sh` links `examples/g2g-noalloc` into a real gc-sectioned ELF (`rust-lld -e g2g_noalloc_run`) and `tools/footprint.py` reports the numbers an MCU integrator budgets against: ROM (`.text` + `.rodata` + `.ARM.exidx` + `.data`), static RAM (`.data` + `.bss`), and the worst-case stack, computed from the disassembly call graph (per-function frames from `push` / `vpush` / `stmdb sp!` / `sub sp`; DFS over `bl` / tail-branch edges with cycle detection; the one indirect call, the noop-waker vtable, bounded by the deepest chain of any non-entry function; any sp-write the parser does not model fails the run rather than under-reporting). Because the no-alloc pipeline keeps all state in locals, the entry frame covers the capture ring + the monomorphized pipeline state machine, so the stack number is the true per-pipeline RAM. Measured: **2080 bytes ROM, 0 bytes static RAM, 1252 bytes worst-case stack** for the whole source -> transform -> sink pipeline. Enforced as regression budgets (4096 / 0 / 2048; static RAM has no headroom on purpose) in CI, with the report published to the job summary like the conformance maturity table.
- M626: link-time panic-free proof for the heap-free pipeline (Phase 4 of the heap-free MCU core begins). `examples/g2g-noalloc` is now also panic-free end to end: every reachable path avoids unwrap / slice-index / overflow panics (payload access via `first()` instead of indexing), and the executor polls the always-ready static chain exactly once (with a noop waker a `Pending` future could never be woken again anyway), which lets the optimizer discharge the compiler's resumed-after-completion guard, the one panic arm source code cannot remove. The optimized `thumbv7em-none-eabihf` archive therefore contains **zero `core::panicking` symbols**, so the mandatory `#[panic_handler]` is provably dead code: on a safety / no-heap part the pipeline cannot halt through the panic machinery. `tools/noalloc-check.sh` asserts this alongside the M625 allocator-symbol check, and now also builds the same crate for the host and runs the pipeline for real through `host-harness.c` (64 frames, checksum asserted), so the symbol proofs are backed by an actual execution. All in the existing CI step.
- M625: link-time no-heap proof for a whole pipeline (Phase 3 of the heap-free MCU core). `examples/g2g-noalloc` is a standalone `no_std` staticlib that depends on `g2g-core` with `default-features = false` (so the `alloc` crate is not even a dependency) and defines **no `#[global_allocator]`**; it builds a real `StaticLendRing` -> source -> transform -> sink pipeline with the M624 static element model and drives it on a bare poll loop. Because there is no allocator and no `alloc` crate, any heap use on a reachable path would fail the build, so that it compiles and links for `thumbv7em-none-eabihf` is the guarantee. `tools/noalloc-check.sh` builds it for the Cortex-M target and asserts the linked archive references zero allocator symbols (`__rust_alloc`, `_ZN5alloc`, `handle_alloc_error`, ...) while the pipeline entry point is present (so the code was really emitted, not eliminated). Wired into CI (`features-linux`), alongside the M624 runtime zero-alloc test. This is the embedded analog of the copy-plan / conformance moat: the heap-free claim is machine-checked, not asserted.
- M624: static (heap-free) element model (Phase 2 of the heap-free MCU core): the generic twin of the object-safe `AsyncElement` / `OutputSink`, which box a future per frame. `g2g_core::staticelem` adds `StaticSource` / `StaticTransform` / `StaticSink` traits using `async fn` in trait (stable on MSRV 1.75), so a stage's future is an anonymous type inlined into the caller, never boxed, plus const-arity runners (`run_source_sink`, `run_source_transform_sink`) and a `Chain` combinator for longer pipelines. A chain built from these is fully monomorphized (no `dyn`, no `Box`) and executor-agnostic (an Embassy task `.await`s it on an MCU, `block_on` on a host). Part of the no-alloc data-plane subset (`--no-default-features`), so it cross-compiles to `thumbv7em-none-eabihf`. Runtime zero-alloc proof: `m624_static_pipeline_noalloc` drives 100k frames through `run_source_transform_sink` under a counting global allocator and observes zero allocations (the runner + trait API complement to M616's data-path and M620's concrete-chain proofs).
- M623: made `alloc` optional in `g2g-core` (Phase 1 of the heap-free MCU core), so the framework can target the safety / no-heap parts of the MCU market that reject a heap outright. `extern crate alloc` and the whole dynamic / build-time / tooling layer (the caps solver, autoplug, `parse_launch`, dynamic `Graph`, the `dyn` element traits, plus `conformance` / `copyplan` / `dot` / `wire` / `tag` / `pool` / `property` / `stream` / `aggregator` / `log` / `clock`) now sit behind a new `alloc` cargo feature; `std` / `runtime` / `metadata` imply it, and `alloc` pulls `spin` (a `no_std` crate, so no `std` leak). The data plane stays: `Frame`, the `Caps` enum + `intersect` / `fixate`, `MemoryDomain::System(SystemSlice::Foreign)` (the `StaticLendRing` zero-copy lend), `staticpool`, and the pure `error` / `time` / `mediaclock` / `segment` / `state` / `link` / `metrics` / `query` modules. Heap-only pieces are gated in place: the GPU / shared-CPU memory domains (`Cuda` / `DmaBuf` / `Wgpu` / `D3D11` / `SystemView` and their keep-alives), `SystemSlice`'s owned / pooled / shared variants (leaving `Foreign`), `Frame::share` (tee is a heap op), `Caps::Tensor` + `TensorShape` (a `Vec`; a fixed-rank no-alloc tensor shape is a follow-on), `CapsSet`, and `to_gst_string`. `default` is now `[]` (the no-alloc subset), which also fixes the long-standing "bare `cargo build -p g2g-core` fails" papercut; host consumers get `alloc` transitively via `runtime` / `std` (all of them already do, so zero downstream change). Proven: `cargo build -p g2g-core --no-default-features` compiles the data subset and cross-compiles clean (clippy included) to `thumbv7em-none-eabihf` with no allocator; the full `dyn-slot` / workspace build is unchanged (390 test groups green, clippy clean). Phase 2 (a generic `async fn`-in-trait static element model + const-generic runner) and Phase 3 (a link-time no-heap proof example for a bare Cortex-M target) follow.
- M622: extended the boundary-scoped time newtypes (M618) to the PTP servo's reference-vs-master seam, the other place the meaningless-offset mixing bug lived. `g2g-core/src/time.rs` adds `RefNs` (the pipeline's monotonic reference nanoseconds, a relative timeline with an arbitrary epoch, distinct from absolute `TaiNs`). `PtpServo` / `PtpClock` `sync_exchange` now take `(t1: TaiNs, t2: RefNs, t3: RefNs, t4: TaiNs)` and `observe_master` takes `(local: RefNs, master: TaiNs)`, so the master (TAI) and reference (monotonic) roles are typed at every call and can no longer be swapped; the internal fit still widens to `i128` as before. Call sites (the SLAVE `Exchange` cycle, the software `PtpClient`, and the OS-`CLOCK_TAI` delegate `PtpSystemClock`) wrap the wire-derived `u64`s at the seam. CI: a `RefNs` accessor test plus the existing servo lock / outlier / delegate tests now typed.
- M621: grew the conformance matrix from two native-muxer oracles to a real interop + hardware matrix, and added the CI job that publishes it. The ffmpeg-interop transport tests now persist peer-tagged `Oracle` evidence on success (`udpsrc` via ffmpeg's RTP payloader, `rtmpsrc` via an ffmpeg RTMP publisher, `srtsrc` / `srtsink` via a libsrt caller / listener including the AES variants), so each derives `InteropTested` against a named reference peer. The Vulkan Video GPU decode tests persist `Hardware` evidence tagged with the physical GPU (new `VulkanVideoDevice::device_name`, from the wgpu adapter), covering `vulkanvideo` for H.264 (m489), H.265 (m503), and AV1 (m506), so it derives `HardwareValidated` on the RTX 3060. The M615/M619 muxer oracles now respect an externally-set `$G2G_CONFORMANCE_LOG` (append, no truncation) so a CI run aggregates every oracle into one log; standalone they keep their dedicated deterministic log. New CI `conformance` job installs ffmpeg, runs the deterministic ffprobe oracles (required) and the timing-sensitive transport interop (best-effort), then folds the accumulated evidence into `g2g-inspect --maturity` and writes the table to the job summary + an evidence artifact. Verified end to end on this host: the aggregate report shows `mp4mux` / `mpegtsmux` / `udpsrc` / `rtmpsrc` / `srtsrc` / `srtsink` at interop-tested (ffmpeg peers) and `vulkanvideo` at hardware-validated (RTX 3060). `Hardware` rows come from a self-hosted GPU runner, not hosted CI.
- M620: extended the no-steady-state-allocation proof from a single stage (M616) to a multi-stage pipeline. `m620_multistage_no_alloc` wires a concrete source -> transform -> sink by direct (non-`dyn`) method calls over a shared `StaticLendRing` and, with the counting `#[global_allocator]`, confirms the whole chain allocates zero heap over 100k frames: a frame flows capture -> inspect -> checksum and its slot recycles, nothing allocated. This is the concrete-link half of the boundary M616 pinned (the object-safe `dyn OutputSink::push` boxes per frame); a fully zero-alloc dyn runner remains a larger, deferred effort, the load-bearing MCU claim (a heap-free data plane) being proven by these two tests.
- M619: grew the conformance matrix with a second reference-implementation oracle, the native MPEG-TS muxer (`TsMux`) validated by `ffprobe` (a different container from the M615 MP4 oracle: transport stream vs ISO-BMFF). `TsMux` muxes synthetic H.264 access units into a `Caps::ByteStream{MpegTs}` stream, ffprobe demuxes it and reports the h264 elementary stream, and on success peer-tagged `Oracle` evidence is persisted, deriving `mpegtsmux` as `InteropTested`. Self-skips without ffprobe. Confirms the persisted-evidence matrix generalizes past one element.
- M618: boundary-scoped time newtypes at the clock / PTP / RTP seam, so the compiler rejects mixing the three "just an integer" times that meet there. `g2g-core/src/time.rs` adds `TaiNs` (PTP/TAI nanoseconds, absolute) and `RtpTs` (the 32-bit wrapping RTP media-clock timestamp), and `MediaClock` now takes a `TaiNs` and returns an `RtpTs` (`ticks` / `rtp_timestamp` / `tai_from_rtp`); durations (`ticks_to_ns`) stay a plain `u64`. This makes the exact confusion the PTP servo work hit unrepresentable (a monotonic reference is not a `TaiNs`; an RTP timestamp is not nanoseconds), and is deliberately narrow to the RTP/TAI boundary, not a `Frame.timing` retrofit (pipeline PTS stays `u64` ns on its own timeline). The ST 2110 packetizers wrap at the `MediaClock` call (`TaiNs(tai_ns)`) and unwrap the wire value (`.get()`), a mechanical change with the -20 / -30 / -40 / -22 loopback round-trip suite confirming no regression. CI: `TaiNs` / `RtpTs` accessor + wrap tests, and the existing media-clock round-trip / wrap-resolution tests now typed.
- M617: made the zero-copy property an *enforced* graph-level contract, not just an inspectable one. `run_graph_with_copy_policy(graph, clock, cap, policy)` runs the copy plan (M613) after negotiation resolves every link's memory domain and, before any frame flows, checks it against a `CopyPolicy`; a violation returns the new `G2gError::CopyBudget` so a pipeline that must stay zero-copy (`CopyPolicy::DenyAll`) refuses to start rather than paying a host round-trip at runtime. The gate is opt-in (plain `run_graph` is unchanged) and threads an `Option<CopyPolicy>` through `run_graph_inner`. CI: an all-System pipeline (`videotestsrc ! videoflip ! fakesink`) satisfies `DenyAll` / `AtMost(1)` / `Allow` and runs, and plain `run_graph` is unaffected; the catching side (a device<->host raw-frame transfer failing `DenyAll`) is unit-tested on the copy plan in M613.
- M616: proved the no-steady-state-allocation embedded contract with a counting `#[global_allocator]`, turning the "heap-free capture path" from a claim into a measured guarantee. `m616_no_steady_state_alloc` runs the fixed-pool capture -> frame -> consume -> drop hot path over a `StaticLendRing` for 100k frames (acquire a pre-allocated slot, fill it, lend it zero-copy as a `System` frame via `SystemSlice::from_foreign`, read it, drop it so the slot recycles) and asserts the allocator counted **zero** allocations across the whole loop. The honest boundary is pinned separately in `m616_dyn_push_allocates`: because the object-safe `OutputSink::push` returns `Pin<Box<dyn Future>>`, driving frames through a `dyn` sink boxes one future per frame (a control-plane allocation), so the test asserts that path allocates at least once per frame and documents that the zero-alloc contract covers the data path plus a concrete (non-dyn) link, not the dyn control path. This is the MCU / RTOS-credibility proof: a heap-free steady-state data plane, with the one place allocation still occurs measured rather than hidden.
- M615: grew the conformance matrix with *persisted* interop / hardware evidence, so the derived maturity can reach `InteropTested` / `HardwareValidated` from the resource-owning tests, not only the in-process `UnitTested` batteries. Core gains `ConformanceDimension::from_label` and `ConformanceReport::{record_mut, absorb}` (absorb unions another report's evidence per element, deduplicating, so a persisted `Oracle` lifts the matching in-process element's level). `g2g-plugins::conformance::persist` (std) is a tab-separated append-only evidence log (`$G2G_CONFORMANCE_LOG`, or a temp-dir default): `record_evidence` appends one line when a check passes, `load_persisted` parses it back (skipping malformed / unknown-dimension lines), and `full_report` folds it into the in-process `report()`. `g2g-inspect --maturity` now renders `full_report`, so the interop / hardware rows earned by the tests appear without inspect needing ffmpeg or a GPU. The demonstrating oracle (`tests/m615_conformance_oracle.rs`, self-skips without ffprobe): g2g's native `Mp4MuxN` muxes a synthetic H.264 + AAC fMP4, `ffprobe` (a real external demuxer) reads both tracks back, and on success `Oracle` evidence (peer = ffmpeg) is persisted, deriving `mp4mux` as `InteropTested`. CI: core merge / dedup / label round-trip tests, and a ffprobe-free persistence round-trip that confirms a persisted `Oracle` datapoint reloads, derives `InteropTested`, and merges into `full_report`.
- M614: conformance harness + derived maturity metadata, so "how validated is this element?" is answered from evidence a passing check produced, never a hand-authored claim (which drifts into an overclaim under fast iteration). `g2g-core/src/conformance.rs` (pure) defines the vocabulary: a `ConformanceDimension` (`Instantiate` / `Properties` / `RoundTrip` / `LossResilience` / `ZeroCopy` / `Latency` / `Oracle` / `Hardware`), an `Evidence` tagging one verified dimension with optional platform / codec / peer context, and a `MaturityRecord` whose `level()` *derives* a `MaturityLevel` (`Unverified` < `Instantiated` < `UnitTested` < `InteropTested` < `HardwareValidated`) from the evidence bag with no setter, so a record cannot claim more than it proves. The derivation has honesty guards: `Oracle` counts toward `InteropTested` only with a named peer and `Hardware` toward `HardwareValidated` only with a named platform, and the *absence* of evidence is the signal, a loopback-only element carries no `Oracle` evidence and so tops out at `UnitTested` (the "not interop-validated" caveat as data). `ConformanceReport::to_table` renders the matrix. `g2g-plugins/src/conformance.rs` holds the batteries: each exercises a real element (the ST 2110-20 video and -30 audio packetizer / depacketizer cores) with cheap in-process checks and adds evidence only when a check passes, deriving `st2110video` = {instantiate, round-trip, loss-resilience via the -7 seamless merge} and `st2110audio` = {instantiate, round-trip}, both `UnitTested` with no interop claim; `report()` aggregates them. `g2g-inspect --maturity` runs the battery live and prints the table. CI: core derivation / honesty-guard / ordering / table tests, and plugin-battery tests asserting the derived level is `UnitTested` and that no `Oracle` evidence is emitted (the loopback-is-not-interop contract). Follow-on: persisting `Oracle` / `Hardware` evidence from the resource-owning integration tests so the matrix shows them too.
- M613: copy / allocation plan, a static pre-run analysis that turns the graph's implicit memory-domain resolution into a checkable, graph-level contract. `g2g-core/src/copyplan.rs` (pure, like `dot`) analyzes a negotiated graph's per-edge memory domains + fixated caps into a `CopyPlan`: the sequence of memory hops (the domain a frame occupies on each edge) and the transfers between differing domains. A transfer is recorded at any node whose output domain differs from the domain it consumed; `classify` sorts it into `TransferKind::{None, Interop, DeviceHost, CrossDevice}` (dma-buf and same-family host hops are free; a GPU download/upload over the bus is `DeviceHost`), and it is a counted frame copy only when a raw heavy buffer crosses on both sides (new `Caps::is_raw_media`, true for raw video / PCM audio / tensor), so a decode (`CompressedVideo` -> `RawVideo`) or an off-GPU encode is surfaced in the trace but not miscounted as a raw-frame copy. `CopyPlan::{frame_copies, host_round_trips, is_zero_copy, to_report}` report it, and `check(CopyPolicy)` (`Allow` / `AtMost(n)` / `DenyAll`) enforces a budget so an accidental host round-trip in a zero-copy pipeline fails at construction instead of being measured after. The runner extracts the flat node/edge profiles from a negotiated graph via `runtime::copy_plan(vg, caps, memory)`; `g2g-launch --copy-plan` negotiates and prints the report then exits (validated end to end on a `videotestsrc ! videoconvert ! fakesink` pipeline: two System hops, zero-copy). CI: `classify` domain-family coverage, an all-System pipeline proven zero-copy, a GPU-resident pipeline staying zero-copy across a decode, a device->host download of a raw frame counted as one copy (and failing `DenyAll` with the offender named), an off-GPU encode not counted, and the report marking the offending copy.
- M612: a full per-format ST 2110-21 VRX validator, `st2110pacing::VrxValidator`, replacing the burst-tolerance approximation (`Pacer::conforms`, kept as a cheap check) with the actual leaky-bucket receiver-buffer model. A conformant receiver reads one packet every `drain_interval_ns` (= the matching `Pacer`'s interval) after a `TR_OFFSET` head start; `evaluate` feeds a run of actual packet emission offsets through the model, tracking buffer occupancy (`sent - read`) over time, and returns a `VrxReport` with the peak occupancy, whether any packet arrived after its scheduled read deadline (starving the receiver), whether it conforms to the profile's `Cmax` buffer depth, and the first violating packet. `Cmax` / `TR_OFFSET` are the per-format -21 compliance parameters (from the SMPTE tables), so the model is format-agnostic; `for_pacer` derives the drain interval from a `Pacer` for the profile under test. CI: a perfectly-paced frame conforming to a 1-packet buffer (occupancy stays at the one-packet head start), a full burst overrunning a narrow 8-packet buffer (early, not late, first violation at the 9th packet), and a late final packet starving the receiver even with a huge buffer.
- M611: reused the ST 2110-21 `Pacer` in the -22 JPEG XS sink. Factored the schedule's socket-bound realization into `st2110pacing::pace_send` (behind the `st2110` feature): given a frame's already-built RTP packets, a socket, and a `Pacer`, it sleeps on the tokio timer to each packet's target offset before sending, so both the -20 video and -22 JPEG XS sinks shape traffic through one helper (the video sink's inline paced loop is now this call). `St2110JxsSink` gains a `pacing` property (`off` / `linear` / `gapped`, default off) and derives the frame period from the negotiated `Caps::CompressedVideo` framerate; when set it paces the codestream's packets across the period, otherwise the default burst path is unchanged. CI: a `pacing` property round trip and a `#[tokio::test]` sending a multi-packet codestream at 50 fps with gapped pacing, asserting it takes a meaningful fraction of the 20 ms period (a burst finishes in microseconds) with the packets arriving.
- M610: wired ST 2110-7 seamless protection into the -20 video source. `st2110dup` gains `RedundantRtpReceiver` (behind the `st2110` feature, the std/socket sibling of the sans-IO `SeamlessDedup`): it binds over several already-bound receive sockets (one per path), polls them round-robin from a rolling cursor, feeds every datagram through the shared dedup, and yields the next novel packet, so two in-order paths merge back into sequence order (draining one path fully first would reorder packets past a frame's marker and lose the other path's tail) and it ends the stream once every path is idle for a timeout. Essence-agnostic, so any `St2110*Src` can adopt it. `St2110VideoSrc` gains `redundant` / `redundant-address` / `redundant-port` properties: when `redundant` is set it binds a second ("blue") path and drains both through the receiver, otherwise the single-socket path is unchanged. The per-frame build is shared by both paths via one `build_frame` helper. CI: a receiver-side test packetizes an RGBA frame with the real -20 packetizer, sends the complete stream down both paths with a few different mid-stream drops each (never the marker, none lost on both), and asserts the frame is reconstructed byte-exact through the redundant source; plus a property round trip. Multicast validation against reference gear remains.

- M609: ST 2110-21 sender pacing, so the -20 video sink spreads a frame's RTP packets across the frame period instead of bursting them (uncompressed HD is multi-Gbps; a burst overruns switch buffers and a receiver's VRX). `st2110pacing` is the sans-IO scheduling core: a `Pacer` yields each packet's target emission offset for a `PacingProfile::Linear` (even across the whole period, narrow-linear) or `PacingProfile::Gapped` (even across the active portion only, `active_ratio` defaulting to HD 1080/1125, leaving the blanking interval idle), and `Pacer::conforms` checks a run of actual offsets stays within a burst tolerance (the pacing model, not a full per-format VRX validator). `St2110VideoSink` gains a `pacing` property (`off` / `linear` / `gapped`, default off): when set and the framerate is known, it derives the frame period from the negotiated caps and sleeps to each packet's offset on the tokio timer between sends (the production runner drives `run_graph` under tokio; the default burst path is unchanged, so the park-executor tests are unaffected). CI: deterministic schedule / gapped-density / conformance / single-packet tests on the sans-IO core, a `pacing` property round trip, and a `#[tokio::test]` that sends a multi-packet frame at 50 fps with linear pacing and asserts it takes a meaningful fraction of the 20 ms period (a burst finishes in microseconds) with the packets arriving. Realizing pacing needs a real framerate + a tokio reactor; JPEG XS (-22) can reuse the same `Pacer`.
- M608: ST 2110-7 seamless protection (redundant-path reconstruction). `st2110dup::SeamlessDedup` is the sans-IO, essence-agnostic core: a -7 sender emits identical RTP packets (same SSRC / sequence / timestamps) down two disjoint paths, and the receiver forwards the first copy of each RTP sequence number and drops the later duplicate, so a loss on one path is filled by the other (hitless). It reads only the 16-bit RTP sequence (so it serves -20 / -22 / -30 / -40 alike), extending it against the highest seen to survive the `2^16` wrap, over a 1 KiB sliding-window bitset; a sequence older than the window is treated as already delivered (never trust the stream). SDP gains `a=group:DUP` grouping on `St2110Session` (a `dup_groups` of `a=mid` index lists, emitted / parsed per RFC 5888), so a redundant pair self-describes. CI: first-copy-forwarded / duplicate-dropped, two lossy paths (complementary drops incl real duplicates) reconstructing every sequence exactly once in order, the sequence wrap, short-packet rejection, an end-to-end reconstruction of an 8x4 RGBA frame through the real -20 depacketizer with each path dropping a third of the packets, and a DUP-group SDP round trip. The receive-side merge is the -7 core; wiring two sockets into a Src element and multicast validation against reference gear remain.
- M607: `AudioFormat::PcmS24Le` (GStreamer `S24LE`, 24-bit signed integer PCM, 3 bytes packed little-endian), the integer sibling of `PcmF32Le` for the ST 2110-30 / AES67 L24 wire, so a professional 24-bit source rides L24 without a detour through float.
