Added to core `Caps` (media type `audio/x-raw` `S24LE`, `is_pcm`, wire tag 4). `st2110audiortp` maps it to the L24 wire depth with a plain per-sample byte reorder (3-byte LE pipeline <-> 3-byte BE wire, sign-extended through `i32`), no scaling: `wire_depth` / `pcm_to_samples` / `samples_to_pcm` / `bytes_per_sample` / `audio_params` and the sink pad templates all accept it. The receive-side SDP default stays L24 -> F32 (S24 is opt-in on the source's `format`), so nothing existing changes. CI: `s24_integer_audio_rides_l24_over_udp_loopback` sends stereo 24-bit samples incl the signed extremes sink -> UDP -> src and asserts a byte-exact round trip (where F32 is lossy by up to one quantum).
- M606: multi-section ST 2110 session SDP, so a whole program (video + audio + ancillary) self-describes in one document, not one SDP per stream. New `st2110sdp::St2110Session` (a session address + a `Vec<St2110Sdp>`) serializes one RFC 4566 session header then each essence's media block tagged with `a=mid`, and `St2110Session::parse` splits an SDP at its `m=` lines and parses every section, a session-level `a=ts-refclk` (before the first `m=`) being inherited by any media that lacks its own. Refactored the single-stream `St2110Sdp::to_sdp` onto a shared `push_session_header` + `push_media` seam (byte-identical output for one stream). Models a multi-essence program, not ST 2110-7 seamless protection (-7 pairs two identical streams under `a=group:DUP`, a separate redundancy feature). CI: a video+audio+anc session round-trips through text (three `m=` sections, one `v=0`, `a=mid` tags), and a hand-written program SDP with one shared reference clock parses with both streams inheriting the grandmaster.
- M605: JPEG XS encode / decode via Intel SVT-JPEG-XS (`SvtJpegXsEnc` / `SvtJpegXsDec`, `g2g-plugins`, `jpegxs` feature, Linux), the actual -22 codec. Hand-rolled FFI to `libSvtJpegxs` (ISO/IEC 21122, no libavcodec): the `#[repr(C)]` structs transcribe `SvtJpegxs*.h` with compile-time size assertions (the `nvenc` / `nvdec` technique), and `build.rs` links the library via pkg-config (`SvtJpegxs.pc`). `SvtJpegXsEnc` takes planar `RawVideo` (`I420` / `I422` 8-bit, `I422p10` 10-bit), configures the encoder (target bits-per-pixel via a `bpp` fraction property, codestream packetization mode) and emits a `CompressedVideo{JpegXs}` codestream per frame; `SvtJpegXsDec` discovers geometry / format from the first codestream (`svt_jpeg_xs_decoder_init`) and refines its output caps via `CapsChanged`. Both `!Send` handles ride the ownership-transfer `unsafe impl Send` contract and are registered as `jpegxsenc` / `jpegxsdec` for `parse_launch`. **Validated on this host** (real SVT-JPEG-XS 0.10): an I422p10 encode -> decode round-trips near-lossless at 10 bpp (mean 10-bit error < 8), and `m605_jpegxs_st2110` proves the full ProAV path end to end (raw -> encode -> `St2110JxsSink` -> UDP -> `St2110JxsSrc` -> decode -> raw). CI-excluded like the other codec features.
- M604: ST 2110-22 JPEG XS over RTP (RFC 9134), the compressed mezzanine essence, the transport sibling of -20. New `VideoCodec::JpegXs` (core `Caps`, `image/x-jxsc`, wire tag 7). `g2g-plugins::st2110jxs` is the sans-IO packetizer / depacketizer in codestream packetization mode (RFC 9134 `K=0`): it slices an opaque JPEG XS codestream into MTU-sized packets each prefixed with the 4-octet payload header (`T|K|L|I|F counter|SEP counter|P counter`), the RTP marker ending the frame, every packet sharing the frame's 90 kHz `MediaClock` timestamp; the depacketizer reassembles on the marker, bounding the buffer, dropping slice-mode (`K=1`) and discarding a partial frame when a new timestamp arrives before the marker (never trust the stream). `g2g-plugins::st2110jxsrtp` (behind `st2110`) wraps it over UDP: `St2110JxsSink` (`CompressedVideo{JpegXs}` in, PTS through the elected clock) and `St2110JxsSrc` (UDP -> codestream frames, geometry from properties / SDP). SDP gains a `St2110Essence::JpegXs` (`rtpmap jxsv/90000`, `fmtp packetmode=0`/`transmode=1`/sampling/geometry/`SSN=ST2110-22:2019`), with `sdp()` / `apply_sdp()` on the elements; the shared video-fmtp parser now feeds both -20 (`raw`) and -22 (`jxsv`). CI: sans-IO round-trip (multi-packet, marker-only-on-last, header field checks, slice-mode / short-packet rejection, runaway-frame bound, lost-marker recovery), a sink -> UDP -> src loopback of a synthetic codestream, SDP round-trip, and a sink-SDP -> src auto-config loop. Wire compliance built from RFC 9134, not yet validated against reference gear.
- M603: ST 2110 SDP auto-config for the audio and ancillary sources, completing the self-describing-stream story across all three essences (M601 wired -20 video). `St2110AudioSink::sdp()` / `St2110AncSink::sdp()` publish their stream's SDP and `St2110AudioSrc::apply_sdp()` / `St2110AncSrc::apply_sdp()` auto-configure a receiver from a parsed one: audio takes the depth (L16 -> `PcmS16Le`, L24 -> `PcmF32Le`), sample rate, channels, and port; ancillary (no geometry) takes the port and keeps its constructed caption service. Each `apply_sdp` returns false and leaves the source unchanged for a non-matching essence. CI: per-essence sink-SDP -> text -> parse -> src round-trip loops (asserting the recovered format / geometry / port) plus the wrong-essence rejection. Now `st2110videortp` / `st2110audiortp` / `st2110ancrtp` all publish and consume SDP. Remaining ST 2110 (deferred, each needs a prerequisite): -22 JPEG XS (needs a JPEG XS codec + a `VideoCodec` variant); -21 sender traffic shaping (needs a runtime async timer to pace real sends); an `S24` pipeline caps format for L24 from integer (rather than float) audio.
- M602: ST 2110-30 L24 / F32 audio, completing the -30 depth story (the core always supported L16 / L24; the elements were L16-only). `St2110AudioSink` / `St2110AudioSrc` now carry `PcmF32Le` as well as `PcmS16Le`: S16 rides the wire as L16 (unchanged), F32 as L24 (float has more than 16 bits of precision, so it maps to the 24-bit wire, scaled from [-1, 1] and clamped so +1.0 does not wrap to full-scale negative). New `pcm_to_samples` / `samples_to_pcm` / `wire_depth` helpers factor the format<->wire conversion (the sink derives its depth and the source its output format from the negotiated caps; the pad templates advertise both). CI: `f32_audio_rides_l24_over_udp_loopback` sends stereo float PCM incl the range extremes sink -> UDP -> src and asserts every sample survives within one 24-bit quantum; the existing S16/L16 exact round trip is unchanged. Still `L16`/`L24` integer PCM on the wire (AES67); adding an `S24` pipeline caps format is separate. Next: SDP auto-config for the audio / ancillary sources.
- M601: ST 2110 SDP (RFC 4566 + SMPTE ST 2110-10/-20/-30/-40), the out-of-band stream description that lets a receiver auto-configure instead of being hand-set, tying the -20/-30/-40 essences together. `g2g-plugins::st2110sdp` is the sans-IO generator / parser: an `St2110Sdp` (essence + payload type + address / port + optional PTP `a=ts-refclk` grandmaster) serializes to an SDP text block and parses back. Essence covers `St2110Essence::Video` (`rtpmap raw/90000`, `fmtp sampling=`/`width=`/`height=`/`exactframerate=`/`depth=`, mapping RGBA-8 / YCbCr-4:2:2-8 / YCbCr-4:2:2-10 to the `Sampling`), `Audio` (`L16`/`L24` rate / channels + `a=ptime`), and `Ancillary` (`smpte291/90000`); generation emits the SMPTE-required attributes (`PM=2110GPM`, `SSN`, `TP`, colorimetry, `a=mediaclk:direct=0`) and parsing is lenient about attribute order / unknown lines but never-trust-the-stream (an unmapped `m=`/`rtpmap`, a missing geometry, or an unknown sampling+depth yields `None`, not a wrong guess). Wired to the -20 elements: `St2110VideoSink::sdp(exact_fps)` publishes the stream's SDP and `St2110VideoSrc::apply_sdp()` auto-configures a receiver's format / size / rate / port from a parsed one, so a stream self-describes end to end (`apply_sdp` for the audio / ancillary sources is a mechanical follow-on). CI (6 tests): round-trips for 10-bit / RGBA / YUYV video, L24 audio (incl 125 us ptime), and ancillary; parsing a realistic hand-written ST 2110-20 SDP (tolerating `a=source-filter:` and attribute reordering, recovering the PTP gmid / domain); rejection of a non-2110 codec, a video section with no fmtp, and an unknown sampling; and the full loop (a sink's SDP -> text -> parse -> a src configured from it, geometry and 59.94->60 fps checked). Built from the RFCs, not yet validated against reference gear. Next: JPEG XS (-22).
- M600: ST 2110-20 10-bit 4:2:2 (RFC 4175 YCbCr-4:2:2 10-bit), the broadcast-norm sampling. Refactored `st2110video` from a byte-reorder to a per-pgroup `Layout` seam (`read_group` / `write_group`) so the packetizer / depacketizer are agnostic to packed-vs-planar and byte-vs-bit packing; the 8-bit RGBA / YUYV paths are unchanged behind it. The new sampling maps the planar `RawVideoFormat::I422p10` (separate Y / Cb / Cr planes, 16-bit little-endian samples in the low 10 bits) to the 5-octet pgroup: the four samples Cb0 Y0 Cr0 Y1 are MSB-first bit-packed (`pack_2px_10` / `unpack_2px_10`), so a pgroup crosses both a planar-to-packed and a byte-to-bit boundary. `St2110VideoSink` / `St2110VideoSrc` accept `i422_10le` (source `format` property + both pad templates). CI: a planar round trip of distinct 10-bit samples, a bit-layout lock test (`Cb0 = 0x3FF` fills octet 0 and the top 2 bits of octet 1; unpack inverts pack), and an end-to-end I422p10 sink -> UDP -> src loopback asserting the three planes survive byte-exact. Uncompressed HD stays multi-Gbps, so the -20 path is bandwidth-bound and the per-pgroup gather / scatter is not the bottleneck. Wire compliance built from RFC 4175, not yet validated against reference gear. Next: SDP.
- M599: ST 2110-20 uncompressed video over RTP (RFC 4175), the -20 essence. `g2g-plugins::st2110video` is the sans-IO packetizer / depacketizer: unlike -30 audio (raw PCM in the payload), -20 carries a media header, an Extended Sequence Number then one or more Sample Row Data (SRD) line headers (`Length` octets, `F`|`Line No`, `C`|`Offset`, the `C` bit chaining another header), so `St2110VideoPacketizer` slices a packed frame into SRD runs sized to the MTU (splitting lines, packing several partial lines per packet) and `St2110VideoDepacketizer` writes each run back into the frame, completing it on the RTP marker bit; every packet of a frame shares the frame's 90 kHz `MediaClock` timestamp. Two RFC 4175 samplings mapped to the packed `RawVideoFormat`s a pipeline already holds: RGBA 8-bit (pgroup = 1 pixel / 4 octets, byte-identical) and YCbCr-4:2:2 8-bit (pgroup = 2 pixels / 4 octets, wire order Cb0 Y0 Cr0 Y1 vs our `Yuyv` Y0 Cb Y1 Cr, so the luma / chroma bytes are swapped on the wire, an involution used both ways). Never-trust-the-stream: an SRD naming a line past the height, an offset off the pgroup grid, or a length overrunning the row / datagram is rejected rather than writing out of bounds. `g2g-plugins::st2110videortp` (behind the `st2110` feature) wraps it over UDP: `St2110VideoSink` (an `AsyncElement`, packed raw video in, geometry from caps, PTS through the elected clock to the media-clock timestamp) and `St2110VideoSrc` (a `SourceLoop`, geometry from properties since -20 signals it in SDP out of band, PTS reconstructed from the RTP timestamp, EOS on a read-timeout gap). Sink properties `host` / `port` / `payload-type` / `ssrc` / `max-packet`; source `address` / `port` / `format` / `width` / `height` / `framerate` (reusing `capsfilter::parse_raw_format` + `videoconvert::raw_format_to_str`, made shared). **CI end-to-end over real UDP** (loopback): `video_sink_to_src_over_udp_loopback` sends a 16x8 RGBA frame with a tiny 80-octet MTU (forcing many SRD-split packets) sink -> UDP -> src and asserts the frame reassembles byte-exact and EOS fires on the gap; plus core round-trip tests (multi-packet RGBA with marker-only-on-last + shared timestamp, YUYV wire-reorder there and back), geometry / out-of-bounds-SRD / short-packet rejection, and property tests. Uncompressed HD is multi-Gbps, so this is bandwidth-heavy (the test uses a tiny frame). Wire compliance built from RFC 4175, not yet validated against reference gear. Next: 10-bit 4:2:2 (pgroup = 5 octets, the broadcast norm), SDP.
- M598: ST 2110-40 caption network elements + the CEA-608/708 bridge, closing the loop on M596 (captions now travel end to end over -40). `g2g-plugins::st2110ancrtp` (behind the `st2110` feature) adds `St2110AncSink` (an `AsyncElement`, compressed H.264 / H.265 video in) and `St2110AncSrc` (a `SourceLoop`, timed `Caps::Text{Utf8}` cues out). The sink taps the video like `CcExtract` (a teed branch leaf), mines each access unit's caption `cc_data` triples, wraps them in a Caption Distribution Packet (new `cea::build_cdp` / `parse_cdp`, CEA-708 / SMPTE ST 334-2: 0x9669 header, ccdata section, footer with a packet checksum), carries the CDP in a DID 0x61 / SDID 0x01 ANC packet, and sends the RFC 8331 -40 RTP timestamped at the frame's PTP/TAI time (elected clock base + PTS through the 90 kHz media clock); the source depacketizes -40 back into triples and decodes the selected service into cue frames. The decode core is factored out of `CcExtract` into a shared `cea::CaptionDecoder` (owns the `CcSource` service selection + the boxed CEA-608 / CEA-708 state machines, driven from triples mined from SEI *or* carried in a CDP), and the cue-to-text-frame emission into `ccextract::push_cue_frames`, so `CcExtract` and `St2110AncSrc` differ only in where the triples come from (no duplication). `CcSource` moves to `cea` (re-exported from `ccextract` for the existing path) and gains `CcSource::parse` (the `cc1`..`cc4` / `service-N` vocabulary, now shared by `uridecodebin`'s `#closed-captions=` and the source's `service` selection). Sink properties: `host` / `port` / `payload-type` / `ssrc` / `cdp-frame-rate`; a video frame with no captions sends no -40 packet. **CI end-to-end over real UDP** (loopback): `captions_sink_to_src_over_udp_loopback` runs a CEA-608 pop-on caption as H.264 AUs -> -40 sink -> UDP -> src and asserts the "HI" cue survives with the right start/end times and the source emits EOS on the gap; plus CDP round-trip / rejection (bad identifier, over-long length, bad checksum, invalid triples, time-code-section skip), the shared decoder rendering a pop-on from triples, the no-caption skip, and property tests. Because the RTP timestamp is the shared media clock, a receiver on the same grandmaster keeps captions frame-aligned. Wire compliance (CDP + -40) built from the specs, not yet validated against reference gear. Next: -20 uncompressed video (RFC 4175), SDP.
- M597: ST 2110-30 audio network elements, the point where the sans-IO cores become a runnable sender/receiver. `g2g-plugins::st2110audiortp` (behind a new `st2110` feature) adds `St2110AudioSink` (an `AsyncElement`) and `St2110AudioSrc` (a `SourceLoop`) around the `st2110audio` core over UDP. The sink maps each PCM `DataFrame`'s PTS through the elected clock (`ClockSync::base_time` + running time) to a PTP/TAI sampling instant, packetizes, and sends RTP to a UDP destination (multicast group in a real deployment); the source binds a UDP socket, depacketizes into PCM `DataFrame`s, and reconstructs each PTS from the RTP media-clock delta (ending cleanly on a read-timeout silence gap). Because the timestamp is the shared media clock, a receiver on the same grandmaster stays in sync with the source. Properties on the sink (`host` / `port` / `payload-type` / `ssrc` / `ptime-us`, so `ptime-us=125` at 48 kHz gives 6-frame packets) per the property convention. Currently `PcmS16Le` <-> L16 (L24 / F32 follow the wider sample-format caps). **CI end-to-end over real UDP** (loopback works here): `audio_sink_to_src_over_udp_loopback` runs sink -> UDP 127.0.0.1 -> src (UDP buffers the packets, so send-then-receive is deterministic without threads) and asserts 96 stereo frames survive as two 48-frame packets, the source emits EOS on the gap, and PCM round-trips exactly; plus a property round-trip test. Multicast against reference gear remains a host/interop task. Next: the same element wrappers for -40 ancillary (+ a CEA-608/708 bridge), and -20 uncompressed video.
- M596: ST 2110-40 ancillary data over RTP (RFC 8331), where the caption stack meets ST 2110. `g2g-plugins::st2110anc` is the sans-IO packetizer / depacketizer for SMPTE ST 291 ANC packets (closed captions DID 0x61, timecode, AFD, ...): a CEA-608/708 ANC packet rides -40 with an RTP timestamp from the 90 kHz video `MediaClock`, so a receiver on the same grandmaster aligns captions with the frame. Implements the exact RFC 8331 wire format (fetched to get it right): an 8-byte payload header (extended 32-bit sequence number split across the RTP header and payload, Length, ANC_Count, F field), then ANC packets each with a 32-bit header (C / Line_Number / Horizontal_Offset / StreamNum) and 10-bit words (DID, SDID, Data_Count, user data, Checksum_Word) bit-packed MSB-first via a small bit cursor and zero-padded to a 32-bit boundary. SMPTE 291 integrity is enforced: every 10-bit word carries even parity (b8) + inverse (b9), the Checksum_Word is the low 9 bits of the sum of the low 9 bits of DID..last-UDW, and parsing rejects any message whose parity or checksum fails or whose declared Length overruns the datagram (never trust the stream). CI (5 tests): parity encoding, ANC packet round-trip, an RTP frame carrying two ANC packets (CEA-708 + CEA-608) with correct marker / timestamp / extended-sequence split, and rejection of corrupted parity/checksum, over-long Length, and short packets. Sans-IO like `st2110audio`; an element wrapper + the CEA bridge come later. Wire compliance should be confirmed against a real -40 sender/receiver before interop (built from the RFC, not yet validated against reference gear).
- M595: ST 2110 media transport, phase 1, the timing primitive + audio essence riding the PTP clock (M593/M594). `g2g-core::MediaClock` (ST 2110-10) is the mapping that ties RTP to PTP: a media clock counting at a fixed rate from the PTP epoch (90 kHz for video, the sample rate for audio) converts a PTP/TAI time to a 32-bit wrapping RTP timestamp and back, resolving the wrap against a reference (extended-timestamp technique). Because it is deterministic from the shared grandmaster time, two receivers compute the *same* timestamp for the same sampling instant, which is what makes cross-device A/V sync possible. Pure `no_std` integer math (runs on an embedded 2110 endpoint). On top of it, `g2g-plugins::st2110audio` is the sans-IO ST 2110-30 PCM packetizer / depacketizer (AES67-style, RFC 3190 L16 / L24): interleaved big-endian PCM straight in the RTP payload, timestamp from the media clock at the first sample's PTP instant and advancing by the sample-frame count per packet. Samples carried as `i32` (L16 low 16 bits, L24 low 24, sign-extended). CI (5 media-clock + 4 audio tests): timestamp round-trips within a tick and resolves the 2^32 wrap; two clocks agree on a timestamp; L16 (incl full-scale) and L24 stereo PCM survive packetize -> depacketize across multiple packets with correct sequence / timestamp progression; short and partial-sample-frame packets are rejected. Sans-IO like `rtppay` (an element wrapper sits on top later). Next ST 2110 phases: -40 ancillary (captions, RFC 8331), -20 uncompressed video (RFC 4175), -22 + JPEG XS.
- M594: in-process software PTP client (SLAVE mode), the portable "own the primitive" path so an endpoint with no OS PTP daemon (embedded, an appliance) can lock to a grandmaster itself. The CI-provable core lands in `g2g-core::ptp` (now a directory module): `wire` parses the PTP-over-UDP messages a delay-request-response SLAVE consumes (the 34-byte common header + Sync / Follow_Up / Delay_Resp bodies, one-step and two-step, correctionField in ns) and builds a Delay_Req, all bounds-checked (returns `None` on a short/malformed datagram, per the parser rules); `slave` is the transport-agnostic `PtpSlave` state machine that assembles one `(t1,t2,t3,t4)` cycle from the message stream (a fresh Sync restarts the cycle so a late Delay_Resp can't cross a stale `t3`, and each Delay_Resp is matched by sequence id + requestingPortIdentity). The UDP transport is `PtpClient` (`g2g-plugins`, `ptp` feature): joins the PTP multicast group on ports 319/320, runs a receive loop per port, drives the slave, sends a Delay_Req on request (software-timestamping `t2`/`t3` with `monotonic_ns`), and feeds each cycle to the servo, offering a `PtpGrandmaster` candidate once locked. CI (17 `ptp` tests, no sockets): the wire parser round-trips and rejects short buffers; the slave yields correct quads for one-/two-step cycles and ignores other domains / other slaves' responses; and `full_slave_path_drives_the_servo_to_lock` chains parse -> slave -> servo on a synthetic two-step master's byte stream and confirms lock (sub-us error, ~100 us path delay recovered, TAI estimate within 100 us). `PtpClient` itself needs privileged ports (319/320, root) and a real grandmaster, so its smoke test (`m594_ptpclient_smoke`) self-skips without them; live validation is a host task (`sudo`, `ptp4l -m`). Not in scope: BMCA/Announce (follows whatever master sends Sync on its domain), peer-delay, unicast, hardware timestamping, `SO_REUSEPORT` co-existence with `ptp4l`. This completes the `PtpClock` milestone (delegate + in-process backends both present).
- M593 phase C: `PtpSystemClock`, the OS-delegate PTP backend that works with `linuxptp` today. On a host running the standard PTP stack (`ptp4l` disciplining the NIC PHC, `phc2sys` copying it onto the system clock), `CLOCK_TAI` tracks the grandmaster; this element (`g2g-plugins`, `ptp` feature, Linux) samples `(CLOCK_MONOTONIC, CLOCK_TAI)` on a ~16 Hz worker thread and feeds the pairs to a `PtpClock` via a new direct-observation path, so the servo fits the monotonic reference to grandmaster TAI and offers a `PtpGrandmaster` candidate once locked. New `PtpServo::observe_master(local, master)` / `PtpClock::observe_master` fold a `(reference, master)` pair directly, bypassing the PTP message math (a delegate has an absolute master time, not raw timestamps); refactored to share the fold/lock/holdover/outlier logic with `sync_exchange`. Honest about "lock": `CLOCK_TAI` is always readable and smooth whether or not `ptp4l` runs, so lock here means the servo tracks the OS clock consistently (which under a real deployment is grandmaster time); confirming true grandmaster lock independently needs phase D or querying `ptp4l`. CI: `observe_master_locks_from_direct_pairs` (synthetic pairs lock the servo, recover a 50-ppm rate, reject zero master). **Validated on this Fedora host**: `m593_ptpsystemclock_smoke` locked onto the real `CLOCK_TAI` (TAI-scale `now_ns`, ~6 us servo residual, advancing with wall time). Next: phase D/M594 (in-process software PTP client, the portable path).
- M593 phase B: `PtpClock` type + `PtpGrandmaster` election tier. Wraps the `PtpServo` (phase A) behind interior mutability (a spin mutex) so one worker drives it via `sync_exchange(&self, ...)` while the pipeline reads the master estimate through a shared `Arc<dyn PipelineClock>`. A new `ClockPriority::PtpGrandmaster` tier sits above `LiveSource` (a grandmaster is the shared reference the whole facility, capture included, slaves to). `PtpClock::candidate()` offers it to election only while the servo is synchronised (`Locked` or `Holdover`); a `FreeRunning` servo returns `None`, so an unsynchronised clock is never made master and the pipeline falls back to a local clock. Validated end to end through the real `run_graph` (`m593_ptp_clock`): a three-arm graph (PTP arm at `PtpGrandmaster`, audio arm at `AudioProvider`, video arm at `Provider`) elects the PTP clock over both local clocks and hands *it* to the video sink, which is then slaved to the grandmaster/TAI timeline (advancing the reference, the sink's clock tracks the PTP estimate, not wall time) - the mechanism that makes A/V sync hold across machines locked to the same grandmaster, not just within one process. Plus unit tests for candidate gating (offered only once locked, reads TAI). Next: phase C (OS-PHC / `CLOCK_TAI` delegate backend so linuxptp works today), phase D/M594 (in-process software PTP client).
- M593 phase A: `PtpServo`, the PTP (IEEE 1588 / SMPTE ST 2059-2) clock servo (`PtpClock` milestone). The servo brain that lets multiple g2g processes/machines share one grandmaster timeline, the sync backbone Pro AV / ST 2110 needs. Pure `no_std` math in `g2g-core` (behind `runtime`, since it reuses the `DriftClock` servo core), no network or OS coupling: a caller feeds the four timestamps of each PTP delay request-response (`t1`/`t4` master clock, `t2`/`t3` our reference) and `sync_exchange` computes `offset = ((t2-t1)-(t4-t3))/2` and `mean_path_delay = ((t2-t1)+(t4-t3))/2`, then folds `(t2, t2-offset)` (the master time at our `t2`) into a `DriftClock`, which both smooths per-exchange jitter and estimates our oscillator's rate error vs the grandmaster. `now_ns()` reads the master (TAI) estimate at the current reference time. A lock state machine (`PtpState::FreeRunning`/`Locked`/`Holdover`) declares lock once >= 8 samples agree with the fit within 1 ms, rejects gross outliers (a queued/delayed packet > 20 ms off the fit) so one bad exchange can't yank the estimate, breaks lock after a run of them, and reports holdover when the grandmaster goes silent past a 5 s timeout (still coasting on the last fit). Because our reference is a monotonic clock (arbitrary epoch) while the master is absolute TAI, the raw PTP offset carries the epoch gap and is not a useful sync-quality number; `error_ns()` (how far a fresh sample lands from the fit) is the servo error that hovers near zero when locked. Reuses/adds `DriftClock::project_ns(local_ns)` (project an arbitrary reference instant through the fit; `now_ns` is now this applied to the reference). Fully CI-testable (6 tests, synthetic TAI-scale exchanges): locks onto a steady GM (sub-us error, ~100 us path delay recovered, TAI estimate within 100 us), recovers a 100-ppm-fast local oscillator's rate, rejects an injected 50 ms delayed packet while holding lock, rejects impossible timestamps, and enters holdover on a silent GM. Next: phase B (`PtpClock` type + a `PtpGrandmaster` election tier gated on lock), phase C (OS-PHC / `CLOCK_TAI` delegate backend for linuxptp), phase D/M594 (in-process software PTP client).
- M592: A/V lip-sync validation (clock-sync track, phase 3). Closes the loop on M590/M591 end to end. `m592_av_lipsync` (1) runs a real two-arm graph through `run_graph` (audio arm: source → a sink providing a disciplined `DriftClock` at `AudioProvider`; video arm: source → a sink offering a plain `Provider` clock and adopting whatever `ClockSync` the runner delivers) and asserts the runner elects the audio clock and hands *that* clock to the video sink, so the video sink is slaved to the audio timeline rather than wall time (moving the reference confirms the video sink's clock tracks the drifted audio one, not the wall clock); (2) drives the real `DriftClock` with a synthetic 0.1%-fast audio master over 10 s at 25 fps and shows the payoff numerically: a video sink reading its deadlines off the drift clock stays locked to the audio (max skew **1 ns**), while one paced to wall time drifts **10 ms** out by the end, exactly the `slope-1` error the disciplined clock removes. Deterministic (a hand-advanced `ManualClock`, no real sleeping) so it runs in CI; a real-time host run would be 10 s+ and timing-flaky. The video sink here is a test harness (adopts `ClockSync` and records) because no headless display sink does yet (`SyncSink` uses its own clock, `WaylandSink` needs a display); a real on-display lip-sync soak stays a host task. Remaining: extend the same discipline to `PulseSink` / `PipeWireSink` (only `AlsaSink` provides a clock today).
- M591: `AlsaSink` DAC-disciplined playout clock (A/V sync, phase 1). The audio sink now becomes the pipeline's sync master, GStreamer's model. Its worker samples `(monotonic_now, frames_played)` after each blocking `writei` (`frames_played = frames_written - snd_pcm_delay()`, the true DAC playout position) and feeds them to a `DriftClock` (M590); the sink offers that clock to election via `provide_clock()` at a new `ClockPriority::AudioProvider` tier, which outranks a video sink's plain `Provider` (so video slaves to audio) but still yields to a `LiveSource` capture clock. A `provide-clock` property (bool, default on, GStreamer's `basesink` knob) gates it; disabling it also skips the per-buffer `delay()` probe. `open_pcm` now bounds the ring (`set_buffer_time_near` ~200 ms / `set_period_time_near` ~20 ms): some backends (pipewire-alsa) otherwise expose a very large default buffer, so `writei` never blocks (the whole stream queues at once) and `snd_pcm_delay` pins at the full backlog, which both defeats the sink's pacing and starves the clock discipline of played-frame progress; this also makes M589's pacing claim actually true. A reusable `MonotonicClock` (the process monotonic wall clock as a `PipelineClock`, `std`) lands in `g2g-core` as the drift clock's reference (several sinks previously each defined their own copy). **Validated on this Fedora / PipeWire host**: `m591_alsasink_drift_clock` plays a tone and measures the real DAC drift, 40 observations, slope 0.999942 (~58 ppm slow), the clock advancing 50 ms across a 50 ms sleep. Next (phase 3 already partly here): a video-sink lip-sync run against this audio master.
- M590: `DriftClock`, a disciplined pipeline clock (A/V sync, phase 2). Every clock the pipeline elects today is just `monotonic_ns()`, so there is one wall-clock timeline and true A/V sync cannot exist; a real audio sink plays samples at its DAC's rate, which drifts from wall time by tens to hundreds of ppm. `DriftClock` (in `g2g-core`, behind the `runtime` feature) turns a sink's coarse, jittery playout readings into a continuous master clock a video sink can pace to. It is fed `(local_ns, master_ns)` observations (`local_ns` from a reference monotonic clock via `reference_now()`, `master_ns` the true playout position, e.g. `(frames_written - snd_pcm_delay()) * 1e9 / rate`) and fits `master ≈ slope * local + offset` by least squares over a sliding window; `now_ns()` projects the current reference time through that fit, so it both estimates the playout rate (`slope`, ~1.0 + drift) and smooths the per-observation jitter. Single-writer by contract (one audio worker `observe()`s, any number of sinks read), serialised by a spin lock, `Send + Sync`, shares as `Arc<dyn PipelineClock>` through clock election. Before the first observation it passes the reference through unchanged. Centred integer means keep the `f64` regression well-conditioned at ~1e18 ns; negative projections saturate. Fully CI-testable: `converges_to_the_master_playout_rate` feeds a synthetic 1.001x-drift master and asserts the slope converges and the projected timeline (including extrapolation past the last observation) tracks the true master within 1 ms; `a_slaved_reader_tracks_the_disciplined_timeline` shares one clock through a typed disciplining handle and an `Arc<dyn>` reader and confirms a slow master makes the reader's timeline lag the reference. Next (phase 1): an `AlsaSink` playout clock feeding this via `provide_clock`, and an election tweak so audio beats video's `Provider` tier.
- M589: Linux audio-sink host smoke test. The three render sinks (`alsasink` / `pulsesink` / `pipewiresink`) were unit-tested (caps mapping, pad templates) but never driven against a real audio device. `m589_audio_sink_smoke` feeds each a short interleaved-PCM sine tone on the host's default output and asserts the full device path runs (`configure_pipeline` opens the device, `process` writes PCM, `Eos` drains, the byte / frame counter advances), across a format + channel matrix (S16 + F32, stereo + mono) so handling beyond the one common shape is covered; a host with no reachable device (CI, headless) skips (a hardware error at configure is treated as "no device", not a failure). **Validated on Fedora / PipeWire** (PulseAudio-on-PipeWire + pipewire-alsa): all three sinks play, and the counters scale correctly with format size and channel count (F32 stereo = 2x the S16 bytes, S16 mono = half). Each sink is behind its cargo feature (`alsa-sink` / `pulse-sink` / `pipewire`); run with the ones built. No behaviour change to the sinks themselves; this closes the "never run on real hardware" gap. Still open: more sample formats (S24 / S32 / U8), multichannel speaker-position layouts, and DMABUF / zero-copy.
- M588: the random-access `VulkanVideoPlayer` scrubs H.265 and seeks to CRAs. The pull-based player (`frame_at(t)` / `frame_at_index`, the timeline-scrubber wedge for a wgpu viewer) was H.264-only. It now sniffs the codec from the stream's parameter-set NALs (`sniff_annexb_codec`) and drives an `H265DpbDecoder` too, behind a `PlayerDecoder` / `PlayerSession` enum that dispatches `index_pictures` / `reset` / `decode_range_to_texture` / `decode_range_all_to_textures` (the last two added to `H265DpbDecoder`, mirroring H.264). Its seek now targets the nearest IRAP random-access point, not only an IDR: `PictureMeta` gains `is_random_access` (an IDR for H.264; an IDR / CRA / BLA for H.265, a superset of the POC-resetting `is_keyframe` the reorder uses), so seeking into a late open-GOP GOP tunes in at that GOP's CRA (M587 discards its RASL) instead of decoding the whole stream from the leading IDR. A leading picture (a CRA's RASL / RADL, POC before its CRA) is not reconstructable by tuning in at that CRA, so `seek_point_for` falls back to the random-access point *before* the CRA and decodes continuously through it (which keeps the CRA's leading references). `decode_range_all_to_textures` now returns `(decode_index, texture)` pairs so a discarded RASL does not misalign the traversed-frame cache. **Validated on the RTX 3060**: `m588_vulkan_video_h265_player` scrubs the committed open-GOP clip (30 pictures) forward, backward and jumping - every displayed frame is bit-exact to the whole-stream `decode_all_to_textures` oracle (which also exercises the leading-picture seek path), and a cold seek to the last frame decodes 5 pictures, not 30 (it tuned in at the last CRA, not the IDR). H.264 scrubbing (`m498` / `m499`) is unchanged. AV1 is not yet a player codec (its display order is `show_existing_frame` / `order_hint`).
- M587: H.265 mid-stream random-access tune-in at a CRA. M577 made full-stream open-GOP HEVC decode correctly (a CRA in continuous decoding keeps the pre-CRA references its RASL leading pictures use). This is the seek case: after a `reset` (a seek that drops the DPB) to a CRA, the CRA is the first picture, so its `NoRaslOutputFlag == 1` and the pre-CRA references its RASL followers need are absent. `H265DpbDecoder` now discards those RASL pictures (new `h265_is_rasl` for `nal_unit_type` 8 / 9, and a `skip_rasl` flag set from each IRAP's `NoRaslOutputFlag`) rather than decoding them against a flushed DPB (garbage or a driver error); the check runs before POC derivation, so a dropped RASL leaves no trace in the state trailing pictures derive against. `decode_into_slot` now returns `Option` (`None` = discarded), threaded through `decode_push_meta` and the texture path. The flag is 0 in continuous decoding, so full-stream open-GOP (M577) is unchanged. RADL leading pictures (types 6 / 7, which reference only the CRA and later) are always kept. **Validated on the RTX 3060**: `m587_vulkan_video_h265_cra_tunein` decodes the committed open-GOP clip whole as an oracle, then `reset`s and tunes in at a mid-stream CRA - it drops exactly the CRA's RASL followers (18 of 20 substream pictures emitted, the 2 RASL skipped) and every emitted frame is bit-exact to a full-decode frame. Remaining H.265 gap: long-term references.
- M586: `VulkanVideoDec` reorders B-frames to display order on the streaming (AU-by-AU) system path. Hardware decode retires pictures in coding order; a stream with B-frames displays in a different (POC) order. The whole-stream `decode_all` / GPU-texture path already reorders (M569), but the element's system (NV12) path is fed one access unit per `process` call through the pipelined `decode_push` ring, which stayed in coding order (the re_video adapter reorders by PTS itself, so `decode_push` deliberately does not; the g2g-native element must). The H.264 / H.265 streaming decode now surfaces per-submitted-picture `PictureMeta` (`decode_push_meta`, the POC computed by the decode itself, so no second POC pass), and the element feeds retired frames through a small `ReorderBuffer` keyed by (coded-video-sequence, POC), the same key `reorder_to_display_order` sorts on. It releases the whole previous coded video sequence at each keyframe (POC resets there) and bumps the lowest-POC held frame once a sequence exceeds the DPB depth (a safe reorder-depth bound), so a long GOP does not buffer unbounded; `Eos` / a reconfig boundary drain it in display order, `Flush` (seek) discards it. AV1 stays in coding order (its display order is `show_existing_frame` / `order_hint`, not a monotonic POC; the whole-stream path handles it). **Validated on the RTX 3060**: `m586_vulkan_video_streaming_reorder` feeds committed H.264 / H.265 B-frame clips one AU at a time and asserts the element's emitted NV12 frames match the display-order `decode_all` oracle byte for byte (the fixtures carry a non-monotonic POC, so coding order would differ). Follow-ups: a VUI-derived tighter reorder-depth bound (lower latency than the DPB size), and AV1 / GPU-texture streaming reorder.
- M585: a searchable web element reference (`docs/elements.html`), the browser counterpart of `g2g-inspect`. New structured introspection in `g2g-core`: `Registry::describe(name) -> ElementDoc` and `describe_all()` return the same facts `inspect` renders as text (name, long-name, klass, description, role, output caps or pad templates, and every property with type / default / range / enum / flags) as typed data (`ElementDoc` / `PropertyDoc`), so tooling reads one source of truth. A new `g2g-docgen` binary renders that catalog into a self-contained, dark-theme page: one card per element (role badge, klass, caps / pads, property list) with a client-side search box (filter by name / class / description / property, shareable via `?q=`). Linked from the landing page nav and the capabilities section. Regenerate with `cargo run -p g2g-plugins --features linux-full --bin g2g-docgen`; the listing reflects the build's feature set, exactly like `g2g-inspect`. `PropKind::label()` factored out and shared by the text dump and the structured doc.
- M584: `scriptrouter` multicast + a live appsink-egress demo. `route(frame)` may now return an **array** of ports (`[0, 1]`) to fan one buffer out to several outputs at once, alongside the single-index (or negative = drop) form; negative entries are skipped and duplicates collapsed so a consumer never receives the same buffer twice. Backed by a new public `Frame::share()` in `g2g-core`, the explicit frame-level fan-out primitive (shares the buffer where the memory domain allows, deep-copies owned CPU bytes, Arc-shares metadata copy-on-write); the broadcast tee's `try_clone_packet` now delegates to it (one primitive, no duplicate logic). New `scriptrouter_appsink_egress` example and integration tests exercise the egress seam end to end: a `scriptrouter` splits a stream onto two `appsink` pull channels drained *concurrently with the running pipeline*, so the frames arrive with real live `pull()` timing (a post-run drain would stall the runner at channel capacity, so completing proves concurrent delivery). Added `ScriptRouter::with_script` / `AppSink::with_channel` builders for ergonomic programmatic construction.
- M583: `scriptrouter`, a Rhai-scripted routing demux (`script-rhai`). A 1-to-N `MultiOutputElement` (registered as a demux) whose per-frame `route(frame)` returns the output port each buffer goes to, or a negative number to drop it; control packets broadcast to every branch, the runner broadcasts EOS. The scripted sibling of the built-in `Router`: put an `appsink channel=...` on each output pad and the script routes each buffer, per decision, into a separate consumer your app pulls (the "route buffers to my own pipeline" use case, control plane in Rhai, buffers moved natively). The `route(frame)` handle is read-only (`pts` / `sequence` / `keyframe` / `len` + `frame[i]` byte peek, reusing the `scriptelement` `FrameGuard`), and media-agnostic: audio / video / byte streams route by metadata, System frames also by content. Registered by name, so `scriptrouter name=r r.0 ! ... r.1 ! ...` parses in a launch line or a declarative graph (first in-tree user of the `register_demux` by-name path). Shared script compile/load with `scriptelement` factored into one helper.
- M582: `scriptelement` native bulk ops + an EOS fix. A per-pixel Rhai loop is interpreted (measured ~2.4 s/frame over a 320x240 RGBA buffer, inherent to any embedded scripting engine), so whole-frame `frame[i]` work is the wrong tool. Added native bulk methods a script calls once and Rust loops at speed: `frame.invert()` (~1 ms/frame, ~2300x faster than the loop), `frame.fill(v)`, and `frame.apply_lut(lut)` (a 256-byte lookup table, so brightness / gamma / threshold / invert / posterize are O(256) script work + one native sweep). The script is the control plane, native code the data plane (the NumPy model). Fix: `scriptelement` was re-emitting the EOS sentinel (`other => out.push(other)` swallowed the explicit no-op EOS arm in the M581 refactor), which the runner also forwards, closing the link early and deadlocking any run with more buffers than the link capacity (surfaced as `Shutdown`); it now drops EOS like `identity` / `pyelement`. Also confirmed `script-rhai` (atomics + the guarded pointer) builds for `wasm32-unknown-unknown`, so scripting reaches the browser / embedded targets the pure-Rust core does.
- M581: zero-copy buffer access for `scriptelement`. The script now edits the frame's bytes in place through a `FrameBuf` handle (`frame[i] = 255 - frame[i]`, plus `frame.width` / `.height` / `.format` / `.pts` / `.sequence` / `.len`) instead of being handed a copied-in / copied-out blob, so an inspection or small-region script pays nothing for pixels it does not touch (a full round-trip of an 8 MB buffer measured ~5.5 ms of pure copy). The copy-free path is a custom-type receiver, not a byte blob, because Rhai clones a value argument on entry (measured) while a custom type is passed by reference. Safe by construction: the handle reaches the buffer through an atomic guard (pointer + length) armed for the call and nulled the instant it returns, so it is `Send`/`Sync` with no `unsafe impl` and a handle kept past the call reads / writes nothing (a clean error) rather than dereferencing freed memory (the only `unsafe` is the guarded per-byte deref). Contract change: `process(frame)` no longer returns a blob (edits are in place); an out-of-range index is a script error.
- M580: `scriptelement` (`script-rhai` feature), a raw-video transform whose per-frame `process(frame)` is a Rhai function, the pure-Rust cousin of the `pyelement` CPython host. Same-format passthrough negotiation; the call runs inline (Rhai is synchronous, no GIL) and the compiled engine is `Send` (rhai `sync`) so it works under the multi-thread runner; `System` memory only (a GPU frame yields `UnsupportedDomain`). Registered by name, so `scriptelement script="fn process(f){...}" ! ...` parses in a launch line or a declarative document. (Per-frame buffer access is zero-copy, see M581.)
- M579: Rhai graph-building scripts (`g2g_plugins::script`, `script-rhai` feature). Where a document describes a fixed graph, a script computes one (loops, parameters, conditionals) via a builder API (`add` / `caps` / `set` / `link` / `link_leaky`) that accumulates into the M578 `GraphSpec`, so a script and a document share one builder and one set of role / caps / policy rules. Pure-Rust engine (no C toolchain, reaches wasm / embedded). `g2g-launch --script <file>` runs one.
- M578: declarative graph format (`g2g_plugins::declarative`, `declarative` / `declarative-yaml` features), the structured sibling of the `gst-launch` text parser. A JSON / YAML `nodes` + `edges` document (with a `{ id, caps }` capsfilter shorthand and a top-level `pipeline:` escape hatch to `parse_launch`) builds a runnable `Graph` through the same registry / role-by-link-degree / auto-tee machinery; each property value is typed by the target element's `PropertySpec` and parsed with the same `PropValue::parse` as a launch string, so JSON and a launch line mean the same thing. Both formats deserialize into one shared, format-agnostic `GraphSpec`. `g2g-launch --graph <file>` runs one.
- M577: H.265 open-GOP (CRA / RASL) decode. x265 defaults to `open-gop=1`, so most HEVC in the wild does random access at a CRA (Clean Random Access) picture, followed in decode order by RASL (Random Access Skipped Leading) pictures that display *before* the CRA and reference pictures decoded *before* it. `H265DpbDecoder` used to flush the DPB at every IRAP (IDR / CRA / BLA alike), which is only correct for `NoRaslOutputFlag == 1`; a mid-stream CRA has it 0, so the flush destroyed the pre-CRA references its RASL followers need and those frames decoded against a cleared DPB (garbage) - the M503 / M569 H.265 fixtures dodged it by forcing closed GOPs. The decoder now computes `NoRaslOutputFlag` (H.265 8.1.3: 1 for every IDR / BLA, and for a CRA only when it is the first picture of the decode, tracked by a new `seen_picture` flag) and flushes only then; otherwise, including an open-GOP CRA, it applies the picture's reference-picture set (which for a CRA retains the pre-CRA pictures - H.265 8.3.2), so RASL leading pictures find their references. POC is monotonic across a mid-stream CRA (no reset), so `reorder_to_display_order` (keyframe = IDR) already gives correct display order. New `H265SliceHeader::is_bla` / `is_cra` helpers. **Validated on the RTX 3060** bit-exact vs the ffmpeg software decoder: `m577_vulkan_video_h265_opengop` decodes a committed open-GOP x265 clip (`keyint=12:open-gop=1:bframes=3:b-pyramid=1`, 30 pictures, one leading IDR then two CRA GOPs with RASL leading pictures), every frame at its display index SAD/px 0 for luma and chroma - which only holds if the CRA kept the references its RASL followers use. Scope: full-stream open-GOP decode (a stream led by an IDR / decoded from the start). Mid-stream random-access tune-in at a CRA (discarding its RASL followers, whose pre-CRA references are then absent) is the follow-up, part of the streaming / element seek path.
- M576: semaphore-based present in `VulkanHdrSink`. The M575 present serialised acquire -> blit -> present on the CPU (an acquire fence + a submit fence, both waited mid-present). It now orders that chain with GPU semaphores instead: `acquire_next_image` signals `image_available`, the blit submit waits it (at the transfer stage) and signals a per-swapchain-image `render_finished` (present waits it) plus a single `in_flight` fence. The only CPU wait is `in_flight` at the top of the next `present`, which overlaps the caller's between-frame work (decode / pacing) rather than stalling within a frame; the fence is reset only after a successful acquire so an out-of-date swapchain returns without deadlocking the next wait. One `render_finished` per image (not one global) is the correct reuse discipline: an image is re-acquired only after its present consumed its semaphore. Still one frame in flight (the decode dominates and the demo paces frames), so this is idiomatic-and-stall-free rather than deeply pipelined. Behaviour is unchanged on screen; validated by compile + clippy + the `m575` device-open test; the present loop is exercised live via the example.
- M575: HDR swapchain present (`hdr-present` feature), the final HDR layer. wgpu 29's surface config has no colour-space knob, so `VulkanHdrSink` (new `vulkanhdrsink` module) owns a raw `VK_KHR_swapchain` on the decode device's `VkInstance` (so the decoded texture and the swapchain share one device: present is a zero-copy GPU blit). `open_decode_device` now enables the present-side device extensions - `VK_KHR_swapchain`, and `VK_EXT_hdr_metadata` when the physical device advertises it - conditionally, so a decode-only GPU is unaffected (`VulkanVideoDevice::present_capable()` / `hdr_metadata_supported()` report what was enabled; `VK_EXT_swapchain_colorspace`, the instance extension that unlocks HDR colour spaces, is already enabled by wgpu-hal). The sink creates the surface from a `raw-window-handle` (Wayland / Xlib / Xcb / Win32), negotiates the best colour space the surface offers (`HDR10_ST2084` PQ, else `EXTENDED_SRGB_LINEAR` scRGB, else SDR) preferring a 10-bit / 16-float format, presents the decoder's passthrough `Rgba16Float` texture (PQ-encoded BT.2020, exactly what an HDR10 swapchain wants) by a raw `vkCmdBlitImage` into the acquired image (CPU-synchronised via fences: the decode + convert already completed, so the queue is idle), and attaches BT.2020 mastering metadata via `vkSetHdrMetadataEXT` when available. **Validated**: the surface-format / colour-space selection and `VkHdrMetadataEXT` construction have unit tests (HDR10 10-bit preferred over scRGB over SDR; an 8-bit HDR10 surface rejected; BT.2020 primaries); the decode device opens present-capable on the RTX 3060 (`m575`, decode unregressed); the on-screen HDR present itself is display + compositor dependent and is validated live via `examples/vulkan_video_hdr_on_screen.rs` (a bundled PQ clip). This completes the HDR track: colour matrix (M570) -> 10-bit decode (M571/M572) -> 10-bit GPU texture (M573) -> PQ/HLG tone-map (M574) -> HDR10 present (M575).
- M574: PQ / HLG HDR -> SDR tone-mapping in the GPU-texture converter. The fixed-function `VkSamplerYcbcrConversion` applies the matrix + range but not the transfer function, so an HDR (PQ / HLG, BT.2020) stream came out of the M573 converter as its raw transfer-encoded R'G'B' (too dark / wrong colour on an SDR consumer). `VideoColorSpace` gained a `TransferFunction` (PQ = CICP 16, HLG = 18, else SDR) resolved from the stream's `transfer_characteristics` (already parsed into the H.264 / H.265 SPS and AV1 color_config), and new opt-in constructors `create_h265_dpb_decoder_gpu_tonemap` / `create_av1_dpb_decoder_gpu_tonemap` enable a transfer stage in the `rgba16f` shader (selected by a 4-byte push constant): PQ ST 2084 / HLG B67 EOTF -> BT.2390 EETF display mapping (maxRGB method, source 1000 -> target 100 nits) -> BT.2020 -> BT.709 gamut -> BT.709 OETF, producing display-ready SDR. Opt-in by design: the default GPU path (`create_*_dpb_decoder_gpu`) stays passthrough (matrix + range only, the stream's PQ / HLG encoding preserved in the float target for a future HDR swapchain), so M573 is unchanged and SDR streams are untouched. **Validated on the RTX 3060**: `m574_vulkan_video_hdr_tonemap` decodes committed PQ- and HLG-tagged x265 Main 10 clips through the tone-mapping converter; each `Rgba16Float` texture matches a CPU port of the identical pipeline over the bit-exact system 10-bit decode (worst frame mean abs diff 0.0065 PQ, 0.0092 HLG) and differs from the passthrough output (the transfer stage demonstrably ran); GPU-free unit tests pin the PQ / HLG EOTF and BT.2390 EETF to spec anchor values (PQ code 0.5 = 92 nits, 100 nits = code 0.508, HLG(0.5) = 1/12, EETF endpoints + monotonic + peak compression). Remaining HDR layer: an HDR swapchain present path.
- M573: 10-bit YCbCr -> RGBA GPU-texture path (zero-copy HDR decode, the layer after M571/M572). The GPU-texture converter was hardcoded 8-bit NV12 -> `Rgba8Unorm`, so the zero-copy path rejected 10-bit with `UnsupportedStream` (only the system readback carried it). `YcbcrConverter` now picks its formats from the decode bit depth: an 8-bit frame keeps `G8_B8R8` -> `R8G8B8A8_UNORM` (the `rgba8` shader); a 10-bit (`G10X6`) frame samples through a 10-bit `VkSamplerYcbcrConversion` and stores into an `R16G16B16A16_SFLOAT` image (a new `rgba16f` compute shader), imported as a `Rgba16Float` `wgpu::Texture`. Float was chosen over `Rgba16Unorm` because SFLOAT storage-image writes and `Rgba16Float` sampling are baseline (no extra Vulkan / wgpu feature to gate), it preserves the full 10-bit precision, and it is the natural target for the later PQ / HLG transfer pass. The `build_dpb_core` gpu+10-bit rejection is gone; the shared readback helper (`read_rgba_texture_dq`) sizes its stride from the texture's texel size (4 or 8 bytes); a 10-bit AV1 film-grain frame takes the grain-free GPU convert (the CPU grain synth is 8-bit only, and `apply_film_grain_nv12` already leaves 10-bit grain-free). **Validated on the RTX 3060**: `m573_vulkan_video_10bit_texture` decodes the committed HEVC Main 10 and AV1 10-bit clips to `Rgba16Float` textures; the HEVC textures match a CPU reference built from the bit-exact system 10-bit decode under the stream's BT.2020 matrix + range (worst frame mean abs diff 0.007, far below an 8-bit misread), AV1 is checked loosely (nondeterministic driver). Remaining HDR layers: the PQ / HLG transfer function and an HDR swapchain present path.
- M572: 10-bit AV1 hardware decode, the AV1 sibling of M571. AV1 Main profile covers 8 and 10-bit 4:2:0; the colour config carries the depth. `create_av1_session` / `build_av1_dpb_decoder` now derive it from `color_config.BitDepth` and select the AV1 Main profile at `TYPE_10` plus the `G10X6` output format, reusing the shared bit-depth machinery added in M571 (`av1_profile(bit_depth)`, `planar_420_format`, `format_bytes_per_sample`, `Nv12Frame::bit_depth`). `apply_film_grain_nv12` is guarded to 8-bit (a 10-bit grain stream is left grain-free rather than corrupted; 10-bit grain is a follow-up). **Validated on the RTX 3060** bit-exact vs the dav1d software decoder: `m572_vulkan_video_av1_10bit` decodes a committed libaom AV1 Main 10-bit clip (BT.2020 / PQ tagged), every luma and chroma sample SAD 0 vs a `yuv420p10le` reference. The 10-bit GPU-texture path is still rejected (`UnsupportedStream`); the remaining HDR layers are a 10-bit GPU converter (RGBA16) and the PQ / HLG transfer function.
- M571: 10-bit HEVC (Main 10) hardware decode (HDR precision, layer 2 of the HDR track). The decoder hardcoded 8-bit NV12, so 10-bit / Main 10 streams (what real HDR content is) could not decode. The session now derives its bit depth from the SPS (`bit_depth_luma_minus8`): a 10-bit stream selects the HEVC Main 10 profile (`h265_profile(bit_depth)`) and the `G10X6_B10X6R10X6_2PLANE_420_UNORM_3PACK16` two-plane 4:2:0 output format (`decode_format` prefers it via `planar_420_format`), and the shared `DpbCore` scales its DPB / readback sizing to 2 bytes per sample (`format_bytes_per_sample`). `Nv12Frame` gained a `bit_depth` field; a 10-bit frame carries little-endian 16-bit samples with the value in the top 10 bits (`sample = u16 >> 6`, the G10X6 packing). **Validated on the RTX 3060** bit-exact vs the ffmpeg / libde265 software decoder: `m571_vulkan_video_hevc_10bit` decodes a committed x265 Main 10 clip (BT.2020 / PQ tagged), every luma and chroma sample SAD 0 vs a `yuv420p10le` reference. Scope: HEVC Main 10 on the system NV12 path. The GPU-texture path rejects 10-bit today (`UnsupportedStream`; its `VkSamplerYcbcrConversion` is 8-bit) - a 10-bit converter + RGBA16 output, AV1 10-bit, and the PQ / HLG transfer function are the remaining HDR layers. 8-bit decode is unchanged (all existing fixtures resolve to NV12 8-bit).
- M570: colour-space-aware YUV -> RGB conversion (the HDR foundation). The Vulkan decoders converted every stream with a fixed BT.601 matrix + studio range, so BT.709 (all HD) came out with subtly wrong colours and BT.2020 (HDR) with very wrong ones. The conversion is now driven by the stream's actual colour space: a new `VideoColorSpace` (matrix + range) is resolved from the H.264 / H.265 VUI colour description (a new shared `parse_vui_color`, the layout is identical in both codecs; `parse_h264_sps` / `parse_h265_sps` now read the VUI colour prefix into the SPS) and the AV1 `color_config`, keyed by the CICP `matrix_coefficients` codepoint (unspecified falls back by resolution: >= 720 -> BT.709, else BT.601, the ffmpeg heuristic). Both conversion paths honour it: the CPU `nv12_to_rgba` takes a `VideoColorSpace` (BT.601 / 709 / 2020 luma weights, studio / full range), and the GPU `YcbcrConverter` builds its `VkSamplerYcbcrConversion` with the matching `YCBCR_601/709/2020` model + `ITU_NARROW/FULL` range so the fixed-function hardware does the right matrix. The general matrix formula reproduces the historical BT.601-studio coefficients (`2*(1-Kr)*255/224 = 1.596...`), so a BT.601 stream is byte-identical to before. Scope: matrix + range only; BT.2020 gets the correct matrix but the PQ / HLG transfer function (true HDR tone mapping / passthrough) and 10-bit (P010) decode are later increments. **Validated:** GPU-free unit tests cover the CICP resolution and the conversion math (BT.601 matches the legacy coefficients; 601/709/2020 differ on chroma; studio/full endpoints); `m570_vulkan_video_colorspace` parses the VUI of committed BT.601- and BT.709-tagged clips (CICP matrix 6 / 1) and, on the RTX 3060, decodes both to textures and confirms they reconstruct the same source (mean abs RGB diff 1.5), which only holds if each stream's matrix is honoured.
- M569: H.264 / H.265 B-frame decode with display-order output. B-frames make coding order differ from display (presentation) order: a frame is coded after pictures that precede it on screen. The hardware decode already reconstructs B-frames bit-exact (the driver builds the L0/L1 reference lists from the DPB slots + per-picture POC that `*DpbDecoder` supplies), but the whole-stream `decode_all` / `decode_all_to_textures` emitted frames in coding order, so a B-frame stream came out scrambled. They now index the stream's POCs (`index_pictures`, added to `H265DpbDecoder` to match `H264DpbDecoder`) and reorder the coding-order output into display order via a new `reorder_to_display_order`, keyed by (coded-video-sequence, POC) so POC resets at each keyframe group are handled; for an I/P stream the reorder is the identity (existing tests unchanged). The streaming `decode_push` stays in coding order (a low-latency consumer reorders by PTS). **Validated on the RTX 3060** bit-exact vs the software decoder's display-order output: `m569_vulkan_video_bframe_reorder` decodes committed B-frame clips (libx264 `-bf 2`; libx265 `bframes=2`, closed GOP), every frame at its display index SAD 0 for luma and chroma. Scope: closed-GOP B-frames for both codecs; H.265 open-GOP (CRA / RASL leading pictures) decode remains a separate open track, and streaming/element B-frame reorder is a follow-up.
- M568: AV1 film grain on the GPU-texture decode path. The zero-copy `decode_all_to_textures` path produced the grain-free hardware reconstruction (the RTX 3060 exposes only `DPB_AND_OUTPUT_COINCIDE`, so the driver cannot apply grain, and the ycbcr compute pass has no grain stage). The reorder-aware texture path now applies grain per displayed frame via `DpbCore::grained_slot_to_texture`: the GPU-mode DPB images gained `TRANSFER_SRC`, so a displayed slot is read back to NV12, grain is synthesized on the CPU (`apply_film_grain_nv12`, the same bit-exact path M566 proved on the system output), and the result is uploaded to the RGBA texture (shared `nv12_to_rgba_texture` helper, factored out of `decode_idr_to_rgba_texture`). Grain is output-only, so the read-back leaves the DPB reference untouched; a grain-free displayed frame stays on the zero-copy GPU convert. **Validated on the RTX 3060** bit-exact vs dav1d: `m568_vulkan_video_av1_filmgrain_texture` decodes the committed film-grain clip to textures, and each RGBA readback matches the BT.601 conversion of the grained reference, all 9 frames SAD 0. This finishes the AV1 Vulkan decode depth track (intra + inter, multi-tile, alt-ref/show_existing, film grain on both output paths, loop restoration, CDEF all bit-exact).
- M567: fix Vulkan Video AV1 loop-restoration decode. A libaom `-cpu-used 4` encode enables loop restoration (Wiener / SGR), which decoded wrong (~62 SAD/px, even on intra frames and even planes with `RESTORE_NONE`, because a bad restoration param desyncs the whole frame). `StdVideoAV1LoopRestoration::LoopRestorationSize` is not the restoration unit's pixel size (64/128/256, which the spec's "as defined in 5.9.20" wording implies and which `parse_av1_loop_restoration` was passing) but `1 + lr_unit_shift` for luma and `1 + lr_unit_shift - lr_uv_shift` for chroma (values 1..3) - the encoding ffmpeg's Vulkan AV1 hwaccel passes (confirmed against its `vulkan_av1.c`). Fixed the mapping; **validated on the RTX 3060** bit-exact vs ffmpeg/dav1d (luma AND chroma): `m567_vulkan_video_av1_looprestore` decodes a committed loop-restoration clip, every plane SAD/px 0. New `av1_uses_loop_restoration` introspection. This closes the "advanced inter tool decodes wrong" gap noted under M565 (it was loop restoration, not an inter tool - it reproduces on all-intra frames).
- M566: Vulkan Video AV1 film grain synthesis. AV1 film grain is applied at output time on the grain-free reconstruction; the Vulkan spec has the driver do it into a *distinct* output image (the DPB reference stays grain-free), requiring `DPB_AND_OUTPUT_DISTINCT`, which the RTX 3060 does not expose for AV1 (only `DPB_AND_OUTPUT_COINCIDE`) - so ffmpeg's own Vulkan AV1 decoder produces grain-free output on this hardware too. `Av1DpbDecoder` now synthesizes grain itself on the decoded NV12: `parse_av1_film_grain` reads `film_grain_params()` (spec 5.9.30; an `update_grain == 0` frame's coefficients are resolved from the referenced frame's stored grain), and `apply_film_grain_nv12` runs the full AV1 grain synthesis (spec 7.18.3: the fixed Gaussian sequence, the autoregressive luma/chroma grain templates, the piecewise-linear scaling LUTs, and per-32x32-block application with overlap blending and restricted-range clipping), ported from the re_rav1d scalar reference (the same crate g2g uses for `Rav1dDec`), specialized to 8-bit 4:2:0. A grain stream routes through the synchronous reorder-aware path so grain is applied per displayed frame (directly or via `show_existing_frame`). **Validated on the RTX 3060** bit-exact vs the ffmpeg/dav1d software decoder (which applies grain): `m566_vulkan_video_av1_filmgrain` decodes a committed SVT-AV1 film-grain clip, every frame's luma **and** chroma SAD/px 0. Scope: the system NV12 path is grain-accurate; the GPU-texture path (`decode_all_to_textures`) still emits grain-free textures (grain as a compute pass over the RGBA output, or read-back + CPU synth + re-upload, is a documented follow-up - the GPU-mode DPB slots would need `TRANSFER_SRC` and the converter a wgpu queue).
- M565: Vulkan Video AV1 alt-ref + `show_existing_frame` decode (decode order != display order). Real AV1 streams code invisible alt-ref frames (`show_frame == 0`, decoded and stored but not displayed) and later re-display them via an `OBU_FRAME_HEADER` carrying `show_existing_frame`, which `Av1DpbDecoder` previously rejected (the OBU was dropped by `split_frames`, and a `show_frame == 0` frame would have been emitted at the wrong position). `Av1DpbDecoder` now scans the bitstream into an op list (`scan_ops`) and, when it sees any `show_existing_frame` or non-shown frame, takes a synchronous reorder-aware path: every coded frame is decoded into its DPB slot (reusing the existing synchronous decode-into-slot), only shown frames are emitted, and each `show_existing_frame` emits the referenced stored slot at its display position (with the AV1 key-frame reference refresh when the shown frame is a key frame). Two new `DpbCore` primitives emit an already-decoded idle slot without a decode: `read_slot_nv12` (system NV12 readback) and `convert_slot_unchained` (GPU-texture convert with a null wait semaphore; `YcbcrConverter::convert` now skips the wait when the semaphore is null). Ordinary all-shown streams keep the pipelined ring / chained-texture fast path untouched. **Validated on the RTX 3060** bit-exact vs ffmpeg/dav1d: `m565_vulkan_video_av1_showexisting` decodes a committed libaom clip with 2 alt-ref frames + 1 `show_existing_frame` (17 coded OBUs -> 15 displayed frames), all display frames SAD/px 0. (A separate, pre-existing limitation surfaced while testing: a very-high-quality `-cpu-used 4` libaom encode uses an advanced inter tool that decodes wrong; CDEF / loop-restoration / alt-ref / show_existing all decode bit-exact.)
- M564: Vulkan Video AV1 multi-tile decode. The `Av1DpbDecoder` previously rejected any frame with more than one tile; real AV1 streams split each frame into a tile grid for parallel decode. A new `av1_tile_layout` parses an `OBU_FRAME`'s `tile_group_obu` header (the optional `tile_start_and_end_present_flag` + `tg_start`/`tg_end`, then `byte_alignment()`) and the per-tile `le(TileSizeBytes)` size prefixes into the driver's `pTileOffsets` / `pTileSizes` arrays (which already flowed through `submit_decode_av1`), so a tiled frame decodes; a single-tile frame yields one entry pointing just past the header, unchanged from before. Every length read from the stream is bounds-checked (untrusted input): a malformed prefix or an out-of-range tile fails the parse rather than reading past the payload. The tile geometry (`TileCols`/`TileRows`/`context_update_tile_id`/`MiColStarts`...) was already mapped into `StdVideoAV1TileInfo` by `to_std_av1_picture_info`. New `av1_frame_tile_grid` introspection returns the first frame's `(tile_cols, tile_rows)`. **Validated on the RTX 3060** bit-exact vs the ffmpeg (dav1d) software decoder: `m564_vulkan_video_av1_multitile` decodes a committed 2x2-tile (4 tiles/frame) libaom fixture, all 11 frames SAD/px 0; a 4x4 (16-tile) clip was also verified out of band. Remaining AV1 depth: film grain and `show_existing_frame`.
- M563: MPEG-4 Part 2 (Visual, ISO/IEC 14496-2, the DivX/Xvid family) software decode via libavcodec. Adds `VideoCodec::Mpeg4Part2` (wire tag 6, media type `video/mpeg`) and its `Id::MPEG4` mapping to `FfmpegVideoDec`'s supported set, so a decode chain reaches raw frames; no hardware path (extinct on modern GPUs). The MP4 demuxer (`mp4demux`/`fmp4` shared core) detects the `mp4v` visual sample entry, confirms the esds objectTypeIndication is `0x20` (a new `parse_esds_video` helper returns the objectTypeIndication + DecoderSpecificInfo, reusing the descriptor walk `parse_esds` already does for AAC), and carries the VOL header as the config. Unlike H.264/H.265, `mp4v` samples are raw elementary stream (their own 3-byte start codes), not AVCC length-prefixed, so `parse_progressive`/`SampleFraming` pass them through instead of de-framing, and a shared `prepend_param_sets` (factored out of the two demuxers) prepends the VOL verbatim rather than injecting a 4-byte start code. MPEG-TS ingest gains stream_type `0x10` (`tsdemux`), and `au_is_keyframe` learns the MPEG-4 I-VOP (VOP start code `0xB6`, coding type 0) for the seek path. No parser element (the demuxer frame-aligns and libavcodec self-parses). Validated end to end: `m563_mpeg4part2` demuxes a committed `mp4v` fixture and decodes it to 640x480 I420 through the real elements; container/esds/framing/wire/TS covered by CI-safe unit tests.

## 0.2.0 - 2026-07-06

First tagged release. Closes the 1.0 extensibility gate (`#[non_exhaustive]` vocabulary,
M561) and publishes the stability policy (`STABILITY.md`). Contains all milestone work to
date; `g2g-core`'s execution surface is de-facto frozen and treated as Tier 1.

- M562: zero-stall external-semaphore sync for the GPU dma-buf egress path - the deferred M560 follow-up. `WgpuToDmaBuf::with_external_semaphore(true)` (default off) drops the producer-side `device.poll(Wait)` that blocked on each GPU copy before export: instead the element creates one exportable `VK_KHR_external_semaphore_fd` *timeline* semaphore per stream, signals the next value on each copy submit via `wgpu_hal::vulkan::Queue::add_signal_semaphore` (wgpu 29 exposes signal-semaphore injection), and attaches the semaphore fd + value to the emitted dma-buf through a new optional `SyncFd` + value slot on `g2g-core`'s `OwnedDmaBuf`. `DmaBufSink` ships the semaphore fd once (a `TAG_SYNC` `SCM_RIGHTS` record) ahead of the first synced frame and tags each frame record with its timeline value; `DmaBufSrc` re-shares the one semaphore across the frames it reconstructs; `DmaBufToWgpu` imports it once and, before handing the buffer downstream, waits for each frame's value by polling the timeline counter (`vkGetSemaphoreCounterValue`) and yielding cooperatively (`tokio::task::yield_now`) between polls, rather than a blocking `vkWaitSemaphores` that would stall the whole runtime (and sibling tasks, e.g. the source pulling the next frame) while the copy is in flight - the common case (copy already done by the time the fd crossed the socket) passes on the first poll. So the wait moves from the producer to the consumer, off the runtime's hot path, and the producer pipelines ahead. A *timeline* semaphore (not a per-frame binary one) keeps the fd single (no multi-fd ancillary passing needed) and the wait a plain host wait; the producer reclaims its exportable copy buffers lazily once the timeline counter passes their value (`vkGetSemaphoreCounterValue`, non-blocking), so it never stalls yet never frees a buffer whose copy is still in flight. wgpu-hal 29 exposes signal- but no wait-semaphore injection, so the consumer wait is a CPU-side cooperative poll rather than a GPU-queue wait (documented); it still removes the producer stall and does not block the runtime. Validated on the RTX 3060: `dmabuf_timeline_probe` (cross-device timeline signal + host wait primitive), `m562_dmabuf_semaphore_sync` (4-frame in-process handoff across two devices, byte-exact, producer never polls), and `gpu_dmabuf_ipc` with `G2G_DMABUF_SEM=1` (full cross-process chain). CI-excluded like the rest of the GPU stack. DESIGN.md §4.21.
- M561: mark the growth-prone public vocabulary enums `#[non_exhaustive]` (`Caps`, `RawVideoFormat`, `AudioFormat`, `VideoCodec`, `ByteStreamEncoding`, `TextFormat`, `TensorDType`, `TensorLayout`, `MemoryDomain`/`MemoryDomainKind`, `G2gError`, `HardwareError`, `PipelinePacket`, `PropKind`, `PropValue`), so adding a variant stops being a breaking change for downstream `match`es - the pivotal 1.0 extensibility gate (STABILITY.md). ~100 match sites across every feature and platform target (default, linux-full, the CI linux/windows/macos/android feature sets, the CUDA/wgpu/dma-buf GPU stack, g2g-ml, g2g-python, g2g-enterprise, tests) gain a wildcard arm: pass-through transforms forward unknown ordered control packets downstream unchanged, terminal sinks no-op, and format/codec namers mirror their existing fallback (error / `None` / unreachable). The deliberately-closed enums (`ConfigureOutcome`, `PadDir`/`PadDirection`, `ClockPriority`, `LinkPolicy`, `SeekType`) are annotated as intentionally exhaustive. Verified: default `cargo test --workspace` + clippy `--all-targets`, `linux-full`, the exact CI linux feature set + `g2g-ml wgpu,burn`, the GPU feature stack (RTX 3060), and Android cross-compile (`mediacodec`/`aaudio`/`camera2`) all green; Windows/macOS arms added by static analysis (checked by their per-platform CI).
- M560: `WgpuToDmaBuf` follow-ups - NV12 export, the full cross-process GPU-egress chain as one example, and external-semaphore de-risking. (1) **NV12/planar export**: `WgpuToDmaBuf` now exports 8-bit NV12 as well as packed RGBA/BGRA. The frame byte size and row stride come from new shared `dmabuf_frame_bytes` / `dmabuf_row_stride` helpers in `dmabufwgpu` that both the export and the `DmaBufToWgpu` import use, so they always agree; this also *fixed* the importer, which computed `stride*height` and thus imported only the luma plane of a planar frame (now `stride*height` + the half-height chroma region). Round trip validated on the RTX 3060 for both RGBA (256 B) and NV12 (96 B, plane-aware), byte-exact (`m559_wgpu_dmabuf_export` gains an NV12 case). (2) **Full chain example** `gpu_dmabuf_ipc` (needs `dmabuf-wgpu,local-dmabuf`): `WgpuToDmaBuf -> DmaBufSink -> [child process] -> DmaBufSrc -> DmaBufToWgpu`, a GPU-resident frame leaving one process and landing GPU-resident in another with only a dma-buf fd crossing (SCM_RIGHTS), no CPU copy either side. Validated on the 3060 (4 frames re-imported GPU-resident in the child, every pixel verified) - which also confirms **cross-process** dma-buf export+import works on this NVIDIA driver, and that the composed lifetime story holds (export frees its Vulkan handles at once; the sink's fd send keeps the buffer alive via the receiver's dup). (3) **External-semaphore sync**: the current cross-device sync is the producer-side `device.poll(Wait)` (correct, small stall). The zero-stall `VK_KHR_external_semaphore_fd` alternative is validated as a *primitive* on this driver (`dmabuf_semaphore_probe` exports a semaphore fd from one device and imports it on another); wiring that fd through the transport alongside the dma-buf + injecting the consumer-side queue wait is the remaining integration (it needs a sync-fd slot in the frame/transport and an importer-injected wait, a cross-cutting change beyond a poll-Wait swap). DESIGN.md §4.21.
- M559: GPU -> DMABUF export element (`WgpuToDmaBuf`, `dmabuf-wgpu`) - the producer half that pairs with the `DmaBufToWgpu` importer, closing the M557 follow-up. Consumes a GPU-resident `MemoryDomain::WgpuBuffer` and emits a `MemoryDomain::DmaBuf` referencing the same pixels, so a rendered/decoded GPU frame leaves the process with no CPU copy (feed the output to `DmaBufSink`). A wgpu-allocated buffer is not itself exportable (wgpu requests no external-memory flags), so the element allocates its own Vulkan buffer backed by `VkExportMemoryAllocateInfo` (dma-buf handle type), copies the input into it on the GPU (`copy_buffer_to_buffer`), and exports the backing memory as a dma-buf fd via `vkGetMemoryFdKHR`. Key lifetime point: the exported fd is an *independent* reference to the underlying buffer (dma-buf refcounting), so the element frees its own Vulkan handles immediately after export and the fd keeps the memory alive (and, once `DmaBufSink` sends it, the receiver's `SCM_RIGHTS` dup does) - validated, not assumed. Input and exportable buffer must share one `wgpu::Device` for the copy, so a producer feeds this element on its device (`gpu()` / `wrap_buffer` accessors). The element waits for the copy (`device.poll(Wait)`) before exporting so a consumer sees complete pixels (a shared `VK_KHR_external_semaphore` hand-off is a follow-up). Registered as `wgputodmabuf`; `DmaBufToWgpu` gains `device()`/`queue()` accessors so an imported buffer can be read back. **Validated on the RTX 3060** (`m559_wgpu_dmabuf_export`): a buffer exported to a dma-buf and re-imported by `DmaBufToWgpu` on a *separate* wgpu device reads back byte-exact - which also confirms Vulkan dma-buf export+import both work on this NVIDIA proprietary driver (a `dmabuf_export_probe` test isolates the export-capability check). Packed RGBA/BGRA only for now (planar/NV12 export is a follow-up). DESIGN.md §4.21.
- M558: reconnection for the distributed-graph transports - make a cut edge resilient across process/machine restarts, on both the TCP (`remote`) and WebSocket (`remote-ws`) pairs. `RemoteSink`/`RemoteWsSink` gain `with_reconnect(attempts)` (and a `reconnect-attempts` property, default 0 = off): when enabled the initial connect is *deferred* and retried with a short backoff (so a downstream node that is not up yet is tolerated, not a hard error at configure time), and a mid-stream send failure drops the dead socket, reconnects, and re-sends the current caps (the far side needs a leading `CapsChanged` on each new connection) before retrying the packet - all bounded by the attempt budget. Symmetrically, `RemoteSrc`/`RemoteWsSrc` gain `with_reconnect()` (a `keep-listening` property): a client that drops *without* a clean `Eos` no longer ends the stream; the source keeps its listener open, accepts a replacement client (re-reading its leading caps and forwarding them downstream so a re-negotiation happens if they changed), and continues - only an explicit `Eos` (or a frame limit) ends a keep-listening source. The send path is refactored into one `deliver` helper (connect if needed -> caps if changed -> packet, retried as a unit) shared shape across the TCP and WS sinks; the default (no-reconnect) behavior is unchanged (a failure still ends the pipeline, and the existing loopback tests stay green). Validated over loopback both ways: `m558_remote_reconnect` proves a TCP sink retries the connect until a late-binding server appears *and* a keep-listening source stitches a 5-frame stream across a sender that drops after 2 frames and is replaced; `m558_remote_ws_reconnect` proves the WebSocket sink retries the handshake until the server is up. DESIGN.md §4.20.
- M557: vendor-neutral DMABUF local transport - the GPU-agnostic complement to M556's CUDA path. Where a CUDA IPC handle is plain bytes (rides any transport), a dma-buf is a *file descriptor*, so it cannot cross a byte transport; it must be passed as `SCM_RIGHTS` ancillary data of a `sendmsg` over a Unix socket, which makes the kernel install a dup of the fd in the receiver. New `local-dmabuf` feature (Linux, no GPU dep) adds `scmfd` (hand-rolled `sendmsg`/`recvmsg` FFI for single-fd passing, no `libc`/`nix` crate; LP64 struct layouts asserted at compile time) and the `DmaBufSink`/`DmaBufSrc` element pair, the vendor-neutral analog of `LocalCudaSink`/`LocalCudaSrc`: they carry a `MemoryDomain::DmaBuf` frame to a same-machine peer, passing the frame's dma-buf fd plus a small fixed-size descriptor (format + geometry + timing). This is both simpler and safer than the CUDA path: the underlying buffer is kernel-refcounted across both processes' fds, so once the sink's `sendmsg` returns the receiver's dup already keeps the buffer alive - the sink drops its frame immediately with **no per-frame ack** (backpressure still comes from the graph's bounded channel). Every message is one fixed-size record sent/received with a single `sendmsg`/`recvmsg`, so a frame's fd is never separated from its bytes and a plain read never crosses (discarding) a pending fd. GPU-agnostic: the transport moves *any* dma-buf (GPU texture, V4L2/CSI capture, `dma_heap`/`udmabuf`); pair with `dmabuf-wgpu` (`DmaBufToWgpu`) on the receive side to import into a wgpu buffer. The `local_dmabuf_transport` example validates the whole path cross-process (self-re-exec) with a genuine `udmabuf` - a CPU-mappable dma-buf built from a sealed memfd - so it needs no GPU driver: 5 frames crossed a process boundary via fd passing and the child mmap-verified every byte. The record serde is unit-tested (runs in CI); the cross-process path is validated locally (needs `/dev/udmabuf`, CI-excluded). `raw_format_to_u8`/`raw_format_from_u8` are now `pub` in `g2g-core::wire` so the transport reuses the one canonical format numbering. `DmaBufSink`/`DmaBufSrc` are registered (`dmabufsink`/`dmabufsrc`) with a `location` (socket path) property for `gst-inspect` / `parse_launch` parity. Follow-up: a `WgpuToDmaBuf` export element (the GPU producer that pairs with `DmaBufToWgpu` across the boundary). DESIGN.md §4.21.
