- M556: local zero-copy IPC over CUDA IPC handles - share VRAM across processes with no device<->host round trip. The wire codec and its transports (`remote`, `remote-ws`) only carry CPU bytes, so a GPU producer feeding a GPU consumer in another process would pay a full device->host->device copy to cross. On the same machine that copy is avoidable: two processes can map the *same* allocation. New `local-ipc` feature (implies `cuda`; Linux + NVIDIA, CI-excluded like the rest of the CUDA stack) adds `localipc`: `ipc_export` turns a `CUdeviceptr` into a 64-byte `CudaIpcHandle` (`cuIpcGetMemHandle`) that another process passes to `ipc_open` (`cuIpcOpenMemHandle`) to read the same VRAM, no copy. Key design point: the handle is *plain bytes* (unlike a DMABUF fd, which needs `SCM_RIGHTS` fd-passing), so a `CudaIpcDescriptor` (handle + size) serializes to a flat buffer that rides any transport, the only constraints being same machine + same GPU and the export-outlives-open lifetime. The `cuda_ipc_smoke` example validates the whole path cross-process on real hardware (self-re-exec: parent fills a device allocation and exports the handle, child in a separate process with its own context maps and reads it back byte-for-byte) - proven on an RTX 3060, 3.1 MB of VRAM shared with only the 64-byte handle crossing. Descriptor serde is unit-tested (GPU-free, runs in CI). Phase 2 adds the graph elements `LocalCudaSink`/`LocalCudaSrc` (the GPU-resident analog of `RemoteSink`/`RemoteSrc`): the sink exports a frame's allocation and sends a descriptor (handle + NV12 plane offsets/pitches/dims + timing) over a Unix socket, the source maps it and takes one on-GPU `cuMemcpyDtoD` copy (still no PCIe) into its own buffer then acks, and the sink holds the source frame only until that ack (one frame in flight), so the two processes' lifetimes decouple cleanly without depending on the runner's frame-drop timing. The `local_cuda_transport` example validates the full element path cross-process on an RTX 3060 (NV12 frames verified pixel-exact in the receiving process). Phase 3 adds `LocalCudaSrc::zero_copy()`: the source emits the producer's *mapped* VRAM directly (no receive-side copy at all; the consumer reads the producer's memory in place, e.g. NVENC-from-mapped). This brings back the lifetime handshake copy mode traded away - the emitted frame's keep-alive closes the IPC mapping and signals the run loop on drop, and the source acks the producer only once that fires (frame fully consumed downstream), so the producer holds the source exactly that long (real backpressure, one frame in flight). Opt-in, since copy mode decouples the two pipelines for a slow / fan-out consumer while `zero_copy()` suits a prompt single-in-flight consumer; both are validated cross-process on the 3060 (`G2G_ZEROCOPY=1`). NVDEC pool frames (planes are a sub-allocation of a larger pool, so `luma_ptr` is not the allocation base) are now handled: the sink resolves the enclosing allocation with `cuMemGetAddressRange` and carries each plane's offset within it, the receiver bounds-checks the offsets and copies the two planes into a tight destination (a pool frame's planes need not be contiguous), so nothing assumes `luma_ptr` is the base (both modes re-validated pixel-exact on the 3060). The vendor-neutral DMABUF-over-Unix-socket (`SCM_RIGHTS`) counterpart is M557. `LocalCudaSink`/`LocalCudaSrc` are now registered (`localcudasink`/`localcudasrc`) with a `location` (socket path) property, for `gst-inspect` / `parse_launch` parity. DESIGN.md §4.21.
- M555: remote-transform primitive - finish the M549 collapse, retire the bespoke shim. Where M554's `RemoteWsSink`/`RemoteWsSrc` cut an edge one-way (the whole downstream subgraph runs remotely), `RemoteWsTransform` (native, tokio-tungstenite client) + `WsWireTransform` (browser wasm twin, `web`) offload a single *middle* stage: they ship each input packet to a remote peer over one WebSocket and emit the processed packet it returns, keeping the graph shape (needed when the stages around the offloaded one, decode + overlay + canvas, must stay in the browser). Caps are identity (the remote stage may attach `metadata`, e.g. `AnalyticsMeta` detections, which crosses in band); the protocol is strictly FIFO (leading `CapsChanged` config with no reply, then one `DataFrame` per frame with one processed reply each, then `Eos`; `Segment`/`Flush` pass through locally), so each per-frame read pairs with its frame. `g2g-web`'s `run_websocket_remotedetect_to_canvas` now uses the generic, detection-agnostic `WsWireTransform` in place of the deleted `WebRemoteDetect`; the demo `detect-server` is rewritten to speak the wire codec (read frame, run the real `OrtInference -> DetectionPostprocess` chain, attach `AnalyticsMeta`, send the frame back) instead of its bespoke binary-request / JSON-response protocol; `WebRemoteDetect` + `remote-shim.js` are removed. So the browser graph `decode -> WsWireTransform -> overlay -> canvas` moves inference to a native peer by swapping one generic element - the browser knows nothing about detection. Native `remote_ws_transform.rs` proves the round trip end to end (a test server inverts each frame's bytes; the pipeline emits the inverted frames in order). Shared `remotewsio` helpers (`send_wire`/`recv_wire`) now back all the native `remote-ws` elements (M554's sink/src refactored onto them). Bandwidth tradeoff vs the bespoke shim (whole frame round-trips both ways) is documented; a `metadata`-only return is a future optimization. DESIGN.md §4.20.
- M554: distributed-graph primitive over WebSocket - the transport that lets a browser join the primitive. New `g2g-plugins` `remote-ws` feature adds `RemoteWsSink` (WebSocket client) + `RemoteWsSrc` (WebSocket server), the WebSocket siblings of the M551 TCP pair: they carry the identical `g2g-core` wire-codec `PipelinePacket` stream, one packet per binary WebSocket message (WebSocket is already message-framed, so no `u32` length prefix), over `tokio-tungstenite` (0.24, matching the detect-server demo so one tungstenite version resolves). Same protocol (caps as the first message, discovered by the server like `RtspSrc`); the only difference from TCP is the async handshake, so the sink connects on its first `process`. New browser element `WsWireSink` (`web`) is the wasm send half: it wraps the browser `WebSocket` around the *same* `encode_packet` (the wire codec already compiled on `wasm32`), so a browser graph `WebSocketSrc -> WebCodecsDecode -> WsWireSink` ships decoded frames to a native `RemoteWsSrc -> ...` tail; `g2g-web` gains `run_websocket_decode_offload_to_wire(url, wire_url)`. This generalizes the bespoke M549 `WebRemoteDetect` shim (a hand-rolled RGBA-over-WebSocket protocol that knew about detection) into the media-agnostic edge cut - the browser element no longer knows anything about the tail it feeds. `remote_ws_loopback.rs` proves a split graph carries caps + N frames byte-identical + `Eos` over a real WebSocket; the `map_wire` wire-error helper is factored into a shared `remotewire` module the TCP pair, WebSocket pair, and `WsWireSink` all use. DESIGN.md §4.20.
- M552/M553: Vulkan Video zero-copy hardening - close the codec test-parity gaps in the re_video adapter, on the RTX 3060. `m552_revideo_texture_codecs` drives the Tier-B GPU-texture path (`VulkanStreamDecoder::new_gpu` / `submit_chunk_texture`) for H.265 and AV1, the sibling of m512's H.264: each coded picture comes back as a GPU-resident RGBA `wgpu::Texture` with no CPU readback. H.265 is anchored strictly to the bit-exact CPU I420 path under the compute pass's fixed BT.601 matrix (mean channel diff < 3/frame); AV1 is anchored loosely (this driver's AV1 decode is run-to-run nondeterministic). `m553_vulkan_video_h265_pipelined` guards the pipelined streaming ring (`submit_chunk_push` + `flush`) for H.265, the sibling of m539's H.264: per-picture push without draining the ring decodes bit-exactly against the whole-clip golden. These adapter paths existed since M517 but had only ever executed for H.264. No source change (test-only); the shared `DpbCore` ring and per-codec decode paths were already correct.
- M551: distributed-graph primitive - cut any graph edge and run the downstream subgraph in another process / on another machine by swapping one element. New `g2g-core` `wire` codec (`encode_packet` / `decode_packet`, `no_std + alloc`, no deps) serializes an entire `PipelinePacket` to a versioned little-endian byte buffer and back: every variant, every `Caps` shape, frame timing / sequence, and (with `metadata`) the `AnalyticsMeta` graph + `BlobMeta` side-data in band; only CPU memory crosses (`System` verbatim, `SystemView` materialized, device domains rejected as `WireError::UnsupportedDomain`). New `g2g-plugins` `remote` feature adds the `RemoteSink` (TCP client, `AcceptsAny`, forwards the whole packet stream length-framed, emits the negotiated caps first) + `RemoteSrc` (TCP listener, discovers caps from the first wire packet like `RtspSrc`, re-emits the stream downstream) pair, both registered for `parse_launch` / `gst-inspect`. Round-trip unit tests per packet variant (incl. metadata) in `wire.rs`; `remote_loopback.rs` proves a split graph carries caps + N frames byte-identical + `Eos` over loopback. The general form of the M549 browser-to-server offload; DESIGN.md §4.20.
- M550: portability showcase - proof that one graph runs across MCU / RTOS / CPU / GPU / WASM. New workspace-excluded `examples/portability-core` holds the detection-overlay processing stages (a `SyntheticDetect` element + `AnalyticsOverlay`) behind a single `overlay_stages()` definition, built from portable g2g elements. Both the new native runner `examples/portability-native` (`VideoTestSrc -> overlay_stages() -> FileSink`) and the browser build `g2g-web` (`WebSocketSrc -> WebCodecsDecode -> overlay_stages() -> CanvasSink`) construct their middle-of-graph from that exact function - the same `SyntheticDetect` / `AnalyticsOverlay` / `run_linear_chain`, compiled once native and once for wasm32; only the source and sink differ. (`g2g-web`'s local `WebDetect` is retired in favour of the shared `SyntheticDetect`; the returned type is a struct of concrete elements, not `Vec<Box<dyn ..>>`, so each `&mut` unsizes with a free object lifetime, which a boxed `dyn + 'static` can't under `&mut` invariance.) New `PORTABILITY.md` is the proof matrix with reproducible evidence per target, all gathered this session: **MCU** ~1.4 KB of g2g `.text` on `thumbv7em` (`examples/g2g-size`; the exercised `g2g_min` slice is 916 B); **RTOS** `m43_embassy` passes (Embassy executor + `embassy-sync`); **CPU** the native runner renders a 640x480 frame with the box drawn; **GPU** `wgpu_preprocess` 4/4 on the RTX 3060 (NV12 -> f32 NCHW tensor, GPU-resident) plus the validated zero-copy Vulkan Video -> `wgpu::Texture` path; **WASM** the same `overlay_stages()` draws the box over decoded video in a real headless-Chromium browser. README and the landing page link the proof.
- M549: server-side detection with a thin browser client (Architecture B) - the differentiated wedge: the SAME graph, inference moved off the browser without a rewrite. New browser element `WebRemoteDetect` (g2g-web) is a drop-in swap for `WebOrtDetect`: the graph stays `decode -> detect -> overlay -> canvas`, but instead of running the model locally it ships each decoded RGBA frame to a native detection server over a WebSocket and reattaches the returned boxes as `AnalyticsMeta`. The client is thin (no model, no postprocess: just transport + RGBA framing; a small `remote-shim.js` owns the socket + request/response, mirroring `ort-shim.js`). New `tools/wasm-demo/detect-server` (workspace-excluded, like the other demo servers) runs the REAL native g2g detection chain - `g2g-ml` `OrtInference` -> native ONNX Runtime -> `DetectionPostprocess`, the exact chain `yolo_detect.rs` / the `detect_overlay` example use - over a tiny binary request / JSON response protocol. `g2g-web` gains `run_websocket_remotedetect_to_canvas(url, canvas_id, detect_url)` and the demo a "Detect (server-side / remote)" mode. **Validated** in a real (headless-Chromium) browser against the running server: 230 frames offloaded at the full ~15 fps stream rate (vs ~3.4 fps for in-browser ort-web CPU-wasm), the server confirming 640x640 -> 5 detections (person + bus) per frame, boxes rendered identically to Architecture A (same detections, computed server-side). Demonstrates the one-typed-pipeline thesis: the detect stage runs in the browser (M548, ort-web) or on an edge/server node (here, native ORT) by swapping one element; the rest of the graph is unchanged.
- M548: real in-browser YOLOv8 object detection (Architecture A, Stage 2) - a real ONNX model detecting in the browser, end-to-end validated. New `WebOrtDetect` (in `g2g-web`) is the drop-in replacement for Stage 1's synthetic `WebDetect`: an RGBA identity transform that (1) preprocesses the decoded frame to a `[1,3,640,640]` NCHW f32 tensor (RGB, `/255`, whole-to-whole resize so boxes map straight onto the display frame), (2) runs a real YOLOv8n via ONNX Runtime Web (a small `ort-shim.js` owns only `session.run`; onnxruntime-web is loaded lazily from the CDN, single-threaded, so NO SharedArrayBuffer / cross-origin isolation), and (3) decodes the `[1,84,8400]` output through the SAME `g2g-ml` `DetectionPostprocess` the native chain uses, attaching `AnalyticsMeta` for `AnalyticsOverlay` + `CanvasSink`. The g2g half stays Rust; only the ONNX session crosses to JS. `g2g-web` gains `run_websocket_ortdetect_to_canvas(url, canvas_id, model_url)` and the demo a "Detect (real YOLOv8 / ort-web)" mode; `tools/wasm-demo/get-detection-assets.sh` fetches the model + builds a `bus_640.h264` sample clip (git-ignored). **Validated** in a real (headless-Chromium) browser on the classic bus.jpg clip: 70+ live CPU-wasm inferences, each yielding exactly 5 detections of classes {0 person, 5 bus} (4 people + 1 bus), boxes rendered correctly over the decoded video (screenshot-confirmed). Also fixes a real `WebCodecsDecode` bug this surfaced: it announced `display_width`/`display_height`, which apply the stream's sample-aspect-ratio and diverge from the copied RGBA buffer for non-square pixels (a stretched/anamorphic source), causing a `CapsMismatch` at the sink; now it announces the `visible_rect` dims that match `copyTo` (also correct for the coded-padding case the M543 fix targeted). Adds the `web-sys/DomRectReadOnly` binding. The differentiated target remains Architecture B (server-side inference, thin client); A proves one typed graph runs the detector native + browser.
- M547: in-browser object-detection chain (Architecture A, Stage 1) - the g2g detection half validated end to end in the browser, before a real model. New `WebDetect` (in the `g2g-web` wasm leaf, which reuses `g2g-ml`'s `DetectionPostprocess` - `g2g-plugins` can't, that would cycle) is an RGBA identity transform that attaches an `AnalyticsMeta`: it builds a tiny YOLOv8-shaped `[1,4+C,A]` output tensor with a planted box and decodes it through the *real* `DetectionPostprocess::detect` (new pub method = `nms(decode(..))`, the reusable core of `process`), so Stage 2 swaps only the synthetic tensor for an `ort-web` `session.run` output. The chain `WebSocketSrc -> WebCodecsDecode -> WebDetect -> AnalyticsOverlay -> CanvasSink` runs via `run_linear_chain` (cooperative on the single browser thread, no worker), reusing the CPU box-draw overlay and 2D canvas sink unchanged. `g2g-web` enables g2g-plugins' `analytics` feature, gains `run_websocket_detect_to_canvas`, and the demo a "Detect (boxes overlay)" mode. **Validated** in a real (headless-Chromium, WebCodecs) browser: on the 640x480 fixture the box border corners are the exact class-0 palette red where the plain 2d path shows decoded video, the box interior stays video (border-only draw), and ~perimeter red pixels are added - the decode -> detect -> overlay -> present half is proven before ort-web lands.
- M546: real 2-layer CNN head for the browser GPU-inference path. `WebGpuCanvasSink::with_cnn()` runs a genuine convolutional network (conv3x3 -> ReLU -> conv3x3 -> ReLU) over each decoded frame, zero-copy from the GPU external texture: one fragment gathers a 5x5 luma neighbourhood and evaluates both layers with no intermediate texture; the texel step comes from `dpdx`/`dpdy` of the interpolated uv (the canvas is sized to the frame), so it needs no dimensions uniform and reuses the existing pipeline. Layer 1's filters are the Sobel x/y edge detectors (the features a trained first conv layer learns); the shader is weight- and depth-agnostic, so trained weights / more layers drop straight in. `g2g-web` gains `run_websocket_to_webgpu_cnn` and the demo a "WebGPU CNN (conv net)" mode. **Validated** in a real browser: on the SMPTE fixture the net emits a clean edge-feature map (the circle outline, bar boundaries, and counter digit traced; ~3% bright edge pixels, dark flats), confirming the conv forward pass runs correctly on the decoded video. A step up from M545's nearest-centroid head toward a full model.
- M545: browser GPU inference (the zero-copy WebGPU-ML wedge). `WebGpuCanvasSink::with_inference()` runs a per-pixel nearest-centroid classifier (argmin over K colour-class centroids, a real prototype-classifier head) directly over the decoded frame's `GPUExternalTexture` in a WGSL fragment stage, no CPU readback, presenting the class map: the browser analog of the native decode -> GPU-compute -> result path, and where a full CNN/ONNX head slots in. `g2g-web` gains `run_websocket_to_webgpu_inference` and the demo a "WebGPU inference (classify)" mode. **Validated** in a real browser: on the SMPTE bar fixture the seven bars classify to the exact eight class-index grey levels (`class/(K-1)`, i.e. {0,36,73,109,146,182,219,255}), confirming the classifier runs correctly on the decoded video. Note: output is visualized to the canvas because this host's WebGPU cannot read a storage buffer back to the CPU (`mapAsync` hangs; canvas present works) - a local Dawn/Vulkan driver quirk, not a code limit; tensor-to-CPU output works on conformant WebGPU.
- M544: real camera capture for the browser egress pipeline. New `WebCameraSrc` (g2g-plugins, `web-codecs`) opens a webcam via `getUserMedia`, reads the track's frames through a `MediaStreamTrackProcessor` (`ReadableStream<VideoFrame>`), and copies each out to RGBA `System` (sharing `WebCodecsDecode`'s `copy_out_rgba`) so it flows straight into `WebCodecsEncode`, i.e. the real "capture" side that replaces the synthetic `PatternSrc` (`WebCameraSrc -> WebCodecsEncode -> WebSocketSink`). Requested resolution is the advertised source caps, framerate a fixable placeholder (not `Rate::Any`, which `fixate()` rejects); real dims land mid-stream via `CapsChanged`. `g2g-web` gains `run_camera_encode_to_websocket(url, width, height, frames)` and the demo a **Send camera** button. Adds the mediacapture-transform web-sys bindings. **Validated** end-to-end in a real browser with a fake device (`--use-fake-device-for-media-stream`): the captured stream saves to a playable 640x480 60-frame `received.h264` (ffprobe-confirmed; the decode shows Chrome's fake-camera pattern). Needs camera permission + a secure context; not headless-testable without a fake device.
- M543: make the browser pipeline actually run end-to-end (M540-542 compiled + CI-green but had never been driven in a browser; all three paths failed at startup). Four fixes, validated via a headless-Chromium (real WebCodecs + 3060) harness: (1) ingest caps advertised `Dim::Any`, which `fixate()` rejects, so receive negotiation returned `CapsMismatch`; now a wide placeholder `Range` (fixates to 0x0, decoder derives real dims from the in-band SPS mid-stream), mirroring `RtspSrc`. (2) `WebCodecsEncode` / `WebCodecsDecode` rejected the `CapsChanged` the runner's transform arm feeds them (their *derived output* caps), hanging encode/decode; now swallowed like `FfmpegEnc` (input validation stays in `configure_pipeline`). (3) `WebCodecsDecode` announced coded dims (e.g. 640x482) but `copyTo` produces the visible-rect buffer (640x480), so `CanvasSink` rejected the size; now uses `display_width`/`display_height`. (4) `WebSocketSink::configure_pipeline` reopened its socket on every mid-stream `CapsChanged`, discarding the already-open connection and its buffered `onopen`, hanging the first send; now idempotent. Plus: `metrics::monotonic_ns` used `std::time::Instant`, which panics on wasm32 ("time not implemented"); now `web-time` on wasm32 (target-gated). **Validated in a real browser:** receive-2D renders real decoded video pixels; send produces a playable 320x240 150-frame `received.h264` (ffprobe-confirmed); and the WebGPU zero-copy path renders the decoded SMPTE color-bar fixture straight to the canvas (`VideoFrame` -> `GPUExternalTexture` -> canvas, no readback). WebGPU hardening from that bring-up: `WebGpuCanvasSink` now requests the high-performance adapter and installs an `onuncapturederror` handler (WebGPU's async validation / OOM / device-loss errors do NOT surface as a Rust `Result`, so a swap-chain failure was a silent black canvas; now it logs). Host gotcha (documented, not a code fault): on a hybrid-GPU box with many Vulkan ICDs, Chrome's Dawn backend can pick a broken ICD and fail the canvas swap-chain alloc (`vkAllocateMemory VK_ERROR_OUT_OF_DEVICE_MEMORY`); force it with `VK_ICD_FILENAMES=.../nvidia_icd.json`.
- M542: browser egress: a wasm pipeline can now capture, encode, and send. New `WebCodecsEncode` (g2g-plugins, `web-codecs`) wraps the browser `VideoEncoder`, RGBA `System` -> H.264 **Annex-B** `CompressedVideo` (SPS/PPS in-band, forced via the encoder's `avc: { format: "annexb" }` config set by reflection since web-sys has no typed setter), async output-callback shape bridged by an `Inbox` like `WebCodecsDecode`, flushed on `Eos`. New `WebSocketSink` (`web`) sends each frame's bytes as a WebSocket binary message, waiting for `onopen` before the first send. New `PatternSrc` (`web`) is a synthetic animated-RGBA `SourceLoop` (the "capture" side when no camera is present), paced with `setTimeout` which also yields the event loop so the encoder's callbacks fire. `g2g-web` gains `run_pattern_encode_to_websocket` (`PatternSrc -> WebCodecsEncode -> WebSocketSink`) and the demo a **Send** button; a new `tools/wasm-demo/ws-recv-server` (native tokio-tungstenite) captures the browser's stream to a playable `received.h264` (`ffplay received.h264`). The `web-codecs` feature adds the `VideoEncoder` / `VideoEncoderConfig` / `VideoFrameBufferInit` web-sys bindings. Encoder codec `avc1.42001f` (constrained baseline). Runs live in a WebCodecs browser. (Real getUserMedia capture is a follow-up.)
- M541: WebGPU zero-copy presentation for the browser pipeline. New `WebGpuCanvasSink` (g2g-plugins, `web-gpu` feature) consumes `WebCodecsDecode`'s GPU-resident output (`with_gpu_output` -> `MemoryDomain::WebGPUExternalTexture`), imports each decoded `VideoFrame` as a `GPUExternalTexture` and samples it with a fullscreen-triangle render pass (`textureSampleBaseClampToEdge`) onto a `<canvas>` WebGPU context, with NO CPU readback: the browser's hardware decoder keeps the frame GPU-resident and it is composited straight into the page (the browser analog of the native Vulkan Video -> `wgpu::Texture` wedge, contrast `CanvasSink`'s system-RGBA `putImageData`). Async device setup (`navigator.gpu` -> adapter -> device) runs lazily on the first frame; the pipeline / sampler / bind-group layout are built once and only the per-frame external-texture import + bind group are rebuilt (an imported external texture is single-frame). New `web-gpu` feature wires the full web-sys WebGPU render surface (implies `web-codecs`; same `--cfg=web_sys_unstable_apis`). `g2g-web` gains a `run_websocket_to_webgpu_canvas` entry point and the demo page a "Canvas 2D vs WebGPU" selector (separate canvases, since a canvas' context type is fixed on first use). `xtask wasm` now also checks `web-gpu`. Renders live in a WebGPU browser; skips where `navigator.gpu` is absent.
- M540: deployable browser (WebAssembly) pipeline + a runnable demo harness, closing the gap between "g2g compiles to wasm" and "you can run a g2g web pipeline". New workspace-excluded `g2g-web` cdylib crate holds the `#[wasm_bindgen]` browser entry points (moved out of `g2g-plugins/src/web.rs`, which is deleted): `run_websocket_to_canvas` / `run_websocket_decode` / `run_websocket_ingest` / `run_datachannel_to_canvas`, each wiring g2g's wasm elements (`WebSocketSrc` / `WebRtcSrc` -> `WebCodecsDecode` -> `CanvasSink`) and driving the graph on the browser event loop via `spawn_local`, plus a `#[wasm_bindgen(start)]` panic hook. It is excluded from the workspace (like `bevy-g2g-stream`) so its cdylib crate-type + std + wasm-bindgen deps never enter a native `--workspace` build or perturb the no_std baseline. `tools/wasm-demo/` is the end-to-end harness: `build.sh` (wasm-pack -> `pkg/`, ~200 KB wasm since WebCodecs supplies the decoder), `index.html` (canvas + Start button), a native tokio + tokio-tungstenite `ws-fixture-server` that splits the H.264 fixture into access units and streams one per WebSocket message on a timer (looping), and `serve.sh` (plain `python3 -m http.server`, no COOP/COEP headers needed since the pipeline is single-threaded, unlike thread-based wasm ports). `xtask wasm` now also `cargo check`s the `g2g-web` cdylib (by manifest path, no wasm-pack) so CI guards it. The single-threaded, WebCodecs-native, one-codebase design is a structurally lighter browser story than an Emscripten C port (gst.wasm).
- M539: pipelined streaming decode for the Vulkan Video system path, through the decoders and the `VulkanVideoDec` element. Each `*DpbDecoder` splits into `decode_push` (submit every picture into the in-flight ring without draining, returning `(submitted, retired)`) + `decode_flush` (drain the pipelined tail at end of stream); `decode_all` is now `push` + `flush` (batch behaviour unchanged). `VulkanStreamDecoder` exposes `submit_chunk_push` + `flush` over all three codecs (shared `to_i420_frames`, `submit_chunk` refactored onto it), the low-latency chunk-at-a-time shape a `re_video::AsyncDecoder` backend feeds (output lags submission by up to `DECODE_RING_DEPTH-1` pictures). The element now decodes each access unit with `decode_push` (no per-AU drain, so the decode queue stays saturated across AUs), re-pairing each retired frame with its own AU timing through a FIFO (decode order == ring retirement order, so `submitted`-count pushes keep it balanced), flushes the tail on `Eos`, resets the decoder on `Flush` (matching ffmpegdec), and flushes the outgoing decoder's tail on a mid-stream resolution reconfig before rebuilding (so no in-flight frames are lost). New `m539_vulkan_video_pipelined_decode` guards the decoder path bit-exact vs the whole-clip golden (solo always-on; a 6-decoder in-process-concurrent case bit-exact standalone but `#[ignore]`d for full-suite GPU-marathon driver flakiness); the element guards (m493 / m504 / m519) now feed `Eos` to collect the pipelined tail. Investigation note: an incremental-decode corruption seen only under concurrent Vulkan device create/teardown on this NVIDIA driver was root-caused to a driver device-lifecycle race (solo and persistent-decoder concurrent decode are bit-exact; `re_video` reuses one decoder per stream so never hits it), not a g2g sync bug; the pipelined path is kept on its streaming merits, not as a corruption fix.
- M538: chain the Vulkan Video texture decode to its ycbcr conversion with a semaphore (no CPU stall between decode and compute). Each `decode_picture_to_texture` / `decode_frame_to_texture` now sets `DpbCore::chain_next`, so `submit_texture` takes `submit_texture_chained`: the decode is submitted on the decode queue signalling `GpuTextureCtx::sem_dc` with no fence and no CPU wait, and its bitstream is held in `pending_tex_bitstream`. The shared `convert_slot_chained` then runs `YcbcrConverter::convert` (now waiting `sem_dc` at the compute stage) on the compute queue and frees the held bitstream once the compute fence is waited. This overlaps the per-picture CPU prep (RGBA image create + `vkAllocateMemory` + views + descriptor set, previously serialized *after* the decode fence wait) with the decode's GPU execution and removes the mid-picture fence wait: `decode_all_to_textures` goes from ~369 to ~690 fps on the 3060 (640x480, ~1.9x). Cross-frame overlap stays impossible by design (a decode referencing the previous frame's slot must wait that slot's in-place compute restore, so the required cross-queue semaphore is exactly what prevents overlap); this is the per-picture decode->compute chain only. `reset` / `Drop` drain the pending bitstream (queue-wait-idle, since the chained decode carries no fence of its own). Also fixes a detached `DpbCore` doc comment split off by the M536 const insertion. All texture (m494/m495/m498/m499/m500/m535) + system (m492/m503/m506) + element/reconfig guards stay green.
- M537: persist the Vulkan Video NV12 -> RGBA compute converter (texture-path prep for pipelining). The free-fn `nv12_to_wgpu_texture` rebuilt the *entire* compute pipeline (ycbcr conversion, immutable sampler, descriptor-set layout, shader module, compute pipeline, descriptor + command pools) on every picture, the dominant per-frame cost in the GPU-texture decode loop. New `YcbcrConverter` builds all of that once and stores it in `GpuTextureCtx` (owned by the shared `DpbCore`); per picture only the RGBA output image, its two image views, and a descriptor set are transient (`make_transients` / `record_convert` / `import_rgba` / `free_transients`, reusable pieces the pipelined path will drive through a ring). `decode_all_to_textures` for all three codecs now runs at ~369 fps / 2.7 ms/frame on the 3060 (640x480, no readback). Behaviour unchanged (still one fence-waited compute submit per picture); m494 / m495 / m498 / m499 / m500 / m535 texture-path tests stay green, as do the m492 / m503 / m506 system guards. The one-shot IDR path keeps the free-fn.
- M536: pipeline the Vulkan Video system-memory decode path through an in-flight ring. The shared `DpbCore` gains a `DECODE_RING_DEPTH`-slot ring (a second `RESET_COMMAND_BUFFER` command pool with a persistent command buffer + fence per slot, one readback buffer holding `DECODE_RING_DEPTH` frames so each slot copies to its own region); `record_and_submit` splits into a synchronous texture path (unchanged: fence-waited, feeds the ycbcr compute pass) and a pipelined system path that records + submits each picture without waiting, retiring the oldest slot (fence wait, NV12 read-back, bitstream free) only when the ring wraps onto it, with a final `drain` for the tail. `decode_all` (H.264 / H.265 / AV1) collects retired frames each iteration; `reset` (seek) and `Drop` drain the ring first. In-order execution on the single decode queue preserves DPB reference correctness, so only the readback buffer needs per-slot isolation. ~16% higher batch decode throughput on the 3060 (H.264, 206 -> 239 fps); the m492 / m503 / m506 bit-exact-vs-ffmpeg guards go through the system path and stay SAD/px 0. The streaming element decodes one AU per `process` call so it drains per AU; the win is on the batch `decode_all` used by the player and tests.
- M535: validated the Vulkan Video zero-copy GPU-texture wedge (`VulkanVideoDec` -> `WgpuSink`, decode straight into an RGBA `wgpu::Texture` on the decode device, present with no GPU->CPU readback) for **all three codecs** on the RTX 3060. M495 proved it for H.264 only; the H.265 / AV1 GPU-texture paths (`create_h265/av1_dpb_decoder_gpu` + `decode_all_to_textures`, in-tree since M517) had never executed. New `m535_vulkan_video_wgpu_sink_codecs` drives each codec's whole elementary stream through the element with the output domain negotiated to `WgpuTexture`, asserts every emitted frame is GPU-resident, presents each through a device-sharing `WgpuSink`, and reads the target back only to confirm real content: 10 real frames per codec, no readback between decode and present. (The element decode-to-NV12 path (M504) and auto-plug selection (M496) already covered H.265 / AV1; this closes the wedge-payload gap, so the cross-vendor GPU-decode-into-wgpu story now holds for H.264 / H.265 / AV1.)
- M534: macOS VideoToolbox HEVC (H.265) encode + decode. `VtDecode::h265` builds its `CMVideoFormatDescription` via `CMVideoFormatDescriptionCreateFromHEVCParameterSets` (VPS+SPS+PPS, NAL types 32/33/34, excluding 32-35 from the decode sample), and `VtEncode::h265` uses the `'hvc1'` codec FourCC + `CMVideoFormatDescriptionGetHEVCParameterSetAtIndex` for the keyframe SPS/VPS/PPS prefix, with H.265 IRAP keyframe detection via the shared `au_is_keyframe`. Both codecs share the session, decode/encode loop, and NV12 packing; the per-layer builder and parameter-set extraction were factored to dispatch by codec. Both pad templates advertise H.264 + H.265. The `h265_parameter_sets` annexb helper's cfg widened to the vtdecode/vtencode features. Compile-pending on Linux CI like the rest of the macOS track (validated on a Mac later); the HEVC objc2 signatures were verified against the fetched objc2-core-media 0.3.2 source. Registry wiring + a `CVPixelBuffer` zero-copy domain remain.
- M533: RTMP window-acknowledgement back-pressure (RFC §5.4.3-5.4.4). `RtmpSession` counts received chunk-stream bytes and emits an `Acknowledgement` (msg type 3) every Window-Ack-Size bytes (configurable via `with_window_ack_size`, default 2.5 MB, advertised at `connect`). `RtmpPublisher` learns the server's Window Ack Size and its acknowledged sequence, exposing `throttled()` / `unacked_bytes()` (unacked backlog vs the window in 32-bit sequence space). `RtmpSink` now blocks on the socket for an acknowledgement while throttled before feeding more media, so a slow server throttles the pipeline instead of the socket buffer bloating unboundedly. Coupled publisher+session unit test asserts the throttle trips past the window and clears on the ack; the ffmpeg ingest interop stays green (the session now acks). Multi-stream RTMP remains open.
- M532: RTSP TCP-interleaved ingest (RFC 2326 §10.12), what `ffmpeg -rtsp_transport tcp` uses. The sans-IO responder recognizes `RTP/AVP/TCP;interleaved=N-M` in SETUP (new `RtspEvent::SetupInterleaved`, echoing the channels; a lone `interleaved=N` defaults RTCP to `N+1`), and `RtspServerSrc` demuxes `$`-framed RTP off the *control* TCP connection on the RTP channel and depayloads it (no jitter buffer: TCP is ordered/lossless). The receive path shares a factored `push_access_unit` helper with the UDP loop; a `RecordTransport` enum picks UDP vs interleaved by what the publisher negotiates, keeping the control stream alive either way. New `rtsp_server_interleaved_loopback` (CI, in-process publisher) covers RTP-channel depayload + RTCP-channel skip; `rtsp_ffmpeg_record_interop` gains an ignored interleaved case validated against `ffmpeg -rtsp_transport tcp` on this host. Serving-sink interleaved + ingest multi-client remain open.
- M531: ML skip/residual-topology import + F16/BF16 weight dequant. A new two-input elementwise-add GPU op (`WgpuInference::add` + `ADD_SHADER`, host `add_reference`) is the residual primitive; `StackLayer::SaveSkip` / `AddSkip` express a `y = f(x) + x` block, built by `residual_stack_from_safetensors` into a `ResidualStack` whose `run` executes the whole model GPU-resident (saving skip tensors on-device, one read-back at the end). The per-layer builder is factored into a shared `build_layer` so the linear and residual paths stay in lockstep. The safetensors loader now dequantizes F16 (IEEE half, subnormals/Inf/NaN handled) and BF16 to f32 in `to_f32`, so real half-precision checkpoints load. `residual_block_from_safetensors_matches_cpu_reference` validates a conv-relu-conv + skip block bit-exact vs a CPU reference on the 3060; F16/BF16 dequant + shape-mismatch guards are CI unit tests.
- M530: WebRTC T1-B, per-input reverse-signal routing through the terminal duplex runner. `MultiDuplexSession` gains a `reverse_channel(input)` default (mirroring `MultiInputElement`), `run_duplex_session` clones each send input's channel and polls it after every push (surfacing a pending PLI / BWE as the source's `PushOutcome`), and `WebRtcDuplexSession` maps a remote per-mid `Event::KeyframeRequest` / `Event::EgressBitrateEstimate` back to the send source feeding that track (BWE relayed to the video track; enable_bwe turned on). New `m530_duplex_reverse` asserts a signal posted on input 0's channel reaches send source 0 and never fires source 1's, in-process (no network). Recv-side per-branch mid-stream re-solve remains open.
- M529: real-peer RTSP ingest interop with ffmpeg, and a control-channel bug it exposed. New `rtsp_ffmpeg_record_interop` has ffmpeg publish over RTSP (`-f rtsp -rtsp_transport udp`, the OPTIONS/ANNOUNCE/SETUP/RECORD direction) into `RtspServerSrc` and asserts the depayloaded access units are Annex-B with a keyframe. It uncovered that `accept_and_handshake` returned only the RTP socket on RECORD, dropping the TCP control stream (a local) the instant it returned, so g2g closed the RTSP control connection immediately; a real publisher (ffmpeg) keeps that connection open while recording and treats the close as a fatal broken pipe, aborting before any RTP flowed. The hand-rolled g2g `record_loopback` publisher never wrote to the control channel again, masking it. Fix: `accept_and_handshake` returns the control `TcpStream` too, and `run` holds it alive across the whole receive loop. ffmpeg now records in cleanly; the g2g<->g2g loopback is unaffected.
- M528: real-peer RTP interop with ffmpeg. New `udp_ffmpeg_rtp_interop` has ffmpeg's RTP H.264 payloader (`-f rtp`, packetization-mode=1) stream into `UdpSrc` and asserts the depayloaded access units are Annex-B framed with at least one recognized keyframe, proving the g2g RFC 6184 depayloader + jitter buffer reassemble ffmpeg's RTP (including FU-A fragmentation of a large IDR) correctly, which the g2g<->g2g `udp_loopback` cannot. Interoperated out of the box. Completes real-peer ffmpeg interop coverage across SRT (both directions), RTMP (ingest) and RTP/UDP (ingest).
- M527: real-peer RTMP interop with ffmpeg. New `rtmp_ffmpeg_interop` test has ffmpeg's native RTMP client publish `-f flv rtmp://...` into the g2g `RtmpSrc` listener and asserts the demuxed FLV byte stream carries the `FLV` signature and that ffprobe decodes the expected video frames from it, proving the g2g RTMP server handshake (auto-detecting ffmpeg's simple/digest C1), chunk-stream reassembly and AMF0 publish flow interoperate with a reference client (the `RtmpPublisher <-> RtmpSession` loopback cannot, both being g2g). Interoperated out of the box, no protocol fix needed. Also made `RtmpSrc::from_listener` mark the element configured (matching `RtspServerSrc::from_listener`), so a caller supplying a pre-bound listener need not also call `configure_pipeline`.
- M526: complete the SRT libsrt/ffmpeg interop matrix with the encrypted reverse direction. `srtsink_encrypted_caller_streams_mpegts_to_ffmpeg_listener` (AES-128) + `srtsink_aes256_caller_streams_mpegts_to_ffmpeg_listener` (AES-256) drive the g2g `SrtSink` caller's key-material (KMREQ) path against an ffmpeg SRT listener and confirm it decodes the stream, the mirror of the forward encrypted tests. No production change needed (the caller KM path, once M525 fixed the conclusion addressing, already interoperates); `run_reverse_interop` is factored to take an optional `(passphrase, pbkeylen)`. All six interop cases (both directions x plaintext/AES-128/AES-256) now pass against real ffmpeg.
- M525: SRT reverse-direction interop (g2g `SrtSink` caller -> ffmpeg/libsrt listener), and a second wire bug it exposed. New `srtsink_caller_streams_mpegts_to_ffmpeg_listener` test streams an MPEG-TS through the g2g SRT caller into an ffmpeg SRT listener and asserts ffmpeg decodes the same video frame count (ignored; needs ffmpeg+ffprobe+libsrt). It uncovered that the caller addressed its conclusion handshake to the wrong destination socket id: a listener's induction response echoes the *caller's* own socket id in its CIF, and g2g used that as the packet's destination, but libsrt demuxes by dst socket id and requires the conclusion be addressed to id 0 during the handshake, so it silently dropped g2g's conclusion (the handshake stalled). The g2g<->g2g loopback masked it (g2g's listener puts its own id in the induction response and does not check the header dst). Fix: the caller sends its conclusion to dst 0 and learns the listener's real socket id from the *conclusion response* (for data packets). Also hardened `SrtSink::connect_and_handshake` to bound the *whole* handshake (an 8 s deadline) rather than resetting a per-recv timeout, so a non-converging / flooding peer can no longer hang the pipeline. Both interop directions (plaintext + AES-128/256 forward, plaintext reverse) now pass against real ffmpeg; g2g<->g2g loopback + encrypt-loopback + SRT unit tests unaffected.
- M524: a whole small CNN classifier runs end to end on the hand-rolled GPU inference path, imported from one safetensors file (past M262's single conv). New `WgpuInference::batch_norm` (inference-mode: folds `gamma/beta/running_mean/running_var` into a per-channel `scale*x + shift` affine on the host, reusing the conv/linear weight+bias GPU buffers via a small `BN_SHADER`; `batch_norm_reference` matches it) and a general `linear_shaped` for a fully-connected head after a global pool (`linear` now delegates to it). `WgpuInference::stack_from_safetensors` + a `StackLayer` enum build a full model as a chain of GPU ops from a weight file, tracking the running `[C,H,W]` shape so each layer's dims follow the previous output and setting every layer but the last GPU-resident (one read-back at the end). New `full_cnn_from_safetensors_matches_cpu_reference` (RTX 3060) drives conv-BN-ReLU-pool x2 -> global-avg-pool -> linear from an in-test safetensors blob and asserts the read-back logits match a CPU reference folding the same ops; architecture compiled, weights a file.
- M523: per-input reverse-signal routing for multi-track fan-in sessions (WebRTC T1-A). New `g2g-core` `ReverseChannel` (an `Arc`-backed keyframe flag + bitrate slot) that a `MultiInputElement` session exposes per input via `reverse_channel(input)`; `run_fanin_session` clones each before running and its per-source `TaggingSink` surfaces any pending signal to that source as a `PushOutcome` (`Reconfigure(ForceKeyframe)` outranks `Bitrate`), the multi-input analog of the linear runner's `take_reconfigure` / `take_bitrate`. `WebRtcSessionSink` now routes a remote str0m `KeyframeRequest` by its `mid` to the source feeding that track (so a video PLI forces only the video encoder's IDR) and relays an `EgressBitrateEstimate` to the video track, instead of dropping both events. New `fanin_session_routes_reverse_keyframe_to_the_right_input` proves a keyframe request posted for input 0 reaches only source 0; a session unit test proves the per-input channels are shared with the runner and independent. The duplex-session reverse path (T1-B) stays a follow-up (its `TaggingSink` passes `reverse: None`).
- M522: SRT real-peer interop with libsrt/ffmpeg, and a wire-format fix it uncovered. New `srt_ffmpeg_interop` test drives an ffmpeg SRT *caller* (libsrt) into the g2g `SrtSrc` *listener* and asserts every received payload lands on an MPEG-TS boundary; it covers plaintext, AES-128 and AES-256 (ignored by default, needs ffmpeg built with libsrt). The encrypted cases exposed a real bug the g2g<->g2g loopback masked: the listener echoed the caller's Keying Material as a `KMREQ` TLV inside its conclusion handshake, but libsrt strictly requires the response to be a `KMRSP` (it rejected the connection with "HS/KMREQ extracted without passing target buffer"). `Handshake` gains an `is_response` flag (set on a listener's conclusion, by role) so `build_handshake_cif` emits `KMRSP` in the response; the HSREQ block stays HSREQ in both directions (libsrt reads its TSBPD delay either way, and emitting HSRSP there regressed the plaintext caller). All three interop cases now pass against real ffmpeg; g2g<->g2g loopback + encrypt-loopback unaffected.
- M521: RTMP "genuine FMS/FP" digest (complex) handshake, the HMAC-SHA256 handshake strict CDNs (Adobe FMS, some Wowza / Facebook Live configs) require in place of the plain byte-echo simple handshake. New `rtmphandshake` module (rtmp-feature gated, pulling `hmac` + `sha2` + `getrandom`) computes the C1/S1 32-byte digest at a data-dependent scheme offset and the C2/S2 signature keyed off the peer's digest, with the published genuine-FP (62-byte) / genuine-FMS (68-byte) keys. `RtmpPublisher` now sends a digest C1 and digest-response C2 by default (`with_complex_handshake` / `RtmpSink` `complex-handshake` property to disable), and `RtmpSession` auto-detects a digest C1 and answers with a validating S1/S2; both auto-fall-back to the simple echo against a non-genuine peer, so g2g<->g2g and OBS/ffmpeg simple clients still interoperate. The sans-IO core stays crypto-free for the `no_std` baseline (cfg-gated shims). Unit tests prove the C1 digest is self-consistent and the full C1->S1->C2/S2 round-trip validates exactly as a genuine-FMS server + Flash client check; `publisher_and_server_negotiate_the_complex_handshake` asserts the two elements complete the complex path (not a silent simple fallback). Live validation against a real strict CDN is owed (user-side).
- M520: `RtspServerSrc` (RTSP RECORD ingest) gains a receive-side jitter buffer, gaining out-of-order RTP tolerance it lacked (a naive in-order `recv_from`). The jitter + RTCP RR/NACK + FEC/RTX + depayload receive loop that `UdpSrc` already carried is extracted into a shared `rtprecv::receive_rtp_h264` helper (with an `RtpRecvConfig`); both ingest sources now ride it, deleting the duplicated loop (`UdpSrc` unchanged behaviourally, all `udp_loopback` tests green). `RtspServerSrc` grows `with_jitter` / `with_rtcp` builders; RTCP defaults off for the RTSP path (a classic publisher puts RTCP on a separate port, not muxed onto the RTP socket, so receiver reports / NACK need a negotiated `rtcp-mux`, a follow-up). New `rtsp_ingest_reorders_out_of_order_rtp` proves the ingest now restores RTP-sequence order across swapped arrivals.
- M519: `VulkanVideoDec` reconfigures mid-stream on a resolution change. The decode session + DPB are built lazily from the first keyframe's parameter sets; previously a later keyframe was ignored (`ensure_decoder` early-returned once built), so a stream that changed resolution kept decoding against the wrong-sized session. `ensure_decoder` now tracks the coded geometry the session was built for and, when a keyframe's parameter sets carry a different geometry, rebuilds the session + `DpbCore` for the new resolution (the old ones free when replaced); an unchanged geometry keeps the existing session and swallows the parameter sets repeated on every keyframe. The next frame carries the new dimensions, so `process` emits a fresh `CapsChanged` for the switch. Works for all three codecs (the check is in the shared per-codec dispatch). New `m519` drives a 640x480 -> 320x240 H.264 stream through the element and asserts the `[(640,480),(320,240)]` caps timeline plus correctly-sized real content on both sides (new fixture `h264_reconfig_640x480_to_320x240.h264`, generated with libx264).
- M517: de-duplicate the three Vulkan Video decoders onto a shared, codec-independent `DpbCore`. It owns the device/queue handles, the video session, the DPB image pool, the persistent NV12 readback buffer, and the command pool, and holds the single `record_and_submit` path (command-buffer alloc, image barriers, begin/decode/end coding, optional NV12 readback copy, fence submit + wait) plus `new_bitstream` / `free_bitstream` / `read_back_nv12`. `H264DpbDecoder` / `H265DpbDecoder` / `Av1DpbDecoder` now each embed one `DpbCore` and keep only codec state (parameter sets, POC / reference tracking, the `Std*` picture and reference structs), so the GPU command recording and fence submission cannot drift between codecs. Behaviour byte-identical: m492/m494/m498 (H.264), m503/m513 (H.265), m505/m506 (AV1) all green on the RTX 3060 and the full `vulkan-video` sweep is clean. Net ~770 lines removed from `vulkanvideo.rs`. On that shared base, the `VulkanVideoDec` pipeline element (previously H.264-only) is generalized over a codec enum (`DpbDecoderKind` / `DecodeSessionKind`): the sink pad advertises H.264 / H.265 / AV1, `configure_pipeline` opens the matching decode device and remembers the codec, and `ensure_decoder` builds the right session + DPB decoder (per-codec parameter-set extraction and geometry, one shared GPU-vs-system fallback helper), so one element decodes all three in a g2g pipeline. New `m504` drives H.265 and AV1 through the element to NV12 frames on the 3060, `m517` streams H.265 through the re_video adapter (byte-exact reset), and `m496` confirms a WgpuTexture-preferring `decodebin` / `playbin` search auto-plugs `vulkanvideodec` for H.265 and AV1 (not just H.264), so the hardware decoder is reachable for all three codecs without an explicit launch line.
- M516: Tier B (zero-copy) proven end to end through the `re_video` fork (kept out of tree). The fork's `DecodedFrameContent` gains a native, feature-gated `gpu_texture: Option<G2gGpuFrame>` field (`G2gGpuFrame { texture: wgpu::Texture, ctx: GpuContext }` + a `read_rgba()` verification helper); in GPU mode (`re_video::set_prefer_gpu_textures(true)`, default off) the g2g backend calls `VulkanStreamDecoder::submit_chunk_texture` (M512), sets `gpu_texture` to the RGBA texture (YUV->RGB already done on the GPU), and leaves `data` empty, so the frame flows out of `new_decoder` GPU-resident with **no CPU readback in the decode path**. Each frame carries the decode device's `GpuContext` so a consumer renders on the right device. New `tests/g2g_gpu_texture.rs` decodes a real `.mp4` in GPU mode and verifies all 10 GPU textures against the software ffmpeg reference (worst per-frame mean channel diff ~1.3) on the RTX 3060; the Tier A tests are unchanged (selector defaults off). Reproducibility verified (revert + re-apply + re-run green).
- M515: g2g `pub use wgpu` re-export + public `gpu::read_rgba_texture(ctx, texture)` helper (256-align readback on a shared `GpuContext`). Groundwork for wiring g2g's zero-copy GPU-texture decode into a downstream consumer (the `re_video` fork / `re_renderer`): the re-export lets the consumer name the exact wgpu version g2g's textures are bound to, and the helper is a verification / cross-device-fallback readback off a shared context. `m512_revideo_texture` exercises the helper (matches the adapter's own readback).

- M514: the `re_video` fork PoC decodes a real `.mp4` end to end (the fork-side of M513). The `re_video` fork's g2g backend now takes codec parameters out of band: `extract_config` pulls the `avcC` / `hvcC` / `av1C` record from the video's `stsd` box (re_video's `VideoDataDescription`) and `build_decoder` builds via `VulkanStreamDecoder::from_config` (reframing the length-prefixed AVCC samples itself), falling back to in-band `VulkanStreamDecoder::new` for a raw elementary stream. `new_decoder` now commits to the g2g backend only when a Vulkan Video decode device actually opens (`can_open_device`), otherwise it logs and falls through to re_video's software path (ffmpeg / dav1d) instead of erroring the stream. New `tests/g2g_mp4_decode.rs` demuxes an actual `.mp4` with re_video's own `VideoDataDescription::load_mp4`, feeds each sample (a byte-span via the player's `VideoSliceSource`, exactly as re_video's player builds chunks) through `new_decoder`, and asserts all 10 H.264 frames are bit-exact I420 vs a software ffmpeg reference on the RTX 3060 (the raw-elementary-stream `g2g_vulkan_decode` test still passes via the fallback path). So the whole container path (demux -> avcC -> hardware decode -> I420) runs through the real crate, not a hand-built description: g2g decodes what the player demuxes, not just fixtures. No g2g crate changes (fork + docs only).

- M513: real-container ingestion on the re_video adapter, so it decodes what a real player actually demuxes (MP4 / CMAF), not just raw elementary-stream fixtures. `VulkanStreamDecoder::from_config(device, CodecConfig, gpu)` builds the decoder from an out-of-band `avcC` / `hvcC` / `av1C` config record (the shape re_video's `VideoDataDescription` carries) instead of scavenging parameter sets from the first sample, and records the NAL length-prefix size so `submit_chunk` / `submit_chunk_texture` reframe each length-prefixed (AVCC) sample to Annex-B automatically (AV1 OBU samples need no reframing; a `new`-built decoder passes samples through untouched). Bounded parsers (`parse_avcc_config` / `parse_hvcc_config` / `parse_av1c_config`, every offset validated, malformed records rejected rather than mis-decoded) and `reframe_length_prefixed`. **Bug caught by the new test:** an earlier auto-detect reframed only when a sample was not already Annex-B, but a 4-byte AVCC NAL length in 256..=511 is `00 00 01 xx`, which sniffs as an Annex-B start code, so those samples were fed raw and decoded to garbage; a `from_config` decoder now reframes unconditionally (the container's stored form is length-prefixed by definition). In-module unit tests cover the parsers + reframe (GPU-free); `m513_revideo_container` (RTX 3060) builds an `avcC` from the H.264 fixture's SPS/PPS, splits the stream into per-frame AVCC samples (params stripped, VCL NALs length-prefixed), feeds them one per `submit_chunk`, and asserts every I420 frame is **bit-identical** to the Annex-B reference decode. Fork side still owed: pass re_video's `VideoDataDescription` codec params into `from_config` and fall back to re_video's software path when g2g cannot open a device / handle the stream (today the backend errors the stream).

- M512: Tier B (zero-copy) output on the re_video adapter -- the g2g-side half of the wgpu-texture wedge's second tier. `VulkanStreamDecoder::new_gpu(device, codec, init)` builds the adapter in GPU-texture mode and `submit_chunk_texture(sample, is_sync)` returns each decoded frame as a GPU-resident RGBA `wgpu::Texture` (`DecodedVideoTexture`), YUV->RGB already applied on the GPU by g2g's `VkSamplerYcbcrConversion` compute pass (M494), with **no CPU readback in the decode path** (unlike Tier A's I420). `gpu_context()` exposes the decode device's wgpu instance/adapter/device/queue so a consumer (a re_renderer, a `WgpuSink`) builds on it; a `read_rgba_texture` verification helper and a `WrongOutputMode` error (CPU vs GPU methods are mutually exclusive, chosen at construction) round out the API. **Device-identity correction:** zero-copy needs the renderer on the *decode* device, not the reverse -- g2g must create the decode device to enable Vulkan video-decode (and compute) queue families a render-only device omits, so the texture is bound to g2g's device. On a single-GPU host that is the display GPU too; on a split decode/present host a cross-device copy is unavoidable and Tier A is the honest path. `m512_revideo_texture` (RTX 3060) drives H.264 (the codec the Tier-A PoC settled on) through `submit_chunk_texture`, asserts 10 GPU-resident `Rgba8Unorm` textures with real, per-frame-distinct content, that a CPU method on a GPU-mode decoder is rejected, and anchors correctness to the (bit-exact vs ffmpeg) CPU I420 path by matching the GPU RGBA to that I420 reconstructed with the same BT.601-limited matrix. The re_video fork side (a native GPU-texture `FrameContent` variant + building `re_renderer` on the adapter's `gpu_context()`) remains and cannot be exercised from this tree.
- M511: cross-thread decode-determinism tests + corrected re_video-PoC teardown story. H.264 and H.265 Vulkan decode are proven **bit-identical whether run on the main thread or a spawned worker** (`h264_/h265_decode_matches_across_threads` in `vulkan_thread_teardown.rs`), so the threaded re_video integration is bit-exact for them; the re_video fork PoC was re-pointed at H.264 (threaded backend, joins its worker on drop) and is bit-exact I420 vs ffmpeg 8/8 runs, clean exit. The AV1 cross-thread equivalent is `#[ignore]`d: on this NVIDIA driver AV1 decode is bit-exact on the main thread but has a small run-varying residual on the late compound / temporal-MV inter frames off the main thread, while every g2g-fed `Std*` param is byte-identical across threads and the GPU op sequence is identical -- since H.264/H.265 share the same decode/readback/session/threading path and are stable, the residual is isolated to the driver's AV1 decode, not g2g (a documented known issue, not a g2g bug). A GPU lock serializes the device-creating tests (parallel Vulkan device creation SIGSEGVs).
- M510: robust Vulkan-Video decode-adapter selection. `open_decode_device` now enumerates Vulkan adapters and picks a discrete GPU that passes the codec's decode probe (with a bounded retry), instead of trusting `request_adapter(HighPerformance)`; on a multi-GPU host the latter could return an adapter with no decode queue for the codec (an intermittent open failure), and this is the correct behaviour for the split-GPU case where the display GPU is not the decode GPU. Added `vulkan_thread_teardown` proving create+decode+drop of the whole decoder on joined worker threads is clean: the M509 PoC double-free was re_video's *detached* `SyncDecoderWrapper` thread racing process exit (fixed in the fork by owning a worker thread that joins on drop), not a g2g decode bug.
- M509: `re_video` proof-of-concept -- g2g Vulkan Video wired into the *real* `re_video` crate as a decode backend, closing M508's contract proof with a working demonstration. A ~160-line fork of `re_video` (behind a native-only `g2g-vulkan` cargo feature) adds `impl AsyncDecoder for G2gVulkanDecoder`, which delegates to `g2g_plugins::revideo::VulkanStreamDecoder` and maps each `DecodedVideoFrame` onto `re_video::decode::Frame`, plus routing in `new_decoder` (H.264 / H.265 / AV1) and a `DecodeError::G2gVulkan` variant. A test drives `re_video::new_decoder` on the AV1 fixture through the crate's own public decode API (chunk in -> frames on the output channel) and asserts all 10 frames bit-exact I420 vs a software ffmpeg reference on the RTX 3060 (5/5 deterministic, clean exit). The fork lives outside this tree (re_video is workspace-coupled); the patch, README, and exact repro were captured out of tree (pinned re_video commit `ef9d94e`). **Discovered gap:** wiring g2g through `re_video`'s pooled-thread `SyncDecoderWrapper` triggers a non-deterministic heap corruption / double-free at teardown; the inline main-thread `AsyncDecoder` path (this PoC and `m508`) is rock-solid, so g2g's Vulkan decoder has a thread-affinity / teardown-robustness gap to harden before a background-thread backend. Tier B (GPU-resident texture handoff, no readback) still needs an upstream/fork `FrameContent` texture variant.
- M508: fork-ready re_video adapter for the wgpu-texture wedge (`g2g_plugins::revideo`, Tier A readback). `VulkanStreamDecoder` wraps the Vulkan Video H.264 / H.265 / AV1 DPB decoders in the chunk-at-a-time contract a `re_video::decode::AsyncDecoder` backend uses: `new(device, codec, init)` takes codec parameters from the stream prefix, `submit_chunk(sample, is_sync)` decodes one coded sample (DPB state carried across calls) and returns each frame as packed I420 (Y, U, V) -- re_video's exact native CPU frame layout -- and `reset()` seeks by re-arming the session RESET control. Output types (`DecodedVideoFrame`, `VideoPixelLayout` / `VideoColorRange` / `VideoMatrixCoefficients`) mirror re_video's `YuvPixelLayout` / `YuvRange` / `YuvMatrixCoefficients` 1:1, so a re_video fork maps them with no lookup and g2g takes no dependency on the (workspace-coupled) re_video crate. AV1 colorimetry comes from the sequence header; NV12 chroma is deinterleaved to I420. Added `Av1DpbDecoder::reset` / `H265DpbDecoder::reset` (the cheap re-arm-RESET seek mirroring `H264DpbDecoder::reset`; rebuilding the decoder over a reused session is not a clean reset on the NVIDIA driver). `m508_revideo_adapter` drives the AV1 fixture one OBU-frame chunk at a time on the RTX 3060: 10 I420 frames, correct geometry / layout / colorimetry, reset + re-decode deterministic, and every frame bit-exact (full I420, chroma included) vs the ffmpeg reference. The remaining `impl AsyncDecoder` (1:1 field mapping + the output-channel send) lives in a re_video fork; Tier B keeps the frame GPU-resident (a native texture `FrameContent`), which needs an upstream/fork addition.
- M506c: chased the AV1 temporal-MV residual from M506b to **full bit-exactness** -- all 10 frames now SAD/px 0 vs the ffmpeg software decoder (previously frames 2+ had a small residual). Root cause: the default loop-filter reference deltas for ALTREF2 / ALTREF were `0` instead of the spec's `-1` (`AV1_DEFAULT_LF_REF_DELTAS` was `[1,0,0,0,-1,0,0,0]`, must be `[1,0,0,0,-1,0,-1,-1]`), so in-loop deblocking was mis-configured for compound blocks referencing the alt frames -- exactly the frames past the first inter frame, hence the propagating residual. Found by writing a Vulkan capture layer that dumps every input the driver receives (the `StdVideoDecodeAV1PictureInfo` **and its sub-structs** -- quantization, loop filter, CDEF, loop restoration, segmentation, tile info -- plus the sequence header and the exact tile bitstream bytes) and diffing ffmpeg's Vulkan hardware decode against ours on the same GPU: everything matched except the loop-filter ref deltas. Along the way this ruled out (each proven bit-identical) the DPB slot scheme, sign bias, global motion, tile framing, bitstream padding, DPB/active ceilings, film-grain support, `VK_KHR_video_maintenance1`, robustness features, the readback layout round-trip, barriers, and the submission model. `m506_vulkan_video_av1_decode` now asserts every frame bit-exact.
- M506b: AV1 full-DPB Vulkan Video decode on the RTX 3060, the AV1 sibling of M492 / M503 (the decode half of M506, on top of the M506a header parse). `to_std_av1_picture_info` maps a parsed frame header onto `StdVideoDecodeAV1PictureInfo` plus every owned sub-struct (`StdVideoAV1TileInfo` with the MI-start / SB-size arrays, `StdVideoAV1Quantization`, `StdVideoAV1Segmentation`, `StdVideoAV1LoopFilter`, `StdVideoAV1CDEF`, `StdVideoAV1LoopRestoration`, `StdVideoAV1GlobalMotion`). `Av1DpbDecoder` (`create_av1_dpb_decoder` / `_gpu`, `decode_all` -> `Vec<Nv12Frame>` / `decode_all_to_textures` -> `Vec<wgpu::Texture>`) manages AV1's reference model directly: a pool of `NUM_REF_FRAMES + 1` physical DPB images, `ref_frame_idx` -> physical-slot mapping, a fresh slot per frame with `refresh_frame_flags` remap, `reference_name_slot_indices` for the driver, per-tile offsets/sizes (single tile), and `vkCmdDecodeVideoKHR` with the same begin/decode/end + sync2 barrier structure as the H.265 path. **Result on the 3060: the intra key frame and the first single-reference inter frame are bit-exact vs the ffmpeg (dav1d) software decoder (SAD/px 0); the compound-reference / temporal-MV inter frames (reference_select == 1, frame 2 onward, with `use_ref_frame_mvs` / `enable_masked_compound`) currently carry a small residual (~50-175 of 307200 luma samples off by one, SAD/px < 0.001), which the later frames inherit through prediction.** The header parse, `Std*` mapping and static per-frame params are therefore proven correct (intra frame exact); the residual is isolated to inter prediction and is the open item for full bit-exactness. Confirmed *not* the NVIDIA `OrderHints` offset quirk (that made it worse, so this driver uses the canonical layout) nor the reference sign bias (0 for this low-delay stream). `m506_vulkan_video_av1_decode` asserts the structure + real per-frame content + that key and first-inter frames are bit-exact against an optional `G2G_AV1_REF` yuv dump.
- M506a: AV1 uncompressed frame-header parse (the correctness-critical half of full-DPB AV1 decode). Unlike H.264/H.265, Vulkan Video AV1 decode does not re-parse the bitstream: the driver takes a fully populated `StdVideoDecodeAV1PictureInfo` and all its sub-structs, so the whole uncompressed header (AV1 spec 5.9.2) must be read by the app. `parse_av1_frame_header` reads frame type / show / order hint / primary ref / refresh flags, `ref_frame_idx`, frame + render + superres size, interpolation filter / motion-mode / ref-frame-mvs, then the sub-parses: `tile_info` (uniform and non-uniform), `quantization_params`, `segmentation_params`, delta-q / delta-lf, `loop_filter_params`, `cdef_params`, `lr_params`, `read_tx_mode`, `frame_reference_mode`, `skip_mode_params` (with the order-hint forward/backward reference search), global motion (`decode_subexp` / signed-subexp-with-ref / `inverse_recenter`), plus `CodedLossless`/`AllLossless` derivation and the `su(n)` / `ns(n)` readers. An `Av1RefFrames` carries the per-slot reference state (order hint, type, dimensions) the inter-frame paths need. Reference-loaded state (loop-filter deltas / segmentation / global motion carried from the primary reference when not re-coded) uses the AV1 defaults, correct for streams that hold those constant (the fixture); threading the full per-slot saved state is a follow-up. GPU-free unit tests validate the parse field-by-field against `ffmpeg -bsf:v trace_headers` on the 640x480 libaom fixture, for the KEY frame and an INTER frame (ref_frame_idx, base_q_idx, loop-filter levels, CDEF, tile layout, ...), and that all 10 frame headers parse in sync. Left (M506 decode half): map onto `StdVideoDecodeAV1PictureInfo` + sub-structs, the `Av1DpbDecoder` with AV1's 8-slot reference model + tile offsets, and `vkCmdDecodeVideoKHR`, bit-exact vs ffmpeg.
- M507: `VulkanVideoPlayer` hardening, two follow-ups to the M499 frame-count LRU. (1) **Memory-budgeted eviction**: the decoded-frame cache now honors a byte budget (`cache_byte_budget`, default 512 MiB, `set_cache_byte_budget`) alongside the frame count, evicting least-recently-used frames to stay under both. A frame-count cap alone pins gigabytes at 4K/8K (one 3840x2160 RGBA frame is ~33 MB, so 64 of them is ~2 GB); the byte budget is the bound that actually matters there, while a small frame keeps the count binding as before (so M498/M499 are unchanged). `cache_bytes` / `cache_byte_budget` getters expose it. (2) **Cache-traversed (opt-in, `set_cache_traversed`, off by default)**: a decode range caches every traversed picture (via the new `H264DpbDecoder::decode_range_all_to_textures`), not just the target, so a backward scrub within an already-decoded GOP is a cache hit with no decode, at the cost of one colour conversion per run-up frame. `m507_vulkan_video_player_budget` (on the RTX 3060) drives the byte budget to a three-frame bound and asserts the resident set stays within it, that an evicted frame re-decodes and is still bit-identical to a linear reference, and that with cache-traversed on a backward scrub within a GOP does no decode and returns the correct frame.
- M505: Vulkan Video AV1 decode session + parameters on real hardware, the AV1 sibling of M488 / M502. `open_av1_decode_device` (over the codec-parameterized `open_decode_device`) opens a wgpu device with the AV1 decode extensions + queue; `av1_profile` builds the `VkVideoProfileInfoKHR` chained with `VkVideoDecodeAV1ProfileInfoKHR` (Main, 8-bit 4:2:0, no film-grain synthesis); `VulkanVideoDevice::create_av1_session` creates the `VkVideoSessionKHR` + `VkVideoSessionParametersKHR` carrying the single Std AV1 sequence header from `StdAv1Params` (M504) via `VkVideoDecodeAV1SessionParametersCreateInfoKHR` (AV1 has no per-picture parameter set; the frame headers arrive at decode time). Creating the parameters makes the driver validate the M504 `Std*` mapping, so `m505_vulkan_video_av1_session` (open device, parse the fixture, map, create session) is an end-to-end proof the AV1 parse + mapping is correct on the GPU, not just self-consistent. On the RTX 3060 (NV12 `G8_B8R8_2PLANE_420_UNORM`, 640x480); skips with no adapter / no AV1 decode support. Remaining for a decoded AV1 frame: the full frame-header + tile parse, the picture-info `Std*` sub-structs, and `vkCmdDecodeVideoKHR` with AV1's 8-slot reference model.
- M504: AV1 OBU framing + sequence-header parse + `StdVideoAV1SequenceHeader` mapping for the Vulkan Video decoder (the parse half, the M487/M501 analog for AV1; correctness-critical, since Vulkan Video does not parse the bitstream). AV1 is not NAL / Annex-B framed: `av1_obus` walks the low-overhead OBU stream by its LEB128 size fields (bounds-checked, stops at the first malformed unit), `parse_av1_sequence_header` reads the sequence header OBU (spec 5.5.1: operating points, optional timing / decoder-model info, frame-id and order-hint config, and the full `color_config`) into a plain `Av1SequenceHeader`, and `to_std_av1_seq_header` maps it onto `StdVideoAV1SequenceHeader` + an owned `StdVideoAV1ColorConfig` pointee block (the Std AV1 color enums are numeric-equal to the AV1 spec codepoints, so they cast directly). `av1_frame_infos` / `parse_av1_frame_lead` classify each coded frame (type / shown / show-existing) from the leading frame-header fields. GPU-free unit tests parse a real libaom 640x480 fixture (`av1_640x480.obu`, 1 KEY + 9 INTER frames, all shown, no hidden altref, verified against ffmpeg `trace_headers`): sequence-header geometry / profile / 4:2:0 8-bit, the Std mapping wiring `pColorConfig` (and leaving `pTimingInfo` null), the 10-frame classification, and LEB128 / OBU-walk rejection of malformed input. Left: the AV1 decode session (`create_av1_session`, the M488/M502 analog) then the full frame-header + tile parse and `Av1DpbDecoder` with AV1's 8-slot reference model (the M492/M503 analog), bit-exact vs ffmpeg.
- M503: Vulkan Video H.265 full-DPB decode on real hardware, the HEVC sibling of M492 (M501/M502 built the parse + `Std*` mapping + session; this decodes pixels). `H265DpbDecoder` (`create_h265_dpb_decoder` / `_gpu` + `decode_all` / `decode_all_to_textures`) parses each slice-segment-header prefix (`parse_h265_slice_header`: first-slice flag, NAL type, slice type, POC lsb, and the inline short-term RPS with its bit length), computes picture-order-count (H.265 8.3.1), applies the reference-picture set to the DPB (every IRAP is a clean reset; otherwise keep only the pictures the RPS lists), and hands the driver the reference-slot lists (`RefPicSetStCurrBefore/After`, POC-keyed `StdVideoDecodeH265ReferenceInfo`) plus `NumBitsForSTRefPicSetInSlice`. The whole 640x480 fixture (IDR + CRA GOPs, 10 pictures) decodes **bit-exact** against the ffmpeg software decoder (SAD/px 0 on the RTX 3060), also straight to GPU-resident RGBA `wgpu::Texture`s via the shared ycbcr compute pass. Shared helpers generalized for both codecs (`create_dpb_image`, `open_decode_device`, `decode_format`); `BitReader::bit_pos()` added to measure the inline RPS bit length. **Gotcha found + fixed on the 3060:** NVIDIA's Vulkan H.265 slice-header parser mis-locates the header with a 4-byte start code and reads a garbage PPS id for every *non-IDR* slice (the IDR tolerates it, decoding from the picture info); framing each slice with a 3-byte start code (`00 00 01`, as ffmpeg's Vulkan HEVC path does) fixes it. The H.264 path is unaffected and keeps its 4-byte code. `m503_vulkan_video_h265_decode` asserts real per-frame content, P-frames differing from their keyframe (inter prediction ran) and consecutive frames differing, plus the GPU-texture path. Left: open-GOP CRA with RASL followers (referencing pre-CRA pictures), long-term references, and B-frame reordering; and the `VulkanVideoDec` element / auto-plug for H.265.
- M502: Vulkan Video H.265 decode session + parameters on real hardware, the HEVC sibling of M488. `open_h265_decode_device` (thin wrapper over a new codec-parameterized `open_decode_device`) opens a wgpu device with the H.265 decode extensions + queue; `VulkanVideoDevice::create_h265_session` builds the `VkVideoSessionKHR` + `VkVideoSessionParametersKHR` carrying the Std VPS/SPS/PPS from `StdH265Params` (M501). Creating the parameters makes the driver validate the M501 `Std*` mapping, so `m502_vulkan_video_h265_session` (open device, parse the fixture, map, create session) is an end-to-end proof the H.265 parse + mapping is correct on the GPU, not just self-consistent. `h264_decode_format` generalized to a codec-agnostic `decode_format` shared by both codecs. On the RTX 3060 (NV12 `G8_B8R8_2PLANE_420_UNORM`, 640x480); skips with no adapter / no H.265 decode support. Remaining for a decoded H.265 frame: the DPB image pool, slice-header parse, and `vkCmdDecodeVideoKHR` with the per-frame `Std*` picture/slice info.
- M501: H.265 (HEVC) VPS/SPS/PPS bitstream parse + `StdVideoH265*` mapping for the Vulkan Video decoder (the H.264 M487 analog; correctness-critical, since Vulkan Video does not parse the bitstream). `parse_h265_vps` / `parse_h265_sps` / `parse_h265_pps` / `extract_h265_parameter_sets` read the RBSP (reusing the `annexb` bit-reader; H.265's NAL header is two bytes, so the RBSP starts at `nal[2..]`) into plain structs, including the full `profile_tier_level` general block and the short-term reference-picture sets, which are parsed to canonical explicit form: an inter-RPS-predicted set is derived from its reference per H.265 7.4.8 (tracking `NumDeltaPocs` to advance the bit reader). `to_std_h265_params` maps them onto the `Std*` layout, returning a bundle (`StdH265Params`) that owns the pointee blocks the SPS/VPS reference by pointer (profile-tier-level, DPB manager, short-term RPS list); the RPS is emitted in explicit form (inverting `DeltaPocS0/S1` back to the `delta_poc_sX_minus1` deltas). Main profile 4:2:0/4:2:2/4:4:4 packed 8-bit; unsupported features (separate colour planes, explicit scaling lists, non-uniform tiles, SPS long-term ref pics) are rejected at parse rather than mis-decoded, and every read is bounds-checked so malformed input fails the parse. GPU-free unit tests parse the real 640x480 x265 fixture (Main, level 3.0, 4-picture DPB; this clip carries its RPS inline per-slice, so `num_short_term_ref_pic_sets == 0` in the SPS) cross-checked against the geometry-only `h265parse`, and drive the short-term-RPS explicit-parse + inter-prediction-derivation paths (which decode-time slice headers exercise) with hand-built bitstreams, verifying the `Std*` round-trip.
- M500: consume decoded frames in an application-owned wgpu render pipeline, the viewer / game-engine integration surface (a viewer brings its own renderer and samples the decoded frame as a texture in its own render pass, rather than g2g's `WgpuSink` presenting it). Proven end to end: the decoder's imported RGBA texture already carries `TEXTURE_BINDING` (+ hal `RESOURCE`), so a foreign pipeline built on the shared decode device (`VulkanVideoPlayer::gpu_context`) binds and samples it zero-copy, no decoder change needed. `m500_vulkan_video_embed` stands in for the consumer: a tiny "engine" with its own shader / bind group / pipeline renders each `frame_at` texture through a grayscale transform into an offscreen target and asserts the output is (a) grayscale everywhere (`R==G==B`, so the app's shader ran), (b) non-uniform (real content was sampled), and (c) the per-pixel grayscale of the actual decoded frame (SAD/byte <= 2, orientation-tolerant). Also `examples/vulkan_video_engine_embed`: the visual sibling, compositing each frame split (left = decoded, right = app grayscale) and dumping PPMs (verified on the 3060: left colourful, right `R==G==B`). This is the integration primitive a real `re_video` / `re_renderer` backend builds on; the remaining step is wiring an actual external viewer, not proving the handoff.
- M499: `VulkanVideoPlayer` caching follow-ups + a display-order fix. (1) **Forward-continue fast path**: a cache miss now continues decoding in place when the decoder already sits within the target's GOP at or before it (a forward seek in reach), resetting to the keyframe only on a backward / cross-GOP seek, so linear playback decodes each coded picture once (O(n)) instead of re-decoding the GOP prefix every frame (O(n^2)); `pictures_decoded()` exposes the true coded-picture count. (2) **LRU cache bound**: the decoded-frame cache is capped (`cache_capacity`, default 64, `set_cache_capacity`) and evicts least-recently-used past the cap, so a long stream does not grow GPU memory without bound. (3) **Display-order fix**: presentation order was sorted by POC globally, but POC resets at each IDR, so a multi-GOP stream came out interleaved (`0,5,1,6,...`); it is now ordered by (GOP, POC) with GOPs in decode order (identity for I/P, correct reordering within a B-frame GOP). `m499_vulkan_video_cache` asserts a linear play-through decodes exactly `n` pictures (not O(n^2)) with every frame bit-identical to a linear reference, and that at capacity 1 a resident frame hits while an evicted one re-decodes. Also fixes latent M496 test-gating: `vulkanvideodec` is a valid H.264 -> raw auto-plug candidate (its NV12 System fallback), so the "no decoder in the baseline" tests (`m193` / `m194` / `m195` / `m196`) now exclude `vulkan-video` alongside `ffmpeg` / `vaapi` / `nvdec` / `mediacodec`, leaving the full `--features vulkan-video` suite green. On the RTX 3060.
- M498: `VulkanVideoPlayer`, a random-access ("pull") scrubber over the Vulkan Video decoder, the timeline-viewer counterpart to the streaming `VulkanVideoDec` push path (the model a wgpu visualization tool needs, whose native decode today is typically CPU software + a GPU upload copy, not hardware-into-the-render-device). It builds a keyframe / POC index without decoding (`H264DpbDecoder::index_pictures`) and serves `frame_at_index` / `frame_at(pts)` as a GPU-resident RGBA `wgpu::Texture`: on a cache miss it `reset`s the decoder (re-arming the session RESET control) and decodes forward from the enclosing keyframe to the target (`decode_range_to_texture`; the run-up pictures decode as references only, no texture materialized), caching each result keyed by decoding index so a revisited frame is free. `m498_vulkan_video_scrub` scrubs the fixture out of order (forward + backward across the GOP boundary, landing on mid-GOP P frames cold) and asserts every returned frame is bit-identical (SAD/byte 0) to a straight linear decode -- a cold mid-GOP P frame only matches if it was decoded from its keyframe with the right references, so this is the decode-from-keyframe proof -- then asserts each distinct frame decodes exactly once and revisits do no GPU work (the cache). Also `examples/vulkan_video_scrubber`: an interactive on-screen scrubber (arrows / Home / End / click-drag / space) that pulls `frame_at_index` per redraw and presents via `WgpuSink`, its title showing the live decode count so the cache is visible; zero-copy when the decode GPU drives the display, cross-GPU readback fallback on PRIME (reusing the `vulkan_video_on_screen` transport). On the RTX 3060 (`m498` passes; the suite stays green). Left: an in-sequence fast path (skip the keyframe re-decode when scrubbing forward within a GOP), an LRU bound on the frame cache, and H.265 / AV1.
- M497: `examples/vulkan_video_on_screen`, the on-screen live present of the Vulkan Video wedge (H.264 -> GPU-resident RGBA `wgpu::Texture` -> `WgpuSink` in a real window), the app-owned-window sibling of the offscreen `m495` test.
