The app owns the winit window + event loop (a wgpu surface is built from a window handle and driven by the app's loop, so this is an example, not a self-checking test) and hands the configured surface to `WgpuSink::with_surface`. Two present paths chosen at runtime: **zero-copy** when the decode GPU also drives the display (the decoded texture blits straight to the swapchain, no readback); **cross-GPU fallback** on a hybrid/PRIME host, where only the discrete GPU exposes `VK_KHR_video_decode_h264` while a different GPU drives the screen, by reading each decoded frame back once and re-uploading it to the display GPU (the transport a real playbin uses on PRIME). The display GPU is found first on a clean wgpu instance so a discrete-GPU surface is never created on a host where it would fail (creating an NVIDIA surface can poison the Wayland window with a DRM-syncobj protocol error); `is_surface_supported` can false-positive, so the real check is whether `Surface::configure` succeeds, captured in an error scope rather than left to abort the process. Validated live on the laptop (RADV iGPU display + RTX 3060 decode): decode on the 3060, cross-GPU present on the AMD iGPU, the 10-frame clip looping on screen on both Wayland and X11. New `winit` dev-dependency (gated to this example via `required-features`, so the default no_std build is untouched).
- M496: `vulkanvideodec` is now an auto-plug candidate (not just a launch name), the wgpu-texture analog of `NvDec`'s `produces(Cuda)`. Registered in `register_autoplug_candidates` tagged `produces(WgpuTexture)` + `hardware()`, so a domain-aware `decodebin`/`playbin` search that prefers `WgpuTexture` picks it for H.264 (the copy-free wedge into a wgpu consumer, domain match dominating the score), while a plain (System) search is unchanged -- a WgpuTexture producer is a domain mismatch there, exactly as `NvDec` (Cuda) is skipped for System. Its source pad template now advertises both outputs it can produce (`Nv12` and `Rgba8`), and it remains a valid System *fallback* when it is the only H.264 decoder present (multi-domain: it emits NV12 then). `m496_vulkan_video_autoplug` (GPU-free, registry capability scoring only) asserts a WgpuTexture-preferring search picks `vulkanvideodec`, and -- with a competing `ffmpegdec` present -- a System search prefers the system decoder.
- M494/M495: zero-copy GPU-resident output for `VulkanVideoDec`, so a decoded frame reaches a wgpu consumer without ever leaving the GPU (the wedge's performance claim, now end to end for full streams, not just a single IDR). `H264DpbDecoder::decode_all_to_textures` (built via `create_h264_dpb_decoder_gpu`) decodes every picture with full DPB reference management (M492) and converts each decoded slot *in place* via the `VkSamplerYcbcrConversion` compute pass into an RGBA `wgpu::Texture`, restoring the slot to the decode layout so it stays a valid reference; DPB slot images are created `SAMPLED` + `CONCURRENT` across the decode/compute families for the GPU path (`TRANSFER_SRC` + `EXCLUSIVE` for the system path). The ycbcr pass is now a shared free function (`nv12_to_wgpu_texture`, with a `restore_to_dpb` flag) used by both the one-shot IDR path (M491) and the DPB loop. `VulkanVideoDec` becomes a multi-domain producer (mirrors `NvDec`): `output_memory` prefers `WgpuTexture`, `output_domains = {WgpuTexture, System}`, and `configure_allocation` settles the choice against the downstream consumer -- a `WgpuTexture`-capable sink keeps the frame on the GPU (RGBA), anything else gets system NV12 (falls back to NV12 if the device has no compute queue). `VulkanVideoDevice::gpu_context` / `VulkanVideoDec::gpu_context` expose the decode device as a `GpuContext` so a `WgpuSink` shares it (the prerequisite for a copy-free handoff); the `gpu` module is now built for the `vulkan-video` feature. `m494_vulkan_video_dpb_texture` decodes the fixture straight to 10 GPU-resident textures and reads each back (real content, P frames distinct); `m495_vulkan_video_wgpu_sink` runs the full wedge -- `VulkanVideoDec` (WgpuTexture) -> `WgpuSink::offscreen` presenting each frame with no GPU->CPU readback -- and verifies the presented target. Both on the RTX 3060, skip with no adapter / compute queue.
- M493: `VulkanVideoDec` pipeline element, the `AsyncElement` wrapper around the M492 `H264DpbDecoder` (vendor-neutral GPU hardware H.264 decode on the same Vulkan device wgpu runs). `Caps::CompressedVideo{H264}` Annex-B in -> `Caps::RawVideo{Nv12}` system-memory out (the layout the decoder already produces, so no colour conversion). `intercept_caps` narrows to H.264; `caps_constraint_as_transform` derives NV12 at the same geometry/framerate so the solver gives each link real caps; `configure_pipeline` opens the decode device (the session + DPB build lazily on the first access unit that carries SPS/PPS, since those arrive in-band, not in the caps); `process` decodes each AU (DPB reference state carries across calls, so P frames after the IDR decode correctly) and emits one NV12 frame per coded picture, emitting the output `CapsChanged` before the first. Registered as `vulkanvideodec` (launch-only for now; no auto-plug rank yet). Field/drop order is decoder -> session -> device so the `VkVideoSession` and per-frame objects are destroyed before the `VkDevice`. `m493_vulkan_video_element` drives it one access unit per `process` call (splitting the fixture into its 10 AUs) and asserts 10 NV12 640x480 frames, each with real luma content (near-black + bright), plus exactly one leading NV12 `CapsChanged`; skips with no adapter. Also `examples/vulkan_video_smoke`: decode an H.264 stream via the M492 decoder and dump PPM frames (BT.601 NV12->RGB) you can open, the visual smoke test (default clip is the bundled 640x480 fixture; on the 3060 it produces the correct SMPTE colour-bar card with the P-frames' animated gradient bar, matching ffmpeg). Left for the wedge: zero-copy GPU-resident `WgpuTexture` output (the decode->texture half is already proven in M490/M491; needs the per-frame DPB path + a wgpu-consuming sink), an auto-plug `CapabilityDescriptor` rank, mid-stream SPS/PPS re-config, and H.265/AV1.
- M492: Vulkan Video H.264 full DPB reference management, so P frames after the IDR decode against their references (M489-M491 hardcoded the lone-IDR `Std*` constants and one DPB slot, decoding only the first frame / all-intra streams). `H264DpbDecoder` (`create_h264_dpb_decoder` + `decode_all`) owns a fixed DPB image pool sized to `max_num_ref_frames + 1`, parses each slice header (`parse_h264_slice_header`: `frame_num`, POC types 0/2, `idr_pic_id`, `slice_type`, `nal_ref_idc`), splits an elementary stream into access units on `first_mb_in_slice == 0`, computes picture-order-count, and runs H.264 sliding-window reference marking, handing the driver the active reference slots (each with its `StdVideoDecodeH264ReferenceInfo`) and the setup slot per picture. The whole 640x480 fixture (2 GOPs of IDR + 4 P frames) decodes bit-exact against the ffmpeg software decoder (SAD/px 0 on the RTX 3060); `m492_vulkan_video_dpb` asserts 10 frames, each with real content, P frames differing from their IDR and consecutive frames differing (inter prediction ran). Rejects `pic_order_cnt_type == 1` (delta cycle not carried) and field pictures up front. Fixes a latent one-bit parser bug that had silently corrupted M489-M491: `parse_h264_pps` read the trailing optional block (`transform_8x8_mode_flag`) without a `more_rbsp_data()` check, so a baseline PPS's `rbsp_stop_one_bit` (1) was misread as `transform_8x8_mode_flag = 1`, telling the driver 8x8 transforms were enabled and desyncing its CAVLC coefficient parse -- every decoded frame was flat mid-grey (the M489-M491 tests only asserted non-uniformity, not correctness, so they passed). New `BitReader::more_rbsp_data()` (H.264 7.2); m489 now also asserts near-black + bright content so a non-uniform-but-wrong decode fails. GPU-free unit tests cover the slice-header parse and the baseline-no-8x8 regression. Left for the `VulkanVideoDec` element: the `AsyncElement` wrapper, in-flight pipelining, and H.265/AV1 mapping.
- M491: zero-copy GPU-resident NV12 -> RGBA, so a decoded frame reaches wgpu without leaving the GPU (the wedge's performance claim). `decode_idr_to_rgba_texture_gpu` decodes the IDR into a `CONCURRENT`-shared NV12 image, then a Vulkan compute pass on a dedicated compute queue samples it through a `VkSamplerYcbcrConversion` (BT.601 narrow) and writes an RGBA `VkImage`, which is imported straight into wgpu via `texture_from_raw` (the RGBA image + memory move into the wgpu texture's drop callback) -- no CPU round-trip, unlike M490. The compute shader is the one already used by the Android `mediacodec-wgpu` path (`shaders/mediacodec_ycbcr.comp.spv`: sample a ycbcr combined sampler, write RGBA), reused unchanged. The decode device now also requests a dedicated compute queue from a distinct compute family (preferring compute-without-graphics); `NoComputeQueue` if none, so the caller uses the M490 CPU path. `m491_vulkan_video_gpu_ycbcr` decodes the 640x480 fixture GPU-resident and reads the wgpu texture back: range 0..=255, mean 120 -- identical to M490's CPU conversion, confirming the GPU ycbcr is correct. Skips with no adapter / no compute queue. This completes the vendor-neutral hardware-decode-into-wgpu-texture path (the wgpu-viewer / Bevy story), still IDR-only; the `VulkanVideoDec` pipeline element and full DPB (P/B frames) remain.
- M490: Vulkan Video decode -> `wgpu::Texture`, the wedge payload (a decoded frame in the render device a game engine / visualization viewer samples). `VulkanVideoDevice::decode_idr_to_rgba_texture` decodes the IDR (M489), reads back the NV12 (now both planes: the decode copies `PLANE_0` luma + `PLANE_1` interleaved CbCr), converts NV12 -> RGBA on the CPU (BT.601 limited range), and uploads to an `Rgba8Unorm` texture on the decode device's own wgpu queue. `decode_idr_nv12` is the shared entry (returns `Nv12Frame`); `decode_idr_luma` is a thin wrapper. `read_rgba_texture` reads a texture back (handling wgpu's 256-byte row alignment) for validation / CPU consumers. `m490_vulkan_video_wgpu` decodes the 640x480 fixture into a wgpu texture, reads it back through wgpu, and asserts non-uniform content with opaque alpha (range 0..=255, mean 120 on the 3060); skips with no adapter. This proves the whole decode -> wgpu-texture path on one Vulkan device, vendor-neutral (no CUDA). NV12 -> RGBA is a CPU conversion here; the zero-copy GPU-resident `VkSamplerYcbcrConversion` path (keeping the frame on the GPU) and the `VulkanVideoDec` element are the next increments.
- M489: Vulkan Video H.264 IDR frame decode, producing real pixels on the RTX 3060. `VulkanVideoDevice::decode_idr_luma` creates the NV12 DPB/output image (coincide mode, decode target == DPB slot 0, with the video profile list chained into `VkImageCreateInfo`), a host-visible coded-bitstream `VkBuffer` holding the first IDR slice (framed with a start code; SPS/PPS come from the session parameters, not the bitstream), records `vkCmdBeginVideoCodingKHR` + a `RESET` control + `vkCmdDecodeVideoKHR` + `vkCmdEndVideoCodingKHR` on the decode queue with `synchronization2` image barriers (`PipelineStageFlags2::VIDEO_DECODE` / the video-decode layouts, which classic barriers cannot express, so `VK_KHR_synchronization2` is now enabled), then copies the luma plane to a readback buffer. IDR-only: the `Std*` picture info is the known constants (frame_num 0, POC 0, `IdrPicFlag`, DPB slot 0, no prior references), so no slice-header parse yet; full reference management is the next increment. `m489_vulkan_video_decode` decodes the 640x480 fixture's IDR and asserts the luma is non-uniform (range 16..=88, mean 73 on the 3060), i.e. the GPU produced a real picture, not a cleared buffer; skips with no adapter. A PSNR-vs-ffmpeg reference comparison is a later hardening step. This is the first end-to-end Vulkan Video decode in the tree; wiring the output `VkImage` to a `wgpu::Texture` (YCbCr->RGBA) and the `VulkanVideoDec` element remain.
- M488: Vulkan Video H.264 decode device + session + parameters, validated on the RTX 3060. `open_h264_decode_device` opens a `wgpu::Device` with the Vulkan Video decode extensions and a `VK_QUEUE_VIDEO_DECODE_BIT_KHR` queue, added through wgpu-hal's `open_with_callback` (which exposes `queue_create_infos`, so the decode queue is requested without building the `VkDevice` by hand), then reaches the raw `ash` device the cudawgpu way (`as_hal::<Vulkan>()`). `VulkanVideoDevice::create_h264_session` queries the decode picture format (`vkGetPhysicalDeviceVideoFormatPropertiesKHR`, NV12 `G8_B8R8_2PLANE_420_UNORM`), creates the `VkVideoSessionKHR`, allocates + binds its device memory (one allocation per requirement), and creates the `VkVideoSessionParametersKHR` carrying the Std SPS/PPS from M487. Creating the parameters makes the driver validate the `Std*` mapping, so `m488_vulkan_video_session` (opens the device, parses the 640x480 fixture, creates the session) is an end-to-end proof the mapping is correct on the GPU, not just self-consistent; it skips with no adapter. Gotcha settled: video-session memory requirements list types that are not all `DEVICE_LOCAL`, so the binding honors each requirement's `memory_type_bits` (preferring but not requiring device-local) rather than forcing a property flag. Remaining for a decoded frame: DPB + output images, the bitstream buffer, `vkCmdDecodeVideoKHR` with the per-frame `Std*` picture/slice info, and the VkImage->wgpu texture handoff.
- M487: H.264 SPS/PPS bitstream parse + `Std*` mapping for `VulkanVideoDec` (the correctness-critical half the design flags). Vulkan Video does not parse the bitstream: the driver takes the parameter sets as filled `StdVideoH264SequenceParameterSet` / `...PictureParameterSet` structs. `parse_h264_sps` / `parse_h264_pps` / `extract_h264_parameter_sets` read the RBSP (reusing the crate `annexb` bit-reader + emulation-prevention strip) into plain `H264Sps` / `H264Pps` structs, and `to_std_sps` / `to_std_pps` map those onto the `Std*` layout (bitfield flags via the bindgen setters, no scaling-list / VUI / ref-frame-offset pointers). Baseline / main / high 4:2:0 8-bit; unsupported features (custom scaling matrices, separate colour planes, POC-type-1 ref cycles, FMO slice groups) are rejected at parse rather than mis-decoded. GPU-free unit tests parse the real 640x480 baseline fixture to its correct macroblock geometry and confirm the `Std*` mapping preserves geometry/ids and sets no pointer fields. Next: the decode device (decode queue via `open_with_callback`), `VkVideoSession` + session parameters (driver-validated against this mapping), then the decode command.
- M486: Vulkan Video decode capability probe, the foundation increment of `VulkanVideoDec` (vendor-neutral GPU-resident hardware decode; DESIGN.md §4.11.6). New `vulkan-video` feature and `vulkanvideo` module. `probe_decode_caps(codec)` reaches the default Vulkan adapter's raw `ash` handles the way `cudawgpu` does (`wgpu::Instance` -> `as_hal::<Vulkan>()` -> `InstanceShared::entry()`/`raw_instance()` + `raw_physical_device()`), finds a `VK_QUEUE_VIDEO_DECODE_BIT_KHR` queue family that advertises the codec (via a `QueueFamilyVideoPropertiesKHR` chained onto `get_physical_device_queue_family_properties2`), verifies the device lists `VK_KHR_video_queue` + `_video_decode_queue` + the codec decode extension, and queries `vkGetPhysicalDeviceVideoCapabilitiesKHR` for H.264/H.265/AV1 (NV12 4:2:0 8-bit baseline profile). Returns the decode limits `intercept_caps` and DPB sizing will negotiate against: queue family, coded-extent range, DPB slot / active-reference budget, bitstream alignments, and the `DPB_AND_OUTPUT_COINCIDE` fast-path flag. Gotcha settled here (the load-bearing integration point the design says to prototype first): the query fails with a generic `ERROR_INITIALIZATION_FAILED` unless BOTH `VkVideoDecodeCapabilitiesKHR` and the codec-specific caps struct (`VkVideoDecodeH264/H265/AV1CapabilitiesKHR`) are chained into the output, plus a `VkVideoDecodeUsageInfoKHR` into the profile. Validated live on the RTX 3060 (`m486_vulkan_video_probe`, skips with no adapter / no support): H.264 up to 4096x4096 (17 DPB slots), H.265 and AV1 up to 8192x8192 (16 slots), all coincide. The decode session (device with a decode queue via `create_from_hal`, `Std*` SPS/PPS mapping, DPB, `vkCmdDecodeVideoKHR`, VkImage->wgpu texture) is the next increment.
- M485: caps ranges/lists in launch caps filters + per-edge queue depth (the two headline gst-launch on-ramp gaps). (1) An inline caps filter now accepts GStreamer range and list syntax: `video/x-raw,width=[1,1920],height=[1,1080],format={I420,NV12}`. `parse_caps_set` splits on top-level commas only (so the commas inside `[..]`/`{..}` are kept), parses each field as fixed / `[min,max]` range / `{a,b}` list, maps a range to `Dim::Range` / `Rate::Range` in one caps, and expands lists to the cartesian product of alternatives in the `CapsSet` (which the capsfilter already carried and the solver already narrows). A malformed range/list now fails the caps (rejected, not silently dropped). (2) `queue max-size-buffers=N` sets the depth of the edge it contracts to, overriding the runner's graph-wide `link_capacity` for just that link (the gst per-queue bound); `0` (gst "unbounded") and the other bounds (`max-size-bytes`/`-time`) are still ignored. New `Edge.capacity: Option<usize>` + `Graph::link_full`; `build_channels` sizes each edge channel from it. The caps error hint and PORTING.md "unsupported syntax" table are updated (ranges/lists moved to supported; only caps features `(memory:...)`, bins, and network-demux-fanout remain listed).
- M484: gst-launch on-ramp papercuts for porting GStreamer devs. (1) `#` comments: a `#` outside quotes runs to end of line and is ignored, so a pasted multi-line pipeline with annotations parses. (2) Single-quoted values: `location='/my file.ts'` works like the double-quoted form (the tokenizer treats `'…'` as one token and `consume_element` strips either quote via `strip_quotes`). (3) Sharper caps error: an inline caps filter with range/list/feature syntax (`video/x-raw,width=[1,1920]`) still fails, but the `BadValue` now explains why (fixed fields only; ranges/lists/features unsupported in a launch caps filter) instead of a bare "invalid value". (4) Fixed stale `gst_compat` NVIDIA mappings: `nvh264enc`/`nvh265enc` -> `nvenc` (previously wrongly "no NVENC element"), `nvh264dec`/`nvh265dec` -> `nvdec`, matching the VAAPI rows. (5) PORTING.md gains a "Launch syntax g2g does not accept" table (caps ranges/lists/features, bins, per-queue depth, network demux fan-out) with the rewrite for each.
- M483: opt-in multicore graph runner (thread-per-arm), the GStreamer streaming-thread model. `run_graph_threaded(graph, clock, cap, spawner)` negotiates a DAG identically to the cooperative `run_graph` (the `prepare_graph` / `build_channels` / `fold_run_stats` phases are now shared helpers, so the two drivers cannot diverge) but hands each arm to a `GraphSpawner` to run on its own OS thread instead of cooperatively multiplexing them, so CPU-bound stages (software decode/encode) overlap across cores. It needs no `Send` futures: the spawner gets a `Send` *builder closure* and constructs + drives the arm's `!Send` future entirely on the worker thread, so only the element + channels (both `Send` under `multi-thread`) cross the boundary and a hardware element with a `!Send` future runs unchanged. Two spawners: core's dependency-free `ThreadSpawner` (std threads + park-based `block_on`) and `g2g-plugins`' `TokioThreadSpawner` (per-arm current-thread tokio runtime with `enable_all`, for network/timer elements). `g2g-launch --threads` selects it; cooperative single-thread stays the default (lower per-frame latency, and the only path for `no_std`/wasm/embassy, which the `std + multi-thread` gate excludes). Parity test `m483_threaded_runner` proves threaded == cooperative frame counts on the same pipeline. DESIGN.md §4.13.3.
- M482: `decodebin name=d` fan-out in a `gst-launch` line, the decode-per-port sibling of the M476 demux fan-out. `filesrc location=movie.mp4 ! decodebin name=d  d.video_0 ! videoconvert ! sink  d.audio_0 ! audioconvert ! sink` probes the container, builds the multi-output demuxer, and auto-plugs a decoder onto each requested port, so every `d.` branch receives DECODED (raw) frames (`d.video_0`/`d.audio_0`/`d.text_0` typed refs and bare positional `d.`, in any order). g2g's `decodebin` resolves statically at parse time (no runtime `pad-added`), so it learns its pads by probing the file, the static-graph analog of GStreamer's runtime `typefind`+`pad-added`. New `DecodebinSelectHook` (`fn(location, pads) -> Option<(demuxer, per-port caps)>`, registered via `Registry::register_decodebin_select`); container hooks (`mkv`/`ts`/`mp4_decodebin_select`) share the M476 selection logic (refactored into `*_select` helpers, M476 behavior byte-for-byte). `expand_decodebin` leaves a name-referenced (fan-out) `decodebin` unexpanded; `build_graph` runs the hooks, builds the demux, and splices `reg.decodebin` onto each A/V port (a text port carries `Text{Utf8}` and links straight through). Multi-stream containers only (a linear `filesrc ! decodebin ! sink` stays the M196 single-stream path). Live-validated: an A/V MP4 decodes both branches to raw (video + audio), in either reference order.
- M481: named input / request pads on muxers, the input-side transpose of M476's output-pad selection. A `gst-launch` line references a muxer's inputs by name instead of by branch order: `... ! o.video   ... ! o.text   textoverlay name=o ! ...` and `... ! m.audio_0   ... ! m.video_0   matroskamux name=m ! ...` route by name in either order. New `MultiInputElement::input_pad_index(req, ordinal)` (dyn-mirrored on `DynMultiInputElement`) maps a parsed `PadRequest` (`video_%u` / `audio_%u` / `text_%u` / `sink_%u`) to a concrete input index per the element's own scheme; default is positional (`sink_%u` -> its index, a bare `m.` -> ordinal), a typed pad declines unless the element defines it. `TextOverlayN` maps `video -> 0` / `text -> 1` (so the video pad stays input 0 regardless of reference order, keeping `output_follows_input(0)` and the PTS merge valid); container A/V muxers (`matroskamux` / `mp4mux` / `mpegtsmux` / `flvmux`) accept the names positionally (their slots are caps-typed). The parser records the destination pad suffix (previously discarded), resolves it at muxer construction, and reports `DuplicateInputPad` / `UnknownInputPad`. Bare `m.` refs keep the historical sequential-by-order behavior, so existing fan-in lines are unchanged.
- M480: parse-time content sniff for `decodebin`, so `filesrc location=X bytestream-format=auto ! decodebin` picks the demuxer from the file's real content even when the extension lies (a `.ts` that is actually an MP4 now decodes), the way GStreamer's runtime `typefind` does. New `SourceLoop::probe_output_caps(&mut self)` (dyn-mirrored on `DynSourceLoop`): like `configured_output_caps` but permitted to do I/O, called once by the `decodebin` expansion (`resolve_upstream_caps`) to choose the demuxer. `FileSrc` overrides it to run the `auto` header sniff at parse time; a missing/unreadable file leaves it unresolved (falls back to the declared default, no parse failure). Previously `auto` resolved only at negotiation, too late for the parse-time demuxer choice, so `auto ! decodebin` mis-plugged from the stale default. Extension typing (M478) still trusts the name when `auto` is not set; a mislabeled file without `auto` needs an explicit `bytestream-format=`.
- M479: progressive / whole-file MP4 through a linear chain, so `filesrc location=X.mp4 ! decodebin` and `filesrc location=X.mp4 ! qtdemux ! h264parse ! ...` run for a plain (non-fragmented) MP4. New `ByteStreamEncoding::Mp4` (whole-file / QuickTime) distinct from `IsoBmff` (streaming CMAF): a file is seekable and its `moov` may sit at the end with absolute `stco` offsets, so it is demuxed after the whole file is buffered, whereas HLS / DASH fragments must be demuxed incrementally. New single-output `Mp4Demux` element (`g2g-plugins/src/mp4demux.rs`): `ByteStream{Mp4}` -> the video track's Annex-B access units, reusing `fmp4::parse_header` + `parse_progressive`, advertising a fixatable `Range` placeholder (like `tsdemux` / `matroskademux`) and refining to the concrete moov geometry via `CapsChanged`. Registered as `qtdemux` in both the launch registry and the `decodebin` autoplug pool. `filesrc` now types `.mp4`/`.mov`/`.m4v`/`.qt` (and a `bytestream-format=auto` MP4 sniff) as `Mp4`, and `bytestream-format=mp4` maps to `Mp4` (the streaming form is `isobmff`/`cmaf`/`fmp4`). `Mp4DemuxN` accepts both `Mp4` and `IsoBmff`, so the `qtdemux name=d d.video_0 ! ... d.audio_0 ! ...` fan-out and the multi-stream playbin still work; a single-branch `qtdemux name=d d.video_0` (or bare `! qtdemux !`) falls to the single-output `Mp4Demux` for a video-only file. The fragmented path is untouched: `IsoBmff` still auto-plugs `fmp4demux`, which HLS / DASH rely on. Whole-file demux buffers to `Eos` before emitting (fine for files, not for a live stream). Live-validated end to end: `filesrc ! decodebin ! videoconvert ! textoverlay` subtitle overlay on a 1080p progressive MP4.
- M478: content/extension typefind, so a GStreamer-style `filesrc` line runs without naming the container or subtitle format. `typefind::sniff` gained ISO-BMFF/MP4 detection (`ftyp`/`moov`/`mdat`/... top-level box, progressive and fragmented both -> `IsoBmff`); a new `typefind::sniff_caps` also sniffs subtitle documents by content (WebVTT signature, SSA/ASS section, TTML root, SubRip comma-decimal `-->` arrow) and returns a `Caps` (a container `ByteStream` or a `Text` format). `filesrc bytestream-format=auto` uses `sniff_caps`, so it now recognizes MP4 and `.vtt`/`.srt`/`.ssa`/`.ttml` (feeding `subparse`), not just the M112 container set. A bare launch `filesrc` (no `bytestream-format`) now derives its type from the `location` extension (`FileSrc::untyped` + `caps_from_extension`): `.mp4`/`.m4v`/`.mov` -> `IsoBmff`, `.mkv`/`.webm` -> Matroska, `.ts`/`.m2ts` -> MPEG-TS, `.ogg`/`.opus` -> Ogg, `.flv` -> FLV, `.vtt`/`.srt`/`.ass`/`.ttml` -> the matching `Caps::Text`. So `filesrc location=subs.vtt ! subparse` and `filesrc location=movie.mkv ! matroskademux name=d ...` type with no hint. Regression-safe: string-only (no filesystem read at parse), `.ts` keeps the MPEG-TS default, an unknown/extensionless name falls back to it, and an explicit `bytestream-format` still pins the type (a later `location` won't re-type). NOTE: `filesrc ! decodebin` on a *progressive* single-file MP4 still needs a progressive-MP4 demuxer in the autoplug pool (`Fmp4Demux` is fragmented-only); `uridecodebin uri=file://...` demuxes progressive MP4 via `Mp4Src` today.
- M477: subtitle handling in a `gst-launch` line. `subparse` (structured subtitle document -> timed `Text{Utf8}` cues) is now a launch element, and `textoverlay` doubles as a video + text-stream fan-in muxer (`TextOverlayN`, the analog of GStreamer's `textoverlay` text_sink request pad), picked by link degree the same way `mpegtsmux` is both a single-input element and a fan-in muxer. A subtitle-overlay line parses end to end: `videotestsrc ! o.  subtitlesrc location=x.srt ! subparse ! o.  textoverlay name=o ! ...` (video on pad 0, text on pad 1). The M476 explicit-demux fan-out also selects an embedded subtitle track by pad name: `d.text_0` / `d.subtitle_0` maps to the k-th subtitle stream (appended after the A/V streams in selection order) for `matroskademux` (`S_TEXT/*` -> `Text{Utf8}`) and `qtdemux` (`tx3g`/`wvtt` -> `Text{Utf8}`, `stpp` -> `Text{Ttml}` through a following `subparse`); MPEG-TS has no demuxer subtitle track so a TS text pad declines. The `resolve_pads` selector generalized from a per-stream video flag to a `PadKind` list, so `video_k` / `audio_k` / `text_k` / positional `src_k` resolve uniformly.
- M476: explicit-demux fan-out in a `gst-launch` line (Phase 2 of demuxer stream selection). A named demuxer fed by a file source, `filesrc location=movie.mkv ! matroskademux name=d  d.video_0 ! h264parse ! avdec_h264 ! sink  d.audio_0 ! aacparse ! sink`, now splits the file into its elementary streams instead of erroring, honoring GStreamer's `video_0` / `audio_0` / `src_N` pad-name selection (a bare `d.` is positional). Mirrors the `playbin` hook so the g2g-core parser stays container-agnostic: a new `DemuxSelectHook` slot on `Registry` (`register_demux_select`); the parser retains demux pad-name suffixes, parses them into ordered `PadRequest`s, and for a fan-out demux with a file upstream calls the hooks to build the multi-output demuxer (one port per pad, in reference order), wiring each user branch to its port; `matroskademux` / `tsdemux` / `qtdemux` hooks in `uridecodebin` probe the file (`forwardable_streams`), resolve each request to a concrete stream, and build `MkvDemuxN` / `TsDemuxN` / `Mp4DemuxN`. Named selection is by media kind regardless of container order (a swapped-reference-order test proves `video_0` still routes video). File sources only; a network source still uses `playbin`. Text/subtitle demux pads and non-file sources decline. Routing fidelity is proved by a strict parser per branch (`h264parse` / `aacparse`) for all three containers. `qtdemux` is a demux-fan-out-only name (single-output MP4 stays on `Mp4Src` / `playbin`).
- M475: app-driven stream selection on the MPEG-TS and MP4 multi-output demuxers, bringing `TsDemuxN` and `Mp4DemuxN` to parity with `MkvDemuxN` (M381). Both gain `with_stream_select(StreamSelectController)`: after the demuxer announces its streams (the `StreamCollection` on the bus, M386), the app names the stream id each port should carry, and the demuxer re-maps its ports before the next batch, re-arming each changed port's `CapsChanged` (MP4 also re-owes the `moov` parameter sets) and confirming the active ids via `BusMessage::StreamsSelected`. TS resolves `"mpegts-pid-{pid}"` ids against the PMT and routes by `stream_type` (two same-codec streams share a port, as in MKV); MP4 resolves `"mp4-track-{id}"` and routes by `track_ID`, so same-codec tracks are distinguishable (a superset). Phase 1 of demuxer stream selection; the gst-launch named-pad path (`d.video_0`) is a separate follow-on. Tested by swapping a two-port [video, audio] demux to [audio, video] mid-stream for both containers.
- M474: worked gst-launch <-> g2g example program (`g2g-plugins/examples/gst_equivalents.rs`), the runnable counterpart to the PORTING.md cookbook. For each recipe (a transform chain, an inline caps filter, a `tee` fan-out) it runs the SAME pipeline two ways, the `gst-launch` text through `parse_launch` and the equivalent hand-built typed `Graph`, and asserts they produce the same frame count, so a porting GStreamer user sees the text-DSL-to-Rust-API mapping proven side by side. Baseline `std` elements only (runs anywhere); linked from PORTING.md §5.
- M473: `parse_launch` auto-inserts a `tee` on fan-out. A non-tee, non-demux node whose output feeds several branches (`... name=s ! sinkA  s. ! sinkB`) previously failed with `FanOutWithoutTee`; the parser now splices a broadcast `tee` onto that node's output (its single output feeds the tee, the tee's pads feed the consumers, per-branch `queue` policies preserved), so a gst-launch line that omits the explicit tee still builds and runs. A registered demuxer still fans out on its own routing pads (the exemption only picks which fan-out primitive is used). Removed the now-dead `ParseError::FanOutWithoutTee` variant and its porting hint. Covered in `m118_launch_branching` (build + run + one `Tee(2)` spliced in; per-branch leaky queue) and `m210_demux_node` (unregistered fan-out gets a broadcast tee).
- M472: `g2g-inspect` now dumps a fan-in muxer's Factory Details. The muxer inspect path previously printed only the name and role because it built no instance (so it could read no property table); it now constructs a one-input instance (the fan-in constructors are side-effect-free) and shows its metadata, output caps, and `Element Properties` the same as the source / launch paths. Needed a `metadata()` method on `MultiInputElement` (defaulting empty, mirrored onto `DynMultiInputElement`); `funnel` (`InterleaveMux`) and `audiomixer` (`AudioMixer`) gained real metadata blocks. The dual-registered container muxers (`mp4mux` / `mpegtsmux` / `matroskamux` / `flvmux`) already inspected via their single-input launch registration; this closes the muxer-only names. Closes the DESIGN_TODO introspection item.
- M471: fan-in muxer property parity. The multi-input muxer variants now expose the same runtime properties as their single-input siblings, wired to real behavior, so the A/V muxing shape (`... name=m`) honors the knobs the single-input shape already did (previously `apply_muxer_props` rejected them with `UnknownProperty` because the N-input `properties()` was empty). `tsmuxn` gains `pat-interval`/`pmt-interval` (forwarded to `TsMuxer::set_table_interval_90khz`, re-emitting the PAT/PMT at the cadence); `mkvmuxn` gains `streamable` (suppresses the EOS `Cues` index); `mp4muxn` gains `fragment-duration`, which required real multi-sample fragmentation: a track's access units now batch into a multi-sample `trun`, closed at the next sync sample once the target is reached and flushed at EOS, versus one fragment per AU by default (the `0` default is byte-for-byte unchanged). Per-module behavior tests plus parse-path tests in `m208_launch_ts_av_fanin` (the fan-in shape accepts each knob and still rejects an unknown one).
- M470: README "Coming from GStreamer?" on-ramp (runnable `g2g-launch` quick-start + `-v`/`--dot`/`g2g-inspect`/bridge pointers) and a PORTING.md equivalence cookbook of verbatim gst-launch lines backed by the M469 corpus; fixed the stale "spaces in property values fail" note (M467's quote-aware tokenizer closed that).
- M469: gst-launch equivalence corpus (`g2g-plugins/tests/gst_launch_corpus.rs`), a regression guard turning "g2g accepts gst-launch syntax" into a checked guarantee. Two halves: **portable** lines (canonical GStreamer recipes over the baseline `std` registry: inline caps, `tee` branches + `queue`, caps-driven `videoscale`/`videorate`, quoted spaced `filesrc location`, an audio chain) must `parse_launch` into a runnable graph and lint clean (no false-positive porting findings), with a representative subset also run end to end (asserting the frame count, e.g. a two-sink `tee` consumes each frame twice); **needs-porting** lines (`theoraenc`, `x265enc`, which have no g2g equivalent under any feature) must be flagged by `lint_launch` with feature-stable guidance. Surfaced a real divergence in passing: g2g's `textoverlay` is subtitle-file-driven (`location`/`font`/`color`), with no static `text=` property like GStreamer's, so the linter reports `text=` as an unknown property (a candidate follow-up: add a static-text property for gst-launch parity).
- M468: `g2g-launch -v` now prints each link's **negotiated caps** + memory domain + `LinkPolicy` (the gst `-v` analog), instead of the previous topology-only wiring list. It reuses the same `runtime::negotiate_graph` caps solve the `--dot` dump uses: since that call consumes a graph, `-v` negotiates a freshly-parsed throwaway copy and keeps the original for the run, and falls back to the topology-only list (with a note) if negotiation fails. Turns the static-negotiation result into something a porter can read at the CLI (e.g. seeing a format flip to NV12 exactly at `videoconvert`). Doc'd in DEVTOOLS.md + PORTING.md.
- M467: quote-aware `gst-launch` tokenizer, closing the launch DSL v1 gap where a property value could not contain spaces. `runtime::parse_launch` now tokenizes with a small state machine that treats a double-quoted `"..."` region as one token, so whitespace *and* `!` inside a value are literal (`gstwrap element="x264enc bitrate=4000"`, `filesrc location="/my file.ts"`, a value containing `!`); the surrounding quotes are stripped from the value as before. Replaces the previous `replace('!', " ! ")` + `split_whitespace()` shortcut. This makes `gstwrap` (M466) usable from `g2g-launch` with a multi-word element description, not only via the programmatic API; validated by a new `videotestsrc ! gstwrap element="videoflip method=horizontal-flip" ! fakesink` run test plus `tokenize` / `parse_chains` unit tests (spaces and `!` inside quotes).
- M466: `gstwrap`, the reverse GStreamer bridge (DESIGN.md §7): a g2g `AsyncElement` that hosts an un-ported GStreamer element *inside* a g2g graph, the mirror of `g2g-bridge` (which embeds g2g inside a GStreamer app). The incremental-migration path in the g2g-as-top-framework direction: adopt g2g now and keep un-ported stages running as real GStreamer elements. The `element` property is a GStreamer element description (`videoflip method=horizontal-flip`, `x264enc bitrate=4000`); internally it drives `appsrc ! <element> ! appsink` in a real GStreamer pipeline on GStreamer's own streaming threads, copying each `System` frame into a `GstBuffer` (`gst_app_src_push_buffer`), draining ready output non-blockingly (`gst_app_sink_try_pull_sample`, 0 timeout), and flushing on EOS. Caps translate via the existing `Caps::to_gst_string()` (→ appsrc caps) and `parse_caps()` (an `output-caps` property → the caps a reformatting encoder/scaler produces; a preserving element declares nothing and couples input == output via `IdentityAny`, a reformatting one uses `DerivedOutput`); emit reuses `encoder_base::emit_packets`. C interop mirrors the bridge shell: a helper (`g2g-plugins/csrc/gstwrap_host.c`, built by a new gated `build.rs` via pkg-config + `cc` over gstreamer-1.0 / gstreamer-app-1.0) driven from `src/gstwrap.rs` over a C ABI; the pipeline handle is `Send` (appsrc/appsink are MT-safe). Behind a new `gstreamer` feature (implies std). v1 is system-memory (copy each way); dma-buf zero-copy through it is future work. Validated locally (`cargo test -p g2g-plugins --features gstreamer --test gstwrap`, not CI) by hosting a real `videoflip` and asserting the pixels come back horizontally flipped. (A multi-word `element="..."` from `g2g-launch` needed the quote-aware tokenizer that landed in M467.)
- M465: the GStreamer bridge shell's zero-copy dma-buf round-trip, wiring both sides so a dma-buf `GstBuffer` flows through an embedded g2g sub-graph and comes back out as a dma-buf `GstBuffer` with no pixel copy. The `glass2glass` data path is now a single `generate_output` override (replacing `transform`/`transform_ip`), so the output buffer may differ from the input in both size and memory kind: on input it detects `gst_is_dmabuf_memory` and imports the fd via `g2g_bridge_push_dmabuf` (else maps + copies as before); on output the FFI `G2gOut` gained a `kind` discriminant (system bytes vs dma-buf fd/stride/offset) and the shell wraps a dma-buf output frame back into a `GstBuffer` via `gst_dmabuf_allocator_alloc` (the fd dup'ed, so the g2g frame and the GstBuffer own independent descriptors). `g2g_bridge_pull_buf` now returns a `DmaBuf` frame instead of erroring (`-2` is reserved for a domain that is neither system nor dma-buf). Links `gstreamer-allocators-1.0`; `set_caps` records the input plane stride and output height (a dma-buf carries no byte length). New `tools/gst-bridge-dmabuf-smoke.sh` validates the full round-trip end to end with a memfd wrapped as dma-buf memory (`dma-buf in -> glass2glass(identity) -> dma-buf out`), no special hardware needed; the system-memory smoke (`tools/gst-bridge-smoke.sh`) passes unchanged through the new path (identity/flip/videoconvert/videoscale/format-change). Remaining for a GPU-*compute* round-trip (`dmabuftowgpu ! <compute>`): a `WgpuBuffer -> System`/`DmaBuf` download/export element at the fragment tail so that leg's GPU output returns to the shell (which already hands both system and dma-buf frames back).

- M464: `dmabuftowgpu`, the GPU-consuming dma-buf element that completes the import side of the DESIGN.md §7 zero-copy story (M463 was ingest-only, with no consumer). It takes a `MemoryDomain::DmaBuf` frame and imports it into a GPU-resident `wgpu::Buffer` with no CPU copy: `VK_EXT_external_memory_dma_buf` + `vkAllocateMemory(ImportMemoryFdInfoKHR)` bind the fd to a `VkBuffer`, which `wgpu_hal::vulkan::Buffer::from_raw_managed` + `Device::create_buffer_from_hal` wrap into a `wgpu::Buffer` (wgpu then owns the imported memory and closes the dup'ed fd on drop). Output is `MemoryDomain::WgpuBuffer`, so a bridge fragment `dmabuftowgpu ! <wgpu compute>` runs the imported buffer on the GPU; `input_domains` = `DmaBuf` so the M354 auto-plug splices it where an upstream produces dma-buf. Gated behind a new `dmabuf-wgpu` feature (wgpu + wgpu-hal + ash, no libcamera dependency). **Validated on an RTX 3060**: a new test exports device-local GPU memory as a dma-buf fd (`VkExportMemoryAllocateInfo` + `vkGetMemoryFdKHR`) and re-imports it through the element, asserting a `WgpuBuffer` frame whose keep-alive owns a real `wgpu::Buffer` aliasing the imported memory. This settles the open hardware question from `libcamera_dmabuf` (a dGPU cannot bind a CPU/vmalloc-backed camera dma-buf, but it *can* bind a GPU-visible one); the element returns `UnsupportedDomain` when the driver cannot bind rather than producing a wrong result. Remaining for a fully automatic GStreamer round-trip (documented, GPU-track): the shell auto-routing dma-buf input to `g2g_bridge_push_dmabuf`, and an output-side `DmaBuf`/GPU -> `GstBuffer` wrap-back.

- M463: zero-copy DMABUF import into the bridge, the ingest half of the DESIGN.md §7 dma-buf story. `appsrc` now accepts a frame in any memory domain, not just system memory: `AppItem` carries a `MemoryDomain`, and `AppSrcFeed::push_dmabuf(OwnedDmaBuf, pts)` feeds an imported dma-buf frame (the run loop builds the `Frame` from the domain directly). `BridgeGraph::push_dmabuf` exposes it, and the C-ABI `g2g_bridge_push_dmabuf(bridge, fd, stride, offset, pts)` `dup`s a GStreamer buffer's dma-buf fd (GStreamer retains the original; g2g's `OwnedDmaBuf` closes only the dup, so the two lifetimes are independent) and imports it with no pixel copy. New `g2g-bridge` test drives a dma-buf frame through an `identity` sub-graph and asserts it stays in the `DmaBuf` domain end to end (placeholder fd; `identity` does not read pixels). Deliberately *not* wired into the C shell's default `transform`/`transform_ip`: a `DmaBuf` frame needs a fragment element that **consumes** the domain (a GPU import) and an output side that **wraps** a produced `DmaBuf` back into a `GstBuffer`; neither exists yet, so auto-routing dma-buf would strand the frame. `g2g_bridge_push_dmabuf` is the ready import primitive; the consuming element + output wrap-back are the remaining GPU-track work. The `AppItem` generalization is behavior-neutral for the system path (m233 appsrc/appsink and the C-ABI app-roundtrip suites pass unchanged).

- M462: a "port my app" source scanner, `gst_compat::scan_source` behind `g2g-inspect --gst-scan <file>`, the app-code counterpart to the launch-line linter (M461). It statically reads a GStreamer *application* source (C or Python) and reports the element factories it instantiates that are not portable as-is, plus the dynamic-pipeline APIs it uses. Element names come from `gst_element_factory_make("x", ...)`, `Gst.ElementFactory.make("x")`, and every element inside a `gst_parse_launch("...")` / `Gst.parse_launch("...")` literal (best-effort: a call passing a *variable* pipeline string is skipped rather than mis-grabbing a later literal, so no phantom findings); each distinct name is classified via `gst_equivalent` (renamed / unsupported / unknown, deduped and sorted). It also flags dynamic idioms with a pointer to PORTING.md §5.1: `pad-added` relink, `pad_add_probe`, and appsrc/appsink usage. `g2g-inspect --gst-scan app.c` prints the elements needing attention and the notes, exiting non-zero if any element is unportable. Findings reflect the feature set the tool was compiled with (a feature-gated element absent from the build reads as unknown, same as the launch linter). Two tests cover a C source (renamed + unsupported elements, pad-added note, available element not flagged) and a Python source (registered `appsink`, and a variable `parse_launch` producing no phantom findings). Pure `no_std + alloc` string scanning, no new deps.

- M461: the launch linter (`gst_compat::lint_launch`, behind `g2g-launch`'s explain-on-error) now reports *every* unportable element in a pipeline line at once, not just the first the parser trips on, so porting a multi-element line is one pass instead of fix-one-rerun. It scans each `!`-separated segment's element name (skipping inline caps filters, `t.` tee branch refs, and stray `key=value` tokens) and collects gst->g2g guidance for all that are renamed / unsupported / unknown; only when every element resolves does it fall back to the authoritative `parse_launch` for a structural / property / caps error (reported singly, as before). `g2g-launch "videotestsrc ! theoraenc ! x265enc ! fakesink"` now surfaces both `theoraenc` and `x265enc` hints together. New tests cover the all-at-once report, a renamed element flagged with its g2g name in a line, and that caps filters / tee branches are not mistaken for elements. No behavior change for portable lines.

- M460: porting-smoothness pass (docs + lint accuracy), the non-bridge levers from the GStreamer-transition analysis. (1) `gst_compat` lint: the `x264enc` fallback hint claimed "no software H.264 encoder", but `FfmpegH264Enc`'s `Software` backend (libx264) has shipped since M266 and `x264enc` is a registered element behind the `ffmpeg` feature; the hint now points at that feature (and `nvenc`/`mfencode`/AV1 alternatives), and `x265enc` likewise. (2) `PORTING.md` refreshed from its stale M217 stamp to M459: the "Things you may need to change" table and error-hint example corrected (x264enc is `ffmpeg`-feature not "unknown"; the unsupported-element example is now `theoraenc`); `appsrc`/`appsink` documented as the named launch elements they became in M233 (the doc still said "no g2g element"); §8 known-gaps rewritten for current reality (Android device-validated, macOS started-but-unverified, SRT/RTP-FEC/WebRTC in, RTMP/RTSP-server/RTX still open; bridge both layers done). (3) New `PORTING.md` §5.1 "Dynamic pipelines (the hardest port)": maps the GObject-app idioms (appsrc/appsink, `pad-added` relink, `pad_block` probes, runtime branch add/remove, A/B switch, element hot-swap, flushing seek, child→parent notify) onto g2g's primitives (`DynamicFanoutHandle`/`DynamicFaninHandle`, `StreamDemux`/`register_demux`, `LinkInterceptor`, `Router`/`Gate`, `ElementSlot::swap`, `PipelinePacket::Flush`, bus messages), keyed to DESIGN.md §4.9; cites only APIs verified present in the tree (design-only `SwapPolicy`/`ShadowWarm` are flagged as design-surface, not promised). No behavior change; the lint message edit is covered by the existing `unknown_encoder_gets_a_suggestion` test.

- M459: caps/size-changing fragments in the GStreamer bridge, lifting the M458 in-place-only limit, so an embedded g2g sub-graph can rescale or reformat: `... ! glass2glass fragment=videoscale output-caps="video/x-raw,format=RGBA,width=640,height=360,framerate=30/1" ! ...`, or a format change (`fragment=videoconvert output-caps=...,format=I420,...`). The `glass2glass` element gains an `output-caps` property; the C shell now also overrides `transform_caps` (advertises `output-caps` on the src pad sink->src, ANY src->sink since an arbitrary fragment cannot be inverted), `get_unit_size` (output buffer size via `gst_video_info_from_caps`, so planar formats size correctly), and a non-in-place `transform` (`inbuf`->`outbuf`) alongside the existing `transform_ip`; GstBaseTransform picks in-place for a caps-preserving fragment (the fast path, unchanged) and the out-of-place path when caps differ. `BridgeGraph` gains `with_output_caps(fragment, in, out)` (the trailing inline caps filter is pinned to the output caps instead of echoing the input), and the C-ABI `g2g_bridge_create` takes an `out_caps` arg (null = same as input). Links `gstreamer-video-1.0`. Tests: `g2g-bridge/tests/bridge_graph.rs` gains a rescale case (8x8 RGBA -> 4x4, 256 -> 64 bytes); `tools/gst-bridge-smoke.sh` gains downscale (64x64->32x16, 2048 bytes) and format-change (RGBA->I420, 6144 bytes) checks, all passing live against host GStreamer 1.26. The preserving in-place path is unchanged. Remaining bridge follow-up: zero-copy `GstDmaBufMemory` -> `OwnedDmaBuf` import (today buffers are mapped and copied).

- M458: the GStreamer GObject shell (`libgstglass2glass.so`), layer 2 of the bridge, so a stock `gst-launch` / GStreamer application can drop an embedded g2g sub-graph in by element name: `... ! glass2glass fragment="videoflip method=horizontal-flip" ! ...`. A thin C shim (`csrc/gstglass2glass.c`, built by `build.rs` via pkg-config + `cc`, gated behind a `gstreamer` feature) registers a `GstBaseTransform` subclass and includes the real GStreamer headers so the GObject struct layouts are correct by construction (no hand-transcribed vtables, the trap the project's C-probe FFI rule exists to avoid); it delegates all work to the C-ABI functions in `src/ffi.rs`, which drive one `BridgeGraph` per element instance (`set_caps` builds it from the `fragment` property + serialized sink caps, `transform_ip` pushes each buffer and copies back the one processed frame, `stop` tears it down). Key discovery while wiring the plugin entry points: rustc exports only its own `#[no_mangle]` symbols from a cdylib and localizes anything pulled from a static C archive, so a C `GST_PLUGIN_DEFINE` descriptor is invisible to GStreamer's loader; the `GstPluginDesc` and the `gst_plugin_glass2glass_get_desc` / `_register` entry points the loader resolves (by the `libgst<name>.so` filename) are therefore authored in Rust, pointing at the C `plugin_init` (the gst-plugins-rs approach). v1 is an in-place transform: the fragment must preserve caps and buffer size (a wgpu effect, videoflip, videoconvert, an ML preprocessor that keeps the pixel format); `BridgeGraph` pins the sub-graph output caps equal to the input to enforce that. Surfaced and fixed a latent `appsink` bug: `configure_pipeline` claimed its delivery mode with an unconditional `SINKS.remove`, so a caps-changing upstream transform (which makes the runner cascade caps a second time) re-ran the claim and clobbered the already-taken sender with `None`, after which every frame was silently dropped and EOS never forwarded; the claim is now idempotent. New `g2g-plugins/tests/appsink_reconfigure.rs` (`appsrc ! videoconvert ! appsink`, pull mode) guards the fix; `g2g-bridge/tests/bridge_graph.rs` gains a caps-driven-transform case. `tools/gst-bridge-smoke.sh` builds the plugin and asserts real data flow through `gst-launch` (frames sized right; `videoconvert` == identity; `videoflip` != identity; `flip!flip` byte-exact identity) end to end. Validated locally against host GStreamer 1.26; the `gstreamer` feature links the system gstreamer-1.0 / gstreamer-base-1.0, so like the other host-coupled paths it is built and smoke-tested locally, not in CI. Caps/size-changing fragments (output-buffer allocation + g2g->GstCaps mapping) remain future work.

- M457: the GStreamer bridge's impedance core (`g2g-bridge`, DESIGN.md §7), the incremental-migration path for a GStreamer *application* (a dynamic pipeline built against the `GstElement` C API, the hardest port; a `gst-launch` line already runs through `g2g-launch`). The new `BridgeGraph` embeds an isolated g2g sub-graph: it wraps a user launch fragment as `appsrc ! <fragment> ! appsink`, runs it on a dedicated OS thread with its own current-thread tokio runtime, and exposes a synchronous push/pull API (`push`/`try_pull`/`pull_blocking`/`end_of_stream`) that GStreamer's streaming thread drives from its `chain` function, neither side blocking the other (the bounded-channel sync/async match §7 calls for). Reuses the already-tested `appsrc`/`appsink` elements as that boundary rather than reinventing it; collision-free per-instance channel names via an atomic counter (no clock/RNG, respecting the no_std policy); `Drop`/`finish` release the drain before signalling EOS and joining, so an un-drained graph cannot deadlock on shutdown. Needs `multi-thread` (the boxed graph must be `Send` to move to the run thread, mirroring `g2g-capi`). New `g2g-bridge/tests/bridge_graph.rs` covers the cross-thread round-trip (buffers and PTS survive `appsrc ! identity ! appsink`), an unknown element surfacing as a `BridgeError::Parse` (the porting diagnostic an app developer sees), and deadlock-free drop without draining. This is layer 1 of 2: the GObject `GstBaseTransform` shell (`libgstglass2glass.so`, mapping `GstBuffer`/`GstCaps` to/from g2g and registering `glass2glass` as a real GStreamer element) is the follow-up, gated separately since it needs a live `gst-launch` to validate.

- M456: streaming-muxer parity, the muxer half of the M455 mid-stream work. `mp4mux` gains `fragment-duration` (milliseconds, `0` = one fragment per AU, the default): the `Fmp4Muxer` now batches access units into a single multi-sample `moof`+`mdat` and closes the fragment at the next sync sample once the target duration is reached, so each fragment begins at a keyframe (the CMAF / DASH segment shape) instead of the per-AU `moof`+`mdat` that bloats box overhead at low fps / high bitrate; the final partial fragment is flushed at EOS. The single-sample `fragment()` writer became a multi-sample one (a `trun` with N per-sample duration/size/flags entries and one concatenated `mdat`); the default per-AU path is byte-compatible (all existing mp4 mux / fmp4 demux round-trip tests pass unchanged). `matroskamux` gains `streamable` (the gst property): in live mode it omits the seekable `Cues` index normally appended at EOS, so the output is a pure forward stream for a pipe / HTTP push. `flvmux streamable` was assessed and not added: g2g's FLV muxer is already forward-only (no duration / filesize backpatch, EOS is a no-op), so the toggle would be a no-op. New in-module tests cover keyframe-aligned batching with sample preservation (six AUs → two fragments, all six samples retained), the per-AU default, and `streamable` suppressing the Cues; the `m454_element_properties` suite gains the two new property round-trips. Defaults unchanged (`fragment-duration` 0, `streamable` false).

- M455: real behavior behind the streaming "tune-in" properties M454 left as `needs-new-behavior` (no accepted-but-ignored stubs). `h264parse` / `h265parse` gain `config-interval` (seconds: `0` off, `-1` every IDR/IRAP, `N` every N s): the re-framer caches the most-recent SPS/PPS (and VPS for HEVC) as they flow and prepends them, as Annex-B, before a keyframe access unit that lacks inline parameter sets, so a decoder joining mid-stream (an HLS/DASH segment, a tuned-in MPEG-TS multicast) finds them without waiting for the next natural set; an AU that already carries config is left untouched and only resets the cadence clock. Applied on the access-unit-aligned re-framing output (the launch-registered construction). `mpegtsmux` gains `pat-interval` / `pmt-interval` (milliseconds, `0` = once): the `TsMuxer` re-emits the PAT+PMT pair before the first access unit whose PTS is at least the interval past the last emission (PSI continuity counters carry on across re-emissions), the TS-side analog of `config-interval` for mid-stream join; the tables are emitted together, so the two properties share one cadence. `mp4mux faststart` was assessed and deliberately not added: g2g's `Mp4Mux` is fragmented MP4 (ftyp+moov init, then moof+mdat), already moov-first/streamable, so faststart (a progressive-MP4 moov reorder) would be a whole new non-fragmented muxer mode, not property plumbing. New in-module tests cover SPS/PPS and VPS/SPS/PPS re-insertion (every-IDR and time-paced), the interval-0 no-op, and PAT/PMT re-emission vs emit-once; the `m454_element_properties` suite gains the three new property round-trips. No change to default (interval 0 / config-interval 0) behavior.

- M454: settable properties across the element set, so `parse_launch` (gst-launch syntax) can configure them. An audit of every element against its GStreamer counterpart found many `with_*` builders / constructor args that were unreachable from a launch string because the element had no `properties()` / `set_property`. Exposed the missing high-value knobs and wired each to the field it already acts on, matching the GStreamer name/unit (kebab-case; `bitrate` is `Uint` bits/second, the existing `ffmpegenc` convention): encoders `av1enc` (bitrate, speed), `vpxenc` (codec, bitrate), `opusenc` (bitrate), `mjpegenc` (quality), `mediacodecenc` (bitrate, framerate, i-frame-interval); sources `rtspsrc` (location, user-agent, user-id, user-pw), `udpsrc` (address, port), `srtsrc` (address, port, latency, passphrase), `v4l2src` (device, width, height, framerate), `rtmpsrc` (address, port); sinks `udpsink` (host, port, payload-type, ssrc), `srtsink` (host, port, latency, passphrase), `waylandsink` (title, app-id, max-lateness), `kmssink` (device), `alsasink` (device); overlays / decoders `analyticsoverlay` (thickness), `textoverlay` (color as 0xAARRGGBB), `mjpegdec` (output-format), `vaapidec` (device), `mediacodecdec` (gpu-output, `mediacodec-wgpu` only). Properties only ever expose behavior the element actually applies (no accepted-but-ignored knobs); deliberate `no_std` omissions (videoscale interpolation method, videobalance hue, resampler quality) and `needs-new-behavior` items (h264parse/h265parse config-interval, mp4mux faststart) are left for follow-ups rather than stubbed. New `g2g-plugins/tests/m454_element_properties.rs` round-trips `set_property` / `get_property` and asserts each name is declared in `properties()` (the kind lookup `parse_launch` needs), plus an end-to-end `parse_launch` check that `mjpegenc quality=50` parses and an undeclared property is rejected. `AGENTS.md` now requires new elements to expose their knobs as properties. No behavior change to existing pipelines; builds clean across the touched feature union and the Android cross-compile.

- M453: the visual end of the one-graph detector, the screenshot-able payoff M452 flagged: a real YOLO's detections drawn back onto the picture. New example `g2g-ml/examples/detect_overlay.rs` (`--features "ort analytics"`) runs the M452 chain once (`OrtInference -> DetectionPostprocess`) to get the `AnalyticsMeta`, reconstructs the exact frame the model saw straight from the preprocessed input tensor (CHW f32 -> HWC RGBA8, so the normalized boxes land pixel-exact), then a single graph paints and presents: `ImageSource(RGBA8 + AnalyticsMeta) -> AnalyticsOverlay -> <display>`. This is the M214 meta-on-frame fan-out contract (the detector's meta rides the frame; the overlay reads and draws it) with a real detector and a desktop sink instead of a hard-coded box and a fake sink. Two backends like `textoverlay_demo`: a headless still path that writes the annotated frame as a PPM (default), and a live path (new `detect-overlay-live` feature, Linux) that loops the frame into a Wayland window via `AnalyticsOverlay -> VideoConvert(NV12) -> WaylandSink`. Validated locally: the still path drew a tight red box around the dog (COCO class 16, 0.899) over the real photo; the live path compiles. Loads the gitignored YOLO fixture and skips with a message when absent, so it stays out of the default build (the "validated locally, not CI" pattern). No new elements: the demo composes existing ones.

- M452: the one-graph detector, the payoff M451 unblocks and the detection sibling of the M451 runner-driven classifier. A real YOLO and its perception post-processing run as a single negotiated g2g graph through `run_linear_chain`: `TensorSource(f32 [1,3,640,640]) -> OrtInference(YOLO) -> DetectionPostprocess -> DetectSink`. The model's raw `[1, 84, 8400]` tensor becomes an `AnalyticsMeta` of bounding boxes (anchor decode + per-class NMS) attached to the frame the sink reads; the runner owns caps negotiation and frame pumping across every tensor hop. New gated test `g2g-ml/tests/runner_driven_detect.rs` (`--features "ort analytics"`) asserts the dog is detected (COCO class 16, 0.899) through the negotiated graph, with per-element latency in `RunStats`; uses the gitignored YOLO fixtures, skips when absent. With M451's classifier this is the "MediaPipe but one typed pipeline, ONNX-not-TFLite" story made tangible end to end (`decode/source -> inference -> NMS -> structured detections` as one graph). The `AnalyticsOverlay` + display-sink extension (drawing the boxes back onto the video frame, the M323 tee topology) is the natural next step.
- M451: `TensorConvert` works as an *interior* runner node, so a full quantized-inference chain runs as one negotiated graph. The M450 chain folded the quantize into the source, blamed on the caps solver; that was wrong. Two new solver unit tests (`solve_linear_tensor_dtype_change_chain`, `solve_graph_tensor_dtype_change_chain`) prove the solver already negotiates a tensor `f32 -> u8 -> [1,N]` chain correctly. The real bug was the element `CapsChanged` contract: the runner's transform arm pushes `process(CapsChanged(c))` the element's pre-fixed forward *output* caps (after `configure_pipeline`/`configure_output`), and a transform must forward `c` + record `last_caps` (the documented `videoconvert` / `videoscale` convention). `OrtInference`, `TensorConvert`, and `TensorPostprocess` instead treated `c` as a new *input*: `OrtInference` hard-errored (`c.intersect(&supported_input())?` — a real model's `[1,1000]` output never matches its `[1,3,H,W]` input), and `TensorConvert` re-`accept_input`'d its own output (the stacked-convert bug). All three now follow the forward-and-suppress convention. The M447 chain `TensorSource -> TensorConvert::quantize -> OrtInference -> TensorPostprocess::argmax -> ClassSink` now negotiates and runs end to end through `run_linear_chain` (top-1 = 258 Samoyed), with per-element latency for all four nodes; `g2g-ml/tests/runner_driven_inference.rs` drives the real interior-`TensorConvert` chain (no folded-source workaround). No regressions (g2g-core 318, the ml `ort` / `analytics` suites, tensorconvert all green).
- M450: a runner-driven quantized-inference Graph. The M444 / M447 probes drive the chain by hand (`element.process(...)` per stage); this hands it to the g2g runner (`run_linear_chain`), which negotiates caps across the chain and pumps the frame through under backpressure, the gst-style orchestration the probes bypass. New host test `g2g-ml/tests/runner_driven_inference.rs` (`--features ort`): a minimal `TensorSource` (the source AppSrc can't be, since a tensor caps has no launch-syntax media type) feeds `OrtInference(uint8 MobileNetV2) -> TensorPostprocess::argmax -> ClassSink`, and the runner-produced top-1 matches the known class (258, Samoyed), with per-element latency in the returned `RunStats`. Uses the gitignored uint8 model from `gen_u8in.py`; skips when absent. This version folded the quantize into the source and blamed the caps solver; M451 corrects that (the solver was fine; the bug was the element `CapsChanged` contract) and makes `TensorConvert` a working interior node.
- M449: QNN + CoreML execution providers for `OrtInference`, the Snapdragon / Apple siblings of the M439 NNAPI / XNNPACK EPs. `from_memory_with_qnn` (Qualcomm AI Engine Direct: the Hexagon NPU / Adreno GPU on Snapdragon, the alternative to reaching the Hexagon through NNAPI) and `from_memory_with_coreml` (the Apple Neural Engine / GPU on macOS / iOS), each a constructor variant that registers the EP ahead of the CPU fallback, identical in shape to the NNAPI / CUDA paths. New `qnn = ["ort", "ort/qnn"]` / `coreml = ["ort", "ort/coreml"]` features; like `nnapi` they link a symbol only the vendor's ONNX Runtime build carries, so they are target-only (a host / CI build never enables them). Validated to compile for their targets (`qnn` cross-checks on aarch64-linux-android, `coreml` type-checks on host); on-device runtime validation is pending the hardware (no Snapdragon / Apple device available, the same caveat as the CUDA EP). With NNAPI (M439) this rounds out the per-vendor edge-accelerator roster on one element shape. DESIGN.md ort EP paragraph updated.
- M448: a real object detector end to end through the g2g element graph (#1b), the detection sibling of the M446 classifier. A real YOLO (Ultralytics YOLO11 / YOLOv8 share the `[1, 4+C, A]` channel-major output `DetectionPostprocess` decodes) runs through `OrtInference -> DetectionPostprocess` and detects the dog in the sample photo: the raw `[1, 84, 8400]` tensor becomes one structured `AnalyticsMeta` detection (COCO class 16 "dog" at 0.899 confidence) after anchor decode + per-class NMS collapses the ~10 overlapping raw boxes. This is the reusable perception-postprocessing element (already present, now exercised on a real model) that closes the gap vs a MediaPipe detection Solution. The model is tens of MB so it is not committed: `g2g-ml/tests/fixtures/detect/gen.py` + `tools/detect-fixture.sh` obtain it on demand into a gitignored dir (anonymous HuggingFace downloads are blocked here, so the model comes from an `ultralytics` export of yolo11n or a path in `$G2G_YOLO_MODEL`) and preprocess the input; only the provenance script + `.gitignore` are tracked. New gated host test `g2g-ml/tests/yolo_detect.rs` (`--features "ort analytics"`) skips cleanly when the fixtures are absent. Validated locally against a YOLO11m export.
- M447: the real MobileNetV2 on the Edge TPU (device phase of M446). The zoo's int8 MobileNetV2 is QOperator format (`QLinearConv` etc.), which ORT's NNAPI EP does not place on the accelerator, so `g2g-ml/tests/fixtures/mobilenet/gen_u8in.py` re-quantizes the *float* zoo model into the NNAPI-friendly form: QDQ, per-tensor, uint8 activations + uint8 weights, with a static batch (NNAPI rejects dynamic shapes), then applies the M442 uint8-input surgery (drop the boundary `QuantizeLinear`, retype the graph input to uint8) so no float op pins the boundary on the CPU. New on-device probe `g2g-ml/tests/android_mobilenet_tpu_probe.rs` (gated `target_os = "android"` + `nnapi`; loads the model + a preprocessed f32 input from pushed paths at runtime, since the 3.6 MB model is not committed / `include_bytes!`d): test 1 runs the full g2g chain `TensorConvert::quantize -> OrtInference(uint8) -> TensorPostprocess::argmax` and gets a valid class; test 2 profiles a raw NNAPI session and reads the per-node provider split. New `tools/android-mobilenet-tpu-smoke.sh` builds the model on demand (throwaway venv), pushes it + the input, runs, and greps the DarwiNN / Edge TPU logcat. Validated on a Pixel 10a: top-1 = class 258 (Samoyed, the correct breed), placement `NnapiExecutionProvider: 2, CPUExecutionProvider: 1` (the conv body on the TPU, one classifier-tail Reshape on CPU), and the DarwiNN HAL log reports `Ops supported = 64, not supported = 0` with `compilation finished successfully on google-edgetpu`. Gotcha found on device: int8 *weights* (`QInt8`) load on a recent host ORT but the older Android ORT prebuilt rejects the int8 initializer (`doesn't have valid type, type: 3`); uint8 weights avoid it and the TPU runs them the same. So a real ImageNet classifier (not the M442 toy conv) runs on the NPU end to end. This is the device half of the host correctness M446 proves.
- M446: a real (non-toy) quantized vision model end to end through the g2g element graph (host phase). Where M440-M444 proved the on-NPU plumbing with a [1,3,4,4] toy conv, this proves utility: the validated int8 MobileNetV2 (ImageNet, `[1,3,224,224]` -> `[1,1000]`) classifies a real image through `OrtInference -> TensorPostprocess::argmax`, and its top-1 matches the ONNX Runtime CPU reference exactly (class 332), so the g2g chain is correct independent of the label. The 3.6 MB model is not committed (this repo's fixtures are KB-scale): `g2g-ml/tests/fixtures/mobilenet/fetch.py` + `tools/mobilenet-fixture.sh` fetch the validated zoo model + a sample image on demand into a gitignored dir and preprocess the f32 NCHW input, the same "validated locally, not CI" pattern as the GPU / Android probes; only the provenance script + `.gitignore` are tracked. New gated host test `g2g-ml/tests/mobilenet_classify.rs` (`--features ort`) reads the fetched model + input, drives the two elements by hand (the probe idiom), asserts a 1000-class logit vector and the top-1 index, and skips cleanly when the fixtures are absent. Device (Edge TPU) phase next: a QDQ uint8-input variant (QOperator won't place on NNAPI) fed via `TensorConvert::quantize`.
- M445: `TensorConvert` layout + F16, the M441 follow-ups, in the same element. NCHW <-> NHWC transposition (4D only) via `TensorConvert::transpose(layout)` or the `.to_layout(layout)` builder on any conversion, and f32 <-> F16 float narrowing/widening via `narrow_f16()` / `widen_f16()` (hand-rolled IEEE-754 half, round to nearest even, no libm). A dtype op and a layout transpose compose in one pass: the elementwise op runs first (positionally independent), then the result is reordered, so `quantize(U8, s, z).to_layout(Nhwc)` does both for a model that wants `NHWC uint8` (NNAPI / TFLite) from an `NCHW f32` source. The output dtype is now optional (`None` = preserve, for a layout-only transpose); a direct int8 <-> uint8 or int <-> f16 has no defined affine and is rejected, and a transpose is defined only for rank-4 tensors. New `layout` property (`nchw` / `nhwc`). The `CapsChanged` arm now re-derives the output caps from a mid-stream input change instead of forwarding the input caps verbatim (the `TensorPostprocess` convention). `quantize` / `dequantize` signatures unchanged. Tests: f16 known-bit-pattern + within-half-precision round trips, the NCHW<->NHWC permutation + its non-4D rejection, derived output caps for dtype+layout, and three element-level `process` drives (transpose-only byte reorder, quantize+transpose composed, f32->f16 halving the byte width).
- M444: the live chain - Android camera -> quantize -> Edge TPU inference, end to end on the device. New on-device probe `g2g-ml/tests/android_camera_tpu_probe.rs` and `tools/android-camera-tpu-smoke.sh` wire `Camera2Src` (M308 capture) -> downsample one frame's luminance to the model geometry + normalize to f32 [0,1] -> `TensorConvert::quantize` (M441) to the uint8 the model wants -> `OrtInference::from_memory_for_android(...).with_tensor_input()` on the uint8 Conv->ReLU (M442, runs 100% on the TPU). New g2g-ml feature `camera2-tpu = ["nnapi", "xnnpack", "dep:g2g-plugins", "g2g-plugins/camera2"]` pulls the capture + quantize elements alongside the EPs (Android-target only). Validated on a Pixel 10a from an `adb shell` run (shell uid holds CAMERA): 3 live camera frames captured, the chain produced a `[1,4,4,4]` output, and the logcat shows `accelerator name: EDGETPU` / `Found interface google-edgetpu` / `compilation finished successfully on google-edgetpu`. The probe falls back to a synthetic frame (still exercising quantize -> TPU) and reports it if the camera cannot open.
- M443: `OrtInference` accepts an integer (uint8 / int8) tensor input, so it can drive a quantized model directly (previously the input was locked to f32). `from_session` reads the model's input element type (f32 / u8 / i8) via the new `input_tensor_dims`; `with_tensor_input` on a quantized model advertises a `Caps::Tensor { U8 | I8, ... }` input and `infer_tensor_int` feeds the integer bytes straight to the session (one byte per element, no normalize), the output still f32. RGBA mode still requires an f32 model (a quantized model must use `with_tensor_input`, enforced in `configure_pipeline`). This is the element-level peer of `TensorConvert::quantize`: `preprocess -> TensorConvert(quantize) -> OrtInference(uint8)` keeps the boundary quantize out of the model so the whole graph is accelerator-eligible. Test: the committed uint8 QDQ fixture runs through `OrtInference` on the CPU EP (the integer-input path), the uint8 tensor pad accepted and the f32 pad rejected.
- M442: proof the *whole* conv graph runs on the Edge TPU (the M440 follow-up: there the f32-input model left its boundary `QuantizeLinear` on the CPU). `gen_qconv.py` now also emits `qconv_relu_u8in.onnx` by retyping the graph input to uint8 and dropping the leading float `QuantizeLinear` (rewiring its `DequantizeLinear` consumer onto the now-uint8 input), so no float-boundary op remains and the caller feeds a pre-quantized uint8 tensor (what `TensorConvert::quantize` produces). New probe test `fully_on_tpu_with_uint8_input` feeds the uint8 model and asserts every node is on `NnapiExecutionProvider` with nothing on the CPU. On the Pixel 10a: `non_nnapi == 0`, and the DarwiNN log reports `Ops supported = 4, not supported = 0` with `ExecutionPlan::finish: compilation finished successfully on google-edgetpu` (the device stating the full graph compiled for the Edge TPU).
- M441: `TensorConvert` (`g2g-plugins`), the tensor-domain sibling of `VideoConvert`. Quantizes an f32 tensor to int8 / uint8 (`q = round(x / scale) + zero_point`, clamped to the dtype range) or dequantizes the inverse (`x = (q - zero_point) * scale`); shape and layout pass through, only the element dtype changes. `TensorConvert::quantize(dtype, scale, zero_point)` / `::dequantize(scale, zero_point)`, plus pure `quantize_f32` / `dequantize_to_f32` helpers; `no_std`-safe (a manual round, no `f32::round`). This is the f32->uint8 step a fully-quantized model wants at its input so the whole graph runs on an NPU (M442) instead of the model carrying a CPU-bound boundary `QuantizeLinear`. Registered as `tensorconvert` (`scale` / `zero-point` / `dtype` properties). Layout (NCHW <-> NHWC) and F16 are follow-ups (same element). Tests: quantize/dequantize round-trip within a step, range clamping (no wrap), signed-int8 byte handling.
- M440: proof the Edge TPU runs a quantized conv (the M439 follow-up: the Identity probe proved only that the EP path links/registers/runs, not that an accelerator executed anything). New committed int8 QDQ Conv->ReLU fixture `g2g-ml/tests/fixtures/qconv_relu_int8.onnx` (built by `gen_qconv.py`, kept for provenance; int8 quantization is what ORT's NNAPI EP folds into a quantized conv the Edge TPU can run, where an fp32 / Identity model is left on CPU/GPU). New on-device probe `g2g-ml/tests/android_nnapi_conv_probe.rs`: one test runs the quantized conv end to end through `OrtInference::from_memory_for_android` (correct-shape, ReLU-nonnegative output), a second builds the session with NNAPI + XNNPACK, enables ORT profiling, and reads the per-node provider out of the profiling JSON, asserting `NnapiExecutionProvider` claimed the conv. New `tools/android-nnapi-conv-smoke.sh` also greps `edgetpu` / `darwinn` logcat to disambiguate the TPU from any other NNAPI accelerator (ORT only reports "NNAPI"). Validated on a Pixel 10a (Tensor G4): ORT placed the conv on `NnapiExecutionProvider`, and the DarwiNN HAL log confirms the Edge TPU compiled and ran it (`/dev/edgetpu core0` firmware load, `Ops supported = 4`, `Finished PrepareValidatedRegularModel`). The only op the TPU declines is the float-typed input-boundary `QuantizeLinear` (`TENSOR_FLOAT32`), correctly delegated to CPU, the expected QDQ split.
- M439: Android NNAPI + XNNPACK execution providers for `OrtInference`, the on-device-accelerator path the CUDA / DirectML EPs are the desktop siblings of. New constructors `from_memory_with_nnapi` (NNAPI: NPU / GPU / DSP via Android's system NeuralNetworks API), `from_memory_with_xnnpack` (XNNPACK, ARM-optimized CPU), and `from_memory_for_android` (registers NNAPI then XNNPACK then ORT's default CPU EP, so ORT assigns each node to the first provider that supports it, the MediaPipe delegate-with-fallback shape in one call). Gated by new `nnapi` / `xnnpack` features (`ort/nnapi`, `ort/xnnpack`): they link symbols only the Android ONNX Runtime build carries (unlike `cuda`, the feature does not select a different prebuilt), so they are Android-target features, never enabled in a host build / CI. New on-device probe `g2g-ml/tests/android_nnapi_probe.rs` (binder-threadpool shim for the vendor NNAPI HAL, the same shim the MediaCodec probes use) + `tools/android-nnapi-smoke.sh` (cross-builds with cargo-ndk, pushes the binary plus the NDK `libc++_shared.so`, runs from `/data/local/tmp`). Validated on a connected Pixel: the EP stack links against the `aarch64-linux-android` ORT prebuilt, registers, and runs a session byte-exact with the CPU reference. The fixture is an Identity model, so it proves the EP path end-to-end (link, register, run on-device), not NPU offload of a real conv, which a Gemm/Conv fixture is a follow-up for. QNN / CoreML slot into the same constructor pattern.
- M438: HLS live-edge start. `HlsSrc` already streamed one `DataFrame` per segment and reloaded a no-ENDLIST live playlist by media sequence, but it began at the *oldest* segment in the sliding window, so live playback started seconds (a whole DVR window) behind and chased the edge. It now starts near the live edge: new `live_edge_start` walks the segments from the end and begins at the earliest one that still leaves ~3 target durations of media ahead (RFC 8216 §6.3.3, the buffer that avoids stalls), clamped to the window start when the window is shorter than that. Applied only on the initial load of a live playlist (the existing media-sequence dedup carries reloads forward); VOD (`#EXT-X-ENDLIST`) still plays from the front. `HlsSrc::with_full_replay()` (property `full-replay`) opts back into starting a live playlist from the window front for a full DVR replay. Tests: a six-segment (1s each) live window plays only the three live-edge segments (seg3..seg5), never fetching the stale front, then ends on the reload's ENDLIST; with `with_full_replay()` the same window plays all six from the front; the existing short-window live-reload test is unchanged (a 2s window is under 3 target durations, so it clamps to the start and still plays every segment).
- M437: progressive `Mp4DemuxN`. The multi-track fMP4 demuxer used to buffer the whole byte stream and parse only on `Eos`, so an fMP4 / CMAF HLS variant (video, audio, *and* the M436 captions on it) emitted nothing until end of stream, useless for playback and broken for live (no `Eos` ever arrives). It now demuxes a *fragmented* file progressively: once the `moov` is buffered it learns the layout (`mvex` present = fragmented) and parses + emits + drains each complete `moof`+`mdat` fragment as it lands, so segments flow as they arrive and the buffer stays bounded. A *progressive* (non-fragmented) `moov`+`mdat` file still parses whole at `Eos` (its samples reference one big `mdat`, nothing can emit earlier). The per-sample emit (caps announce, out-of-band parameter-set prepend on the first video frame, ADTS re-framing) is shared between the two paths, and `announced` / `need_param_sets` persist across the incremental fragments so caps and SPS/PPS are emitted exactly once per port. New `next_box` walks a complete top-level box at an offset (32-bit sizes, matching the `boxes()` parser).
