Test: a two-track fragmented file streamed one byte per `DataFrame` emits all four samples *before* any `Eos`, opens the first video frame with its parameter sets, and a trailing `Eos` adds nothing (no double-emit); the existing fan-out / encrypted / tx3g / ADTS tests still pass on the shared emit path.
- M436: HLS-`playbin` closed-caption auto-plug, the network sibling of the M430 file hooks. `hls_playbin` now reads the `#closed-captions=cc1` (alias `#cc=`, `service-N` / `708-N`) URI fragment alongside the M418 `#audio-lang=` / `#subtitle-lang=` hints, and when set overlays the in-SEI CEA-608 / 708 captions onto the variant's video by teeing the compressed video (one copy decodes for display, the other reframes + runs `CcExtract` into the `TextOverlayN` text pad), the same shape as the file path. Three new network-free builders pick the carrier: `build_hls_ts_cc_overlay` (muxed MPEG-TS variant, captions ride the video, any muxed audio fans out to its own sink), `build_hls_fmp4_cc_overlay` (fMP4 / CMAF variant, tracks from the `#EXT-X-MAP` init `moov`), and `build_hls_separate_cc_overlay` (video-only TS variant + a separate audio rendition merged in as its own source). The caption request wins over an auto-selected SUBTITLES rendition (one overlay text pad). Tests: `build_hls_ts_cc_overlay` tees a muxed video and joins the CcExtract branch at the overlay while the audio fans out; `build_hls_separate_cc_overlay` builds the two-source caption overlay; both decline an audio-only set; and `hls_lang_hints` parses `#closed-captions=` / `#cc=` from the fragment.
- M435: CEA-708 (DTVCC) *encode*, the inverse of the M428 `Cea708` decoder and the windowed counterpart of the M431 `Cc608Enc`. New `Cc708Enc` builds the window command stream for a cue (DefineWindow a hidden window 0, sized to the text and anchored from the cue's relative `line` / `position`; SetPenLocation per row; the G0 text; DisplayWindows to reveal it atomically; HideWindows to erase), packs the commands into DTVCC service blocks (never splitting a command across the 31-byte `block_size`), wraps each block in a DTVCC packet (data padded to the odd length a `packet_size_code` describes, the trailing pad reading as a NULL service block), and queues the `(cc_type, cc_data_1, cc_data_2)` triples (`cc_type` 3 starts a packet, 2 continues). Triples drain one per video frame via `next_triple` (an ignored padding triple when idle). New `char_to_g0` maps glyphs to the G0 set. `CcInsert` now selects the encoder: `CcInsert::new()` stays CEA-608, `CcInsert::cea708(service)` authors DTVCC (a `CcEncoder` enum drains either as one triple per frame; CEA-608 is always cc_type 0). Tests: `Cc708Enc` -> `Cea708` round trips a placed cue (text + relative anchor) and a multi-line caption spanning several service blocks / packets, plus idle padding; and `CcInsert::cea708` authors a 708 caption into the SEI that `extract_cc_data` + `Cea708` recover. CEA-708 encode now completes the encode side alongside 608.
- M434: caption-authoring robustness + a turnkey example. `CcInsert` now warns (once, at end of stream) when cues were received but no caption byte ever reached a video access unit, the silent-drop symptom of an untimed video source (a `pts=0` stream makes the PTS merge deliver every cue after the last frame, so there is nothing left to carry it); it tracks `cues_received` / `caption_emitted` and logs via the new `LogSource` impl. New `examples/cc_author.rs` is the canonical authoring pipeline, `mp4src -> h264parse -> ccinsert -> tsmux -> filesink` with `subtitlesrc -> subparse` on the cue pad: a subtitle file becomes a captioned MPEG-TS in one command, replayable through the M430 `playbin` caption path. The example ends in a muxer (not a raw `.264` file), the fix for a self-authored-replay failure: a raw elementary-stream round trip through an external remuxer duplicates parameter sets and the doubled SPS/PPS fail re-demux, whereas the `tsmux` output replays cleanly. `cea::CC_NULL` is now public (the idle-pair sentinel). Test: `CcInsert` flags a cue that arrives after all video as dropped.
- M433: `SubtitleSrc` subtitle / text file source, the head of a text pipeline and the last piece of turnkey caption authoring. It reads a `.srt` / `.vtt` / `.ssa` / `.ttml` file and emits its contents as a `Caps::Text{format}` stream (the whole small document as one frame, then `Eos`), the streaming counterpart of the out-of-band file `TextOverlay` loads with `location=`. The format is sniffed from the path extension (`.vtt` -> WebVtt, `.ass` -> Ssa, `.ttml` / `.xml` / `.dfxp` -> Ttml, else SubRip) or set with a `format=` property; `location` / `format` are settable for `gst-launch`, and it is registered as the `subtitlesrc` source. So `subtitlesrc location=subs.srt ! subparse ! ...` feeds timed `Text{Utf8}` cues to a `TextOverlay` (overlay) or `CcInsert` (caption authoring) with no hand-built Rust. Tests: extension sniffing, the document-frame + `Eos` emission, the not-configured guard, and `m433_cc_authoring` driving the full real graph `subtitlesrc -> subparse -> ccinsert.cue` + `h264 -> ccinsert.video -> sink` through the multi-input runner, then extracting + decoding the output to recover the SRT cue ("HELLO") from the bitstream SEI: a subtitle file becomes embedded CEA-608 captions end to end.
- M432: `CcInsert` element, the encode-side counterpart of `CcExtract`: a compressed H.264 / H.265 access-unit stream and a timed `Text{Utf8}` cue stream in, the same video out with a `GA94` caption SEI written into each access unit. A `MultiInputElement` (video on pad 0, cues on pad 1) that opts into `input_pts_ordered` so a cue is queued just before the frames carrying its `cc_data`; it `output_follows_input` the video pad. The video provides the caption clock: each access unit drains the next `cc_data` pair from an internal `Cc608Enc` (null padding when idle) and `build_cc_sei` wraps it in a SEI NAL, inserted before the first VCL slice (`vcl_start`, so after any AUD / parameter sets; emulation-prevention escaped). A cue is queued as a pop-on sequence on arrival and an erase when the displayed caption's window ends (a newer cue supersedes it). New `cea::build_cc_sei` (the inverse of `extract_cc_data`: triples -> Annex-B SEI NAL, H.264 type 6 / H.265 prefix-SEI 39) + `write_ff_extended`; `annexb::add_emulation_prevention` is un-gated for the always-on `cea` build (it was `hls`-only). Tests: a full insert -> extract -> decode round trip (`CcInsert` SEI recovers "HELLO" through `extract_cc_data` + `Cea608`), SEI placement before an AUD-led AU's slice, and the not-configured guard. With M431 this is the inverse of the M426-M429 decode path; a `subparse -> cc608enc/ccinsert -> ... -> ccextract -> textoverlay` round trip is now pure in-graph.
- M431: CEA-608 caption *encode* (`Cc608Enc`), the inverse of the M427 `Cea608` decoder and the start of the caption-authoring / broadcast-egress direction. Feed it cues (text + placement) via `push_cue` and clear the screen with `erase`; it builds the pop-on command sequence (RCL to load the back buffer, a PAC per row from the cue's `line` / `position`, the row text, EOC to flip it on; EDM to erase) and queues the resulting `(cc_data_1, cc_data_2)` byte pairs, doubling the control codes and setting odd parity the way a conformant line-21 stream does. The caption channel carries two bytes per video frame, so the queue is drained one pair per frame via `next_pair` (a null padding pair when idle), the pacing an inserter applies against the video frame rate. Channel 1 (CC1) pop-on only for now. New helpers invert the decoder tables: `char_to_608` (glyph -> basic-set byte), `pac_encode` (1-based row + indent -> PAC `(b0, b1)`), `odd_parity`. Tests: a full encode -> decode round trip (`Cc608Enc` -> `Cea608` recovers "HELLO" with the erase-frame end time), and control-doubling + odd-parity + idle-null-padding.
- M430: closed-caption `playbin` auto-plug. The file-container fan-out hooks (`mkv_playbin` / `ts_playbin` / `mp4_playbin`) now overlay the in-SEI captions onto the video when the URI carries a `#closed-captions=` fragment. Captions are not discoverable up front (they ride in the video bitstream, not a container track), so they are opt-in via the fragment, the file analog of the HLS `#subtitle-lang=` hint: `#closed-captions=cc1` (alias `#cc=`, accepting `cc1`..`cc4`, `on` / `1`, or `service-N` / `708-N`). New `build_cc_overlay` / `wire_cc_overlay` tee the parsed video (`Graph::add_tee`): branch 0 is the `wire_overlay_av` display chain (`decode -> videoconvert(RGBA8) -> TextOverlayN -> videoconvert(NV12) -> autovideosink`), branch 1 reframes the compressed video to access units (the same `H264Parse` / `H265Parse` re-framer `decodebin` auto-plugs, so a TS PES does not split an SEI NAL) and runs `CcExtract` into the overlay's text pad; audio tracks fan out through the usual decode/convert branch. A `cc_request` helper strips the fragment off the file URI (so the path opens) and maps it to a `CcSource`. The explicit caption request wins over an auto-selected subtitle track (one overlay text pad). HLS caption auto-plug and the MP4 raw-caption track remain follow-ups. Tests (`m430_playbin_cc`): the `#closed-captions=` fragment builds the tee + `CcExtract` overlay topology, it overrides a present subtitle track, and a URI without the fragment keeps the plain fan-out (no tee, no overlay). Closes the CEA-608 / 708 track (DESIGN.md §4.18).
- M429: `CcExtract` closed-caption element, the pipeline node wrapping the M426-M428 decoders. A compressed H.264 / H.265 video stream in, timed `Caps::Text{Utf8}` cue frames out (the same shape `SubParse` emits, so a `TextOverlay` / text sink consumes either interchangeably). Captions ride in-band in the bitstream SEI, not a container text track, so the element sits on the compressed-video link in parallel with the decoder (tee the parser output: one branch to the decoder, one to `CcExtract`); it consumes each access unit, runs `extract_cc_data`, and drives the CEA-608 or CEA-708 state machine selected at construction (`CcSource`; default CEA-608 CC1, with `CcExtract::cea608(channel)` / `cea708(service)` constructors). A 608 source feeds only its channel's field (`cc_type` matching `Cea608Channel::field`); a 708 source feeds the `cc_type` 2 / 3 DTVCC bytes. The codec (selecting the SEI framing) is fixed at `configure_pipeline`; cue placement rides as `TextCueMeta` frame-meta (no-op on the ZST baseline); a still-shown caption is flushed at the last access unit's PTS on `Eos`. The element is a decoder-style transform (`DerivedOutput` video -> `Text{Utf8}`) and is registered as the `ccextract` launch element. Tests: video-in / text-out negotiation, a 608 pop-on caption extracted from a built `GA94` SEI access unit with start / end timing, service filtering (a 708 decoder ignores a lone 608 pair), and the not-configured guard.
- M428: CEA-708 (DTVCC) decode. New `Cea708` decodes the windowed DTVCC presentation state machine carried in the `cc_type` 2 / 3 caption triples (the digital-TV caption stream alongside the legacy 608 field data). It reassembles the DTVCC packets from the triples (header `packet_size_code` -> data length, a new packet on `cc_type` 3 abandoning any incomplete one), splits each packet into service blocks, and runs the selected service's (service 1 by default, the primary caption service) command stream against an 8-window model. The window command set drives layout: `DefineWindow` (anchor resolved to a percent of the safe area, grid allocated `rows` x `cols`), `SetCurrentWindow`, the DisplayWindows family (`DisplayWindows` / `HideWindows` / `ToggleWindows` / `ClearWindows` / `DeleteWindows` / `Reset` over a window bitmap), and `SetPenLocation`; G0 (ASCII, `0x7F` -> music note) / G1 (Latin-1) bytes write text at the pen, with the C0 layout codes (BS / FF / CR / HCR) handled. A cue is emitted whenever the joined visible-window text changes (windows ordered top-to-bottom by anchor then priority), its `CueSettings` placement derived from the topmost window. C1 command lengths (`c1_len`) advance the stream past commands whose effect is not modelled (delay / pen / window attributes), so they do not desync the text. Every count / length / offset is bounds-checked. Tests: a define-window pop caption with timing + anchor-derived line, `SetPenLocation` row layout, service filtering (a service-1 decoder ignores a service-2 block), and packet reassembly across continuation triples.
- M427: full CEA-608 decode (positioning, channels, roll-up / paint-on, mid-row + extended character sets). `Cea608` is rebuilt around a 15x32 character grid: it tracks the channel a control code addresses (the `0x08` bit of the base byte, normalized to the channel-1 form) and renders only the selected `Cea608Channel` (CC1..CC4, each a field + in-field channel), so the other channel's interleaved codes are ignored. Pop-on (RCL / EOC, hidden back buffer flipped on), roll-up (RU2/RU3/RU4 + CR scrolling its 2/3/4-row window, emitting each state as a cue), and paint-on (RDC, direct-to-display) modes; PAC row + indent / colour, mid-row style, tab offset, backspace, EDM / ENM erase. The basic North-American set is joined by the special-character (`0x11`) and both extended Western-European sets (`0x12` / `0x13`, which overwrite the preceding fallback glyph). Cue placement is derived from the grid (vertical from the topmost row, horizontal from the smallest indent, left-set) and carried in `CueSettings` (with the 608 colour). Tests: roll-up scroll, single-channel selection (CC2 ignores CC1), special + extended characters, PAC indent -> `position` / `line`, and H.265 prefix-SEI field-2 extraction.
- M426: CEA-608/708 closed-caption foundation, the SEI `cc_data` extractor + CEA-608 pop-on core. New `cea` module (`no_std`) mines the closed-caption byte triples carried in-band in H.264 / H.265 SEI `user_data_registered_itu_t_t35` (ATSC A/53) messages: `extract_cc_data` walks the NAL units, finds the SEI NALs (H.264 type 6, H.265 prefix 39 / suffix 40), parses each SEI message's `0xFF`-extended `payloadType` / `payloadSize`, and decodes the `GA94` `cc_data` block into `(cc_type, b0, b1)` triples (every count / length / offset bounds-checked, so a malformed SEI yields no triples rather than panicking). `Cea608` decodes the field-1 / CC1 pop-on path (RCL / EOC / EDM / ENM, channel-1 PAC row select, the basic North-American character set with its accented-Latin substitutions, doubled-control-code suppression) into the existing `subparse::Cue`s the overlay renders. `annexb`'s `h264_nal_type` / `h265_nal_type` helpers are un-gated for the always-on `cea` build. Tests: SEI triple extraction (+ non-GA94 / truncated fail-safe), pop-on caption decode with timing, doubled-EOC suppression, charset / PAC-row mapping. (Full 608 positioning / channels / roll-up / paint-on, CEA-708, the `CcExtract` element, and playbin auto-plug are M427-M430.)
- M425: H.265 access-unit re-framing + Opus decode auto-plug, the HEVC / Opus siblings of M421 / M422. `H265Parse` gains a `reframing()` mode (the HEVC analog of `H264Parse::reframing`): it accumulates the bitstream, splits on access-unit boundaries (new `h265_au_starts`: a VCL NAL with `first_slice_segment_in_pic_flag == 1`, an AUD, or the VPS / SPS / PPS / prefix-SEI that lead a picture), and emits one Annex-B coded picture per `DataFrame`, latching the Annex-B vs HVCC framing from the first frame and stamping the keyframe flag from the IRAP NAL types (16..=23); `video_parser_provider` now prepends it before an auto-plugged H.265 decoder, so TS / HLS HEVC is fed access-unit-aligned input instead of mis-framed PES slices. Opus now auto-plugs `opusdec` in the playbin audio branch: `mkvdemux::forwardable_streams` surfaces the track's concrete channel count (libopus is created per channel count, unlike AAC where libavcodec discovers it from the bitstream; the sample rate stays the unknown-until-parsed placeholder, since compressed rate intersects strictly), and `OpusDec`'s sink pad template is relaxed to any channels / nominal rate (`ANY_CHANNELS` / `ANY_SAMPLE_RATE`) so it matches that demuxer caps (it ignores the nominal rate, decoding at 48 kHz, and reads the real channel count at configure). Tests: `h265parse` AU grouping / two-AU split / split-AU reassembly / keyframe stamping, `forwardable_streams` carrying concrete Opus channels, and `m425` auto-plug (H.265 re-framer spliced before the decoder, Opus decode chain plugs, OpusDec rejects a channels-0 configure).
- M424: plain A/V fan-out routes audio through the convert/resample branch. The no-subtitle `playbin` hooks (MKV / TS / MP4 file, plus the HLS muxed-TS, fMP4, and separate-audio fan-outs) linked a decoder straight to the audio sink via the g2g-core `build_playbin_graph_with_source`, so the sink saw the stream's raw channels / rate (e.g. bipbop's 22050 Hz) instead of a fixed format, the same gap the M412 subtitle-overlay path already closed with `wire_audio_branch`. New plugin-side `uridecodebin::build_av_fanout` / `wire_av_fanout` assemble `source -> demux -> { video: decode -> auto video sink ; audio: decode -> audioconvert -> audioresample -> auto audio sink }`, the non-overlay sibling of `build_mkv_subtitle_overlay`; every plain fan-out hook now uses it (the g2g-core `playbin_ports` / `map_playbin_err` plumbing they shared is retired). Video branches are unchanged (decoder auto-plugged straight to the sink, as before). Tests: the MKV / TS / MP4 / HLS fan-out topologies updated for the audio branch's two extra nodes (decode+convert+resample+sink).
- M423: mono / multichannel audio (a channels wildcard in `Caps::Audio`). `Caps::Audio.channels` gains an `ANY_CHANNELS` (0) wildcard, the channel analog of `ANY_SAMPLE_RATE`: `intersect` treats `0` as "any" in both the compressed and PCM cases (so a decoder's concrete output channels coupling back onto a demuxer's unknown `Aac{0,..}` input is no longer an empty link, retiring the M422 constant-stereo workaround), `is_fixed` reports a PCM `0` as unfixed, and `fixate` collapses it to a stereo placeholder (the real layout arrives via `CapsChanged`, mirroring video `Dim::Any` -> 16). `FfmpegAudioDec` now advertises a `PcmS16Le { ANY_CHANNELS, .. }` output (it genuinely does not know the layout until it parses a frame) instead of lying about stereo. `AudioConvert` handles the full N -> M channel space: besides identity / mono fan-out / downmix-to-mono, a layout-agnostic round-robin fold (general downmix, e.g. 5.1 -> stereo) and replicate (upmix), so a mono or multichannel runtime `CapsChanged` no longer fails the convert (it was rejected loud as an unsupported remap). Tests: `intersect` / `is_fixed` / `fixate` channel-wildcard cases, and `AudioConvert` 6 -> 2 round-robin downmix + 2 -> 6 upmix.

- M422: Linux AAC decode, so an HLS / MPEG-TS stream with muxed AAC now plays with sound. New `FfmpegAudioDec` (`ffmpegaudiodec`, Linux + `ffmpeg`) wraps libavcodec's AAC decoder and emits interleaved `PcmS16Le`: it splits each demuxed buffer into individual ADTS frames (`adts_frames`, one access unit per `send_packet`, the audio analog of h264 AU-framing, since libavcodec rejects a multi-frame packet as `INVALIDDATA`) and converts the decoder's planar-float (`FLTP`) output to interleaved S16. Registered in the auto-plug pool + as a launch element. The decoded channel count / rate are only known once a frame decodes, so the element advertises a constant `PcmS16Le { 2ch, 48000 }` output at negotiation (a constant, not an input-coupled value, so the solver does not back-couple a concrete channel count onto the demuxer's `Aac{0,0}` and empty the link) and emits the real layout via `CapsChanged`; the playbin audio branch wires `decode -> audioconvert(stereo) -> audioresample(48 kHz) -> autoaudiosink` (`uridecodebin::wire_audio_branch`, the audio analog of the overlay's explicit `videoconvert`s) so the converters absorb the stream's real params (bipbop is 22050 Hz) while the sink sees a fixed 2ch/48000. `audioresample` now accepts an `ANY_SAMPLE_RATE` input at configure (deferred, resolved from the runtime `CapsChanged`). The HLS muxed-audio routing fix lands here too: `variant_streams` keeps the muxed AAC when the bound `AUDIO` group has a URI-less rendition (the muxed track is the default, e.g. bipbop), instead of dropping it. Validated live: Apple bipbop over HLS plays clean video + audio (`PulseSink` -> pipewire-pulse) + English subtitles. Tests: `adts_frames` splitting / truncated-tail / non-sync. (Mono / multichannel want a channels wildcard in `Caps::Audio`, and the plain A/V fan-out wants the same converter wiring; both follow-ups.)
- M421: access-unit re-framing in `h264parse` + auto-insert before decoders, fixing corrupt playback of MPEG-TS / HLS H.264. A decoder is fed one packet per coded picture, but `tsdemux` emits one buffer per PES, which is not access-unit-aligned (a picture's slices can span PES packets, and `FfmpegH264Dec` has no internal parser), so the decoder mis-parsed slice boundaries (libavcodec "changing field mode between slices", cascading B/P-frame concealment). `H264Parse` gains a re-framing mode (`H264Parse::reframing()`): it accumulates the bitstream, splits it on access-unit boundaries (new `h264_au_starts`: AUD / parameter-set / SEI lead-in, or a VCL slice with `first_mb_in_slice == 0`), and emits one Annex-B access unit per `DataFrame`, holding the trailing AU until the next one's start (flushed on `Eos`). The framing (Annex-B vs AVCC) is latched from the first frame, since a mid-AU Annex-B continuation buffer has no leading start code and a per-buffer guess would misread it as AVCC and corrupt it. `Registry` gains `set_parser_provider`: `decodebin` / `decodebin_preferring` consult it to splice the re-framing parser ahead of every auto-plugged decoder (the GStreamer `decodebin` model), wired in `default_registry` for H.264. The `gst-launch` `h264parse` now re-frames too. Verified against a live HLS stream (Apple bipbop) and a real TS capture: 20203 -> 0 decode-error lines, matching GStreamer. `g2g-launch` also now builds its tokio runtime with `enable_all` (was `enable_time` only), without which any network source (HLS / RTSP / http) panicked with "IO disabled" at run. Tests: `h264_au_starts` grouping, two-AUs-in-one-buffer split, split-AU reassembly, and `decodebin` parser auto-insert. (The H.265 re-framer and a Linux AAC decoder are follow-ups; HLS with muxed AAC still plays video-only.)
- M420: HLS three-source subtitle overlay (separate audio + separate subtitle). New `uridecodebin::build_hls_separate_subtitle_overlay` handles a variant that carries video in its own TS segments but pairs it with both a separate audio rendition and a `SUBTITLES` rendition: the video rides `HlsSrc -> TsDemuxN -> decode -> videoconvert(RGBA8) -> TextOverlayN` (via the shared `wire_overlay_av`), the audio is a distinct `HlsSrc -> TsDemuxN -> decode -> autoaudiosink` chain, and the subtitle is a distinct `HlsSrc(text) -> SubParse -> overlay text pad` chain (via the shared `link_text_into_overlay`), three independent sources in one graph (the union of `build_hls_separate_fanout` and `build_hls_subtitle_overlay`). `hls_playbin` resolves both renditions up front (new `resolve_rendition` helper, honouring the `#audio-lang=` / `#subtitle-lang=` hints) and dispatches on the pair: separate-audio + subtitle -> the three-source overlay, subtitle-only (muxed audio) -> M419, audio-only -> M397, else the plain muxed fan-out. Subtitles are no longer gated on muxed audio. Tests: `build_hls_separate_subtitle_overlay` three-source fan-in topology (+ decline without muxed video). Network-coupled; validated live, not in CI.
- M419: HLS subtitle-rendition playback fan-out (the cross-source overlay join). `HlsSrc` gains a text mode (`with_text`, M419): a WebVTT subtitle rendition advertises `Caps::Text { WebVtt }` instead of a `ByteStream` container and forwards each `.vtt` segment's text with a trailing blank line, so a downstream `SubParse` sees each segment's `WEBVTT` / `X-TIMESTAMP-MAP` header as its own non-cue block (those parse as non-cues and are skipped; cues survive across the boundary). New `uridecodebin::build_hls_subtitle_overlay` assembles `HlsSrc -> TsDemuxN -> decode -> videoconvert(RGBA8) -> TextOverlayN` for the muxed video while the subtitle is a *separate* `HlsSrc(text) -> SubParse` source linked into the overlay's text pad (the cross-source join, vs the single-demuxer MP4 / MKV overlay). The shared overlay assembly is factored into `wire_overlay_av` (video + converts + sinks + decode) + `link_text_into_overlay` (the text pad, straight in for UTF-8 or via `SubParse` for a structured format), reused by `wire_subtitle_overlay`. `hls_playbin` builds it for a TS variant carrying muxed A/V plus a `SUBTITLES` rendition (picked by the `#subtitle-lang=` hint); the separate-audio + subtitle 3-source combo and the fMP4 `wvtt` subtitle path are follow-ups. Raw `.vtt` segments only; the `X-TIMESTAMP-MAP` offset is applied for absolute-time (VOD) renditions, the live-offset case is a follow-up. Tests: `build_hls_subtitle_overlay` cross-source fan-in topology (+ decline without muxed video), and `parse_webvtt` skipping repeated segment headers across a boundary. Network-coupled (the sources fetch at run); validated live, not in CI.
- M418: HLS subtitle-rendition discovery + rendition language selection. `variant_streams` now also surfaces a variant's `SUBTITLES` group renditions (each a separate WebVTT playlist) as `HlsStreamInfo` with `Caps::Text { WebVtt }`, the read-side complement of the audio renditions it already returns. New `MasterPlaylist::pick_rendition(media_type, group, language)` chooses a rendition by language preference (exact case-insensitive `LANGUAGE` match, then a primary-subtag prefix so `en` matches `en-US`; absent a match or preference, the `DEFAULT=YES` rendition, else the first). `hls_playbin` reads a `#audio-lang=` / `#subtitle-lang=` (alias `text-lang=`) URI fragment (`uridecodebin::hls_lang_hints`, stripped before the playlist URL is built) and uses it to pick the alternate audio rendition (the separate-audio fan-out now honours the language hint instead of always taking the first). The subtitle *playback* fan-out (wiring the chosen text rendition into the overlay across sources) is the remaining network-coupled stage: it needs an `HlsSrc` text mode + segmented-WebVTT (`X-TIMESTAMP-MAP`) handling for raw `.vtt` segments, or the fMP4 `wvtt` path (reuses M416) plus the cross-source overlay join. Tests: `pick_rendition` language / default / first / empty selection, `variant_streams` discovering subtitle renditions, and `hls_lang_hints` fragment parsing.
- M417: Matroska `S_TEXT/ASS` / `S_TEXT/WEBVTT` subtitle extraction. `MkvCodec::from_codec_id` now maps `S_TEXT/ASS` / `S_TEXT/SSA` to `Subtitle(Ssa)` and `S_TEXT/WEBVTT` to `Subtitle(WebVtt)` (bitmap `S_DVBSUB` / `S_HDMV/PGS` stay `Other`, a `SubPicture` track). The demuxer de-frames each block to plain UTF-8 cue text at emit (new `mkvdemux::deframe_block` -> `subparse::deframe_subtitle_block`): an ASS block is the comma-separated `ReadOrder,Layer,Style,Name,MarginL,MarginR,MarginV,Effect,Text` fields, of which the `Text` field is taken with its `{...}` override tags and `\N` breaks resolved; a WebVTT block is the cue text with inline `<...>` tags stripped. Both forward as `Caps::Text { Utf8 }` (the source syntax only selects the de-framing; the container carries the timing), so they ride the M415 playbin overlay like `S_TEXT/UTF8`. Tests: `deframe_subtitle_block` per source format, and an ASS / WebVTT MKV demuxing to de-framed `Text { Utf8 }` cues.
- M416: MP4 `wvtt` / `stpp` subtitle-track extraction. `fmp4::parse_text_entry` now recognizes the `wvtt` (WebVTT-in-MP4, ISO 14496-30) and `stpp` (TTML-in-MP4) sample entries alongside `tx3g`, carried on a new `TrackKind::Text { format, sample }` where `sample: TextSampleFormat` selects de-framing: `wvtt` cues de-frame (new `deframe_wvtt`) by concatenating the `payl` payloads of the sample's `vttc` boxes to plain UTF-8 (`Caps::Text { Utf8 }`, like `tx3g`), and `stpp` samples pass through as the whole TTML document (`Caps::Text { Ttml }`, parsed by `SubParse` on the overlay's text pad). Both flow through the existing `mp4_playbin` subtitle overlay (M412) via `subtitle_streams`. Tests: `parse_text_entry` recognizing tx3g / wvtt / stpp, and `deframe_wvtt` extracting / joining `payl` payloads (empty / truncated samples fail safe).
- M415: `playbin uri=*.mkv` routes an embedded subtitle track through a `TextOverlayN` onto the video, the Matroska sibling of M412 (MP4). The overlay-assembly subgraph (overlay + RGBA8 / NV12 converts + auto sinks + per-track decode, with the structured-format `SubParse` branch) is factored into a shared `uridecodebin::wire_subtitle_overlay`, and `build_mp4_subtitle_overlay` / new `build_mkv_subtitle_overlay` only build their container's source + demux before calling it. New `mkvdemux::subtitle_streams` (the text-track complement of `forwardable_streams`, which stays A/V-only); `mkv_playbin` builds the overlay when a probed MKV carries both a video and a subtitle track, else the plain M382 fan-out. Tests: `m415_playbin_mkv_subtitle` (overlay fan-in topology + plain-fan-out regression).
- M414: auto-plug ffmpeg decoder honours the chosen output layout. The `ffmpegdec` / `ffmpegvaapidec` `ElementFactory` build closures were `|_| FfmpegH264Dec::new()`, discarding the `ChainLink::output` caps the search chose for the hop and always building an I420 decoder. The source pad template lists NV12 before I420, so a strict-NV12 sink (KMS / `waylandsink`, `Accepts(NV12)`) makes the search settle the decode hop on NV12; the runner then forward-prefixes `CapsChanged(NV12)` into the decoder, which the I420-built element rejected with `CapsMismatch` (its run loop only forwards a raw caps whose `format == output_format`), failing startup negotiation. This was the `playbin -> waylandsink` I420/NV12 startup gap. The factories now map the chosen output caps to the decoder's `OutputFormat` (`ffmpegdec_output_format`: NV12 caps -> NV12, else I420), so the auto-plugged decoder emits exactly what the sink accepts, no inserted `videoconvert`. A loose `is_raw_video` target still picks NV12 (first alternative) over the old I420 default. Test: `ffmpeg_smoke::autoplug_builds_nv12_decoder_for_strict_nv12_sink` (fixture-free: auto-plugs a strict-NV12 chain and drives the boxed decoder through the NV12 forward-prefix; fails with `CapsMismatch` on the old factory).
- M413: Matroska / WebM subtitle-track extraction. `MkvCodec` gains a `Subtitle(TextFormat)` variant; `from_codec_id` maps the `S_TEXT/UTF8` `CodecID` to `Subtitle(Utf8)` (plain UTF-8 cues), and `MkvDemuxN` forwards such a track as a `Caps::Text { Utf8 }` port (new `MkvStream::Subtitle(format)`), announced as `StreamType::Text` in the `StreamCollection`. The cue's display window now rides the frame: `MkvFrame` gains `duration_ns`, read from the `BlockGroup`'s `BlockDuration` (scaled by `TimestampScale`) via a shared `parse_block_group` helper used by both Cluster paths, so a subtitle cue carries its `FrameTiming.duration_ns` (a `SimpleBlock`, e.g. video / audio, leaves it `0`). Like the MP4 path, `forwardable_streams` keeps subtitle tracks out of the `playbin` A/V fan-out (no MKV text-branch overlay wiring yet); `S_TEXT/ASS` / `S_TEXT/WEBVTT` (whose per-block payload needs the track's `CodecPrivate` header to reconstruct) stay `MkvCodec::Other`. Validated against a real ffmpeg `S_TEXT/UTF8` MKV (21 cues with correct PTS + `BlockDuration` + multi-line text). Tests: a hand-built `S_TEXT/UTF8` track with a `BlockGroup` + `BlockDuration` demuxes to a `Subtitle(Utf8)` cue with the scaled PTS / duration and the UTF-8 payload.
- M412: `playbin` subtitle-overlay auto-plug. When a probed MP4 carries both a video track and a subtitle track (M411 `tx3g`), `mp4_playbin` now routes the video branch through a `TextOverlayN` fed by the subtitle track instead of straight to the sink: `FileSrc -> Mp4DemuxN -> { video: decode -> videoconvert(RGBA8) -> overlay.video ; text: -> overlay.text } -> videoconvert(NV12) -> autovideosink`, plus the usual per-stream branches for any audio. New `mp4demuxn::subtitle_streams` (the text-track complement of `forwardable_streams`, which stays A/V-only) and `uridecodebin::build_mp4_subtitle_overlay` (a non-linear builder: the decoder is auto-plugged, but the `videoconvert`s bracketing the overlay are wired explicitly because they are caps-driven `register_launch` elements outside the auto-plug pool, and the overlay needs RGBA8 in/out while the display sink needs NV12). A plain-UTF8 cue stream (MP4 `tx3g`) links straight into the overlay's text pad; a structured format would insert `SubParse`. An MP4 with no subtitle track keeps the plain M392 fan-out. Validated: the assembled graph has the single fan-in (overlay) join, and the real graph (`Mp4DemuxN[video+text] -> ffmpegdec -> videoconvert -> TextOverlayN -> sink`) runs end to end on a real `tx3g` clip (2000 frames, text track wired in, no negotiation failure). On-screen `playbin -> waylandsink` is still gated by a pre-existing mid-stream-reconfigure gap on the convert -> strict-NV12-sink leg (it breaks plain A/V `playbin -> waylandsink` too, independent of subtitles). Tests: `m412_playbin_subtitle` (overlay fan-in topology + plain-fan-out regression).
- M411: MP4 subtitle-track extraction. `fmp4::parse_all_tracks` now reads a timed-text `trak` (handler `text` / `sbtl` / `subt`) carrying a `tx3g` (3GPP timed text) sample entry into a new `TrackKind::Text { format }`, and both sample paths (`parse_progressive_multi`, `parse_fragments_multi`) de-frame a tx3g sample (strip the 2-byte big-endian length prefix, take the UTF-8 cue, ignore trailing style boxes) so an embedded subtitle track fans out as a `Caps::Text { Utf8 }` port with the container's per-cue PTS + duration, feeding `SubParse` / `TextOverlayN` with no sidecar file. `Mp4DemuxN` announces the track as `StreamType::Text` in its `StreamCollection`; an empty gap sample forwards as an empty string (clears the overlay). `forwardable_streams` deliberately omits text tracks for now (no `playbin` text-branch auto-plug yet, so an unplumbed `Caps::Text` branch can't leak into the A/V fan-out). `wvtt` (WebVTT-in-MP4) and `stpp` (TTML) sample entries are recognized-but-declined (their per-sample box structure is a follow-up). Validated against a real ffmpeg `mov_text` clip (34 cues, multi-line, gap-clearing). Test: a hand-built progressive tx3g track fans its cues out as `Caps::Text { Utf8 }` with correct payloads + PTS, and stays out of `forwardable_streams`.
- M410: WebVTT `::cue` styling (per-cue colour / background). `parse_webvtt` now reads `STYLE` blocks: `::cue` (all cues) and `::cue(#id)` (by cue identifier) selectors' `color` and `background-color` are parsed (hex `#rgb`/`#rrggbb`, `rgb()`/`rgba()`, `transparent`, and common named colours; CSS comments stripped) and resolved onto each cue's `CueSettings` (global first, then the id rule overrides). New `CueSettings.color` / `.background` (`Option<[u8;4]>`); both render paths (bitmap + TrueType) use them, falling back to the element defaults, so a zero-alpha background draws no box. `::cue(.class)` span selectors and other CSS properties (font-size, etc.) are still ignored. Hand-rolled CSS subset, no dep, stays on the `no_std` baseline. Validated on the real `id_selectors` clip (white-on-black, gold cue3, black-on-transparent). Tests: global + id-override resolution with mixed colour syntaxes, and no STYLE -> no colours.
- M409: TrueType text overlay (CJK / accented / mixed-case). New `truetype-overlay` feature gives `TextOverlay` a real font backend (`fontdue`): load one or more `.ttf` / `.ttc` faces (`with_font` / `add_font` / `font=`) and glyphs are rasterized and alpha-blended onto the RGBA8 frame instead of the 8x8 ASCII bitmap (which paints nothing for CJK and drops Latin accents). Renders horizontal and vertical (`vertical:rl` / `lr`, the M407 `CueSettings::vertical`) layout, honouring `position` / `line` / `align`. fontdue does no font fallback, so the overlay holds a fallback *chain*: each glyph is drawn from the first face that has it (a Latin primary + a CJK fallback covers mixed text). Caveat: fontdue rasterizes TrueType (glyf) outlines, so a CFF / CFF2 font (e.g. variable Noto Sans CJK) yields empty glyphs; full shaping + CFF is the deferred cosmic-text upgrade. The no_std baseline keeps the bitmap font. `subtitle_player` defaults to DejaVu Sans + Droid Sans Fallback (override via `G2G_SUBTITLE_FONT` / `G2G_SUBTITLE_FALLBACK`); validated on the real Japanese (vertical) and English clips. Tests: CJK renders where the bitmap font cannot, and vertical text lays out in stacked columns.
- M408: mid-stream caps forwarding fixes a decode -> convert -> overlay chain. When the runner's mid-stream re-solve has no downstream-feasibility snapshot for an edge (`resolve_forward_output` with `downstream_feasible: None`), it now forwards the element's output when the constraint pins it to a single producible caps, instead of always deferring (which leaked the element's *input* caps downstream). So `mp4src ! avdec_h264 ! videoconvert(RGBA8) ! textoverlay ! videoconvert(NV12) ! waylandsink` plays: the decoder's mid-stream `CapsChanged` (framerate settling from the negotiated `Range` to a fixed value) used to make the converter forward NV12 to the strict RGBA8-only overlay, which rejected it with `CapsMismatch`. An ambiguous output (a caps-driven converter with several producible formats) still defers. New `subtitle_player` example plays a real MP4 + sidecar `.srt`/`.vtt` in a Wayland window (validated end to end on a 35s 640x334 H.264 clip, 872 frames, Portuguese subtitles). Test: `resolve_forward_output` forwards a property-driven converter's single output with no downstream snapshot.
- M407: WebVTT `vertical:` writing mode. New `WritingMode` (`Horizontal` default / `VerticalRl` / `VerticalLr`) on `CueSettings`, parsed from the `vertical:rl` / `vertical:lr` cue setting (the CJK vertical-subtitle case, as in real Japanese WebVTT files). The mode is carried through `SubParse` -> `TextCueMeta` -> `TextOverlayN` like the other placement; the bitmap overlay does not yet lay text out vertically (it renders these horizontally), so this is the parse / plumbing half. Tests: `vertical:rl` + `lr` parsed with placement, and a cue with no `vertical:` token staying horizontal. (Found by running the parsers against real subtitle fixtures: parsing is robust across SRT / WebVTT / SSA / TTML, mixed timestamp forms, multi-line CJK, and `<c.class>` markup; the open gaps are vertical layout and an ASCII-only overlay font that paints no CJK / accented glyphs, both now catalogued in `DESIGN_TODO`.)
- M406: streamed-cue positioning frame-meta. New `TextCueMeta` (a `FrameMeta`, behind the new `metadata` feature; ZST baseline carries nothing) wraps a cue's `CueSettings`. `SubParse` attaches it to each emitted cue frame and `TextOverlayN` reads it back, so WebVTT / SSA `position` / `line` / `align` survive the plain-UTF8 text stream and a placed cue renders where it asks instead of always bottom-centre. The `analytics` feature now implies `metadata` (the detection graph shares the container). Placement is normalized (percent of frame), so the meta keeps through a scale / crop (`propagate` default). Tests (feature-gated): `SubParse` attaching the WebVTT placement as `TextCueMeta`, and `TextOverlayN` rendering a meta-placed cue into the top-left.
- M405: incremental `SubParse`. The line-based formats (SRT / WebVTT / SSA) now emit each cue as soon as its block is fully terminated, instead of buffering the whole document and batch-emitting at `Eos`. Each `process` call drains the blocks (or SSA `Dialogue:` lines) bounded by a blank-line / newline separator, retains the partial trailing block in the buffer, and flushes the remainder at `Eos`; the SSA `[Events]` / column-order state is held across chunks. A multi-byte char split across a chunk boundary is handled (only the valid-UTF8 prefix is parsed, the partial bytes wait for the next chunk), and a leading BOM is resolved once. TTML stays batch (XML has no blank-line boundary). This unblocks `TextOverlayN`'s PTS-merge, which no longer buffers video to the end of the subtitle stream. Tests: a terminated cue streaming out before `Eos` while a dangling cue is held, and a cue whose char is split across chunks reassembling correctly.
- M404: identity-passthrough muxer output (`MultiInputElement::output_follows_input`). A multi-input element whose merged output *is* one of its input streams (an overlay / watermark / alpha mixer decorating a primary stream with a sidecar one) returns `Some(pad)`, and the CSP solver derives the output edge from that input edge (a `couple_edges` on `NodeConstraint::Muxer { follows }`) instead of from a declared `caps_constraint_for_output`. So such an element need not know its output caps up front: `TextOverlayN::new()` is now argument-free (was `new(output)`), the output following its video pad whatever geometry the source negotiates. The fixpoint solve makes the derivation order-independent (the pad edge couples to the output once the source cascades forward). Default stays `None` (independent output: a container interleave, a fixed-size compositor). Test: `solve_graph_muxer_follows_input_derives_output` (output edge equals the video source's caps with no declared output), plus `m403_textoverlay_stream` now runs through `TextOverlayN::new()`.
- M403: `TextOverlayN`, a streamed-subtitle overlay. The `N`-pad sibling of `TextOverlay` (which loads cues from a file): a `MultiInputElement` with a video pad (`RawVideo{Rgba8}`) and a *text stream* pad (`Caps::Text{Utf8}`), painting cues that arrive as a stream onto the video, the `subtitleoverlay` analog. Pair it with `SubParse` to overlay a parsed subtitle track: `srt ! subparse ! overlay.text` + `video ! overlay.video ! sink`. It opts into the runner's `input_pts_ordered` merge, so each cue (PTS = its start) is delivered before the first video frame it covers, giving correct A/V-text alignment; the rendering is reused wholesale from `TextOverlay` (composition), the text pad only feeds it cues. Output caps are pinned at construction (`TextOverlayN::new(output)`, RGBA8 at fixed geometry) like `InterleaveMux` / the compositor, since a muxer's merged output is solver-fixed rather than derived from a pad; the video pad is `Accepts(output)` so the two are coupled. v1 limitations (documented): cues stream in but carry no positioning (`SubParse` emits plain text, so WebVTT/SSA placement is lost over `Text{Utf8}` until text frame-meta lands), and the PTS-merge buffers video until the (small, fast) subtitle stream ends because `SubParse` batch-emits. Tests: `textoverlay` unit tests (pad negotiation, a streamed cue painting only inside its window, text-pad flush clearing cues) and `m403_textoverlay_stream` running `video + (srt -> subparse) -> textoverlayn -> sink` end to end through the fan-in runner, asserting frames inside the cue window come out painted and those outside untouched.
- M402: TTML / DFXP (W3C Timed Text, also SMPTE-TT / EBU-TT / IMSC) subtitle parsing. New `subparse::parse_ttml` scans the XML for `<p>` paragraph elements (any namespace prefix), reading their `begin` / `end` time attributes and text content: inline markup (`<span>`...) is stripped, `<br/>` becomes a newline, XML entities (`&amp;` / `&#10;` / `&#xNN;`) are decoded, and insignificant XML whitespace is collapsed (TTML default `xml:space`). Times accept clock-time (`HH:MM:SS.fff`, via the shared `parse_timestamp`) and offset-time (`5s` / `1.5s` / `400ms` / `2m` / `1h`, folded in `u128`); frame / tick offsets (need a rate) are unsupported. Hand-rolled (no XML dep, stays on the `no_std` baseline), with safe char-boundary scanning so malformed markup fails safe. The `SubParse` element now accepts `Text{Ttml}` (all four formats derive `Text{Utf8}`); `parse_auto` picks TTML from a leading `<`; `TextOverlay::from_ttml` + the `location=` loader handle `.ttml` / `.dfxp`. Tests: paragraph cues (entity decode, `<span>` strip, `<br/>` break, whitespace collapse), offset-time, namespace-prefixed tags, bad-time skip, and the element parsing a TTML document to timed UTF-8 cues.
- M401: SubStation Alpha / ASS subtitle parsing. New `subparse::parse_ssa` reads the `[Events]` section of a `.ssa` / `.ass` script: its `Format:` line gives the column order (`Start` / `End` / `Text` looked up by name) and each `Dialogue:` line is split accordingly, keeping the last `Text` column intact (it may contain commas), with `{...}` override blocks stripped and `\N` / `\n` line breaks turned into real newlines (ASS centisecond `.cc` fractions reuse the shared `parse_timestamp`). The `SubParse` element (M400) now accepts `Text{Ssa}` alongside `Text{Srt}` / `Text{WebVtt}`, all deriving `Text{Utf8}`; `parse_auto` picks SSA from a leading `[` section header; `TextOverlay::from_ssa` + the `location=` loader handle `.ass` / `.ssa`. Tests: SSA `Format:`/`Dialogue:` parsing (reordered columns, comma-in-text, `\N`, tag strip, non-`[Events]` lines ignored) and the element parsing an ASS document to timed UTF-8 cues.
- M400: `Caps::Text` + `TextFormat` (`Utf8`, `PangoMarkup`, `Srt`, `WebVtt`, `Ssa`, `Ttml`), text as a first-class media kind in the caps algebra alongside video / audio / tensor / byte-stream. Generalizes "subtitles": a `Text` link carries any text payload (subtitle, caption, transcription, OCR, overlay string), and "subtitle" is just timed `Text` (cue window on the frame's PTS + duration), so one variant serves overlay, captioning, and analytics alike. Wired through `intersect` / `fixate` / `dims` / `to_gst_string` (plain / markup text -> `text/x-raw`, the structured formats -> their `application/x-subtitle-*` media types). New `SubParse` element (`g2g-plugins::subparse`): the pipeline-native counterpart of the M171 `parse_srt` / `parse_webvtt` functions (which `TextOverlay` calls on an out-of-band file), it takes a `Text{Srt}` / `Text{WebVtt}` byte stream and emits timed `Text{Utf8}` cue frames, refining the media type the decoder way (`CapsConstraint::DerivedOutput`), so a demuxed subtitle track or network rendition can feed an overlay / sink as a stream. v1 batch-parses at `Eos` (small whole documents, like `Mp4DemuxN`); incremental streaming + WebVTT cue-position frame-meta are follow-ups. Tests: `subparse` element negotiation + timed-cue emission, and `m400_text_caps` runs `source(Text{Srt}) -> SubParse -> sink(Text{Utf8})` end to end through the linear runner.
- M399: measured per-element latency + input-link fill. New `runtime::ElementProbe` / `ElementLatency` (and `RunStats::per_element`): the graph runner's transform/sink arms and the two linear runners (`run_simple_pipeline`, `run_source_transform_sink`) now time every `DataFrame` `process()` call (lock-free log2 histogram, wall-clock via the `std`-only `monotonic_ns`) and sample each element's input-link fill, so `RunStats::report()` prints a measured p50/p99 + avg/max-fill table per element, the by-hand NVDEC-floor / `link_capacity` analyses turned into a number. `std`-gated where it needs a clock (the histogram is `no_std`; under `no_std` the timing compiles out and the table is empty); fan-in / fan-out / session / muxer runners leave it empty (deferred, like their declared latency). Sources carry no `process()` so they do not appear; their cost surfaces as the downstream element's input fill. Tests `m399_per_element_latency`: a deliberately-slow transform dominates the measured p50 across both the linear and graph runners, named `<category>N` (graph) / short-type-name (linear).
- M398: encrypted (cbcs) multi-track MP4 demux. `fmp4::parse_all_tracks` now reads encrypted sample entries (`encv` / `enca`: original codec from `frma`, cbcs defaults from `sinf`/`schm`/`tenc`) into a per-track `TrackHeader.cenc`, and `parse_fragments_multi` takes a per-track decrypt callback, parses each `traf`'s `senc` subsample map, and decrypts an encrypted track's samples in place before de-framing (an encrypted track with no decryptor fails loud). The cbcs primitive (`cbcs_decrypt_sample`) moved from `fmp4demux` into a shared `cenc` module behind a new `mp4-cenc` feature (shares it with `hls`, standalone so a plain MP4 build needn't pull HLS). `Mp4DemuxN::with_cenc_key` (under `mp4-cenc`) supplies the clear-key 16-byte content key; the constant IV + crypt/skip pattern come from each track's `tenc`. Test `mp4demuxn::tests`: a hand-built `encv` fragment (AES-128-CBC encrypted under a known key) round-trips through the demuxer back to the clear Annex-B IDR, and a keyless demuxer fails loud.
- M397: HLS separate audio-rendition fan-out. A variant that binds an `#EXT-X-MEDIA` `AUDIO` group carries video-only segments while its audio is a distinct rendition playlist, so `hls_playbin` now builds *two* independent `HlsSrc -> TsDemuxN -> decode -> sink` chains (one per rendition source) merged into one graph via `Graph::merge`, rather than a single-demuxer fan-out. The first (declaration-order, typically `DEFAULT`) audio rendition is chosen. Factored into `build_hls_separate_fanout` (network-free assembly). Test `m395_playbin_hls`: a master with an AUDIO group builds an 8-node two-chain graph (video variant + audio rendition).
- M396: fMP4 / CMAF HLS fan-out. The `hls_playbin` hook now picks the demuxer from the selected variant's media playlist: an `#EXT-X-MAP` init segment is fMP4 (fetch the init, discover its tracks via `mp4demuxn::forwardable_streams`, fan out `HlsSrc -> Mp4DemuxN -> {decode -> sink}`), otherwise muxed MPEG-TS (the M395 `TsDemuxN` path). The network-free assembly is factored into `build_hls_fmp4_fanout` (takes the init segment bytes). `Mp4DemuxN` buffers the byte stream and parses on EOS, so an fMP4 HLS playlist fans out as VOD after it ends rather than progressively (the batch limitation of the file-shaped demuxer). Test `m395_playbin_hls`: a two-track init segment (built by `Mp4MuxN`) fans out to a 6-node graph. The master / init probe is network-coupled (validated live, not CI).
- M395: HLS master-playlist rendition discovery + `playbin uri=hls://...` fan-out. The `hls` parser now reads `#EXT-X-MEDIA` alternate renditions (`Rendition`: audio / video / subtitles / closed-captions, with group-id, name, language, URI, default / autoselect) and the `AUDIO` / `SUBTITLES` / `VIDEO` group bindings on `#EXT-X-STREAM-INF` (`Variant::{audio_group, subtitles_group, video_group}` + `codec_list()`); `MasterPlaylist::renditions_in` enumerates a group's renditions. `hlssrc::variant_streams` maps a selected variant's `CODECS` + alternate audio renditions to `HlsStreamInfo` (StreamType + discovery caps + separate-rendition URI), the HLS analog of the container demuxers' `forwardable_streams`. New `hls_playbin` hook (`g2g-plugins`): probes a `hls://` master (mapping the scheme to an `https` origin), and for a muxed MPEG-TS variant assembles `HlsSrc -> TsDemuxN -> {decode -> auto sink}`, one branch per muxed stream, the HLS sibling of `mkv_playbin` / `ts_playbin` / `mp4_playbin`; the network-free assembly is factored into `build_hls_ts_fanout`. New single-stream `hls_handler` URI factory (`hls://` -> `HlsSrc`, declared `ByteStream{MpegTs}`) is the fallback the hook declines to (a media-only playlist, an fMP4 variant, a single-stream variant, or a probe network failure). Both registered in `default_registry` (behind `hls`). Tests: `hls` parser rendition discovery + group links, `hlssrc::variant_streams` (muxed vs separate-audio variants), and `m395_playbin_hls` (the fan-out core builds a 6-node graph and declines single-stream / separate-audio variants). The master probe itself is network-coupled, validated live (not CI), like the RTSP / WHIP paths.
- M394: AAC audio decodes from the MP4 fan-out. `Mp4DemuxN` now re-frames every demuxed AAC access unit to ADTS, building a 7-byte ADTS header from the track's `esds` AudioSpecificConfig (audio-object-type, sampling-frequency index, channel config), the inverse of `Mp4MuxN`'s de-ADTS write. The audio elementary stream is now self-describing (carries its profile / rate / channels per frame), symmetric with the in-band video parameter sets, so a decoder can start without the out-of-band config (which the generic auto-plug cannot inject). Tests `mp4demuxn::tests`: `adts_from_asc` builds a valid LC header, and the audio port's output round-trips through a real `AacParse` that recovers 48 kHz / stereo from the wired-in ASC.
- M393: progressive (non-fragmented) multi-track MP4 demux. New `fmp4::parse_progressive_multi` walks every A/V track's `stbl` sample tables (factored shared `parse_progressive_track` core, `video` flag selecting AVCC->Annex-B de-framing vs audio passthrough; `find_trak_by_id` matches each `TrackHeader` to its `trak`), the progressive analog of `parse_fragments_multi`. `Mp4DemuxN` picks it when the file has no `moof` (the classic `moov`+`mdat` layout), so a progressive A/V `.mp4` fans out to its tracks instead of only the fragmented case. Test `fmp4::tests`: a hand-built two-track progressive file (H.264 `vide` + AAC `soun` sharing one `mdat`) routes each track's samples by `track_ID` with correct de-framing and the `stss` keyframe flag.
- M392: `playbin uri=*.mp4` multi-stream fan-out. New `mp4_playbin` hook (`g2g-plugins`): probes a `file://` fragmented MP4's `moov` (via `mp4demuxn::forwardable_streams`) and assembles `FileSrc -> Mp4DemuxN -> {decode -> auto sink}`, the MP4 sibling of `mkv_playbin` / `ts_playbin`, reusing the shared `open_file_prefix` / `playbin_ports` / `map_playbin_err` helpers. Registered third in `default_registry` (after MKV and TS), declining a container whose `moov` is not in the probed prefix (a non-MP4, or a progressive file whose `moov` trails the data, which stays on the single-stream `file://` -> `Mp4Src` path). Tests `m392_playbin_mp4`: a lone `playbin uri=file://x.mp4` (an A/V file muxed by `Mp4MuxN`) fans out to a 6-node graph, and on one registry the MP4 is handled by `mp4_playbin` (MKV / TS hooks decline it).
- M391: multi-output fragmented-MP4 demuxer `Mp4DemuxN` (`g2g-plugins`), the MP4 sibling of `MkvDemuxN` / `TsDemuxN` and the multi-track read-side analog of `Mp4Src`. A `MultiOutputElement`: one `ByteStream{IsoBmff}` in, N elementary streams out, one track per output port. It buffers the byte stream and, on `Eos`, parses every `moov/trak` and routes each `moof`+`mdat` fragment to the port matching its `track_ID`, de-framing video AVCC->Annex-B (and prepending the `moov`'s parameter sets to the first video frame if it carries none) and passing audio through. Per-port negotiation caps come from `port_output_caps` (video `Fixed` geometry; compressed audio `0/0`); the real channel layout / sample rate is refined per port at runtime via `CapsChanged`, and announced as an M386 `StreamCollection` with a bus. New `Mp4Port` (a forwarded `track_ID` + caps), `Mp4StreamInfo`, and `forwardable_streams` for the M392 fan-out (the MP4 analog of `tsdemux`'s). Scope (v1): fragmented multi-track files (what `Mp4MuxN` writes, CMAF shares); clear H.264/H.265 + AAC. Tests `mp4demuxn::tests`: an A/V file round-tripped through `Mp4MuxN` fans back out to two ports (video AUs with parameter sets on port 0, AAC on port 1).
- M390: multi-track fragmented-MP4 parser (`fmp4`), the read-side groundwork for `Mp4DemuxN` (M391). New `parse_all_tracks` walks every `moov/trak` into a `TrackHeader { track_id, timescale, kind }` (`TrackKind::Video { codec, geometry, param_sets }` from `avc1`/`hvc1`, `TrackKind::Audio { format, channels, sample_rate, asc }` from `mp4a`/`esds`), classifying by the `hdlr` handler type and skipping non-A/V tracks; `parse_fragments_multi` walks the `moof`+`mdat` fragments keyed by each `traf`'s `tfhd` `track_ID`, de-framing video and passing audio through (clear tracks only; encryption stays single-track via `parse_header`). The single-track `parse_header` / `parse_fragments` (one video track) are unchanged. The `esds` AudioSpecificConfig reader moved from `mp4audiosrc` into shared `mp4box` (`parse_esds` / `find_descriptor`). Tests `fmp4::tests`: a hand-built two-track file parses to two `TrackHeader`s with the right codec/geometry/timescale, and fragments route by `track_ID` with correct de-framing.
- M389: `playbin uri=*.ts` multi-stream fan-out + multi-hook playbin dispatch. The `Registry` playbin hook slot becomes a list (`register_playbin` appends, `playbin_hooks()` returns the slice; `parse_launch` tries each in turn until one handles the URI, each declining a container it does not parse), so one hook per container type coexists. New `ts_playbin` hook (`g2g-plugins`): probes a `file://` transport stream's PMT and assembles `FileSrc -> TsDemuxN -> {decode -> auto sink}`, the MPEG-TS sibling of `mkv_playbin`. The two hooks share factored helpers (`open_file_prefix`, `playbin_ports`, `map_playbin_err`); new `TsStreamInfo` / `forwardable_streams` in `tsdemux` (the PMT analog of `mkvdemux`'s). Both registered in `default_registry` (MKV then TS). Tests `m389_playbin_ts`: a lone `playbin uri=file://x.ts` fans out to a 6-node graph, and on one registry a TS file is handled by `ts_playbin` while an MKV file is handled by `mkv_playbin` (each declines the other's container). HLS rides on this: `HlsSrc` emits `ByteStream{MpegTs}`, so `HlsSrc -> TsDemuxN` fans out an HLS variant's streams.
- M388: multi-output MPEG-TS demuxer `TsDemuxN` (`g2g-plugins`), the MPEG-TS sibling of `MkvDemuxN` and the multi-output counterpart of `TsDemux`. A `MultiOutputElement`: one `ByteStream{MpegTs}` in, N elementary streams out, one selected `TsStream` per output port. It parses the transport stream once (reusing the `TsDemuxer` parser + packet realignment) and routes each PES access unit to the port whose codec matches the unit's PMT `stream_type`, emitting each port's elementary `Caps` (`CapsChanged`, via `port_output_caps` for startup branch negotiation) before its first frame; a stream no port carries is dropped, an absent stream's port stays dark. With a bus, announces the same M386 `StreamCollection`. So one TS demuxer can feed audio + video decode branches in one pipeline (the `playbin uri=*.ts` fan-out core, M389). Tests `m388_tsdemuxn`: a hand-built A/V transport stream (PAT + 2-stream PMT + video/audio PES) splits onto two ports (H.264 AUs on port 0, AAC on port 1, each with one CapsChanged, collection announced once), and a video-only multiplex leaves the audio port dark.
- M387: gapless playbin convenience builder `gapless_playbin` (`g2g-plugins`), the one-call front door to the M383-M386 gapless stack (which was hand-wired before). Given a registry, a playlist of URIs, a sink, and a target shape, it builds the first URI's source, wraps it in a `GaplessSrc`, enqueues the remaining URIs' sources on a shared `GaplessController`, and auto-plugs one decode chain (reused across items) to the sink, returning the runnable `GaplessSrc -> decode -> sink` graph plus the controller (so the app can `enqueue` more, `switch_now`, and must `finish()` when done). Factors a core `Registry::build_source_decodebin` out of `build_uridecodebin` (auto-plug `decode -> sink` from an already-built source) for the wrapped-source case. New `GaplessPlaybinError` (empty playlist / URI). Tests `m387_gapless_playbin`: a 3-URI playlist builds a 3-node graph with the two successors pre-enqueued, and empty-playlist / unknown-scheme / bad-later-item are rejected. Completes the multi-stream playback arc (M376-M387).
- M386: stream discovery for MPEG-TS and MP4, the M376 `StreamCollection` pattern extended past Matroska. `TsDemux` gains `with_bus` and announces every elementary stream the PMT declares as a `BusMessage::StreamCollection` (id `mpegts-pid-N`, kind + media-type caps mapped from the PMT `stream_type`, geometry `Any` until refined), once when the PMT parses. `Mp4Src` (already bus-attached for tags) announces its single video track (`mp4-track-0`, the probed codec + geometry) alongside its tag post. So an app can discover the streams of a `.ts` / `.mp4` the same way it does an MKV (the discovery half of multi-stream playback; a multi-output TS demuxer + a `playbin` TS/MP4 fan-out hook remain follow-ups). Tests `m386_stream_collection`: a PAT + 2-stream PMT (H.264 + AAC) yields one collection listing both streams keyed by PID, and an Mp4Mux-written H.264 file read back through `Mp4Src` yields a one-stream video collection.
- M385: A/V offset transform `AvOffset` (`g2g-plugins`), the g2g form of GStreamer playbin's `av-offset`. A 1-in/1-out pass-through (wildcard `IdentityAny` caps, like `identity`) that shifts every `DataFrame`'s PTS/DTS by a signed `offset` ns: positive delays the stream, negative advances it (saturating, clamped at 0 since a PTS cannot go negative), `0` is a no-op pass-through. Put one on a branch of a multi-stream playback graph (typically audio) to re-align it against the others. Registered as `avoffset` with a settable `offset` (`PropKind::Int`). Tests `m385_avoffset`: positive offset delays PTS+DTS (`[0,1000,2000]`->`[500,1500,2500]`), negative advances + clamps (`[0,1000]` at `-500`->`[0,500]`), zero is pass-through, and the element is registered with a round-tripping `offset` property + builds from `audiotestsrc ! avoffset offset=40000000 ! fakesink`.
- M384: instant (flushing) URI switch on `GaplessSrc`, the `instant-uri` analog (vs the M383 gapless `enqueue`). New `GaplessController::switch_now(source)` (a latest-wins instant slot) + `wait_instant` future; `GaplessSrc::run` now races the current item's `run` against `wait_instant` via `select2`, so a `switch_now` preempts the playing item: `select2` drops the losing `run` future, cancelling the inner source mid-stream (its remaining frames are abandoned, the instant-uri contract), then the source pushes a `Flush`, resets the timeline to 0, and plays the requested source. A `switch_now` between items also flushes + resets (vs `enqueue`'s gapless continuation); `wait_event` now also wakes on `switch_now`, and about-to-finish is suppressed when an instant switch is pending. Frame counting moved into the `ShiftSink` adapter (the inner's own count is lost when a preemption drops its future). Tests: `gapless` controller units (`switch_now` latest-wins + take-once, `wait_instant` resolves only on `switch_now` not `enqueue`) and `m384_instant_switch` (a long clip1 is preempted mid-playback by `switch_now(clip2)` — a concurrent app polls a shared frame counter and switches after 2 frames — asserting exactly one flush, clip1 truncated well before its 100 frames, and clip2 playing from a reset timeline `[0,500,1000]` then a single terminal Eos).
- M383: gapless playback, the playbin `about-to-finish` + next-`uri` analog. New `g2g-core` `GaplessController` (a cloneable app<->source channel mirroring `SeekController`: a `VecDeque` playlist the app `enqueue`s, an about-to-finish back-channel `notify`/`take`, a latching `finish` flag, and a wakeful `wait_event` so an idle source parks rather than busy-polls) and a `GaplessSrc` element (`g2g-plugins`) that wraps a current `DynSourceLoop` + a `GaplessController`. It plays the current item, posts about-to-finish when nothing is queued behind it (so the app can enqueue the next item *during* playback, a seamless swap), and on the item's EOS pulls the next, rebasing that item's PTS/DTS onto the running timeline (the previous item's end becomes the new item's zero) via an interposing `ShiftSink` that also swallows the inner item's `Eos`; the only terminal `Eos` is emitted once the playlist is `finish`ed and the queue drains, so the downstream decode chain is reused across items with no flush and no gap (the read-side analog of GStreamer reusing one decodebin across URIs). Builds directly on the M211/M358 running-time machinery (this concatenates *different* items where the segment loop loops *one*). Scope v1: items share a codec (decode chain reused; a per-item caps refinement still flows via the inner source's `CapsChanged`); instant (flush) URI switching and an A/V offset are follow-ups. Tests: `gapless` controller unit tests (FIFO enqueue/take, about-to-finish take-once, finish latches, `wait_event` wakes on enqueue/finish) and `m383_gapless` (a pre-loaded two-clip playlist concatenates to rebased PTS `[0,1000,2000,3000,4000]` with a single Eos and no about-to-finish needed, and a dynamic playlist where the app enqueues each successor in response to about-to-finish then finishes, concatenating gaplessly across the swap).
- M382: `playbin uri=X` auto-fan-out, the gst-launch DSL front door to the M376-M381 multi-stream stack. A lone `playbin uri=file://x.mkv` in `parse_launch` probes the container and auto-builds `FileSrc -> MkvDemuxN -> {decode -> auto sink}` with one decode branch per forwardable stream, the multi-stream form of `playbin` (vs the M196 single-stream expansion). Cross-crate by design (the text DSL is in `g2g-core`, Matroska parsing in `g2g-plugins`): core gains a `Registry` `PlaybinHook` fn-pointer slot (`register_playbin` / `playbin_hook`, `Default`-friendly), and `parse_launch` calls it for a lone `playbin` (a `playbin` mid-pipeline or without `uri=` is left to the single-stream builder; `Ok(None)` / no hook falls back to single-stream `playbin`). `build_playbin_graph` is refactored to expose `build_playbin_graph_with_source`, so the hook supplies a Matroska byte `FileSrc` directly instead of the `file://` handler's MP4-self-demuxing source. The plugin hook `mkv_playbin` reads a bounded 4 MiB prefix, parses `Tracks`, and (new `forwardable_streams` / `MkvStreamInfo` in `mkvdemux`) builds one `PlaybinPort` per track (autovideosink for video, autoaudiosink for audio); a non-`file://` URI, unreadable file, or non-Matroska container declines. Tests `m382_playbin_uri`: a real two-track (H.264 + AAC) MKV fans out to a 6-node graph, a registry without the hook (or a non-Matroska file) stays single-stream (3 nodes), and a non-lone `playbin` never fires the hook. Gapless URI switching is the next follow-up (M383).
- M381: app-driven stream selection on the multi-output demuxer `MkvDemuxN::with_stream_select`, the multi-output counterpart of M377 (single-output `MkvDemux` switch). A `StreamSelectController` re-maps which stream each port carries: port `i` takes the `i`-th selected stream id (from the announced M376 collection), the demuxer re-arms that port's `CapsChanged` when its stream changes, and confirms the active ids on the bus (`BusMessage::StreamsSelected`). The id->`MkvStream` resolution and codec mapping are factored into shared `resolve_stream_id` / `codec_to_stream` free functions used by both demuxers. Switching a port to a different *codec* needs its downstream decode branch re-plugged (the decodebin re-plug, a follow-up); a same-codec switch takes effect directly. Test `m381_mkvdemuxn_select`: a two-port demux starts `[video, audio]`, the app swaps it to `[audio, video]` after the collection is announced, and the Clusters re-route so port 0 carries AAC and port 1 H.264, with `StreamsSelected` confirming the per-port ids. The remaining playbin gap: a `playbin` gst-launch DSL node.
- M380: per-branch decoder negotiation, so a real decoder configures against its codec downstream of a demux node (the gap M379 left). A multi-output demux now declares each port's elementary-stream caps via `MultiOutputElement::port_output_caps` (default `None` = a broadcast fan-out like `Router`); `MkvDemuxN` returns each port's `MkvStream` caps. The graph solver gains a `NodeConstraint::Demux { input, ports }` (built when a demux declares every port): instead of a broadcast tee coupling `in == every out`, it narrows each branch's out-edge to its port's `Produces` caps decoupled from the byte-stream input (`apply_demux_node`, the `node_consistent` / `graph_downstream_feasibility` tee arms made demux-aware). The startup configure pass then hands each branch element its port caps, so a decoder that *requires* H.264 / AAC (and rejects the byte stream) configures at startup rather than having to be accept-anything and retype only at runtime. A pass-through fan-out (declaring no port caps) stays a plain tee. Test `m380_branch_negotiation`: `BytesSrc(Matroska) -> MkvDemuxN(H.264, AAC) -> picky decoder -> sink` per port, where each `PickyDecoder` rejects anything but its codec, so the graph runs only because per-branch negotiation handed it the port caps (asserted: each decoder configured with its elementary caps, frames flow). The remaining playbin gaps: wiring `StreamSelectController` into `MkvDemuxN` and a `playbin` gst-launch DSL node.
- M379: `playbin`-equivalent graph builder `Registry::build_playbin_graph`, the multi-stream counterpart of `build_uridecodebin`. Given a URI, a multi-output demuxer (a `MultiOutputElement`, e.g. `MkvDemuxN`), and one `PlaybinPort` per selected stream (`{ input_caps, target, sink }`, derived by the app from the demux's announced M376 `StreamCollection` + its M377 selection), it assembles `source -> demux -> {auto-plugged decode chain -> sink}` per port and returns a `Graph` for `run_graph`. Reuses the existing `build_uri_source` (URI dispatch), `Graph::add_demux` (the M210 demux node), `Registry::decodebin` (per-port chain splice), and `run_graph` (the M210 demux arm broadcasts EOS, each branch retypes from the byte-stream input via the demux's per-port `CapsChanged`). New `PlaybinPort` / `PlaybinGraphError` types, exported from `g2g_core::runtime`. Per-branch *static* negotiation against the port caps (so a real codec decoder, not just an accept-any branch, configures at startup rather than retyping at runtime) is the remaining gap, the M10 per-branch-negotiation follow-up; wiring a `playbin` node into the `gst-launch` DSL also remains. Tests `m379_playbin`: the builder assembles the right topology (source + demux(2) + two stub decoders + two sinks, 5 edges) and rejects no-ports / unknown-scheme, and `MkvDemuxN` runs as a first-class `run_graph` demux node end-to-end (a `BytesSrc` feeds a muxed H.264 + AAC stream through the demux to two counting sinks, two access units on each port).
- M378: multi-output Matroska demuxer `MkvDemuxN` (the decodebin core, the read-side analog of `MkvMuxN`). A `MultiOutputElement` driven by `run_source_fanout`: one Matroska / WebM byte stream in, N elementary streams out, one selected `MkvStream` per output port (the §4.9.3 "dark slots"). It parses the container once and routes each track's access units to its port by codec, so one demuxer feeds several decode branches in one pipeline (audio + video together) instead of one single-output demuxer per stream. Each port emits its concrete `Caps` (`CapsChanged`) before its first frame (the branch retypes from the byte-stream input caps to the elementary stream); a parsed track no port carries is dropped, and a port whose stream the container lacks stays dark. Reuses `MkvDemux`'s codec/caps mappings (`selected_codec`, `output_caps`, `track_to_stream`, and a `concrete_caps` refactored into a shared `concrete_caps_of(demux, stream)`); with a bus, announces the same M376 `StreamCollection`. Per-branch caps negotiation (each branch sink still configures with the byte-stream caps, retyping at runtime) and wiring a `demux`/`playbin` node into the `gst-launch` DSL are the follow-ups (M379). Tests: `m378_mkvdemuxn` mux an H.264 + AAC stream with `MkvMuxN`, demux through a two-port `MkvDemuxN` (port 0 = H.264, port 1 = AAC), asserting each port gets its own CapsChanged and only its track's frames, the collection is still announced, and an unselected/absent stream leaves its port dark.
- M377: app-driven stream selection, the playbin `SELECT_STREAMS` analog (building on M376 discovery). New `g2g-core` `StreamSelectController` (a cloneable app->demuxer channel mirroring `SeekController`: `select(ids: Vec<String>)` / `take_pending`, latest-wins, poll-based) and a `BusMessage::StreamsSelected { ids }` confirmation (the `GST_MESSAGE_STREAMS_SELECTED` analog). `MkvDemux::with_stream_select` makes its single output app-selectable: it polls the controller in `emit_ready`, resolves a published id (`matroska-track-N`) to the track's `MkvStream`, switches which stream it forwards (clearing `last_caps` so the new stream's caps re-emit as a `CapsChanged`), and confirms the active id on the bus. Switching to a different-kind stream re-negotiates caps (video->audio) at the demuxer; a real single decoder can only follow a same-kind switch, the cross-kind case is what the M378 multi-output demuxer is for. `TsDemux`/`Mp4Src` don't yet surface their full stream lists (TsDemux filters by `stream_type` at emit, Mp4Src is single-track progressive), so announcing + selecting their streams is a follow-up. Tests: `stream_select` unit tests (latest-wins take, clone shares the slot) and `m377_stream_select` (mux an H.264 + AAC stream, drive `MkvDemux` header-first so it announces the collection with no frames, then select the audio id and feed the Clusters: the output switches mid-stream, emitting a video->audio CapsChanged, forwarding the AAC payloads not the video, and posting `StreamsSelected`).
- M376: stream discovery, the multi-stream playback foundation (the stream-collection model that extends the single-stream playbin g2g already has, M196). New `g2g-core` baseline types (`StreamType` {Video, Audio, Text, Unknown}, `Stream` {id, stream_type, caps}, `StreamCollection` {id, streams} with `streams_of_type` / `get` / `len`), the `GstStreamCollection` analog, and a `BusMessage::StreamCollection` (the `GST_MESSAGE_STREAM_COLLECTION` analog; `BusMessage` drops its `Eq` derive since `Caps` is only `PartialEq`, nothing keyed on it). `MkvDemux` is the reference: it announces *every* track the container declares (id `matroska-track-N`, kind + caps from the codec) on the bus once `Tracks` is parsed, regardless of which single stream it forwards, mirroring its existing `post_tags` (kept once across a mid-segment seek's `reset_keeping_tracks`). App-driven selection among the streams, multi-output routing, the `playbin` element, and gapless are follow-ups (M377+); `TsDemux` (PMT) / `Mp4Src` (moov) announce via the same pattern. Tests: `stream` unit tests (filter-by-type, get-by-id, empty) and `m376_stream_collection` (mux an H.264 + AAC stream with `MkvMuxN`, demux it with a bus, assert one collection listing both streams with the right kind / caps, announced exactly once).
- M375: the Matroska muxer writes a `Cues` index, closing the seek round-trip (the write side of M373's read). `MatroskaMuxer` tracks each Cluster's byte offset (relative to the Segment data start, the anchor `cue_seek_offset` adds back) as it streams and records a `CuePoint` for the first keyframe in each Cluster on the cue track (the first video track, else track 0; deduped per Cluster to bound the index). A new `finish()` returns the `Cues` element, which `MkvMux` / `MkvMuxN` flush as one final frame at EOS (after the last Cluster). A streaming, unknown-size-Segment muxer cannot place a front `SeekHead` pointing at the end-of-stream `Cues` (the front is already emitted before the `Cues` position is known), so seeking the muxer's own output uses the M373 read-to-end-then-seek path, not the M374 `SeekHead` prefetch; a front `SeekHead` (seekable from byte 0 without reading past the Clusters) would need a two-pass / seekable-output finalize mode (open). Tests: a `matroska` unit test muxing two Clusters then asserting the written `Cues` resolve (via `cue_seek_offset`) to the exact Cluster element ids, and `m375_mkvmux_cues` driving the full round-trip (`MkvMux` -> bytes -> `MkvDemux` with `with_seek`: a seek lands on Cluster 2 through the muxer-written index, not a re-scan from 0).
- M374: Matroska `SeekHead`-driven `Cues` prefetch, making the M373 index usable on the first seek of a real (end-of-`Cues`) file. The `matroska` parser reads a `SeekHead` (a `Seek` entry whose `SeekID` is `Cues`) into the `Cues` byte position, exposing `cue_index_offset()` (absolute). `MkvDemux` services a seek in three tiers (`poll_seek`): `Cues` already parsed -> seek straight to the target Cluster (M373); only a `SeekHead` locating `Cues` -> a two-hop prefetch (byte-seek to `Cues`, parse, then byte-seek to the target Cluster), the internal prefetch flush consumed rather than forwarded so downstream sees a flush only on the real seek; neither -> re-scan from 0 (M364). `DemuxSeek` gains `is_seeking` / `begin_indexed_seek` for the demuxer-driven second hop; `MkvDemux` holds its own controller clones for the prefetch byte-seeks. Tests: `matroska` unit tests for `SeekHead` -> Cues position, and `m374_mkvdemux_seekhead_prefetch` driving the full SeekHead -> Cues -> target two-hop (asserting both byte-seek offsets, the consumed-vs-forwarded flushes, and the re-sync). (The muxer writing `Cues` / `SeekHead` so its own output is seekable remains a follow-up.)
- M373: Matroska `Cues`-indexed seeking. The `matroska` parser now reads the `Cues` element into a `Vec<CuePoint>` (time -> Cluster byte position, the position kept relative to the Segment data start) and tracks the Segment's absolute data offset, exposing `MatroskaDemuxer::cue_seek_offset(target_ns)` (the absolute byte offset of the Cluster with the largest `CueTime` at/before the target). `MkvDemux` seeks through it: `DemuxSeek` gains `poll_request_indexed`, so when the index is known the demuxer byte-seeks straight to the target Cluster (mid-segment) and `reset_keeping_tracks` preserves Tracks / TimestampScale / Cues across the landing, instead of the M364 re-scan from offset 0 (the fallback when no `Cues` are parsed, via `poll_request`/`keeps_state`). Tests: `matroska` unit tests for `Cues` parse + `cue_seek_offset` (SNAP-before, clamp, no-index -> None), and `m373_mkvdemux_cues_seek` driving the demuxer through a full-file feed (parsing `Cues`) then a seek that requests the *Cluster1* offset (not 0) and re-syncs there. End-of-file `Cues` need read-past or a `SeekHead` prefetch (a follow-up); the muxer does not yet write `Cues`.
- M372: throughput-driven ABR for `DashSrc` (`with_abr()`), reusing the shared `abr::BandwidthEstimator` from M371. A `load_rep` helper resolves any Representation (Template / List / `sidx`-fetched SegmentBase) into the run loop's `(segments, timescale, init)` working set, so ABR is "re-select the Representation whose declared bandwidth fits the estimate, re-resolve it, re-emit the init, keep the time-aligned index". The estimate-derived cap drives both the per-reload pick and a per-segment re-selection (so a static VOD also adapts within one pass). Off by default. Test: an end-to-end `m160` test over a bandwidth-throttled two-Representation MPD that starts on the high rendition then downswitches to the low one (re-emitting its init) after the slow segment.
- M371: throughput-driven ABR for `HlsSrc` (`with_abr()`), with a shared `abr::BandwidthEstimator` for the adaptive sources. The estimator keeps an EWMA of measured download throughput (bytes over elapsed `monotonic_ns`, the caller supplies the timing so it stays pure `no_std`) and turns it into an effective bandwidth cap (estimate scaled by a safety factor, bounded by the user's `max-bandwidth`). ABR reduces to feeding that cap to the *existing* `MasterPlaylist::select`: the run loop times each segment download, re-selects the best-fitting variant, and on a change swaps the active media playlist and re-emits the init segment, keeping the time-aligned segment index. Off by default (a fixed up-front variant, unchanged behaviour); a media-only playlist has nothing to switch.
