Tests: estimator unit tests (EWMA, safety cap, user-cap bound, zero-sample) and an end-to-end `m156` test over a bandwidth-throttled two-variant master that starts on the high variant then downswitches to the low one after measuring the slow download. (DASH ABR reuses the estimator in a follow-up.)
- M370: DASH `SegmentBase` (`sidx`-indexed single-file CMAF), completing DASH byte-range addressing. A `SegmentBase` Representation is one resource whose media-fragment byte ranges are not in the manifest but in a `sidx` (Segment Index) box at `indexRange`. New `SegmentSource::Base` carries the `indexRange` + `<Initialization>` range; at run time `DashSrc` fetches the index range, parses the `sidx` (new `parse_sidx`, bounds-checked against untrusted input per the parser policy: a malformed box / hostile `reference_count` fails to `None`), and `Sidx::subsegments` turns the referenced sizes + durations into byte ranges of the `BaseURL` (anchored at `indexRange + box_size + first_offset`) with cumulative times in the `sidx` timescale. These feed the same `ResolvedSegment` path as Template / List, so the run loop, byte-range fetch, and M367 seek work unchanged; the index bytes themselves are never pushed downstream. Tests: `mpd` unit tests for `sidx` parse + subsegment resolution, truncated/wrong-box rejection, and `SegmentBase` parsing; an end-to-end `m160` test building an `[init][sidx][frags]` resource served with `206` Range that reassembles init+frags (skipping the index) and demuxes to the access units.
- M369: DASH `SegmentList` byte-range addressing (the DASH counterpart of M368). The `mpd` parser generalizes `Representation` from a single `SegmentTemplate` to a `SegmentSource` enum (`Template` | `List`); `SegmentList` is an explicit ordered list of `<SegmentURL>` entries, each a `@media` URL and/or a `mediaRange` byte range of the `BaseURL` resource, with an `<Initialization>` (`sourceURL` / `range`). New `Representation` accessors (`timescale`, `init`, `resolved_segments`, `template`) drive both addressing modes through one `ResolvedSegment { url, byte_range, time }` path, so the `DashSrc` run loop and the M367 seek work unchanged across both. A range-only entry (empty `@media`) fetches just its sub-range of the BaseURL via `fetch::get_range_bytes` (now shared by `hls` + `dash`); inclusive `"start-end"` ranges parse via `parse_dash_range`, rejecting reversed/malformed ones. Tests: `mpd` unit tests for SegmentList parsing (byte-range and explicit-URL forms) + range parsing, and an end-to-end `m160` test serving one resource with `206` Range support that reassembles byte-exact and demuxes to the access units. (`SegmentBase`'s `sidx`-indexed single resource stays open.)
- M368: HLS `#EXT-X-BYTERANGE` single-file CMAF. A media segment (or the `#EXT-X-MAP` init segment via its `BYTERANGE` attribute) that addresses a byte sub-range of a resource now fetches only that range with an HTTP `Range` request, so a single-file CMAF stream (init + all fragments packed in one resource) plays. The `hls` parser gains a `ByteRange { offset, length }` on `Segment` / `MediaPlaylist`; an absent `@offset` continues from the previous sub-range of the same URI (RFC 8216 §4.3.2.2). New `fetch::get_range_bytes` issues the `Range` request, caps the body like `get_bytes`, and is robust to a server that ignores the range (replies `200` with the whole resource) by slicing the requested window. Tests: a parser unit test for implicit/explicit offsets, and an end-to-end `m156` test serving one resource with `206 Partial Content` Range support that reassembles to the byte-exact stream and demuxes back to the access units. (DASH `SegmentList` / `SegmentBase` byte-range is the still-open counterpart.)
- M367: adaptive sources `HlsSrc` / `DashSrc` are time-seekable (`with_seek`). Unlike the BYTES-format `FileSrc`, an app TIME seek resolves to the media segment containing the target: HLS walks cumulative `#EXTINF` durations, DASH maps the target onto the `SegmentRef` `$Time$` line. The source then emits `Flush`, jumps to that segment, re-emits the fMP4 `#EXT-X-MAP` / init segment (a downstream `fmp4demux` reset on the flush needs its `moov` again), emits the post-flush `Segment` at the segment start, and resumes there. Clamped to the last segment (a target past the end lands there). The CMAF / DASH segment-transition case; discontinuity / multi-period `SEGMENT` emission stays separate. Tests `m156` / `m160`: a pre-armed seek over a multi-segment VOD playlist starts playback at the target segment, emitting one `Flush` and a `Segment` at the segment's cumulative start.
- M362-M366: byte-stream demuxers are seek-aware. A demuxer is a transform with no random access; it becomes seekable by driving its upstream byte source. A shared `DemuxSeek` helper (M362): on an app time seek (the demuxer's own `SeekController`) it requests an upstream byte-seek to offset 0 (the source's `FileSrc` controller, a clone), drops in-flight pre-seek input until the returned `Flush`, resets the demuxer's parser, then discards decoded units until the keyframe at/after the target and emits a resume `Segment`. Correct for any container without an index (re-scan from start); index-derived byte offsets are a later perf refinement. Wired into all five: `Fmp4Demux` (M362, trun keyframe flag), `TsDemux` (M363; TS units carry no keyframe flag, so a new no_std `annexb::au_is_keyframe` detects H.264 IDR / H.265 IRAP in the access unit, AAC always a resync point), `MkvDemux` (M364, Matroska block keyframe flag), `FlvDemux` (M365; adds a keyframe flag to `FlvUnit` from the FLV video frame-type), `OggDemux` (M366; the Ogg demuxer had no per-packet PTS, so the element now accumulates one from each Opus packet's decoded duration via the TOC byte at 48 kHz, every audio packet a resync point). Each `with_seek(app, upstream)` wires it; each resets its parser on a `Flush` (also correct for any discontinuity). Tests `m362`-`m366`: a `FileSrc -> demux` chain over a real container fixture (Mp4Mux / TsMux / hand-built WebM / FlvMuxer / hand-built Ogg) seeks between two keyframes and asserts the demuxer re-syncs from the target keyframe, discarding the pre-target units.

- M361: `FileSrc` byte-offset seek (`with_seek`). A `FileSrc` is a byte source, so a `Seek` it observes is in BYTES format: `start` is a file byte offset, not a timestamp. The run loop polls the `SeekController` between chunks and, on a flushing seek, emits `Flush`, repositions the read (`File::seek`), and resumes (also honouring a seek that races EOF). This is the source half of demuxer seeking: a downstream demuxer resolves a time seek to a byte offset and drives a clone of this controller. Test (`m361_filesrc_seek`): a one-shot byte-seek mid-read flushes and the post-seek bytes are exactly the file tail from the offset.

- M360: re-preroll after a flushing seek issued while paused. A non-live pipeline in `Paused` prerolls one frame and holds, backpressuring the source, so a flushing seek issued now cannot otherwise take effect (the held sink never drains, so the source never observes the seek). `StateController::request_repreroll()` (called by the app alongside the seek) bumps a new preroll generation (`preroll_gen`) and re-arms the preroll latch; `flow_gate` now takes the arm's generation and reopens for a stale one, so each sink arm re-prerolls. The sink arms (simple + graph runner) drain the stale pre-seek frames (discarding, not presenting) until the `Flush`, then preroll the post-flush target frame and re-fire `AsyncDone`. Tests: `state::request_repreroll_reopens_a_held_gate_for_the_next_generation` / `_is_a_noop_while_playing` (core gate logic); `m360_repreroll_paused` drives it end-to-end (paused preroll of frame 0, then a flushing seek + `request_repreroll` makes the target frame the new visible preroll, exactly two frames presented, then holds).

- M359: `Mp4Src` loops a clip gaplessly on a `SeekFlags::SEGMENT` seek, the first real source to consume the M358 mechanism. The run loop now tracks the active `Segment`, clips playback to its `stop`, and on a `SEGMENT` segment reports segment-done (`notify_segment_done(stop)`) and parks for the app's loop seek instead of running to `Eos`; a non-flushing loop seek snaps to the keyframe at or before the target and emits an accumulating `Segment` (no `Flush`, base advancing one span per iteration), and `shutdown()` ends the loop with `Eos`. The restructure also makes `Mp4Src` honour non-flushing repositioning seeks generally (previously it acted on flushing seeks only). The idle park is now **wakeful**: `SeekController::wait_event()` returns a future that resolves when `seek` / `shutdown` wakes a registered waker (added to `SeekInner`), so a looping source between loops costs nothing instead of busy-polling, the poll-free analog of GStreamer pausing the source task. Tests: `seek::wait_event_resolves_and_wakes` (core, parks then a `shutdown` wakes it); `m28_mp4src::segment_seek_loops_clip_gaplessly_then_shuts_down` records a 4-AU clip, drives 3 gapless loops (each restarting at the keyframe, one flush total, base accumulating one span per loop) then `shutdown()` -> `Eos`. Existing `Mp4Src` flush-seek / scrub tests unchanged.

- M358: `SeekFlags::SEGMENT` playback / gapless looping (the flag was defined but had no consumer). A segment seek plays `[start, stop]` and, at `stop`, reports *segment-done* instead of running to `Eos`, so the app can loop seamlessly. g2g has no `SEGMENT_DONE` `PipelinePacket` (a new control variant would break every element's exhaustive `match` on `PipelinePacket`), so the signal rides the existing app<->source channel: `SeekController` gains a segment-done back-channel (`notify_segment_done` on the source side; `segment_done_count` / `take_segment_done` on the app side) and a `shutdown()` / `is_shutdown()` stop signal. A `SEGMENT`-flagged seek runs to `stop`, the source calls `notify_segment_done(stop)` and parks (polling) for the app's next move; the app re-arms a *non-flushing* `SEGMENT` seek to loop (so `Segment::accumulate_seek` advances `base` one span per iteration, gapless, no `Flush` downstream) or calls `shutdown()`, at which point the idle source emits `Eos`. The idle park is a poll (the poll-model analog of GStreamer pausing the source task; a wakeful wait is a follow-up). Mirrors how M82 (flush seek) / M211 (accumulating seek) proved their mechanisms: a controlled source + the existing data plane, no runner/packet changes. Tests: `seek::tests` unit-cover the controller (segment-done count/take-once, latching shutdown); `m358_segment_seek` drives end-to-end, asserting N gapless loops (one flush total, `base` accumulating one span per loop, running time monotonic across the loop) then a clean `shutdown()` -> `Eos`, plus a single-segment-then-shutdown case. Wiring real sources (`Mp4Src`) to loop on `SEGMENT` and a wakeful idle park remain open (DESIGN_TODO).

- M357: `g2g-pyapi` `Pipeline::wait` surfaces *why* a run failed instead of a single opaque "pipeline errored". The run thread returns `Result<RunStats, G2gError>`; `wait` previously collapsed every failure (and, via `unwrap_or`, every run-thread *panic*) into one placeholder message. It now maps each `G2gError` variant to a descriptive message (`describe_error`: caps negotiation, not-configured, pool-exhausted, unsupported-domain, allocation-conflict, hardware/driver failure with the backend code, shutdown) and surfaces a run-thread panic with its payload text (`panic_message`) rather than swallowing it into `Shutdown`. The cached outcome (idempotent across repeated `wait()` calls) now stores the formatted message so it can carry a panic, which is not a `G2gError`. Tests (`g2g-pyapi`, embedded interpreter / pure): `describe_error_is_specific_per_variant` asserts every variant yields a distinct, non-empty, non-placeholder message and that the hardware arm carries its code; `panic_message_extracts_common_payloads` covers the `&str`/`String`/other payload cases.

- M356: make the embedded-Python analytics sink free-threaded-safe. `host.rs`'s native `g2g.MetaSink` (handed to a hosted element as `meta`, the `AnalyticsBackend` mirror) was a `#[pyclass(unsendable)]` over a `RefCell<Vec<Staged>>`: an element that staged a detection from a thread other than the host's worker thread (e.g. parallel ML post-processing) tripped pyo3's thread-affinity check and raised even on a GIL build, and on a free-threaded (PEP 703) interpreter the `RefCell` would be an outright data race, so the module's "free-threaded with no code change" claim did not hold for the sink. `MetaSink` is now a plain `#[pyclass]` (`Sync`) backed by a `Mutex<Vec<Staged>>`, so `add_object`/`add_classification`/`add_blob` are safe from any thread on either interpreter; contention is nil in the common single-threaded-element case. `FrameBuffer` stays `unsendable` by design (its raw pointer into the worker thread's frame is valid only on that thread for the duration of the call, and it never crosses threads). New `m356_metasink_threadsafe` test: a fixture element stages a detection from a spawned `threading.Thread` and the host materializes it into the frame's `AnalyticsMeta` (the call fails the frame with the old `unsendable` sink, so the test fails if the sink regresses to thread-affine).

- M355: cap the adaptive-streaming HTTP body read (DASH/HLS DoS). The shared `fetch::get_bytes`/`get_text` (used by `HlsSrc`/`DashSrc` for manifests, keys and media segments) buffered the whole response into one `Vec` with no bound, so a hostile or buggy server could exhaust memory with one oversized reply. Both now take a `max` and stream the body chunk-by-chunk, rejecting (loud I/O error) when the running total or an honest `Content-Length` exceeds the cap: `MAX_MANIFEST_BYTES` (16 MiB, playlists/MPDs/keys) and `MAX_SEGMENT_BYTES` (256 MiB, one media segment). `Content-Length` is an advisory early-out; the streamed running total is the real bound (a server may omit or lie about the header). Tests (`fetch::cap_tests`, a local HTTP server, CI-runnable): an over-cap body is rejected via both the `Content-Length` early-out and the streamed total, and an under-cap fetch still returns the whole body unchanged.

- M354: domain-converter auto-plug, the structural complement to the M351/M352 in-band domain negotiation (which settles a *shared* domain when one exists; this inserts a converter when one does not). `auto_plug_domain_converters(graph, factory)` (in `g2g-core`, converter-agnostic) walks each original edge, traces the producer domain through structural tee/demux nodes back to the real producer (`output_domains`), and if it shares no domain with the consumer's declared `input_domains`, asks the `factory` for a converter from the producer's preferred domain to one the consumer accepts and splices it onto that edge (`Graph::insert_on_edge`: `P -> C` becomes `P -> K -> C`, original node/edge ids preserved). New caps-free `AsyncElement::input_domains` (default `DomainSet::ALL`, so only domain-strict elements force a converter) and `DomainSet::ALL`/`iter`. Converters are caps-`Identity`, so the subsequent caps solve is untouched; an unconvertible pair is left to fail loud as before. `g2g-plugins` supplies the CUDA wrapper `auto_plug_cuda_converters` + `cuda_domain_converter` (`Cuda->System` = `CudaDownload`, `System->Cuda` = `CudaUpload`); `NvEnc`/`CudaGlSink`/`CudaKmsSink` now declare `input_domains = {Cuda}`. Also fixes a latent `NvEnc` use-after-free surfaced by the cross-element context sharing: its `Session` now pins the producer's keep-alive `Arc` (new `OwnedCudaBuffer::keep_alive_arc`) so the upstream-owned CUDA context cannot be torn down before the encoder is destroyed in it (the two run in separate runner arms). Tests: `m354_auto_plug` mechanism tests (fake elements, no GPU, CI-runnable) prove a converter is spliced on a linear conflict and on only the conflicting tee branch, and the spliced graph negotiates and runs; the hardware test (`nvenc`, skips without a GPU) runs `System NV12 source -> [auto-plugged CudaUpload] -> NvEnc -> H.264` with zero hand-wiring on the RTX 3060.

- M353: `CudaUpload` (System NV12 -> CUDA), the host->device mirror of `CudaDownload`, and the converter that lets a CPU-side NV12 stream feed `NvEnc` (which ingests `MemoryDomain::Cuda` only, so a System frame was an unconditional `UnsupportedDomain`). A pass-through transform (`Identity` NV12 caps): a System frame is uploaded into a pitched device allocation (`cuMemAllocPitch`, NVENC-aligned) via per-plane host->device `cuMemcpy2D` and emitted as `MemoryDomain::Cuda`; a frame already on the GPU is forwarded untouched. Unlike `CudaDownload` (whose Cuda input carries the foreign context), an upload's System input has none, so the element creates and owns its own CUDA context at configure (`cuInit`/`cuDeviceGet`/`cuCtxCreate`) and tears it down once every uploaded frame's keep-alive (`DevAlloc`, which `cuMemFree`s the allocation) is released. New libcuda FFI: context create/destroy, `cuMemAllocPitch`/`cuMemFree`. `cuda::download_nv12` made `pub(crate)` (M352) has its sibling. This is also the `System->Cuda` half of the converter pair the domain-converter auto-plug (next) will splice on a tee domain conflict; `CudaDownload` is the `Cuda->System` half. Tests (`m353_cuda_upload`, `cuda`/`nvenc` features, skip without a GPU): a System NV12 frame comes out `Cuda` with geometry preserved; an already-CUDA frame passes through untouched; and the headline `System NV12 -> CudaUpload -> NvEnc -> H.264` pipeline produces Annex-B access units. All pass on the RTX 3060.

- M352: multi-domain `NvDec`, proving the M351 negotiation zero-copy on a real RTX 3060. `NvDec` was a single-domain producer (always `MemoryDomain::Cuda`); it now advertises `output_domains = {Cuda, System}` and, in `configure_allocation`, reconciles the (possibly tee-joined) downstream proposal against that capability with `AllocationParams::resolve_for_producer` to pick its output domain: `Cuda` keeps each decoded NV12 surface device-resident (zero-copy, the default), `System` downloads it device->host (reusing `cuda::download_nv12`, now `pub(crate)`) before emitting. So the *same* decoder, driven only by what is downstream, either stays on the GPU or downloads, with no flag, the canonical multi-domain producer consuming the M351 contract from inside the element (no runner change). New `m352_nvdec_domain_negotiation` (hardware test, `nvdec` feature, skips gracefully without an NVIDIA GPU) drives real NVDEC decode of the committed H.264 fixture through `run_graph` and inspects each frame's `MemoryDomain::kind()` at the sink: NVDEC -> CUDA-accepting sink keeps every frame `Cuda`; NVDEC -> System-only sink downloads every frame; and two diamond cases (NVDEC -> tee -> two sinks) exercise the M351 tee `join` set-intersection on real frames, settling both branches on `Cuda` (zero-copy fan-out) or `System` purely from the branches' accepted domain sets. All four pass on the 3060 (CUDA 13.2); the default workspace suite and clippy are unchanged.
- M351: two-sided allocation-domain negotiation. The memory domain of an allocation was a one-sided dictate: each consumer named exactly one domain, the producer silently obeyed (`configure_allocation` can't refuse), and a tee whose branches named different domains failed loud (`AllocationConflict`) even when a domain satisfying both existed. Domain choice is now a negotiation. A new `DomainSet` (a `u16` bitmask over the ten `MemoryDomainKind`s, with a preference order putting GPU-resident domains before `System`) lets a consumer advertise every domain it can *accept* (`AllocationParams.accepts`, default `only(domain)`) and a producer every domain it can *emit* (`AsyncElement::output_domains` / `SourceLoop::output_domains`, default `only(output_memory())`). The tee join (`AllocationParams::join`) becomes a set intersection picking the most-preferred common domain instead of an equality check, and the source reconciles the joined proposal against its own capability (`AllocationParams::resolve_for_producer`) so the frame stays on the GPU when both ends can and falls back to System when the producer can't reach the consumer's preferred domain; an empty intersection is still a loud `AllocationConflict` (a genuine case for a future auto-plugged converter). All defaults reduce to today's exact-match behaviour, so a single-domain pipeline negotiates the identical domain it did before. Reconciliation is at the buffer-pool origin (the source) and the sibling join (the tee), not at every hop: a plain transform is a memory-domain pass-through, so enforcing its `System` default mid-cascade would wrongly reject a GPU proposal merely passing through. The memory-axis analog of M350: a diamond that failed to negotiate because a greedy single-value choice dead-ended now finds the common assignment. Tests (`m351_domain_negotiation`): a `{System,Cuda}` producer behind a tee to a `{System,Cuda}` branch and a `{Cuda}`-only branch now negotiates Cuda (was an `AllocationConflict`); a no-overlap control still conflicts; a `{System}`-only producer forces System even when both branches prefer Cuda. `query` unit tests cover the join / resolve set algebra; M343's same-domain join and CUDA-vs-D3D11 conflict are unchanged.
- M350: backtracking fixation for true diamonds (DAG solver completeness). `solve_graph` ran arc consistency (pairwise per-edge narrowing) and then fixated each edge *independently* with `CapsSet::fixate`. Arc consistency is incomplete on non-tree topologies, so a true diamond (a tee whose branches diverge through format-changing transforms and re-converge at a fan-in) could leave each edge a locally-valid domain whose greedy per-edge fixation picked a jointly-impossible combination, e.g. two branches mapping the shared tee value `V`/`W` to outputs `A`/`C` and `B`/`D` with misaligned alternative orders: greedy picks tee=`V`, branch1=`A`, branch2=`B`, but `(V, B)` is not a branch-2 mapping pair, returning an inconsistent solution (confirmed by a new test before the fix). The fixation step is now a bounded **backtracking search** over the arc-consistency-narrowed domains: it assigns one fixated `Caps` per edge in id order, tries each edge's greedy choice first (so a chain or independent fan-out fixates byte-for-byte as before), and prunes the moment a fully-assigned node violates its cross-edge relation (`node_consistent` / `transform_pair_consistent`: a tee's branches all carry its input; a transform's `(in, out)` is a real `Mapping` pair / `Identity` equality / derived `f(in)` image). A coupled diamond with no jointly-valid assignment fails loud with the new `NegotiationFailure::NoConsistentFixation`. Recursion depth is the edge count and domains are almost always single-candidate, so the search is free for the common case. Test (`solve_graph_diamond_fixates_globally_consistent`): the misaligned-mapping diamond now fixates both branches to real mapping pairs; all existing `solve_graph` tests (chain, fan-out, fan-in, legacy bridges) unchanged.
- M349: mid-stream element hot-swap validated live under load. `ElementSlot` (M8, ArcSwap-backed) was unit-tested in isolation; this proves a swap works *inside a running graph*. An `ElementSlot` sits as a transform in `source -> slot -> sink` driven by `run_graph`; the element inside it holds a `SwapHandle` and, on its threshold-th frame, swaps itself out for a replacement, so the rest of the stream flows through the new element with no drain or rebuild. Because `ElementSlot::process` reads its contents (`load_full`) at the start of each call and the swap is sequenced from inside the slotted element's own `process`, the split point is deterministic (`link_capacity` 1 keeps source and slot in lock-step). Test (`m349_element_hot_swap`): element A handles the first 3 frames then swaps to B, B handles the remaining 2, and all 5 reach the sink across the swap; stable across repeated runs. No production code change, this closes the "live swap under load isn't wired" gap with the integration coverage it lacked.
- M348: merged downstream output for dynamic fan-in (`run_muxer_sink_dynamic`). `run_aggregator_dynamic` (M320) drives a *terminal* aggregator: its merged output is discarded (processed into a `NullSink`). `run_muxer_sink_dynamic` extends it to the `run_muxer_sink` shape, a trailing sink fed the muxer's merged output, for runtime-added inputs (attach a late audio track to a running `muxer ! filesink`). The muxer's output caps are coupled to the sink without a global re-solve: because inputs attach one at a time through the same `DynamicFaninHandle`, the merged output (`output_caps`) firms up as pads configure, so the muxer arm emits a `CapsChanged` to the sink whenever the derived output changes (the dynamic analog of the static MX-2 coupling) and the sink configures against it before the first merged frame; when every input has ended and the handle is dropped, the muxer arm closes the merged link with `Eos`, ending the sink arm. `MultiInputElement::output_caps` is mirrored onto the `DynMultiInputElement` bridge so the dyn muxer arm can derive it. `RunStats::frames_consumed` is the sink's merged-frame count. Test (`m348_muxer_sink_dynamic`, `std`): two sources added at runtime to a passthrough muxer feed a recording sink all 8 merged frames, and the sink asserts it was configured (output `CapsChanged`) before any frame.
- M347: `GraphTemplate` for graph re-run / replay. `run_graph` consumes the elements it runs (it `take()`s the boxed payloads out of the graph), so a graph can be run only once; seek-and-replay (re-run from the start after a flushing seek), retry-on-error, and A/B benchmarking all need a fresh set of elements per run, because real elements carry state (a decoder's reference frames, a source's file offset) that a rewind cannot undo. `GraphTemplate::new(closure)` wraps a graph-builder closure and `instantiate()` hands back a fresh `Graph<GraphNode>` each call. This is cleaner than making `Graph` itself reusable, which would force every element to be `Clone` or re-initialisable in place, a contract the element traits deliberately avoid. Exported from `g2g_core::runtime`. Test (`m347_graph_template_replay`): one template instantiated and run twice, each run getting fresh elements so both deliver the full frame count (a single reused graph would not even compile, the graph having been moved into the first run).
- M346: graceful per-branch drop on fan-out (`FanOutPolicy::AllowBranchDrop`). A behind-a-tee branch that cannot negotiate a mid-stream `CapsChanged` previously failed the whole run loud (a shared upstream can't honour a per-branch reconfigure). A new per-tee `FanOutPolicy` (a field on the graph `Node`, so `NodeKind` is untouched) makes that a choice: `add_tee` keeps the `FailLoud` default, `add_tee_with_policy(.., AllowBranchDrop)` instead drops just the rejecting branch (its arm ends Ok) while the siblings keep flowing. The branch arm's three-way reaction is captured in a `BranchMode` enum derived from `behind_tee_policy` (single-producer `Reconfigure`, `FailLoud`, or `Drop`), replacing the old `strict: bool`; the tee tolerates the dropped branch's closed channel via `broadcast_drop_closed`, which removes a sender whose receiver has closed and keeps broadcasting to the rest (winding the tee down once all branches drop). A genuine downstream error still surfaces through that branch arm's own result, so swallowing the closed channel at the tee is safe. Tests (`m346_fanout_branch_drop`): an `AllowBranchDrop` tee whose NV12-only branch rejects an RGBA switch keeps the accept-any branch consuming all frames while the dropped branch stops at the pre-switch ones, and the same graph under the default policy still fails loud.
- M345: `DerivedCoupled` passthrough-mask soundness guard. A `DerivedCoupled` constraint carries both a `derive` closure and a `passthrough` field mask, two sources of truth for which fields couple backward; a mask that claims a field the closure actually retargets is unsound (the solver would narrow the input on a field the transform rewrites). The solver's forward-derivation step now runs a `debug_assert!` (`verify_passthrough_sound`) that every field the mask declares passthrough is repeated unchanged across *all* of the closure's output alternatives for the concrete input. Unlike `discover_passthrough` (which collapses to `NONE` on the multi-valued closures `DerivedCoupled` exists for), it checks the declared fields rather than requiring a single output, and it flags only the unsound direction (a field the closure passes through but the mask omits is a sound, merely-missed coupling). A full closure-free / declarative forward-derivation descriptor was considered and rejected as a deliberate non-goal: forward derivation is genuinely imperative (a scaler branches on format membership and enforces 4:2:0 even-dims, the cross-field validity DESIGN.md §4.13.10 keeps out of the declarative constraint), so the guard addresses the real hazard (the dual-source-of-truth drift) without re-importing what the design excluded. All existing `DerivedCoupled` elements (videoscale / videoconvert / audioresample) pass the guard. Tests (`caps`): an honoured mask on a multi-valued scaler passes, an over-claiming mask (claiming `width` passthrough when the closure retargets it) fails, and a closure that rejects its input is vacuously sound.
- M344: mid-stream β allocation re-cascade across a muxer. M343 made a muxer's per-pad allocation demand cross the boundary at startup; this closes the mid-stream gap. The DAG coordinator's `Recascade` report gains a `target: Option<NodeId>` override: an ordinary single-input transform/sink leaves it `None` (the coordinator walks every arm feeding the reporter via the node-keyed `upstream_arms`), but a muxer sets it to the one interior arm feeding the pad that changed, so a `CapsChanged` on one input re-derives that pad's `propose_allocation_for_input` and re-cascades it up that branch alone, leaving the other inputs untouched (the node-keyed walk would have hit them all). The runner precomputes each muxer pad's nearest upstream arm (`nearest_upstream_arm` per input edge, resolved through structural tees; `None` when a source feeds the pad directly, which has no interruptible arm) and threads it plus the coordinator handle into both muxer arms (`muxer_arm` and the PTS-ordered `muxer_arm_pts`). With this the DAG β walk no longer terminates at a muxer in either direction. Test (`m344_muxer_midstream_recascade`): a mid-stream geometry change on muxer pad 0 makes that branch's transform record the startup proposal then the re-cascaded one (8x8 -> 16x16), while pad 1's transform (no change) records only its startup proposal.
- M343: diamond allocation join policy + β allocation crossing a muxer (DAG negotiation). Two startup-cascade gaps closed. (1) A tee's branch proposals were joined by keeping the largest `size_bytes` and silently dropping the other branch's memory domain, so a tee feeding a CUDA sink and a D3D11 sink "agreed" on whichever was bigger. The join is now a most-restrictive intersection (`AllocationParams::join`): same domain folds to the larger size, count, and alignment; a differing domain is an empty intersection (no single producer pool satisfies both) and fails the whole negotiation loud with a new `G2gError::AllocationConflict` rather than honouring one branch and copying for the other. `AllocationParams::merge` is unchanged (it stays the asymmetric consumer-dictates-domain fold the linear upstream walk needs). (2) A muxer was an allocation black hole: its Phase-3.5 arm did nothing, so a muxer wanting device-resident input buffers could not ask for them. `MultiInputElement::propose_allocation_for_input(pad, caps)` (default `None`, so existing muxers are unaffected) now lets a muxer state its per-pad demand; the DAG runner stores it on each input edge so it crosses the boundary and re-cascades up that branch independently at startup. The mid-stream per-pad re-cascade channel (the coordinator still terminates the live β walk at a muxer) remains a follow-up. Tests (`m343_diamond_join_muxer_alloc`): a same-domain diamond joins to the most-restrictive params, a CUDA-vs-D3D11 diamond fails with `AllocationConflict`, and a muxer's per-pad CUDA proposal is absorbed by the transform on that branch while the unproposed pad is left untouched.
- M342: `videoconvert` converts the full high-bit-depth / 4:2:2 / 4:4:4 matrix. The element now negotiates the M338 planar family on both pads (it joins `FORMATS` and `INPUT_FORMATS`), and any conversion the existing fast 8-bit pairs do not special-case routes through a new general hub (`convert_via_hub`): the frame is unpacked to a canonical full-resolution (4:4:4) planar YUV intermediate at a single working depth (`to_hub`) and repacked to the target (`from_hub`), turning the N x N matrix into N unpackers + N packers. Chroma is upsampled by replication and downsampled by box-averaging (`avg_chroma`); bit depth is scaled by the full-range ratio (`scale_depth`); the YUV <-> RGB color step (BT.601 limited range, factored out of the existing 4:2:0 routines into per-pixel `rgb_to_yuv` / `yuv_to_rgb`) runs at 8-bit, the precision an `Rgba8` endpoint carries anyway. So e.g. a decoded 10-bit 4:2:0 stream now converts to RGBA for display, a 4:4:4 12-bit source down to I420 for an 8-bit encoder, or any depth/chroma to any other. The fast 8-bit paths (RGBA<->I420/NV12, NV12<->I420, YUYV->*) are unchanged, and identical-format passes still short-circuit to a copy (cheap passthrough for any format). Even-dimension validation across all four format-touching elements moved from the 4:2:0-only `is_yuv420` (now removed) to the per-axis `pixel::even_dims_required`. Tests: depth scaling (8 -> 10-bit luma), the display path (neutral-chroma high-bit-depth YUV -> grey RGBA), and a chroma down-then-up round trip preserving a flat field.
- M341: high-bit-depth / 4:2:2 / 4:4:4 in the geometric elements (`videoscale`, `videocrop`, `videoflip`). The three now negotiate and process the full M338 planar family alongside the existing formats: each replaces its hand-written 4:2:0 arm with one generic path that walks the format's three planes (a shared `pixel::planar_planes` gives each plane's byte offset and subsampled dimensions, `bytes_per_sample` the sample width). Crop and flip are sample-moving (never blend), so they treat a sample as an opaque `bps`-wide unit and are depth-agnostic; `videoscale` adds a `u16`-aware bilinear path (`resample_plane16` / `bilerp16`) because a byte-wise bilerp would blend the high and low byte of a 10/12-bit sample independently and corrupt it. Even-dimension validation generalizes from the 4:2:0-only `is_yuv420` to a per-axis `pixel::even_dims_required` (horizontally-subsampled formats need even width, vertically-subsampled need even height; 4:4:4 needs neither). `videoflip` additionally rejects a dimension-swapping rotation (90 CW/CCW, transpose) on a 4:2:2 format, since transposing it would need a vertically-subsampled layout that I422 cannot represent (4:2:0 / 4:4:4 are symmetric and fine). Tests: crop of 4:4:4 10-bit (per-plane offsets), flip of 4:4:4 10-bit (column mirror on `u16` samples) plus the 4:2:2-rotation rejection, and `u16` resample interpolation + a 4:2:0 10-bit downscale. `videoconvert` is next (M342) for actual format conversion of these.
- M340: 10/12-bit AV1 encode (`Av1Enc`), closing the high-bit-depth round trip. rav1e is generic over the sample type, so the encoder's context becomes an enum (`RavCtx::U8(Context<u8>)` / `U16(Context<u16>)`) selected from the input format's bit depth, and a single generic `encode_frame<T: Pixel>` (plus a generic `drain_ready<T>`) drives both: it fills the rav1e frame from the tightly-packed planar input via `copy_from_raw_u8` with the format's bytes-per-sample, so 8-bit (`u8`) and 10/12-bit (`u16`, little-endian) share one body. `chroma_for` now maps all three subsamplings at any depth (it reads the format's `chroma_shift`), and `build_context` passes the real `bit_depth` (8/10/12). The encoder also pads each plane's edges into its allocation up front: rav1e pads in place only when it can uniquely borrow the frame, but the retry-on-`EnoughData` loop holds a clone, so it then asserts the padding is already present (`v_frame`'s `Plane::pad`). With high-bit-depth encode in hand, the 10/12-bit AV1 decode path (M339) gains its end-to-end coverage: new round-trip tests encode flat mid-grey 10- and 12-bit frames in 4:2:0 / 4:2:2 / 4:4:4 and decode them with both `Dav1dDec` and `Rav1dDec`, asserting the decoder announces the exact high-bit-depth format and recovers a tight little-endian `u16` buffer whose luma mean survives the lossy round trip. The full 3x3 matrix (4:2:0 / 4:2:2 / 4:4:4 at 8 / 10 / 12-bit) now encodes and decodes end to end.
- M339: AV1 decoders emit 4:2:2 / 4:4:4 and 10/12-bit; `Av1Enc` encodes 8-bit 4:2:2 / 4:4:4. Both AV1 decoders (`Dav1dDec` / libdav1d and `Rav1dDec` / `re_rav1d`) previously rejected anything but 8-bit 4:2:0; they now map the decoded picture's chroma layout and bit depth to the matching M338 planar format (`pic_format`) and pack it with one generic stride-honoring path (`pack_planar`) whose chroma plane dimensions and per-sample byte size come from the format's own `chroma_shift` / `bytes_per_sample`, so 4:2:0 / 4:2:2 / 4:4:4 at 8 / 10 / 12-bit share a single routine (10/12-bit samples pass through as native little-endian 2-byte words; monochrome I400 is rejected). The format is recovered per picture and carried in the `CapsChanged` (the decoders now track `(format, w, h)` so a re-emit fires on any of them changing, not just geometry). `Av1Enc` (rav1e) gains 8-bit 4:2:2 (`I422`) and 4:4:4 (`I444`) input alongside `I420`: it derives the rav1e `ChromaSampling` and the per-frame plane geometry from the input format (`chroma_for` + `chroma_shift`), and its sink pad template, `intercept_caps`, `caps_constraint`, and `configure_pipeline` accept the three planar formats. Tests: the existing I420 round trips plus new `Av1Enc` -> decoder round trips for 4:2:2 and 4:4:4 on both decoders, asserting the decoder announces that exact format and recovers a tightly-packed buffer whose luma survives the lossy round trip (proving the multi-plane / subsampling packing). 10/12-bit AV1 encode (a `Context<u16>`) is the remaining piece; once it lands the 10/12-bit decode path gains its end-to-end round trip (M340).
- M338: high-bit-depth and 4:2:2 / 4:4:4 raw-video formats (core caps). `RawVideoFormat` gains the fully-planar YUV family across the three chroma subsamplings and three sample depths: `I420p10` / `I420p12` (4:2:0 10/12-bit), `I422` / `I422p10` / `I422p12` (4:2:2 8/10/12-bit), `I444` / `I444p10` / `I444p12` (4:4:4), the GStreamer `I420_10LE` / `Y42B` / `Y444` / `*_10LE` / `*_12LE` formats (10/12-bit samples are little-endian in a 2-byte word). Three `const` accessors centralize the layout so a future variant needs no per-site edit: `bit_depth()` (8/10/12), `bytes_per_sample()` (1 or 2), and `chroma_shift()` (the `(horizontal, vertical)` luma->chroma right-shift, `(1,1)` / `(1,0)` / `(0,0)` for 4:2:0 / 4:2:2 / 4:4:4; `None` for non-planar), with `is_planar_yuv()` over them; the frame-size helpers (`pixel::frame_byte_size`, the Python-host `frame_bytes`) derive size from these. GStreamer `format=` parsing / printing round-trips the new names (`caps`, `capsfilter`, the Python-host format map). The geometric elements (`videoscale` / `videocrop` / `videoflip`) and `videoconvert` do not yet negotiate the new formats (their `SUPPORTED` sets are unchanged), so a pipeline must keep them on a raw sink / appsink for now; full conversion + scaling support is a follow-up. This is the caps groundwork; the AV1 decoders emitting these formats (and `Av1Enc` producing them) is M339. Tests: the layout helpers and per-format frame sizes (4:2:0 / 4:2:2 / 4:4:4 at 8/10/12-bit), unique GStreamer names for every format, and the format-string round trip.
- M337: pure-Rust AV1 decode via `re_rav1d` (`Rav1dDec`, `rav1d` feature). The pure-Rust counterpart to M336's `Dav1dDec`, same caps (`CompressedVideo{Av1}` -> `RawVideo{I420}`) and same element logic, with the backend swapped from libdav1d (C FFI) to `re_rav1d`, the line-for-line Rust port of dav1d. The earlier blocker (upstream `rav1d` exposes only dav1d's C ABI as `pub(crate)`, unusable from a dependent crate) is sidestepped: `re_rav1d` re-exports dav1d-rs's safe API (`Decoder::{new,send_data,send_pending_data,get_picture}`, `Picture::{plane,plane_data_geometry,bit_depth,width,height,pixel_layout}`, `Error::is_again`), so `Rav1dDec` reuses the exact send/drain protocol and stride-honoring 8-bit 4:2:0 -> tight I420 packing, with no hand-rolled FFI. Pulled with `default-features = false` (drops the NASM asm; keeps `bitdepth_8` / `bitdepth_16`), so it builds with no system deps and reaches the pure-Rust / wasm targets the libdav1d path cannot; this is the AV1 decoder on those targets and the portable fallback elsewhere. Registered as an auto-plug candidate (`rav1ddec`) at `rank(-10)` so libdav1d (hand-written asm, faster) wins the tiebreak when both are built, plus a launch element. `re_rav1d`'s MSRV is 1.79, so the `rav1d` feature raises the build floor to 1.79 (the no_std baseline stays 1.75); no system dependency, so it is added to the CI Linux feature check. Validated end to end by a round-trip test (`Av1Enc`/rav1e encode -> `Rav1dDec` decode), asserting recovered frames are correctly-sized I420 of the encoded geometry whose luma mean stays near the grey input across the lossy round trip. 10/12-bit and 4:2:2/4:4:4 remain rejected at decode (a follow-up, shared with `Dav1dDec`).
- M336: AV1 decode via libdav1d (`Dav1dDec`, `dav1d` feature). New decoder element, `CompressedVideo{Av1}` -> `RawVideo{I420}`, over the `dav1d` crate's safe bindings to libdav1d (the C AV1 decoder with hand-written assembly, the speed reference; pairs with the existing rav1e `Av1Enc`). Drives the stateful send/drain protocol (`send_data`; on `Try again`, drain `get_picture` then `send_pending_data`) so frame-threading / reordering delay does not strand input, recovers geometry per picture (a `CapsChanged` before the first frame and on any change), and packs the decoded 8-bit 4:2:0 planes into tight planar I420 honoring each plane's stride. 10/12-bit and 4:2:2/4:4:4 are rejected at decode (a follow-up); System memory; software path (no `.hardware()` tag). Registered as an auto-plug candidate (`dav1ddec`) and launch element, with a gst-compat `avdec_av1` alias. `dav1d` is a system dependency (links libdav1d via pkg-config), so it is feature-gated and added to the CI Linux feature check (`libdav1d-dev`). Validated end to end: a round-trip test encodes flat-grey I420 to AV1 with `Av1Enc` (rav1e) and decodes it back with `Dav1dDec`, asserting the recovered frames are correctly-sized I420 of the encoded geometry whose luma mean stays near the grey input across the lossy round trip. The pure-Rust `rav1d` port (which exposes only dav1d's C ABI, not a Rust API) is a follow-up.
- M335: `CapabilityDescriptor` for auto-plug element selection. Generalizes the bare `ElementDesc::output_memory` tag into a small descriptor, `CapabilityDescriptor { output_memory, acceleration, rank }`, the principled alternative to GStreamer's flat global rank (a single integer cannot express that the best element is context-dependent: a hardware decoder that keeps frames on the GPU beats a faster one that forces a PCIe download when the consumer is GPU-resident). `score(ctx)` ranks a candidate against a `SelectionContext { preferred_memory, prefer_hardware }`, a memory-domain match dominating, then a hardware preference, with the numeric `rank` only the deterministic tiebreaker among otherwise-equal candidates (the explicit-override knob worth keeping from GStreamer's rank). `find_chain_with(.., ctx)` and `Registry::{autoplug,autoplug_names}_with(.., ctx)` score-order which candidate is tried first; still breadth-first (a shorter chain always wins), and a default `ctx` scores all candidates equally so the visit order is registration order, leaving a plain pipeline's selection unchanged. `find_chain_preferring` / `{autoplug,decodebin}_preferring(.., domain)` stay as the memory-only special case (now delegating). Factory builders `.hardware()` / `.rank(n)` join `.produces(kind)`; the genuinely-hardware decoders (`nvdec`, `vaapidec`, `ffmpegvaapidec`, `mediacodecdec`) are tagged. Ranking matters only on the auto-plug path, so the descriptor never touches the typed-graph core. Tests (g2g-core): `score` ordering (domain > hardware > rank), a default context keeping registration order, a Cuda preference flipping to a GPU decoder registered second, and `rank` breaking a tie; the existing nvdec+ffmpeg domain-aware registry test passes through the generalized search. DESIGN.md updated.
- M334: FlexFEC (RFC 8627) forward error correction. New sans-IO `flexfec` module, the wide-mask sibling of ULPFEC: a repair packet rides a dedicated FEC SSRC (its own RTP stream) and a variable-length protection bitmask (15 / 46 / 109 bits, the per-word continuation flag picking the shortest form) names which media packets, by sequence offset from an `SN base`, it covers. One repair therefore protects up to 109 packets, past ULPFEC's 16, and arbitrary strided / 2-D patterns are expressible. `build_flexfec_packet` / `recover_packet` XOR the same RTP fields as ULPFEC (P/X/CC, M/PT, timestamp, length, payload); `FlexFecEncoder` emits one repair per group and `FlexFecDecoder` buffers media + repairs and chains recoveries, so 2-D (row + column) repairs reconstruct a multi-loss row. Wired into both elements: `UdpSink::with_flexfec(group, pt, ssrc)` (a `FecMode::FlexFec`) and `UdpSrc::with_flexfec(pt)` (a parallel decoder routed by payload type, alongside the ULPFEC path). Tests: mask round-trips across all three widths, single-loss recovery, a 24-packet group recovered by one repair (impossible for ULPFEC), an encoder/decoder round trip, and 2-D recovery of two losses in one row via column repairs; an end-to-end `flexfec_recovers_a_loss_in_a_group_beyond_ulpfec` loopback recovers a drop in a 20-packet group through a one-way (no-feedback, no-retransmit) path. Real-peer interop unverified (sandbox); validated g2g <-> g2g.
- M333: SRT live-mode congestion control (output pacing). SRT live mode does not use the window-based AIMD of file transfer; it paces packets so the egress does not burst-flood the path and leaves headroom for retransmits. New sans-IO, integer-only `LiveCc`: it either caps at a fixed bandwidth or follows the measured input rate (an EWMA over per-packet byte/time samples) plus an overhead margin, and reports `snd_period_us(len)`, the microseconds to wait before the next packet to hold the target rate (0 before the estimate warms up = send freely). `SrtSink::with_max_bandwidth(bytes_per_sec)` enables it (SRT semantics: a positive value is a hard cap, `0` is rate-follow with 25% headroom); the send loop tracks a `next_send_us` cursor and `tokio::time::sleep`s each packet to its scheduled slot. Tests: unit tests for the fixed cap (1 MB/s -> 1000 B = 1 ms), rate-follow tracking + overhead (1.25 MB/s input, 25% headroom -> 800 us for a 1250 B packet), and no-pacing-before-warmup; an end-to-end `congestion_control_paces_egress_to_the_bandwidth_cap` loopback that sends 30 packets with no inter-frame sleep under a 200 kB/s cap and asserts the caller's wall-clock elapsed is held near the expected ~197 ms (a lower bound robust to scheduler slack), where an unpaced loop would finish ~instantly.
- M332: SRT mid-stream key rotation. The stream cipher key no longer lives for the whole session: `SrtSink::with_key_rotation(every_packets)` rolls to a fresh random key periodically so a recovered key exposes only a bounded window. Rotation rides SRT's two key slots (`KK` even/odd): `SrtSender`/`SrtReceiver` now hold both an even and an odd `SrtCrypto`, each data packet is stamped and decrypted by its `KK` parity, and a rekey installs the new key into the *inactive* slot then switches to it, so packets still in flight (and NAK retransmits) under the previous key keep decrypting until the next rotation overwrites that slot. The sender buffers `(seq, kk, ciphertext)` so a retransmit carries the parity it was originally encrypted under, not the current active key. A new `Control::KeyMaterial { rsp, km }` control packet (SRT user/extended type `0x7FFF`, subtype KMREQ/KMRSP) carries the rekey: `SrtSender::rekey` builds it (via `SrtCrypto::build_km(pass, kk)`) and announces it before the first packet under the new key; `SrtSrc` unwraps it (`SrtCrypto::km_kk` + `from_km`) and installs it into the named slot. Tests: a sans-IO `rekey_switches_keys_and_receiver_decrypts_across_the_switch` (even->odd flip, wire `KK` flips, all payloads decrypt) and a `KeyMaterial` control round-trip; an end-to-end `key_rotation_rolls_the_cipher_mid_stream` loopback rekeying every 3 packets where the listener installs each new key from the KM and decrypts all 12 payloads in order across `>= 2` rotations. Lossless-path rekey only; KM retransmit-until-KMRSP for a lossy rekey announcement is a follow-up.
- M331: AES-256 for the SRT stream cipher. `srtcrypto` was AES-128 only; the SEK is now an `Aes128([u8;16])` / `Aes256([u8;32])` enum and `process` selects AES-128-CTR or AES-256-CTR (the 128-bit CTR counter block is key-size independent, only the key schedule differs). The KM (Keying Material) message already carries `KLen`, so the two sizes interoperate on one wire layout: `build_km` records the key length and the KEK is derived to match (PBKDF2-HMAC-SHA1 to 16 or 32 bytes, wrapped with `Kek::<Aes128>` / `Kek::<Aes256>` RFC 3394), and `from_km` reads `KLen` to rebuild the right cipher, so the listener picks up AES-256 from the handshake with no extra config. `SrtSink::with_aes256()` opts in (default stays AES-128); `SrtCrypto::generate` takes an `AesKeySize`. `build_km` also gained a key-parity (`KK`: even/odd) argument and a `km_kk` reader, the groundwork for mid-stream rekeying. Tests: AES-256 CTR round-trip, AES-256 KM round-trip (asserts `KLen` = 32/4 and parity preserved) and wrong-passphrase rejection (unit); an `aes256_encrypted_stream_round_trips` end-to-end loopback where the caller opts into AES-256 and the listener decrypts all payloads to their tags from the KM alone. No new dependencies (the `aes` / `aes-kw` / `ctr` crates already provide the 256-bit types).
- M330: interleaved (column) ULPFEC for burst-loss recovery. Single-level ULPFEC emits one repair per contiguous group and recovers only one loss per group, so a burst of consecutive losses defeats it. `InterleavedFecEncoder` buffers a `rows x stride` block (capped at 16, the level-0 mask width) and emits `stride` *column* repairs, where column `c` protects the strided set `c, c+stride, c+2*stride, ...`; a burst of up to `stride` consecutive losses then hits at most one packet per column, so each column repair recovers its loss and the whole burst is reconstructed. `build_fec_packet` now derives the protection mask from each packet's actual sequence offset from the SN base (identical bits for a contiguous run, so existing single-level behavior is unchanged) and rejects a set spanning more than 16 sequence numbers; the decoder needed no change (it already reads arbitrary masks and chains recoveries). `UdpSink::with_interleaved_fec(rows, stride, pt, ssrc)` wires it in (the sink's `fec` field became a `FecMode` enum: None / Single / Interleaved). Tests: a sans-IO unit test recovers a 4-consecutive-packet burst through `FecDecoder` that single-level cannot, plus a `>16`-span rejection; an end-to-end `udp_loopback` test sends a 4x4 block through a lossy proxy that drops the consecutive burst seqs 5..=8 (columns 1/2/3/0) over a strictly one-way path (no feedback, retransmit off) and the receiver recovers all 16 AUs via the column repairs alone. FlexFEC (RFC 8627) remains the open FEC item.
- M329: RTCP sender reports on `UdpSink` (RFC 3550 SR). `with_rtcp_sender_reports(interval_ms)` opts the sink into emitting an RTCP SR on the RTP/RTCP-muxed socket at most every interval: it pairs the current NTP wall time with the last media RTP timestamp and this SSRC's packet / octet counters, the mapping a receiver needs to sync the RTP clock to wall time (the basis of inter-stream A/V sync). Off by default (SR is a session concern, and `gst udpsink` likewise leaves it to the session) so existing byte-exact egress consumers and tests are unchanged. The sink tracks media-only counters (`rtp_packets` / `rtp_octets`, payload octets past the 12-byte header; FEC and RTX ride other SSRCs and are excluded) and the last RTP timestamp, and builds the SR via the existing `rtcp::build_sender_report`; NTP-now is `SystemTime` since the 1900 epoch. Test (`m47_udp_egress`): with `interval_ms = 0` the first frame emits one SR after its two media packets; the loopback receiver finds the RTCP datagram (told from media by payload type), and it carries the media SSRC, the last RTP timestamp (0 for pts 0), a nonzero NTP, and packet/octet counts of 2 / 8 (two 4-byte NAL payloads). RTP-clock-to-NTP extrapolation precision and `UdpSink` RTCP BYE on EOS remain follow-ups.
- M328: SRT TSBPD (Timestamp-Based Packet Delivery) receiver timing. `SrtReceiver` previously delivered each packet the moment it was in order (jitter passed straight through); `set_tsbpd(latency_us)` now holds packets to a fixed buffering delay so the output is steady. The sans-IO core stores each packet's sender timestamp (the data header's microsecond field, already stamped by `SrtSink` from `pts_ns/1000`) and `take_ready_at(now_us)` releases an in-order packet only once its scheduled time is due, where `delivery_time(pkt) = base + pkt.timestamp` and `base` is anchored on the first deliverable packet so it releases `latency_us` after that instant and every later packet inherits the same delay. Without `set_tsbpd`, `take_ready_at` is a pass-through to the old `take_ready` (no gate). `SrtSrc` enables it at the advertised handshake latency and adds a 5 ms receive timeout so the buffer still flushes due packets during a silent gap (bounding the extra delivery jitter); the run loop drains on both datagram arrival and timer wake, in sequence order regardless of arrival order. Tests (sans-IO, injected clock): three packets 20 ms apart held until each scheduled instant; reordered arrivals (5 before 4) still delivered in sequence order on schedule; the no-TSBPD pass-through. The SRT loopback + encrypted-loopback integration tests stay green with the 120 ms hold active. Timestamp 32-bit wrap (~71 min) and congestion control remain follow-ups.
- M327: bindings polish follow-up, a portable abi3 wheel, type stubs, and CI guard. The `g2g-pyapi` wheel now builds against the stable ABI (`pyo3/abi3-py311` in the maturin feature list), so a single `g2g-0.1.0-cp311-abi3` wheel runs on every CPython >= 3.11 instead of one wheel per minor version. The 3.11 floor is forced by the buffer protocol: `FrameView.__getbuffer__` / `Py_buffer` / `PyBuffer_FillInfo` only entered the limited API in 3.11 (a py38 build fails to compile), so `requires-python = ">=3.11"`. Added `g2g.pyi` + `py.typed`, which maturin packages as `g2g/__init__.pyi` + `g2g/py.typed`, giving IDE completion / type-checking for `Pipeline` / `AppSrc` / `AppSink` / `FrameView`. New CI `bindings` job (`.github/workflows/ci.yml`) runs `cargo test -p g2g-pyapi --features python` (embedded interpreter), builds the abi3 wheel + runs the Python example, and `make`s + runs the C example, so the bindings and both example programs cannot rot. Verified on this host: the abi3 wheel (built on a cp314 host, tagged cp311-abi3) imports and drives the pipeline, the stub parses, and all three CI commands pass locally.
- M326: bindings polish, a redistributable `g2g-pyapi` wheel plus in-tree C and Python example programs. Added `g2g-pyapi/pyproject.toml` (maturin backend) so `maturin build` / `maturin develop` produce an importable `g2g` extension: the build enables the `python` code gate plus `pyo3/extension-module` (the wheel is loaded by an existing interpreter and does not link libpython, the inverse of the auto-initialize path the in-crate `cargo test` suite needs, both coexist in pyo3 0.26 so `cargo test -p g2g-pyapi --features python` is unchanged). `examples/g2g-c-example/` (standalone, not a workspace member) drives an `appsrc ! appsink` pipeline through the `g2g-capi` C ABI: a `Makefile` builds the `g2g-capi` staticlib via cargo and links `main.c` against it (`-lpthread -ldl -lm`); it pushes three synthetic RGBA frames, pulls them back zero-copy, polls the bus, and asserts the frame counters. `g2g-pyapi/examples/appsink_numpy.py` is the Python counterpart, pushing numpy frames and pulling each back as a `FrameView` wrapped in a buffer-sharing `np.frombuffer` (asserts `OWNDATA is False`, the zero-copy lend). New `g2g-pyapi/README.md` (wheel build + example) and a per-example README. Both example programs were built and run on this host (wheel imported into a fresh venv; C example linked the staticlib) and produce the expected 3-frame output.
- M325: zero-copy `g2g-pyapi` `AppSink` pull. `AppSink.pull()` / `try_pull()` previously copied each frame into a Python `bytes` at the language boundary; they now return a `FrameView` that lends the frame's host bytes through the buffer protocol with no copy (wrap with `memoryview(view)` or `np.frombuffer(view, np.uint8)`). `FrameView` owns the `Frame`, and `PyBuffer_FillInfo` increfs it into the buffer view, so the lent bytes outlive any `memoryview` / numpy array over it: pulling later frames and tearing the pipeline down cannot dangle a retained view (the inverse of the `g2g-python` host, where the frame is borrowed for the call and a retained view is rejected). A `System` frame is lent directly; a strided `SystemView` is materialized once into a stable contiguous buffer the view owns; a GPU / foreign domain raises `BufferError`. Bytes are lent read-only (`readonly = 1`). `pull(timeout_ms=...)` adds a bounded blocking pull (poll until a frame or the deadline; `None` on timeout or EOS, told apart via the pipeline's `is_done()`). Tests (embedded interpreter): the round-trip asserts the pulled object is a read-only `FrameView` whose `memoryview` matches the pushed bytes; a lifetime test holds a `memoryview` across a later pull and `p.wait()`, then asserts it still reads the original frame, and checks numpy's `OWNDATA is False` (shares, not copies) when numpy is present.
- M324: `Mp4Src` progressive (non-fragmented) MP4 demux. `Mp4Src` was fMP4-only (it walked `moof`+`mdat` fragments), so a plain `ftyp/moov/mdat` file, what most tools write and the gst-python-ml `data/*.mp4` clips are, would not load. Added `parse_progressive`, which reads the `moov` sample tables (`stsz` sizes, `stts` decode durations, `ctts` composition offsets, `stsc` + `stco`/`co64` chunk layout, `stss` sync samples) and slices each sample out of the `mdat` by absolute file offset, yielding the same Annex-B `Sample` list as `parse_fragments`; `run` picks the path by `moof` presence, so fragmented and progressive files both just work. Validated live on the RTX 3060: raw `data/people.mp4` (no pre-fragmenting) runs the full `uridecodebin uri=file://… ! videoconvert ! videoscale ! RGBA ! pyelement(objectdetector,onnx,cuda) ! analyticsoverlay ! videoconvert ! autovideosink` YOLO pipeline with boxes drawn. Unit test `fmp4::parse_progressive_reads_stbl_sample_tables` builds a minimal two-sample `moov`+`mdat` and asserts the offsets, timing, and `stss` keyframe flag. (Single video track, the first `trak`, matching `parse_header`; multi-track selection is a follow-up.)
- M323: pure-g2g file -> hosted-YOLO -> overlay -> display, the `gst-launch ... ! decodebin ! pyml_objectdetector ! pyml_overlay ! autovideosink` workflow run entirely on g2g. New `g2g-launch-py` binary (g2g-python `launch` feature) = `g2g-launch` plus `g2g_python::register`, so one text pipeline mixes built-in elements with the hosted Python `pyelement` / `pysrc` / `pyaggregator`. Registered `analyticsoverlay` as a launch element (draws `AnalyticsMeta` boxes; `analytics`-gated). Validated live on the RTX 3060: `uridecodebin uri=file://clip.mp4 ! videoconvert ! videoscale ! video/x-raw,format=RGBA,width=640,height=640 ! pyelement module=objectdetector class=ObjectDetector engine-name=onnx model-name=yolo11m.onnx device=cuda:0 ! analyticsoverlay ! videoconvert ! autovideosink` plays `people.mp4` and `soccer_tracking.mp4` with detection boxes drawn (and the same chain from `v4l2src` for live camera). Five real bugs in the file-decode path surfaced and were fixed, each its own latent gap: (1) `Mp4Src` advertised `framerate: Rate::Any`, which aborts fixate; now a `Rate::Range` like `RtspSrc` (PTS carries the real timing). (2) `fmp4` `parse_trun` rejected `trun` v1, the version ffmpeg writes for B-frame streams; v0/v1 parse identically (the signed cts field is skipped), so both are accepted. (3) `FfmpegH264Dec` emitted its mid-stream `CapsChanged` with `framerate: Rate::Any`; a downstream format/geometry transform then could not `fixate()` the forwarded caps and fell back to forwarding the decoder's raw I420 verbatim, which a constraining capsfilter rejected, so the decoder now stamps the negotiated framerate (default 30/1). (4) `PyTransform` was a "legacy transform" with an unconstrained output, unsolvable behind a decoder's runtime caps change; it now declares an identity `DerivedOutput` constraint (it is a passthrough), so the solver derives its output edge and the runtime forward-resolve steers a mid-stream `CapsChanged` through it. (5) the host stored detector boxes as raw pixels in g2g's normalized-`[0,1]` `BBox`, so an `analyticsoverlay` denormalized them off-screen (boxes invisible); the host now divides by the frame dims it already knows. Tests: `fmp4::parse_trun_accepts_v0_and_v1`, updated `ffmpegdec` caps tests, `m198_analytics` asserts the normalized bbox.
- M322: end-to-end host of the real gst-python-ml `objectdetector` under `GSTML_BACKEND=g2g`, the payoff of the M198/M321 host track. `PyTransform` imports the actual `objectdetector` element, forwards `engine-name=onnx` / `model-name` / `device`, and drives one real video frame through `g2g_process`; the hosted element loads its ONNX YOLO model on the GPU and runs inference, with detections surfacing as `AnalyticsMeta` on the output frame. Validated on the developer's RTX 3060: a frame of `data/people.mp4` yields 21 detections (incl. label 0 = person) through the PyO3 host. Two real host<->package gaps surfaced and were fixed on the gst-python-ml side: the `objectdetector` leaf now imports under g2g (gst factory registration is gated on `backend.BACKEND`, not on whether `gi` merely imports), and the g2g backend's lazy model load now guards on the model, not the engine (setting `device` eagerly creates the engine, so an engine-only check skipped the load); the g2g `VideoTransform` also reduces the host's 4-channel RGBA/BGRA to 3-channel RGB for the RGB-native ML models (the bridge gst gets from upstream `videoconvert`). Test `m322_objectdetector_e2e` (`analytics` feature) is host-only: it skips cleanly unless `G2G_PYML_DIR` points at a gst-python-ml checkout with its `.venv` + model + CUDA, so CI is a no-op.
- M321: `g2g-python` forwards element properties to the hosted Python instance. `PyTransform` gained the common ML tunables (`model-name`, `engine-name`, `device`, `batch-size`, `frame-stride`, `input-format`, `post-process`, `device-queue-id`, `compile`, `track`) as declared properties; any declared property beyond `module`/`class`/`draw-label` is stashed and `setattr` onto the Python object at construction (gst `model-name` -> Python `model_name`, the PropValue scalar -> the matching Python scalar via `into_py_any`). This is what lets a hosted gst-python-ml element under `GSTML_BACKEND=g2g` actually load its model: previously only `draw-label` reached the instance. An undeclared property name is still rejected (a typo, not a silent pass-through). Forwarding for `PySource` / `PyAggregator` is a follow-up (they pass no params yet). Tested (`m321_property_forwarding`, `analytics` feature): a `PropEcho` fixture echoes the forwarded properties back as metadata, asserting `model-name`/`device` reach `self.model_name`/`self.device` as strings and `batch-size=4` arrives as a Python int (used directly as an integer detection label, which fails loudly if it were a string).
- M320: fan-in request pads, the runtime equivalent of GStreamer's aggregator/muxer request *sink* pads and the dual of the M310/M319 dynamic fan-out. `run_aggregator_dynamic` returns a `DynamicFaninHandle` whose `add_input` attaches a source to a *running* terminal aggregator (`MultiInputElement`); the aggregator declares a fixed pad capacity (`input_count`), the handle reserves the next pad index atomically (rejecting past capacity with `Shutdown`, the M205 dark-slot bound), and a single aggregator arm owns `&mut` and fixates + configures each new pad inline before its first frame (no aliasing). Per-pad-tagged frames merge as in `run_fanin_session`; a per-input EOS flushes that pad, and the run ends once the handle is dropped *and* every attached input has ended (the `DynamicJoin` completion rule, with the aggregator arm holding one tagged-sender keepalive so a no-input run does not finish early). Pending inputs are drained before each blocking select so an input requested before a frame is never missed. A merged downstream output (the `run_muxer_sink` shape) for the dynamic fan-in is a follow-up. Tested: two runtime inputs land on distinct pads (5/3 frames, EOS each), a third pad stays dark, and an add past capacity is rejected.
- M319: dynamic broadcast tee. `run_source_tee_dynamic` is the broadcast counterpart of M310's `run_source_router_dynamic`: where the router distributes each `DataFrame` round-robin to one branch, the tee shares every frame to *every* attached branch via the M250 zero-copy path (`MemoryDomain::make_shareable` once, then a refcount handle per branch), so an inference branch and a display branch both see the whole stream with no byte copies. This closes the M310 follow-up that a true broadcast tee needed frame sharing (the sharing landed in M250; M319 wires it into the dynamic fan-out). Route and broadcast share one driver (`run_source_fanout_dynamic` with a `FanOutMode`), differing only in `DataFrame` distribution; `CapsChanged` / `Segment` / `Flush` / `Eos`, sticky caps, branch attach, and shutdown are identical. Tested: two runtime branches each receive the full 6-frame stream (vs M310's split), each sees the sticky caps once, and a single branch still gets the whole stream.
- M318: zero-copy libcamera -> GPU dma-buf import, investigated and settled on real hardware. New `libcamera-dmabuf` feature + module probes whether a GPU can import a libcamera `FrameBuffer` dma-buf (the Linux analog of the CUDA / AHardwareBuffer interop): `dmabuf_import_memory_type_bits` queries `vkGetMemoryFdPropertiesKHR`, and `import_dmabuf_to_gpu_buffer` actually attempts the import + `VkBuffer` bind via raw Vulkan (wgpu-hal + ash). Finding on the developer's UVC webcam + RTX 3060: libcamera does export a real dma-buf fd, and the driver *reports* it importable (`memory_type_bits=0x11`), but the real `vkAllocateMemory` import fails to bind for every reported memory type, so zero-copy is NOT viable for a USB camera feeding a discrete GPU (the buffer is CPU/vmalloc-backed; the dGPU cannot map it) and the M315 CPU-upload path is correct. The full import-to-`wgpu::Texture` element is deliberately gated behind this probe rather than shipped blind; it is expected to pay off on an integrated GPU (shared memory) or a CSI/ISP camera (GPU-visible buffers). Feasibility probes (`inspect_buffer_fd`, `gpu_can_import_camera_dmabuf`) are `#[ignore]`. Also rounds out `LibCameraSrc`: camera-by-id selection landed in M317; this leaves no open follow-ups on the libcamera track beyond the iGPU/CSI zero-copy path.
- M317: `LibCameraSrc` image controls + camera-by-id selection. Adds `with_brightness` / `with_contrast` / `with_saturation` (and `brightness` / `contrast` / `saturation` properties): post-capture image adjustments that, unlike exposure / gain, do not change the exposure time, so brightness is the low-light lever that brightens a short-exposure frame *without* lowering the frame rate. Also `with_camera_id(substring)` / `camera-id` property selects the camera by an id substring (stable across reboots, unlike enumeration order); a non-matching id fails rather than silently falling back to index 0. All controls go through the M316 `set_if_supported` guard (this webcam exposes Brightness/Contrast/Saturation but not AnalogueGain). Validated live: at a fixed 8 ms exposure, brightness -0.8 vs +0.9 moved mean luma 16 -> 117 (no fps change), and selecting the camera by its USB VID:PID substring captured while a bogus id failed. Unit tests cover the builders/properties (image adjustments do not flip auto-exposure off; camera-id round-trips); the brightness-luma and by-id capture tests are `#[ignore]`.
- M316: `LibCameraSrc` exposure / gain controls, the real lever for frame rate in low light. `with_exposure(us)` / `with_gain(g)` (and `with_auto_exposure(bool)`, plus `exposure` / `gain` / `auto-exposure` properties) set a manual `ExposureTime` / `AnalogueGain` and turn auto-exposure off, applied as start controls alongside the M313 frame-rate cap. With AE on the camera lengthens exposure in a dim room until the rate collapses (M314 found this webcam pinned to ~9 fps); a fixed short exposure removes that bottleneck. Validated live: at a 30 fps request the same camera went from 8.8 fps (AE on) to 24.9 fps with an 8 ms manual exposure, ~3x, and displayed smoothly to a Wayland window at ~28 fps (darker, as expected for a short exposure). Robustness fix surfaced here: setting a control a UVC camera does not advertise makes libcamera throw a C++ `std::out_of_range` that aborts the process across the FFI boundary, so every control is now applied through a `set_if_supported` guard that checks the camera's `ControlInfoMap` first (this webcam exposes `ExposureTime` but not `AnalogueGain`, so gain is skipped, not set). Unit tests cover the builders/properties (manual exposure implies AE off); the AE-vs-manual comparison test is `#[ignore]`.
- M315: libcamera into the GPU/ML path. New g2g-ml `libcamera-wgpu` feature (Linux) chains `LibCameraSrc -> VideoConvert(NV12) -> WgpuPreprocess`, turning live camera frames into a normalized f32 NCHW RGB tensor on the GPU, the camera-side entry to the ML tensor graph (`-> inference -> postprocess`). No new code in the elements (`WgpuPreprocess` already uploads System NV12 to a storage buffer and runs the compute shader); the milestone is the feature wiring (forwards `g2g-plugins/libcamera`) plus an end-to-end test. Validated live on the developer's UVC webcam + RTX 3060: 640x480 YUYV camera frames convert to NV12 and preprocess to `Tensor{F32,[1,3,480,640],Nchw}` on the GPU, 5 frames captured -> 5 tensors at the sink with the expected tensor caps. The test (`libcamera_preprocess_to_gpu_tensor`) is `#[ignore]` and skips cleanly without a wgpu adapter. (Zero-copy dma-buf import of libcamera buffers straight into wgpu, avoiding the CPU upload, is a deeper follow-up, the Linux analog of the CUDA / AHardwareBuffer interop paths.)
- M314: `LibCameraSrc` MJPEG capture. `with_mjpeg(true)` (or `format=mjpeg`) negotiates the camera's MJPEG mode and emits `CompressedVideo{Mjpeg}` instead of raw NV12/YUYV, for `MjpegDec` downstream, the on-camera-compression path for resolutions / frame rates uncompressed YUYV cannot sustain over USB. Refactored the format negotiation around an `OutKind` enum (Nv12 / Yuyv / Mjpeg) that carries both the libcamera pixel format and the `Caps` it maps to (raw vs compressed); MJPEG mode asks for MJPEG only (no raw fallback, since the caller explicitly wants compressed), raw mode keeps the NV12-then-YUYV auto-pick. The capture path is unchanged: each frame's planes are already packed by `bytes_used`, which for MJPEG is the single JPEG plane. Added a `format` property. Validated live on the developer's UVC webcam: the source negotiated 640x480 MJPEG and `LibCameraSrc(mjpeg) -> MjpegDec -> FakeSink` captured and decoded 30 real JPEG frames end to end. Finding: this webcam runs ~9 fps in *every* format and resolution (640x480 and 320x240, YUYV and MJPEG, on AC or battery), the signature of auto-exposure lengthening the exposure time in low light, not a bandwidth or power limit; MJPEG's frame-rate benefit only appears once the sensor is not exposure-bound (more light). Unit tests cover the `OutKind` pixel-format / caps mapping and the `format` property; the MJPEG capture+decode test is `#[ignore]`.
- M313: `LibCameraSrc` frame-rate enforcement. The requested `with_fps` / `framerate` is now pinned on the camera via a fixed `FrameDurationLimits` (min == max, in microseconds) passed as a start control, which libcamera's `uvcvideo` handler maps to the UVC frame interval (M312 stamped PTS from the requested rate but let the camera free-run). Validated live on the developer's UVC webcam: 5 fps and 8 fps capture track the requested rate within a frame of slack (a forced 3 fps is visibly choppy in a Wayland window). Finding worth recording: a cap cannot exceed a capture mode's own ceiling, and this camera's uncompressed YUYV 640x480 tops out near ~10 fps (USB-bandwidth bound), so 30 fps at that resolution needs the MJPEG path. The fps test (`libcamera_fps_limit_is_enforced`) is `#[ignore]` (needs a camera) and asserts the measured rate neither exceeds the cap nor collapses below it for an achievable rate.
- M312: libcamera capture source. `LibCameraSrc` (`libcamera` feature, Linux-only) captures from a camera via the libcamera stack, the modern Linux camera path: it covers UVC webcams through libcamera's `uvcvideo` pipeline handler (same devices as `V4l2Src`) plus CSI/ISP cameras V4L2 alone cannot drive. Links the system libcamera through the `libcamera` crate (lit-robotics bindings; needs libcamera-devel + libclang at build). The source asks libcamera for NV12 (planar, decoder/ML/GPU-friendly) and falls back to YUYV (the UVC-universal packed format) when the camera does not offer NV12, mapping whatever survives validation to `Caps::RawVideo`; geometry is negotiated in `intercept_caps` (libcamera may adjust the request). libcamera is callback-driven and thread-affine, so all libcamera work (manager, camera, request ring, completion callback) runs on a dedicated capture thread that packs each completed frame's planes contiguously (Y then interleaved UV for NV12) and forwards them over a bounded channel to the async `run` loop, the same structure as `V4l2Src`; keeping no libcamera handle in the struct between negotiation and `run` keeps the element `Send`. Registered `libcamerasrc` with `camera` / `width` / `height` / `framerate` properties. Validated live on the developer's UVC webcam: libcamera enumerated the device via `uvcvideo`, negotiated 640x480 (fell back to YUYV, the camera offers no NV12), and 30 frames flowed end to end through `LibCameraSrc -> FakeSink` in order. Unit-tested offline (format mapping, property round-trip, unconfigured-source error path); the live capture test is `#[ignore]`. Not in CI: distro libcamera (e.g. Ubuntu runners) is older than the `libcamera` crate's >= 0.4 floor, so this is host-validated like the NVIDIA stack. Best-effort `framerate` is advisory (PTS / latency stamping); libcamera `FrameDurationLimits` enforcement is a follow-up.
- M311: ONVIF camera source. `OnvifSrc` (`onvif` feature) turns an ONVIF camera into an H.264 source by handling the camera's *control plane*: it discovers the RTSP URL over SOAP, then delegates the RTP/decode loop to `RtspSrc`. `discover()` sends one WS-Discovery `Probe` to the `239.255.255.250:3702` multicast group and collects the `ProbeMatch` device-service URLs; `resolve_stream_uri()` runs `GetCapabilities` (find the Media service) then `GetProfiles` (pick a profile) then `GetStreamUri` (read the RTSP URL), authenticated with a WS-Security `UsernameToken` digest (`Base64(SHA1(nonce ++ created ++ password))`). The SOAP layer is hand-rolled (the lumeohq `onvif` crate is git-only with nested git deps): fixed request templates + `roxmltree` response reads, so the footprint is reqwest + roxmltree + sha1 + base64 + getrandom, no git dependencies. `RtspSrc` gained `with_credentials` (threaded into retina's `SessionOptions`) because cameras gate the media stream behind the same account. `OnvifSrc` resolves the URI lazily in `intercept_caps` and builds the inner `RtspSrc` once, so re-fixate retries and `run` reuse it; registered `onvifsrc` with `location` / `user` / `password` properties. Scope is discovery + stream-URI only (PTZ / events deferred). Tested offline: SOAP envelope build, password digest, the four response parsers, ISO-8601 timestamp, UUID layout, property round-trip, unconfigured-source error path (9 lib tests), plus a loopback integration test that drives the full GetCapabilities -> GetProfiles -> GetStreamUri sequence over real sockets against an in-process SOAP mock and asserts the WS-Security digest is sent on each call; live discovery / resolve are `#[ignore]` (need a camera on the LAN). CI compiles the feature and runs the offline tests.
- M310: runtime request pads (dynamic fan-out branches), the runtime equivalent of GStreamer tee request pads. `run_source_router_dynamic` returns a `DynamicFanoutHandle` whose `add_branch` attaches an output branch *while the pipeline runs*; the branch configures from the fan-out's sticky caps (the source's fixated output caps, replayed into each branch the moment it attaches) and then receives its share of subsequent frames. Built on a new no-spawn `DynamicJoin` primitive (`runtime/join.rs`): a `join_all` that also polls a control channel and folds newly-arrived arms into the running poll set, completing when the channel closes and all arms finish, so a branch can be added without an executor `spawn` (preserving the `no_std` structured-concurrency model). The router distributes `DataFrame`s round-robin across attached branches and broadcasts `CapsChanged` / `Segment` / `Flush` / `Eos` to all; pending branches are attached before each routing step so a frame backlog is never dropped to an empty port set. Two limits, both noted as follow-ups: frames are not `Clone` (zero-copy design), so this *routes* rather than *broadcasts* (a true broadcast tee needs frame sharing); and `mux` runtime *input* addition (fan-in request pads) is still static. Tested: `DynamicJoin` unit tests (late-arm fold-in, stays-pending-while-open) + `m310_dynamic_pads` (two runtime branches split an 8-frame stream and each receive the sticky caps; a single runtime branch receives the whole stream).
- M308: Android camera capture. `Camera2Src` (`camera2` feature) is a `SourceLoop` that captures `YUV_420_888` from a camera via the NDK Camera2 API (`ACameraManager` / `ACameraDevice` / `ACameraCaptureSession`) and emits tight NV12, the Android analog of `V4l2Src` / `avfvideosrc` and the capture mirror of the decode path.
