The safe `ndk` crate does not wrap Camera2, so the camera control surface is called through `ndk-sys` directly (the camera symbols are not feature-gated); frame delivery reuses a safe `ndk` `ImageReader` (the session targets its `ANativeWindow`, we acquire `Image`s and pack the planes to NV12, handling any vendor layout via the row/pixel strides). `ACameraManager_openCamera` is synchronous, so the whole session is built inline in `configure_pipeline`; a `CameraSession` owns every raw handle and tears them down in dependency order on drop. Registered `camera2src`. Validated on a Pixel (`android_camera2_probe` + `tools/android-camera2-smoke.sh`): real rear-camera capture, 5 NV12 frames at 460800 bytes each (640x480). Two device-found fixes: `ndk-sys` declares the Camera2 externs but links no library, so a `#[link(name = "camera2ndk")]` is needed; and the camera HAL delivers buffers via binder callbacks into the process (like Codec2), so the run loop must yield the CPU between `acquire` attempts (a tight busy-poll starved the callback threads and no frame ever landed) and a bare-binary caller must start a binder threadpool. CI cross-checks the feature.
- M307: Android AAudio. `AAudioSink` (PCM render) and `AAudioSrc` (PCM capture), the Android analog of the WASAPI / ALSA / PulseAudio elements, via the `ndk` crate's `audio` module (`AAudioStream`); `aaudio` feature (implies `std`, needs `ndk/audio` = api-level-26). The sink opens an output stream and writes interleaved `PcmS16Le` / `PcmF32Le` (looping over partial writes); the source opens an input stream, reports the device's actual format / rate / channels as its caps, and reads 10 ms buffers in its run loop. Both drive the stream synchronously on the owning task and assert `Send` under the single-thread-executor contract. Registered `aaudiosink` / `aaudiosrc`. Validated on a Pixel (`android_aaudio_probe` + `tools/android-aaudio-smoke.sh`): render (24000 frames) and mic capture (5 buffers) both succeed. Two device-found fixes: the streams open with `PerformanceMode::None`, not `LowLatency` (low-latency opens an MMAP stream that is callback-driven, on which a blocking `read`/`write` fails; true low latency would need the AAudio data-callback API, a follow-up); and ndk 0.9's `read`/`write` wrappers pipe the positive frame count through `AudioError::from_result`, which treats only `0` as success, so a completed transfer surfaces as `Err(__Unknown(frames))` and is recovered as a count. CI cross-checks the feature.
- M306: Android hardware video encode. `MediaCodecEnc` (`mediacodec` feature) is the encode mirror of `MediaCodecDec` and the Android analog of `MfEncode` / `VtEncode`: NV12 in (`MemoryDomain::System`), Annex-B H.264 / H.265 out. Unlike the decoder it uses the ordinary ByteBuffer path on both sides (no Surface). The MediaCodec encoder emits the parameter sets as a `BUFFER_FLAG_CODEC_CONFIG` Annex-B buffer; the element captures that and prepends it to every key frame, so the elementary stream is self-contained (the pipeline's Annex-B framing convention). Configured with `COLOR_FormatYUV420SemiPlanar` (NV12) so a decode -> encode transcode is copy-compatible; `with_bitrate` / `with_framerate` / `with_keyframe_interval` builders. Drains on EOS (empty input + end-of-stream flag). Registered launch-only as `mediacodecenc` / `mediacodecench265`. Validated on a Pixel (`android_mediacodec_enc_probe` + `tools/android-mediacodec-enc-smoke.sh`): 30 NV12 frames in, 30 access units out, the first key frame `[SPS, PPS, IDR]`. Two device-found fixes: a bare-binary caller must start a binder threadpool (Codec2 allocates encoder buffers via an in-process binder callback, like the decoder); and the parameter sets are prepended to a key frame only when the encoder did not already inline them (the Pixel encoder repeats SPS/PPS on each IDR, so an unconditional prepend duplicated them). CI cross-checks the feature.
- M305: Android on-screen present, closing the decode -> GPU -> display loop entirely on the GPU. The decoded RGBA `wgpu::Texture` from M304 is presented through a `wgpu::Surface` built over an Android `ANativeWindow` by the existing `WgpuSink`, on the *same* interop device the decoder converts on (a wgpu texture binds only to its own device). New `mediacodec_wgpu::create_android_surface` builds + configures the surface from a `NativeWindow` (raw-window-handle via wgpu's `rwh` re-export, `get_default_config` for the device's preferred format / present mode); `InteropDevice::gpu_context()` shares the interop device as a `GpuContext`; and `MediaCodecDec::with_gpu_device(dev)` decodes onto that shared device instead of one created lazily, so decode and present are copy-free. `gpu::texture_of` now also recognises the decoder's `WgpuRgbaTexture` keep-alive, so the one `WgpuSink` presents either an overlay's or the Android decoder's texture; the `mediacodec-wgpu` feature now pulls `wgpu-sink`. Validated on a Pixel (`android_surface_present_probe` + `tools/android-surface-present-smoke.sh`, cargo-ndk `--platform 26`): the decode -> GPU convert -> `wgpu::Surface` present chain runs end to end, 9 frames presented to an `Rgba8UnormSrgb` surface, and the presented content reads back through the `ImageReader` with real per-channel variance. (A real on-screen `SurfaceView` / `NativeActivity` is the production target; the `ImageReader`-backed surface is the headless equivalent.) CI cross-checks the feature.
- M304 (pipelining + negotiation): two refinements to the Android decode->GPU path. (1) `YcbcrToRgba` no longer blocks on a fence per frame: it runs a `RING_DEPTH`-slot ring (each slot its own fence / command buffer / descriptor set + the in-flight conversion's transient import objects), submitting without waiting and reclaiming a slot's resources only when it is reused, so up to `RING_DEPTH` conversions overlap downstream consumption (the returned texture's writes still complete on the same queue before any later wgpu use, so a consumer sees correct data without an explicit wait; importing the AHB gives Vulkan its own reference so the decoder buffer is released immediately). (2) Caps negotiation now matches the runtime: in GPU-output mode `MediaCodecDec` derives `Rgba8` output (`caps_constraint_as_transform`) and its source pad advertises both NV12 and RGBA; `WgpuPreprocess` accepts `Rgba8` input (`intercept_caps` + `caps_constraint_as_transform`), so a runner can auto-plug the GPU path. Validated on the Pixel 10a: the 9-frame decode->preprocess chain still produces a correct NCHW tensor through the ring, and the negotiation is asserted in the on-device test. NV12 surface-import unchanged (4 tests pass on the RTX 3060).
- M304 (decode -> preprocess on GPU): `WgpuPreprocess` now consumes the RGBA `MemoryDomain::WgpuTexture` that `MediaCodecDec` emits in GPU-output mode, closing the Android decode -> preprocess loop entirely on the GPU (no CPU round-trip of the frame). Adds a `TEX_SHADER_RGBA` compute path (samples an already-converted `Rgba8Unorm` `texture_2d<f32>` straight into the NCHW f32 tensor, no colour math, the RGBA analog of the NV12 surface-import shader) + `dispatch_tex_rgba` / `build_tex_rgba_gpu`; the `WgpuTexture` branch now tries the `WgpuNv12Texture` keep-alive first, then the RGBA `WgpuRgbaTexture` (M304), and `configure_pipeline` accepts `Rgba8` input. New g2g-ml `mediacodec-wgpu` feature (pulls `g2g-plugins/mediacodec-wgpu` for the keep-alive type, the Android analog of `cuda-wgpu`); the RGBA consume path is Android-gated since that is the only RGBA-GPU producer today. Validated on the Pixel 10a end to end: `MediaCodecDec(gpu_output)` -> 9 `WgpuTexture` frames -> `WgpuPreprocess` -> a 921600-float NCHW tensor (3x640x480), all in [0,1] with real variance, no CPU frame copy. The NV12 surface-import path is unchanged (its 4 tests still pass on the RTX 3060). Runner-level caps negotiation for the RGBA-GPU path (the element is driven directly today) is the remaining polish. CI cross-checks the feature.
- M304 (complete): `MediaCodecDec::with_gpu_output()` keeps decoded frames on the GPU end to end. The reusable `YcbcrToRgba` converter builds the ycbcr conversion / immutable sampler / compute pipeline once and, per frame, imports the decoded `AHardwareBuffer`, runs the convert pass into a fresh RGBA `wgpu::Texture` (self-allocated VkImage wrapped via `texture_from_raw` + `create_texture_from_hal`, the cudawgpu pattern), and releases the buffer back to the decoder (the conversion waits on its fence). The decoder emits these as `MemoryDomain::WgpuTexture` (RGBA caps) carried by a new public `WgpuRgbaTexture` keep-alive (the RGBA analog of g2g-ml's `WgpuNv12Texture`; a wgpu-linking consumer downcasts it to recover the texture + adopt the device), instead of the CPU NV12 pack. Submits raw Vulkan to the wgpu device's queue, so the element documents the single-thread-executor contract it already required. Validated on the Pixel 10a: 9 frames decode to `WgpuTexture`, recovered via the keep-alive and read back through wgpu (proving wgpu consumes the externally-written texture and its content survives adoption) with full per-channel range + opaque alpha, no CPU readback of the decoded YUV. Consuming the RGBA texture in `WgpuPreprocess` (it currently only imports NV12) is the follow-up, an ML-on-Android concern. CI cross-checks the feature.
- M304 (ycbcr conversion): the opaque AHardwareBuffer now converts to RGBA on the GPU. Because the decoded buffer is opaque (the probe below), the conversion can't go through wgpu (its bind-group API can't express the immutable `VkSamplerYcbcrConversion` an opaque buffer requires), so `ahb_to_rgba_readback` does it in raw Vulkan on the interop device: import the AHB as a sampled image, build a `VkSamplerYcbcrConversion` from the buffer's suggested model/range/components/offsets + an immutable sampler, sample it in a compute shader (`shaders/mediacodec_ycbcr.comp`, glslc -> SPIR-V, the conversion is implicit in the sampler so the shader just samples + writes RGBA), write a self-allocated `R8G8B8A8` storage image, and `vkCmdCopyImageToBuffer` for validation. No CPU/PCIe readback of the decoded YUV is involved (the readback is only the validation tap). Validated on the Pixel 10a: a real decoded frame converts to RGBA with full per-channel range (R/G/B means 123/128/130 over 0..255) and opaque alpha, in the same `android_mediacodec_wgpu_probe` test. Remaining for the element path: wrap the RGBA image as a `wgpu::Texture` (`MemoryDomain::WgpuTexture`) for `WgpuPreprocess` and reuse the pipeline objects per frame.
- M304 (first step): the Android MediaCodec -> wgpu/Vulkan zero-copy bridge module (`mediacodec_wgpu`, `mediacodec-wgpu` feature) plus the on-device linchpin probe. `create_android_interop_device` opens a Vulkan-backed wgpu device with `VK_ANDROID_external_memory_android_hardware_buffer` (+ `VK_EXT_queue_family_foreign`) via the wgpu-hal create-device callback (the cudawgpu pattern), and `ahb_format_info` runs `vkGetAndroidHardwareBufferPropertiesANDROID` on a real decoded buffer. `MediaCodecDec` gained a feature-gated hook that captures (acquires a ref on) the first decoded frame's `AHardwareBuffer` so the probe inspects an actual vendor buffer without re-driving decode (`captured_hardware_buffer`); needs the ndk `api-level-26` feature (the AHardwareBuffer NDK API). Probe verdict on the Pixel 10a: the buffer imports *opaque* (`VkFormat::UNDEFINED`, `externalFormat=0xee`, suggested YCbCr 601 / narrow), so there is no per-plane image access and the originally planned per-plane `vkCmdCopyImage` device-local copy is not viable; the path forward is a raw-Vulkan `VkSamplerYcbcrConversion` + immutable sampler (which wgpu's bind-group API cannot express) feeding a convert-to-RGBA pass output as `MemoryDomain::WgpuTexture`. The probe is an on-device integration test (`android_mediacodec_wgpu_probe`, built at cargo-ndk `--platform 26`); CI cross-checks the `mediacodec-wgpu` feature.
- M303: H.265 / HEVC in `MediaCodecDec`, validated on the Pixel 10a alongside H.264 (10 HEVC frames decoded to NV12). The element is now codec-parameterized: `MediaCodecDec::h265()` selects MIME `video/hevc`, and the codec-specific data differs by codec, so a new `codec_specific_data` packs VPS+SPS+PPS into a single `csd-0` for HEVC (H.264 keeps SPS=`csd-0`, PPS=`csd-1`). Adds `annexb::h265_parameter_sets` (H.265 NAL type is `(b >> 1) & 0x3F`; VPS=32/SPS=33/PPS=34), unit-tested on the host. Registered as `mediacodecdech265` (the H.264 factory stays `mediacodecdec`; one factory per codec, the gst `amcviddec-<component>` model). The on-device smoke test now covers both codecs (shared `decode_to_nv12` helper, codec-aware access-unit splitter). The ImageReader output path and binder-threadpool setup are unchanged (HEVC rides the same Surface plumbing).
- M302: `MediaCodecDec` now actually decodes on Android hardware (validated end to end on a Pixel 10a, the first on-device run of the Android track). The first hardware run exposed that the v1 ByteBuffer/no-Surface output design is unusable on modern devices: the vendor Codec2 decoder only delivers graphic (gralloc) buffers, so a no-Surface configure corrupts the buffer handoff and a binder call hangs ~23 s. Reworked the decoder's output half onto an `AImageReader`: configure MediaCodec to render into the reader's Surface, release each output buffer with `render=true`, then acquire the decoded `Image` and pack its `YUV_420_888` planes to NV12 (the per-plane row/pixel strides describe any vendor layout uniformly, so the old colour-format guessing is gone). Needs the frame geometry up front (the `ImageReader` and `configure()` both require it; it arrives via `configure_pipeline` as `h264parse` derives it from the SPS). Enables the ndk `api-level-24` feature for `AImageReader`. The `android_mediacodec_smoke` integration test (embeds a 640x480 H.264 clip, drives the decoder, asserts NV12 frames of the right geometry) plus `tools/android-mediacodec-smoke.sh` (cargo-ndk build at `--platform 24` + adb push/run) run it on a connected device; a bare native process must start a binder threadpool first (Codec2 allocates output buffers via a binder callback into the process), which the test does by dlsym'ing `ABinderProcess_startThreadPool` from the device's libbinder_ndk (the NDK link stub omits it). `MediaCodecDec` is also registered as `mediacodecdec` for on-device `g2g-launch`.
- M301: package a host's full element set into `g2g-launch` without hand-writing a 30-feature string. Cargo has no meson-style auto-detect (build scripts run after feature resolution, so they cannot toggle features or pull optional deps), so this is split in two: a `linux-full` cargo feature bundles every element that builds on a Linux desktop with the usual `-devel` packages present (the gst-plugins-good analog, "I have the deps, give me everything"; excludes the Windows/macOS/Android/wasm features, the proprietary NVIDIA codec stack, and the no_std `embassy*` backends); and `cargo xtask install-launch` is the auto-detect front-end, the meson "checking for X ... no" analog: it probes the host (`pkg-config`/device nodes/`nvidia-smi`), `cargo install`s `g2g-launch` with exactly the features that compile here, and reports every skipped element with the dev package it needs (e.g. `[ ] vpx (skipped: needs libvpx-devel + clang)`). `--enable`/`--disable f[,g]` override the detected set, `--bin N` targets another binary, `--dry-run` prints the plan without building. The installed binary's actual element set is then introspectable with `g2g-inspect`. Adds the OpenSSL/libvpx/PipeWire/clang probes the launch set needs (the existing `test --here` probe didn't gate on them); unit-tested (skipped-feature notes, `--enable`/`--disable` CSV parsing).
- M300: VP8/VP9 video in A/V `mp4mux` (`Mp4MuxN`), so VP9 muxes into ISO-BMFF alongside Opus/AAC (e.g. `vp9enc ! m.   opusenc ! m.   mp4mux name=m ! filesink`). The video track gets a `vp09` (or `vp08`) `VisualSampleEntry` + `vpcC` VPCodecConfigurationBox (the VP-in-ISOBMFF binding; 8-bit 4:2:0 unspecified-colour defaults, no bitstream parsing) instead of `avc1`/`avcC`; frames are stored verbatim (no AVCC reframing) with the sync-sample flag read from the VP frame header. The VP8/VP9 keyframe parsers moved to the shared `fmp4mux` (one copy, reused by `mkvmuxn`). H.264/H.265 + AAC unchanged. The `moov` sample entry is unit-tested (`vp09` + `vpcC`, no `avcC`) and integration-tested (`m300`, VP9 + AAC); ffprobe identifies the VP9 stream from the sample entry (a real `vp9enc` decode needs libvpx, absent in the sandbox).
- M299: runner-level PTS-ordered fan-in. A `MultiInputElement` can return `input_pts_ordered() == true` to be driven by the new `muxer_arm_pts` instead of the default arrival-order round-robin `muxer_arm`: the runner owns an `InputAggregator<Frame>` and delivers `process(pad, DataFrame(..))` in global presentation-timestamp order (the earliest released only once every still-open input has one queued), so a multi-camera grid / PTS-synchronized compositor gets time-aligned input without hand-rolling its own aggregator. Per-input `Eos` (flush + merged-EOS aggregation) and `CapsChanged` (MX-1/MX-2) are handled as before; only `DataFrame`s are reordered, and the default arrival-order path is unchanged (the element-level mergers `InterleaveMux`/`tsmuxn`/`mp4muxn` keep working as-is). Tested (`m299`) with a deliberately non-buffering pass-through muxer over two time-skewed sources: the sorted output proves the runner did the merge. Closes the DESIGN_TODO "runner-level timestamp-ordered fan-in" item.
- M298: Opus audio in A/V `mp4mux` (`Mp4MuxN`), so `videotestsrc ! videoconvert ! x264enc ! m.   audiotestsrc ! opusenc ! m.   mp4mux name=m ! filesink location=av.mp4` muxes Opus alongside H.264/H.265 in ISO-BMFF. The audio track gets an `Opus` sample entry with a `dOps` OpusSpecificBox (RFC 8316: big-endian config, channels + rate from the caps, an 80 ms pre-skip) instead of `mp4a`/`esds`; Opus packets are stored raw (no de-ADTS), and the sample duration defaults to a 20 ms Opus frame. AAC is unchanged. Verified end-to-end (H.264 + real `opusenc` -> ffmpeg decodes the 48 kHz stereo Opus track in the MP4); the `moov` sample entry is unit-tested (`Opus` + `dOps`, no `esds`).
- M297: VP8/VP9 video + Opus audio in A/V `matroskamux` (`MkvMuxN`), so `videotestsrc ! videoconvert ! vp9enc ! m.   audiotestsrc ! opusenc ! m.   matroskamux name=m ! filesink location=av.webm` muxes a WebM (both are WebM-subset codecs, so the DocType is `webm`). Extends the H.26x+AAC muxer: VP8/VP9 frames are stored verbatim (no AVCC reframing, no `CodecPrivate`) with the keyframe flag read from the codec frame header (VP8 frame-tag bit 0; the VP9 uncompressed-header frame_type, superframes aside); Opus packets are stored raw with a synthesised 19-byte `OpusHead` `CodecPrivate` (channels + rate from the caps, a conventional 80 ms pre-skip). The Opus path is verified end-to-end (H.264 + real `opusenc` -> ffmpeg decodes the 48 kHz stereo Opus track); VP8/VP9 are unit-tested by round-trip through `MatroskaDemuxer` (WebM DocType, raw frames, keyframe flag, codec IDs) since the sandbox lacks `libvpx`-dev for a real `vp9enc` run.
- M296: A/V `flvmux` (`FlvMuxN`), the last muxer that was single-track only, so every standard container (`mpegtsmux`/`mp4mux`/`matroskamux`/`flvmux`) now does A/V: `videotestsrc ! videoconvert ! x264enc ! m.   audiotestsrc ! avenc_aac ! m.   flvmux name=m ! filesink location=av.flv`. A multi-input muxer registered as the `flvmux` fan-in (the parser picks it for >1 input link, the single-track `FlvMux` for one), FLV's one-video + one-audio model (H.264 + AAC); a second pad of either kind is rejected. Unlike the single-track muxer (media frames only), it writes the decoder-config sequence-header tags a player needs: `FlvMuxer` gained an A/V path (`new_av`, `push_video`/`push_audio`) that emits the H.264 `avcC` record and AAC `AudioSpecificConfig` as FLV AVC/AAC sequence headers up front, captured in-band from the first AU (parameter sets from the first IDR, ASC from the first ADTS header), then interleaves video / audio media tags by PTS with the FLV keyframe flag set per frame. Samples are reframed to FLV's convention (video AVCC length-prefixed, audio de-ADTS'd). Verified end-to-end with ffprobe + a full ffmpeg decode (h264 320x240 + aac 48 kHz stereo); integration-tested (`m296`). std-gated like `mkvmuxn` (reuses the MP4 family's NAL / ADTS / avcC helpers); the single-track baseline `flvmux` is unchanged.
- M295: remove the `Mp4Sink` convenience element (no combined muxer+file-writer elements: muxing is a separate element feeding any sink, the gst model `mp4mux ! filesink`). g2g muxes *fragmented* MP4 (forward-only, no moov backpatching), so a dedicated seekable sink was never needed; `Mp4Sink` predated the M291 muxer/sink split and only duplicated `Mp4Mux`. Its module `mp4sink.rs` is renamed `fmp4mux.rs` and keeps just the pure `Fmp4Muxer` box writer + the NAL / `avcC` / `hvcC` helpers (reused by `mp4mux`/`mp4muxn`/`mkvmuxn`); the element, its file I/O, and the dead `fragments()` accessor are gone. The 6 tests that used `Mp4Sink` as an fMP4 fixture now generate the bytes through `Mp4Mux` (`m28`/`m31` still write a file for `Mp4Src` to read; `m156`/`m158`/`m160` capture the forwarded bytes directly); the standalone `m24_mp4sink` is dropped (its round-trip / `ftyp`+`moov` / fragment-per-AU coverage is `m291` + the `fmp4mux` unit tests, and its reject-caps check moved into `m291`).
- M294: A/V `matroskamux` (`MkvMuxN`), so a Matroska / WebM recording carries video and audio together: `videotestsrc ! videoconvert ! x264enc ! m.   audiotestsrc ! avenc_aac ! m.   matroskamux name=m ! filesink location=av.mkv`. A multi-input muxer (the A/V analog of the single-track `MkvMux`, registered as the `matroskamux` fan-in the way `mpegtsmux`/`mp4mux` are, so >1 input link picks it): H.264/H.265 video + AAC audio, access units interleaved by PTS via the M204 `InputAggregator` into shared-timeline Clusters. `MatroskaMuxer` gained a multi-track path (`new_multi`, `push_frame_on`): the Tracks element carries one TrackEntry per stream, each with its `CodecPrivate` (the avcC / hvcC record for H.26x, the AAC AudioSpecificConfig), built once each track's init arrives in-band from the first AU (video parameter sets ride the first IDR; the ASC is synthesised from the first ADTS header). Samples are reframed to what the Matroska codec mappings expect: video AVCC length-prefixed, audio de-ADTS'd. Verified end-to-end with ffprobe + a full ffmpeg decode (h264 320x240 + aac 48 kHz stereo, both tracks decode cleanly); integration-tested (`m294`). Reuses the MP4 family's NAL / ADTS / avcC helpers, so the fan-in is std-gated (the single-track baseline `matroskamux` is unchanged).
- M293: A/V `mp4mux` (`Mp4MuxN`), so a fragmented-MP4 recording carries video and audio together: `videotestsrc ! videoconvert ! x264enc ! mp4mux name=m   audiotestsrc ! avenc_aac ! m.   m. ! filesink location=av.mp4`. A multi-input muxer (the A/V analog of the single-track `Mp4Mux`, registered as the `mp4mux` fan-in muxer the way `mpegtsmux`/`tsmuxn` is, so >1 input link picks it): H.264/H.265 video + AAC audio, access units interleaved by PTS via the M204 `InputAggregator`. The `moov` carries one `trak` per stream and is built once each track's init data arrives in-band (video parameter sets ride the first IDR; the audio AudioSpecificConfig is synthesised from the first ADTS header, with the ADTS stripped from the `mdat` samples); then one `moof`+`mdat` per AU with a per-track `tfdt`. Shared box helpers extracted from `mp4sink`/`mp4audiosink`. Verified end-to-end with ffprobe + a full ffmpeg decode (h264 320x240 + aac 48 kHz stereo, both tracks decode); integration-tested (`m293`).
- M292: `avenc_aac` (`aacenc`) libavcodec AAC-LC audio encoder, the audio companion of the H.264 `ffmpegenc` and the Linux audio-encode path the A/V muxers needed (the existing `MfAacEncode` is Windows-only). Interleaved PCM in (`PcmS16Le`/`PcmF32Le`), ADTS-framed AAC out (`Caps::Audio{Aac}`, the elementary-stream convention `aacparse` and the muxers expect). Converts PCM to the encoder's planar-float format and buffers into 1024-sample AAC frames, flushing the tail at EOS; allocates the codec context with `Context::new_with_codec` (the M289 fix). Verified `audiotestsrc ! avenc_aac ! aacparse ! fakesink` and an ffprobe-valid `.aac` (48 kHz stereo). Also unlocks AAC audio for `mpegtsmux`/`matroskamux`/`flvmux`, which already accept it.
- M291: `mp4mux` element (gst `mp4mux`/`qtmux` analog), so `... ! x264enc ! mp4mux ! filesink location=out.mp4` works (gst has no `mp4sink`; muxing is a separate element feeding any sink). H.264/H.265 Annex-B in, an ISO-BMFF byte stream (`Caps::ByteStream{IsoBmff}`) forwarded downstream: `ftyp`+`moov` init segment then one `moof`+`mdat` fragment per access unit. Extracted the fragmented-MP4 box writer out of `Mp4Sink` into a shared pure `Fmp4Muxer`; `Mp4Sink` (writes to a file) and `Mp4Mux` (forwards downstream) now wrap the same writer, mirroring `MkvMux`/`MatroskaMuxer`. Registered `mp4mux` + the `qtmux` alias (std-gated, like its module). Round-trip tested (`m291`: mux through `Mp4Mux`, recover byte-exact AUs through `Fmp4Demux`); ffprobe confirms a real playable MP4.
- M290: make `videorate` caps-driven, the last rate/format-changing element that wasn't. The standard gst idiom `videorate ! video/x-raw,framerate=N` previously failed `CapsMismatch` because `videorate` ignored the downstream pin and forced its own 30 fps default; only the `framerate=` property worked. New `VideoRate::auto()` (now the registry default) takes the target framerate from the negotiated output caps via a `DerivedCoupled` constraint (format + geometry passthrough, framerate the retargeted field), matching M186/M187 `videoconvert`/`videoscale`/`audioresample`. `videorate framerate=N` still works (sets the property, disables auto); bare `videorate` passes the input rate through. Unit + smoke verified up/downsample.
- M289: fix `x264enc` (libx264 via `FfmpegH264Enc`) failing to open at runtime. The encoder context was allocated with `encoder::new()` (no codec), leaving the generic legacy `AVCodecContext` defaults (`qmin=2`, `qmax=31`, `max_qdiff=3`, `qcompress=0.5`, `me_range=0`) which are exactly libx264's "broken ffmpeg default settings" fingerprint, so it aborted the open (`Hardware(Other)`) despite the `preset` being passed. Now allocates with `Context::new_with_codec(codec)` so codec-appropriate defaults apply, matching the `ffmpeg` CLI. Verified `videotestsrc ! videoconvert ! x264enc ! fakesink` encodes end-to-end. Also gated the `gst_compat` `unknown_encoder_gets_a_suggestion` test to `not(feature = "ffmpeg")` (it asserts `x264enc` is unregistered, false under the feature).
- M288: fix the stacked auto-converter cascade bug. Two chained auto `videoconvert`s into a format pin (`videotestsrc ! videoconvert ! videoconvert ! NV12`) emitted the raw RGBA bytes mislabeled NV12. The transform arm calls `configure_pipeline(input)` then `process(CapsChanged(forward_caps))` with the element's pre-fixed *output*, but `videoconvert` / `videoscale` / `audioconvert` / `audioresample` re-read that arg as a new *input* (`accept_input`), clobbering their input to the output format so the next frame became an unconverted `X->X` passthrough. They now forward the arg downstream and record `last_caps` (matching the decoder elements), leaving the `configure_pipeline`-set input alone. Byte-compare regression test `m288_stacked_convert_bytes` (1 vs 2 converts must produce identical NV12). Contract documented in DESIGN.md §4.13.4.
- M287: end-of-run telemetry report. New `RunStats::report()` formats the run telemetry, frame counts + drop rate %, the aggregated declared latency window (`min .. max`, live/non-live, the per-element `latency()` fold the runner already computes), the elected clock, and the negotiated head allocation, into a readable block. `g2g-launch` prints it at end (replacing the terse one-liner) together with the measured wall-clock throughput (e.g. `0.03 s wall, 601.8 fps`). The latency is *declared*, not a measured runtime histogram; per-element / per-link p50/p99 + fill-level needs frame-level instrumentation in the runner and stays a follow-up. Unit-tested formatting (drop-rate computation, bounded vs unbounded latency window).
- M286: runner-loop throughput bench + a CI regression guard. New `runner` bench in `g2g-bench` (criterion `async_tokio` + tokio) times the bounded per-edge channel, the runner loop's inner transport (the full `run_graph` paces to PTS, so it is unsuitable for a microbench), sweeping link capacity 2 (live) vs 8 (throughput) to show the backpressure round-trip cost; ~350K frames/s at cap 2 here. New `.github/workflows/bench.yml` (separate from the lean main CI, so criterion never hits the check/test/clippy jobs; runs only when `g2g-core` / `g2g-plugins` / `g2g-bench` change or on dispatch) benches the PR head and its base, then `bench_compare.py` fails the job if any benchmark's mean regressed > 50% vs base, a deliberately loose threshold given shared-runner noise (catches a lost fast path / accidental O(n^2), not drift). Comparator unit-checked locally both ways.
- M285: per-edge memory domain in the DOT dump. New `AsyncElement::output_memory` / `SourceLoop::output_memory` (default `MemoryDomainKind::System`, mirrored on the dyn traits + `GraphNodeRef::output_memory`) declares the domain of the frames an element emits, the runtime peer of M276's auto-plug `ElementDesc::output_memory` (it is not part of `Caps`). `NvDec` overrides it to `Cuda` (it emits NV12 in VRAM). `negotiate_graph` now also returns the per-edge memory domain (the producing node's `output_memory`), and `g2g-launch --dot` passes it so a GPU / zero-copy link is drawn bold + labelled `memory:Cuda` while CPU links stay plain. Fan-in / fan-out nodes report `System` (per-edge propagation through them is deferred). Tested: `m282_dot_negotiated_caps` asserts a CPU pipeline's edges are all `System` and the dump carries no `memory:` marking.
- M284: criterion benchmarks for the hot paths, so the latency moat is regression-guarded. A standalone `g2g-bench` crate (excluded from the workspace, like `examples/g2g-size` and the bevy demo, because criterion pulls plotters / rayon that `--all-targets` would otherwise build on every CI job, `required-features` does not gate dev-deps there) holds two benches: `caps` (the negotiation hot path, the hardest code) times `Caps::intersect` / `CapsSet::intersect`+`fixate` / `solve_linear` / `solve_graph` on a decode chain; `convert` times the per-pixel `videoconvert::convert` (now `pub` so the bench reaches it) for RGBA<->NV12/I420 + NV12<->I420 at 1080p with a pixels/s throughput. New `cargo xtask bench` runs them by manifest path (criterion args pass through, e.g. `-- --save-baseline main`). Indicative on the dev host: caps intersect ~13 ns, `solve_graph` ~1.6 us, RGBA->NV12 ~4.1 ms/1080p-frame. CI stays lean (criterion is not in the workspace lock; verified `--workspace --all-targets` builds none of it).
- M283: `xtask ffi-probe <header> <struct> [--field f]...`, automating the hand-rolled-FFI ritual (the C probe + `repr(C)` size assert convention `cuda.rs` / `nvenc.rs` use). It generates a C program that includes the header(s) and prints `sizeof` of the struct plus `offsetof` of each requested field, compiles it (`cc`, or `$CC` / `--cc`, with repeatable `-I` include dirs), runs it, and emits the ready-to-paste `const _: () = assert!(core::mem::size_of::<Struct>() == N);`. This locks down a version-tagged SDK struct's layout before trusting it, and catches SDK drift (a changed size fails the build, not the GPU). Verified on this host against `ffnvcodec/nvEncodeAPI.h`: `NV_ENC_INITIALIZE_PARAMS` probes to 1800 bytes, matching the committed assert in `nvenc.rs`. The C-source generation and size parsing are unit-tested.
- M282: negotiated caps in the DOT dump, closing the M279 follow-up. New `negotiate_graph` runs startup caps negotiation only (Phase 1 source-caps probe + Phase 2 whole-graph solve) without running the pipeline, returning the `ValidatedGraph` plus the fixated `Caps` per edge (indexed by edge id, as `DotAnnotations::edge_caps` expects). The runner's Phase 2 is refactored onto two shared helpers it now also uses (`build_node_constraints`, `caps_label`), so there is one constraint-builder, not two. `g2g-launch --dot` negotiates first and renders the chosen caps on each edge (e.g. `video/x-raw,format=RGBA,width=320,height=240,framerate=30/1`); on a negotiation failure it warns and falls back to a topology-only dump (re-parsing, since negotiation consumed the graph). Note: `--dot` now probes source caps, so a source that connects on `intercept_caps` (a live ingress) does so for the dump too. Tested: `m282_dot_negotiated_caps` (caps land on both edges of a 3-element chain; a video->audio pin fails to negotiate rather than panicking).
- M281: `xtask` dev-command crate (`cargo xtask <cmd>` via a `.cargo/config.toml` alias), the third developer-tooling item, consolidating the build / test invocations that were shell-history tribal knowledge. Zero dependencies (it only orchestrates `cargo` + toolchain tools). Commands: `ci` runs locally what CI runs (workspace check / test / clippy, the Linux feature build of g2g-plugins + g2g-ml, the embassy no-alloc tests, and the wasm core check), `--locked` like CI, stopping at the first failure; `test --here` probes the host (NVIDIA via `nvidia-smi`, VAAPI / Opus / ALSA / Pulse / Wayland / ffmpeg via `pkg-config`, `/dev/video*` cameras, `/dev/dri` GPU nodes) and runs exactly the feature-gated tests it supports (`--dry-run` prints the detected plan only); `size` builds the `examples/g2g-size` Cortex-M harness and reports the gc-sectioned `.text` (locating `rust-lld` in the toolchain sysroot, 3280 bytes here); `wasm` builds the wasm32 targets (core `runtime`, plugins `web` / `web-codecs`). The cross builds prepend `~/.cargo/bin` to `PATH` so cargo uses the rustup toolchain, baking in the Fedora distro-`rustc` gotcha; `web-codecs` gets `--cfg=web_sys_unstable_apis`. Unit-tested capability-to-feature mapping; `size` / `wasm` / dry-run probe validated on the dev host.
- M280: caps-negotiation explainer, the second developer-tooling item. `solve_graph` now narrates the DAG negotiation under a reserved `caps` log category: a setup dump (each node's constraint, e.g. `VideoTestSrc produces video/x-raw,...` / `VideoConvert derives output (coupled)` / `FakeSink accepts ANY`) and, per edge, the surviving `CapsSet` and its fixated result (`VideoTestSrc -> VideoConvert: ... ✓ -> video/x-raw,format=RGBA,...`). On failure it narrates at ERROR: `no caps overlap between <A> and <B>` plus the set on every edge incident to the conflict (so a `CapsMismatch` reads as "these two can't agree, here's what each wanted"), and an unfixable edge logs `... ✗ cannot fixate`. New `solve_graph_labeled` lets the caller supply node labels; the runner passes each element's `log_category` so the narration reads in element names, while direct callers get an `n{id}:{kind}` default. Turned on by `G2G_CAPS_TRACE=1` (a boolean shortcut, or a level name / number for verbosity) or `G2G_DEBUG=caps:debug`; both install the stderr sink via `log::init_from_env`, which `g2g-launch` already calls. All trace formatting is skipped unless the category is enabled (one atomic load when off). Tested: solver unit tests (set / constraint formatting, labeled == default solution) and an `m280_caps_trace` integration test capturing the log to assert the success + failure narration.
- M279: pipeline -> Graphviz DOT visualizer (the `GST_DEBUG_DUMP_DOT_DIR` analog), the first developer-tooling item. New `g2g_core::dot` module adds `Graph::to_dot` / `ValidatedGraph::to_dot`: a `digraph { .. }` with role-coded nodes (green sources, red sinks, blue transforms, diamond tees / trapezium muxers), labelled by a caller-supplied closure (returning `None` falls back to the structural kind, so a tee reads as `tee`). Edges carry the negotiated caps and memory domain from a `DotAnnotations { edge_caps, edge_memory }` (both indexed by edge id, matching `solve_graph`'s `Vec<Caps>`), the non-default `LinkPolicy`, and fan-out / fan-in pad indices; a non-`System` (GPU / zero-copy) link is drawn bold. Self-contained `no_std + alloc` (only formats `String`s, no I/O), builds on `thumbv7em`. Wired into `g2g-launch --dot`: dumps the parsed pipeline to stdout (pipe to `dot -Tsvg`) labelled by each element's log category, without running it; supporting `GraphNodeRef::log_category` plus `Graph::{node_count,node_kind,element}` and `ValidatedGraph::edges` accessors. Tested: `g2g-core` unit tests (linear chain, structural fallback + pads, GPU-memory marking, escaping) and an end-to-end `m279_dot` launch-parser test (linear dump, tee branch pads + leaky-queue policy).
- M278: zero-copy GPU-render egress, the `examples/bevy-g2g-stream` rewire (closes the M271 follow-up). Bevy now renders on g2g's *interop* wgpu device (new `create_interop_device_full`, opened with the adapter's full features so a renderer is happy on it; handed to Bevy via `RenderCreation::Manual`), so a render-world system copies each rendered texture device->device through the `WgpuToCuda` bridge (M275) into a CUDA surface and encodes it with native `NvEnc` (M269/M271), emitting H.264 access units with **no GPU->CPU read-back**; the M267 version read the full RGBA frame back and encoded via ffmpeg. The encoded access units cross to a sink thread (`AppSrc(H.264) -> FileSink | WebRtcSink`) over a channel, so the WHIP egress is unchanged. Supporting changes: `WgpuToCuda::ingest_texture` made public (a host renders into the bridge directly), `InteropDevice.adapter`/`.instance` exposed (Bevy's `RenderResources` needs all four handles). Two NVIDIA-driver hazards handled: `synchronous_pipeline_compilation: true` (Bevy's async Vulkan pipeline compile faults when it overlaps the CUDA encode on the shared driver), and `std::process::exit` after flush (skip the render-world CUDA/wgpu teardown that races Bevy's device shutdown). Validated on the RTX 3060: a run produces a 640x480 H.264 stream that decodes back to the rendered scene (cube on a lit plane). The example is excluded from the workspace / CI as before.
- M277: NvEnc depth, two NVENC encoder improvements. (1) Output-bitstream pool: the output buffer is now created once at session open and reused every frame (NVENC runs sync-mode, one locked + copied output per encode), replacing the per-frame `nvEncCreateBitstreamBuffer` / `nvEncDestroyBitstreamBuffer`; it is destroyed before the encoder on session teardown. (2) Runtime bitrate retarget via `nvEncReconfigureEncoder`: `set_property("bitrate", ..)` (an adaptive sink, e.g. a WebRTC BWE drop) is applied to the live session before the next frame, with no session re-open and no forced IDR (`resetEncoder=0`), so the rate control retargets smoothly. The config / init building is factored into shared helpers so open and reconfigure stay in lock-step. New `NV_ENC_RECONFIGURE_PARAMS` FFI (size-asserted 1816 bytes against nvEncodeAPI.h 13.0; the reconfigure fn pointer is now typed); `nvenc_round_trips_a_cuda_nv12_surface` on the RTX 3060 now drops 4 Mbps -> 1 Mbps mid-stream and decodes the result back, and asserts the applied bitrate tracked the retarget. Remaining NvEnc depth (10-bit / P010, finite-GOP repeatSPSPPS, mid-stream resolution reconfigure) stays deferred; AV1 needs RTX 40-series.
- M276: domain-aware auto-plug. The memory domain a decoder produces (`NvDec` -> NV12 in `MemoryDomain::Cuda`) is not encoded in `Caps` and threading it through all 446 `Caps` sites would be wrong (it is orthogonal to the format algebra), so it rides as a *memory feature* on the auto-plug metadata: `ElementDesc::output_memory: MemoryDomainKind` (GStreamer's `memory:CUDAMemory` caps-feature analog), set per factory by `ElementFactory::produces(kind)` and defaulting to `System`. `find_chain_preferring(.., preferred)` and `Registry::{autoplug,autoplug_names,decodebin}_preferring(.., preferred)` bias ties toward a chain whose terminal element emits `preferred` (still breadth-first, so a shorter chain always wins; among equal-length chains the matching-memory candidate is tried first). The default `System` preference is exactly registration order, so a plain pipeline is unchanged and `NvDec` (registered last, now tagged `produces(Cuda)`) never hijacks a CPU path; a GPU consumer requests `Cuda` and gets `NvDec` ahead of the CPU decoder. New `nvdec`+`ffmpeg` test asserts default H.264 decode picks `ffmpegdec` while a `Cuda` preference picks `nvdec` (no GPU; metadata-only search). Deriving the preference from a downstream consumer's accepted memory is a follow-up. Architecture in DESIGN.md 4.13.9.
- M275: `WgpuToCuda` (M271) promoted to a pipeline `AsyncElement` plus a linear-buffer reuse pool. The bridge now implements `AsyncElement` (`Identity(RGBA)` caps, `MemoryDomain::WgpuTexture` in -> `MemoryDomain::Cuda` out): `process` extracts the upstream texture (via `gpu::texture_of`), copies it into the bridge's exportable render target on the interop device, drains, and emits a CUDA RGBA frame for `NvEnc`, no read-back. Unlike the lazy-device M220 `CudaToWgpu`, the element owns its interop device up front and exposes `device()` / `queue()` so the upstream renderer draws onto it (the `WgpuSink` app-wired pattern; a `wgpu::Texture` is device-bound and only this device's memory is CUDA-importable). `to_cuda_frame` now draws its linear output buffer from a `LinearBufferPool` free list (recycled by size when the emitted frame's keep-alive drops) instead of `cuMemAlloc`/`cuMemFree` per frame. The `gpu` module gate gains `cuda-wgpu` (it reuses `texture_of` / `WgpuTextureKeepAlive`). New on-hardware test `wgpu_to_cuda_element_bridges_and_recycles` drives 10 frames through the element into NVENC on the RTX 3060, each consumed + dropped before the next so the pool recycles.
- M274: registry wiring for the ffmpeg H.264 encoder (`FfmpegH264Enc`, M266), the encode-side gap surfaced during M272. Two launch names, `ffmpegenc` (default NVENC `h264_nvenc` backend) and `x264enc` (libx264 software backend), plus the gst `avenc_h264` alias resolving software-first (`x264enc` -> `ffmpegenc`). Launch-only: an encoder is never an auto-plug candidate. New `ffmpeg`-gated test asserts all three names resolve to constructible elements (no GPU; `new()` opens no libavcodec context).
- M273: HEVC (H.265) for the native `NvEnc` / `NvDec` (M269 / M270), the highest-value codec gap on Ampere/3060 (NVENC AV1 still needs RTX 40-series). The encode/decode paths are codec-agnostic bar the codec id, so the addition is small: `NvEnc` gains a `codec` field / `with_codec(VideoCodec)` builder / `codec` property (`h264` default | `hevc`), picking `NV_ENC_CODEC_HEVC_GUID` for the preset + initialize calls and announcing `CompressedVideo{H265}` out; its `DerivedOutput` and pad-template source now advertise both codecs, and configure rejects anything but H.264 / HEVC. `NvDec` infers the codec from its input caps (accepts `CompressedVideo{H264|H265}`), maps it to the `cudaVideoCodec` (H264=4, HEVC=8) stored on the decoder state, and creates the NVCUVID parser + decoder for it; the rest of the callback machinery is unchanged. New on-hardware test `nvenc_to_nvdec_hevc_round_trip_on_gpu` runs the full native HEVC loop on the RTX 3060 (CUDA NV12 -> `NvEnc(hevc)` -> HEVC Annex-B -> `NvDec` -> CUDA NV12, decoded luma verified), alongside the existing H.264 one; a no-GPU unit test checks the HEVC GUID / H.265 output-caps selection. 10-bit, mid-stream resolution reconfigure, and a finite-GOP `repeatSPSPPS` remain deferred.

- M272: registry / auto-plug wiring for the native `NvEnc` / `NvDec` (M269 / M270), so `gst-launch` / `gst-inspect` / `decodebin` see them. Both register as named launch elements (`nvenc`, `nvdec`) under their feature gates, with GStreamer-canonical aliases resolving to them (`nvh264enc` / `nvv4l2h264enc` -> `nvenc`, `nvh264dec` -> `nvdec`, the same first-registered rule as the VA-API names). `NvDec` is also an auto-plug `ElementFactory` candidate, but **registered last, after the CPU decoders, on purpose**: it emits NV12 in CUDA device memory (`MemoryDomain::Cuda`), which caps do not encode, so a generic `decodebin` to a system-memory sink must still pick a CPU decoder; ranking is by registration order (breadth-first finds the earliest-registered among equal-length chains), so registering `NvDec` last keeps it available to an explicit chain without hijacking CPU pipelines. Selecting the native decoder is therefore explicit (the `nvdec` / `nvh264dec` name) until a caps memory-feature gates auto-plug by domain (the follow-up). New test (`nvenc nvdec` features) asserts the names and aliases resolve to constructible elements and that `nvdec` is an auto-plug factory; it needs no GPU (`new()` opens nothing, the session / context are lazy at configure). Noted gap surfaced while here: `FfmpegH264Enc` (M266) is still unregistered; folding it in (`ffmpegenc` + `x264enc` / `avenc_h264` aliases) is a small separate follow-up.

- M271: `WgpuToCuda`, the wgpu -> CUDA bridge (feature `cuda-wgpu`), plus RGBA input for `NvEnc` (feature `nvenc`): the zero-copy encode path for a GPU render, the reverse of M220's `CudaToWgpu` and the moat the M267 Bevy demo pays for today (it reads the rendered texture back to system memory and encodes with the ffmpeg NVENC backend). A renderer writes a packed-RGBA `wgpu::Texture` backed by FD-exportable Vulkan memory (`export_rgba_image` / `wrap_rgba_as_texture`, the `R8G8B8A8` mirror of the NV12 export); CUDA imports the same memory as a 4-channel array (`import_rgba_into_cuda`) and `WgpuToCuda::to_cuda_frame` copies it device->device into a fresh linear `CUdeviceptr`, handed downstream as a `MemoryDomain::Cuda` `Rgba8` frame, so the pixels reach the encoder with **no PCIe download**. The bridge retains its own CUDA primary context (the GPU the interop device also selects, released last on drop after the import and the Vulkan image) and owns the exportable render-target texture (`texture()`); each output frame's keep-alive frees its linear buffer on release. `NvEnc` gains RGBA/BGRA input alongside NV12: it negotiates `RawVideo{Rgba8|Bgra8}` (NVENC color converts internally, so still H.264 out) and registers the single packed plane as `ABGR` (wgpu `Rgba8` byte order) / `ARGB`. New on-hardware test on the RTX 3060 (`wgpu_to_cuda`, features `cuda-wgpu nvenc`) writes a moving RGBA pattern into the bridge texture and encodes 10 frames through `NvEnc` to valid Annex-B H.264 with no read-back; it skips with no Vulkan interop device / NVIDIA GPU. Deferred: rewiring the `examples/bevy-g2g-stream` demo to render on the interop device (`RenderCreation::Manual`) into the bridge texture (the demo-side plumbing; the standalone test is the validation of record), and registering the bridge as a pipeline element with `MemoryDomain::WgpuTexture` input + a reuse pool (one linear buffer is alloc/freed per frame today).

- M270: `NvDec`, a native NVDEC H.264 decode element (feature `nvdec`, `cfg(linux)`): the decode half of the gst-`nvcodec`-style pair and the mirror of M269's `NvEnc`. It promotes NVIDIA hardware decode from a `FfmpegVideoDec` backend flag (`Backend::NvdecCuda`, which reaches NVDEC *through* libavcodec's cuvid hwaccel) to a first-class element driving the NVIDIA Video Codec SDK's NVCUVID parser+decoder API directly, so the decode path no longer needs libavcodec. With `NvDec -> ... -> NvEnc` both native, the whole H.264 transcode loop stays on the GPU and out of libav. `Caps::CompressedVideo{H264}` (Annex-B) in, `Caps::RawVideo{Nv12}` out in CUDA device memory (`MemoryDomain::Cuda`), the zero-copy hwframe domain `CudaToWgpu` / `CudaGlSink` / `NvEnc` consume with no PCIe download. NVCUVID is callback-driven: a parser (`cuvidCreateVideoParser`) is fed the elementary stream and synchronously invokes a sequence callback (creates the decoder once the SPS geometry is known), a decode callback (`cuvidDecodePicture`), and a display callback (a frame is ready in display order). Because the display callback cannot `await`, it maps the surface (`cuvidMapVideoFrame64`) and pushes a ready frame onto a queue that `process` drains and emits after the parse call returns; the callbacks reach element state through a `*mut DecoderState` passed as the parser's user-data, a pointer that targets a heap `Box` so it stays valid as the runner moves the element between worker threads. Bindings are hand-rolled FFI linking `libnvcuvid` + `libcuda` directly (no `cudarc`, like `nvenc` / the `cuda` module); NVCUVID exports real symbols (no `CreateInstance` table), so the calls are plain `extern "C"`, and the structs are transcribed `#[repr(C)]` with **compile-time size assertions** checked against the installed `cuviddec.h` / `nvcuvid.h` (field offsets verified with `offsetof`), with the per-picture `CUVIDPICPARAMS` left opaque (the parser fills it; we pass the pointer straight to the decoder). Each output frame carries a `CudaKeepAlive` that `cuvidUnmapVideoFrame64`s on drop plus an `Arc` to the decoder, so the decoder / context outlive any frame still in flight (the decoder, its context lock, and the CUDA context are torn down, in that order, only once the last frame is released); the element owns its own CUDA context. The NV12 nanosecond PTS round-trips through the packet/display timestamp; the runtime `CapsChanged` carries the actual cropped display geometry. New on-hardware test on the RTX 3060 runs the **full native loop**: a synthesized CUDA NV12 surface is encoded by `NvEnc` to Annex-B, then decoded by `NvDec` back to CUDA NV12, asserting frame count, the announced NV12 geometry, and (via a small device->host copy) that the decoded luma holds real, non-uniform content; it skips cleanly with no NVIDIA GPU. Pure-logic tests (caps H264->NV12, decoded-vs-negotiated output dims) cover negotiation without a GPU. Like `nvenc` / `ffmpeg` / `cuda`, the `nvdec` feature is CI-excluded. Deferred: mid-stream resolution change (decoder reconfigure), HEVC / other codecs, 10-bit output, and a configurable display-delay (fixed at a low-latency 1 today). This completes the native gst-`nvcodec`-style decode/encode pair.

- M269: `NvEnc`, a native NVENC H.264 encode element (feature `nvenc`, `cfg(linux)`): the zero-copy, device-resident counterpart of `FfmpegH264Enc` and the moat follow-up to M267 (which captured Bevy's render via `from_wgpu` and encoded with `FfmpegH264Enc(NVENC)` *after* a device->host read-back). Where the ffmpeg encoder takes system-memory I420 and copies it into libavcodec, `NvEnc` ingests an NVDEC/CUDA NV12 surface (`MemoryDomain::Cuda`) **in place** and drives the NVIDIA Video Codec SDK (`nvEncodeAPI`) directly, so the pixels never leave the GPU, closing the native `NvdecCuda -> NvEnc` loop with no PCIe download (the encode-side mirror of the M220 `CudaToWgpu` import bridge). `Caps::RawVideo{Nv12}` in, `Caps::CompressedVideo{H264}` Annex-B out; caps do not encode the memory domain, so negotiation matches a system encoder and the frame must be `MemoryDomain::Cuda` at runtime (an `UnsupportedDomain` error otherwise, the symmetric contract `FfmpegH264Enc` upholds for `System`). Bindings are hand-rolled FFI linking `libnvidia-encode` + `libcuda` directly (no `cudarc`, matching the `cuda` module decision): the SDK's giant version-tagged structs are transcribed `#[repr(C)]` with **compile-time size assertions** checked against the installed `nvEncodeAPI.h` (SDK 13.0, verified field offsets via `offsetof`), and the one field-heavy codec-config union is left opaque (the driver fills it via `nvEncGetEncodePresetConfigEx`; we only tweak rate control / GOP). The session opens lazily on the first frame, on that frame's `CUcontext`, so it runs in the NVDEC source's context; per frame it registers the NV12 device pointer (`CUDADEVICEPTR`), maps it, encodes, locks the bitstream out, and releases. Low latency like `FfmpegH264Enc`: preset P4 + the LOW_LATENCY tuning info, CBR, no B-frames (`frameIntervalP=1`), and an *infinite GOP* so IDRs are emitted only on demand (the first frame + a downstream PLI via `Reconfigure::ForceKeyframe`), each forced IDR carrying in-band SPS/PPS (`OUTPUT_SPSPPS`); the NV12 nanosecond PTS round-trips through NVENC's `inputTimeStamp`. New on-hardware round-trip test on the RTX 3060 synthesizes a CUDA-resident NV12 surface (CUDA driver alloc + upload), encodes it through `NvEnc`, and decodes the Annex-B back through `FfmpegVideoDec` to 320x240 I420; it skips cleanly with no NVIDIA GPU / SDK. Pure-logic tests (caps NV12->H264, non-NV12 / System-domain rejection, the `NVENCAPI_STRUCT_VERSION` macro vs the probed `*_VER` values, the H.264 codec GUID bytes) cover the negotiation and FFI constants without a GPU. Like `ffmpeg`/`cuda`, the `nvenc` feature is CI-excluded (no NVENC runtime in CI). Deferred: system-memory NV12 input (host upload; I420 is already `FfmpegH264Enc`'s job), HEVC via the HEVC GUID, finite-GOP periodic IDRs with `repeatSPSPPS`, an output-bitstream-buffer pool (one is allocated/freed per frame today), and runtime bitrate retarget via `nvEncReconfigureEncoder`. A matching native `NvDec` (promoting NVDEC from the `FfmpegVideoDec` backend flag) remains the other half of the gst-`nvcodec`-style pair.

- M267: `examples/bevy-g2g-stream`, a Bevy + g2g server-side render-and-stream demo (standalone crate, excluded from the workspace so the heavy `bevy` dep stays out of CI; its own `Cargo.lock` pins Bevy 0.19 + wgpu 29.0.3, the exact wgpu g2g uses, so a `wgpu::Texture` crosses between them). The adoption artifact for the bring-your-own-device path (`GpuContext::from_wgpu`, M263), in the consuming direction: Bevy renders a 3D scene **headless** (no window, `ScheduleRunnerPlugin`, `WinitPlugin` disabled) to an offscreen texture on its GPU; g2g joins Bevy's wgpu device via `from_wgpu` (cloning Bevy's `RenderDevice`/`Queue`/`Adapter`/`Instance`) and a render-world system reads the rendered texture back off the *shared* device each frame; the frames feed `AppSrc -> VideoConvert(RGBA->I420) -> FfmpegH264Enc(NVENC) -> sink` on a tokio runtime. Sink is `FileSink` (writes `bevy_g2g.h264`, the self-contained default) or, when `G2G_WHIP_URL` is set, `WebRtcSink` (live WHIP/WebRTC publish to a browser; `G2G_FRAMES=0` streams forever). Validated on the RTX 3060: the headless render + `from_wgpu` read-back captures non-blank frames off the shared device, and the file path produces a valid `h264` 640x480 stream (`ffprobe`-confirmed); the WHIP routing + graceful no-server failure are verified, with the live browser publish human-validated. The fully zero-copy path (wgpu texture -> CUDA -> NVENC, no read-back) is the native-NVENC follow-up.

- M268: restore the Cortex-M (`thumbv7em-none-eabihf`) build of `g2g-core` and add a footprint-measurement harness. `clock.rs` imported `core::sync::atomic::AtomicU64` for the `SharedClock` counter, which does not exist on targets without native 64-bit atomics (Cortex-M, RISC-V32), so the standalone core crate no longer compiled for an MCU target; switched to `portable_atomic::AtomicU64` (the same dependency the metrics histogram already uses; native where available, lock/critical-section fallback elsewhere). New `examples/g2g-size` (excluded from the workspace): a `no_std` staticlib exercising a representative embedded slice (caps `intersect`, a `Frame`, the no-alloc `StaticLendRing` DMA ring, a runtime bounded channel), built `opt-level="z"` + LTO + `panic="abort"` and linked with `--gc-sections`. Measured `.text` for that slice is ~3.2 KB on Cortex-M, so the core's per-pipeline code cost is low-single-digit KB (a complete minimal app adds the executor + allocator + element code on top). Known remaining no_std-baseline gap (not this fix): `log.rs` uses `spin::Mutex`, only a dependency under the `runtime` feature, so a no-`runtime` baseline build still fails there; the realistic embedded config enables `runtime`.

- M266: `FfmpegH264Enc`, a Linux H.264 *encoder* element (feature `ffmpeg`, `cfg(linux)`), the encode-side mirror of `FfmpegVideoDec`. The Linux production path had no H.264 encoder (the existing encoders are AV1 via rav1e, VP8/9 via libvpx, MJPEG), so the H.264-only egress sinks (`WebRtcSink`, `RtpH264Packetizer`, the RTSP server) could not be fed on Linux; this closes that gap. `Caps::RawVideo{I420}` in, `Caps::CompressedVideo{H264}` Annex-B out via `ffmpeg-next`, with two backends: `Nvenc` (default, `h264_nvenc`, hardware/realtime, the server-side render-and-stream path) and `Software` (`libx264`, portable CPU fallback). Tuned for low latency: `max_b_frames=0` (presentation-order output, no reorder hold), in-band SPS/PPS (no `GLOBAL_HEADER`, so parameter sets ride each IDR), per-backend low-latency preset/tune, and a downstream PLI (`Reconfigure::ForceKeyframe`) forces an IDR via `pict_type`. Input nanosecond PTS round-trips through the encoder's frame-index PTS. New round-trip test on the RTX 3060 encodes I420 through `Nvenc` (and `Software`) and decodes the result back through `FfmpegVideoDec`, asserting Annex-B framing and decode to I420 at the original geometry; both backends skip cleanly when their encoder is absent. Reuses the `encoder_base::emit_packets` batch loop (now also gated on `ffmpeg`). Like the decoder, the `ffmpeg` feature is CI-excluded, so this is validated on libav hosts. Deferred: runtime bitrate retarget, NV12 input, 10-bit, and a native NVENC element (Video Codec SDK) for zero-copy CUDA/wgpu-resident encode.

- M265: GPU layer zoo, so a small CNN body runs entirely on-device, not just a single conv. `WgpuInference` could do `linear` (M216) and `conv2d` (M261), but a CNN also needs a nonlinearity and a downsampler, and they had to run without leaving the GPU between layers. Adds four ops as additional WGSL compute passes behind the same device-adopt / dispatch / read-back machinery: the elementwise activations `relu` / `sigmoid` (`ACT_SHADER`) and the spatial pools `maxpool2d` / `avgpool2d` (`POOL_SHADER`, `kh x kw` window, stride `(sh, sw)`, no padding, output `[1, C, OH, OW]`). These are *weightless* ops, so the `Gpu` weight / bias buffers become `Option` and the bind group is op-aware: weighted ops (linear, conv2d) bind 5 entries (meta, input, weights, bias, out), weightless ops bind 3 (meta, input, out), the layout following the active shader (auto-derived from the pipeline). New host references `relu_reference` / `sigmoid_reference` / `maxpool2d_reference` / `avgpool2d_reference`. New `conv_relu_pool_chain_runs_on_gpu_and_matches_cpu_reference` test on the RTX 3060 chains `NV12 -> preprocess -> conv2d -> relu -> maxpool` with every intermediate kept GPU-resident (`with_gpu_output`, asserted `MemoryDomain::WgpuBuffer`) until the final pool reads back, and matches a CPU reference folding the same ops over the exact preprocess tensor (weights tuned so the conv produces negatives, so the relu provably clamps); plus standalone `avgpool2d` and `sigmoid` GPU tests (covering the avg / sigmoid shader branches the chain doesn't) and a `pool_validates_window_and_dims` unit test (window > input, zero stride / channels fail loud). Remaining toward a full trained model: batch-norm / attention ops and a multi-layer topology imported from one weight file.

- M264: a pipeline runs as independently *spawned* tasks on a real `embassy-executor`, not just the single `block_on`-joined future of M43/M45/M260. The embedded story had executor-agnostic runner futures driven by `embassy-futures::block_on` (one task), but never the multi-task model an RTOS app actually uses, where each element is its own scheduled task and the executor interleaves them. New `SharedPacketChannel` alias (`PacketChannel<CriticalSectionRawMutex, N>`): unlike `SinglePacketChannel`'s `NoopRawMutex` it is `Sync`, so the inter-task link can live in a `static` that spawned tasks (whose arguments must be `'static`) reach by reference. New `m264_embassy_multitask` test wires a three-stage `VideoTestSrc -> IdentityTransform -> consumer` pipeline as three `#[embassy_executor::task]`s over two static `SharedPacketChannel`s and runs it on a real `Executor` (the `platform-std` backend) via `run_until` (polls, then returns once the consumer raises a `DONE` flag, the host-testable counterpart of the diverging `run()` an embedded `fn main() -> !` calls), with the link depth below the frame count so the source blocks on backpressure and the scheduler must interleave the tasks; asserts all frames cross both static links. No HAL time driver needed (no element uses `embassy-time`), so it runs in CI under the existing embedded step. `embassy-executor` (platform-std) added as a dev-dep.

- M263: bring-your-own-device GPU output, the integration keystone for the game-engine / lightweight-app (Tauri, Bevy) use case where the application owns rendering and wants g2g to hand it textures, not present them. `GpuContext::from_wgpu(instance, adapter, device, queue)` wraps an embedder's *existing* wgpu device instead of opening one (the inverse of `for_surface`), so every GPU element produces textures on the embedder's device and a decoded frame's `MemoryDomain::WgpuTexture` is bindable directly in the embedder's render graph (recover it with `gpu::texture_of`) with no second device, no surface hand-off, no copy. New `gpu` unit test on the RTX 3060: a texture produced through a `from_wgpu` context reads back correctly on the embedder's *own* device handles (had g2g opened its own device, the texture would be bound elsewhere and the read-back would be a validation error). The frame still reaches the app through any sink, including the `appsink` pull channel, which carries a GPU-domain `Frame` unchanged (M233).

- M262: import trained weights at runtime via a dependency-free `safetensors` reader. The workspace has no `serde`, so rather than pull `serde` + the `safetensors` crate, `g2g-ml::safetensors` is a focused reader/writer for the format (a `u64` LE header length, a JSON-subset header `{name: {dtype, shape, data_offsets}}` parsed by a small recursive-descent reader, then raw tensor bytes), validating header length, offsets, and dtype, with `TensorRef::to_f32` decoding F32 tensors and a matching `serialize` (F32) for export / fixtures. `WgpuInference::conv2d_from_safetensors(st, weight_key, bias_key, h, w)` reads the `[Cout, Cin, KH, KW]` weight and `[Cout]` bias, infers the kernel dims, and builds the GPU conv layer (M261), so picking a different trained checkpoint is "parse a different file" while the architecture stays this compiled element (truly dynamic graphs are the `ort` backend; `burn-import` is the Burn topology path). New `conv2d_imports_safetensors_weights_and_runs_on_gpu` test serializes weights, parses them back, builds the conv, runs it on the RTX 3060, and matches the CPU reference over the round-tripped weights; 5 parser unit tests (round-trip, `__metadata__` + whitespace, truncation, out-of-range offsets, wrong-dtype). Also hardened the wgpu test suite with a shared GPU lock (`gpu_guard`): creating several wgpu devices on one adapter in parallel could fault the driver (a SIGSEGV once the suite grew), so each GPU test serializes its device work (CI has no adapter and skips them).

- M261: `WgpuInference` gains a GPU-resident 2D convolution, the keystone op for running an actual CNN layer on the device (it could previously only do the `input . W + b` matmul). The element is parameterized over an op (`linear` | `conv2d`); both share the device-adopt / dispatch / read-back machinery and the bind-group layout (uniform meta + 4 storage buffers), differing only in WGSL shader, the meta uniform, and the I/O tensor shapes, so the conv was additive. `conv2d(cin, cout, kh, kw, h, w, weights, bias)` runs a same-padding stride-1 convolution (`CONV_SHADER`, one invocation per output element accumulating over the `Cin*KH*KW` receptive field) over the `[1, Cin, H, W]` NCHW tensor `WgpuPreprocess` emits, with `[Cout, Cin, KH, KW]` weights, leaving a `[1, Cout, H, W]` feature map on the device (read back to System, or GPU-resident via `with_gpu_output`). New `conv2d_reference` host implementation; new `conv2d_on_gpu_resident_tensor_matches_cpu_reference` test chains NV12 -> preprocess -> conv2d on the RTX 3060 and matches the CPU reference over the exact preprocess tensor (the existing linear tests are unchanged, so the refactor is behaviour-preserving). The remaining gap toward a full vision model is imported trained weights (`burn-import` / ONNX) and the other ops (activation, pooling, attention), not the conv primitive.

- M260: `StaticLendRing`, a no-alloc zero-copy DMA capture ring, and an end-to-end heap-free capture path. The strict-`no_std` story had `StaticBufferPool` (move-out, RAII return) and the embassy stack channel (M45), but nothing proved a frame could be *captured and consumed* without the heap. `StaticLendRing::<N, BYTES>` (pure `core`) holds `N` inline slots; the producer fills the next free slot and `publish`es it as a `SystemSlice` that borrows the slot, and a per-slot lease (`AtomicBool`, plain load/store, no CAS, so it builds on `thumbv6m`) is cleared when the lent frame drops, so a slot is reused only after the consumer is done (genuine ring back-pressure: the producer stalls when all slots are in flight). The borrow is runtime-guarded, not a Rust lifetime: `OutputSink::push` and the stack channel take `PipelinePacket` by value (`'static`), so the lend reuses the existing `'static` foreign-buffer carrier (`SystemSlice::from_foreign`) with the lease standing in for the borrow, keeping `Frame` / `MemoryDomain` lifetime-free (no element-signature churn) and requiring zero core-type changes. Unit tests cover lease/recycle and a zero-copy witness (`ring.contains(ptr)`); new `m260_dma_ring` integration test drives a DMA-ring capture `SourceLoop` -> embassy stack channel -> consumer under `block_on`, asserting all frames cross zero-copy (bytes alias the ring), 10 frames recycle <= 4 physical buffers (no per-frame allocation), and every slot is reclaimed after drain. A real capture wires a DMA-completion ISR / vendor HAL into the same ring (hardware-gated).

- M259: forward Caps-β through a `DerivedOutput`, plus an M257 soundness fix that was failing CI on all three platforms. (1) The mid-stream snapshot froze a `DerivedOutput`'s *non-passthrough* (re-derived) fields to the startup input sample (M258 reused the full-chain coupling primitive `couple_passthrough_derived`). A transform stacked below another format-changing transform then had its upstream snapshot pinned to the startup geometry, so when it re-derived a new geometry mid-stream the upstream's frozen snapshot rejected it (`EmptyLink`) and the change was dropped. New `caps::project_passthrough_derived` *widens* every non-passthrough geometry / rate field to `Any` (same-variant defers to `project_passthrough`; the cross-variant decoder / encoder case keeps the sample's variant + scalar id, takes passthrough geometry from the downstream pin, widens the rest), and `backward_feasible`'s `DerivedOutput` arm uses it. A `DerivedOutput` below another format-changing transform now re-derives its output on a mid-stream input change and the runner cascades it downstream. New driver `m259_derived_recascade` (source -> Rgba8->I420 converter -> I420 geometry-halving scaler -> I420-any sink, geometry flips 640x480 -> 1280x720 mid-stream; the sink applies the re-derived I420 640x360). (2) `discover_passthrough` was unsound on a *multi-valued* closure: a converter offering `{passthrough, retargeted-NV12}` for an RGBA input is single-valued only at the format-probe values (Nv12 / I420), so probing mis-read `format` as passthrough; at startup `backward_field_narrow` then coupled the RGBA input against the NV12 pin, conflicted, dropped the sole input alternative, and the whole graph failed to negotiate (`midstream_change_with_no_acceptable_output_fails_loud_to_bus` regressed at M257). Discovery now bails to `NONE` unless the closure is single-valued on the sample's representative input (a genuinely ambiguous transform has no well-defined per-field passthrough); single-valued decoders / scalers are unchanged. New `discover_passthrough_none_for_multivalued_closure` unit test.
- M258: mid-stream backward coupling through a `DerivedOutput` (the snapshot half of M257). The per-edge downstream-feasibility snapshot (`graph_downstream_feasibility` / `backward_feasible`), computed once at startup so a mid-stream `CapsChanged` can steer an element's output without reaching its peers, used to return `None` on the input edge of a plain `DerivedOutput`: a decoder had no input to probe there, so a decoder sitting below a geometry / framerate pin exposed an unconstrained input edge and the mid-stream re-solve could not couple the pin back toward the source. The snapshot is now threaded the element's startup-fixated input caps (the solved per-edge `Caps` already in hand at the call site); for a `DerivedOutput` whose discovered passthrough mask is non-empty, the input-edge feasibility is the downstream feasible set's passthrough fields coupled onto that sample via `couple_passthrough_derived` (the same variant-crossing primitive the full-chain solve uses), else `None` (an empty mask or a missing sample, the prior behavior). `solve_graph` returns fixed `Caps` per edge, so the probe sample is exact. New `graph_feasibility_couples_pin_back_through_a_decoder` test: src(H264, open geometry) -> decoder(`DerivedOutput`, geometry passthrough) -> sink pinned Nv12 1280x720, asserting the decoder input edge now carries the coupled 1280x720 and rejects an off-geometry frame (was `None`). The remaining Caps-β gap is a `DerivedOutput` *downstream* re-deriving on a mid-stream input change.
- M257: backward caps coupling through a `DerivedOutput` (decoder / rescaler). A plain `DerivedOutput` declares no passthrough mask, so the solver could only invert it by dropping whole input alternatives, never narrowing a ranged field within the single input a decoder has, so a downstream geometry / framerate pin behind a decoder failed loud at startup (the input link could not fixate). New `caps::discover_passthrough` probes the closure with two distinct concrete inputs per field and marks a field passthrough only when the single output tracks it in both (conservative: a fixed/retargeted field, a rejected probe, or an ambiguous output yields non-passthrough, so a genuinely non-invertible closure is untouched). The new `solver::derived_backward` uses the discovered mask to narrow the input field-by-field via the existing `backward_field_narrow`, falling back to the alternative-drop walk when nothing is invertible. `caps::couple_passthrough_derived` extends the field coupling across the variant change a decoder/encoder makes (`CompressedVideo <-> RawVideo`), coupling the geometry / framerate both carry (`format` is a codec boundary, never passthrough there); same-variant transforms defer to the exact `couple_passthrough`, so `DerivedCoupled` behaviour is unchanged. Wired into both full-chain solve paths (linear `apply_constraint` + graph `apply_node_constraint`). Tests: `discover_passthrough` unit tests (decoder geometry+rate, fixed-output → none, identity → all fields, scaler → geometry retargeted) + solver tests (a downstream 1280x720 pin couples back through a geometry-passthrough decoder to fixate the H264 input; a fixed-output decoder imposes no spurious narrowing). The mid-stream `backward_feasible` snapshot still imposes none for `DerivedOutput` (no input to probe there), tied to the Caps-β re-solve item.
- M256: `PoolStage`, a real resizable-pool consumer of the mid-stream β allocation re-cascade. The N-hop β re-cascade (M18) already delivered a re-derived `AllocationParams` to an interior element's `configure_allocation` on a mid-stream caps change, but the elements that received it only recorded it (test probes) or had pools fixed at codec open (decoders). `PoolStage` is a passthrough transform that actually reacts: each `configure_allocation` rebuilds a live `BufferPool` to the proposal (`min_buffers` x `size_bytes`, same-shape proposals ignored to avoid churn), and every System frame is staged through a pooled buffer. New `poolstage_recascade` test drives the β path through it (source emits a mid-stream `CapsChanged`, geometry-sized sink re-proposes) and asserts the live pool resized: built at 640x480 startup, rebuilt to 1920x1080 on the β re-cascade (reconfigures == 2), all frames staged. Closes the "real consumer that re-sizes its pool" gap.
- M255: `CudaKmsSink`, the CUDA-GL display sink on DRM/KMS (the tty / no-compositor counterpart of `CudaGlSink`). Same CUDA-GL interop + NV12->RGB shader, but EGL renders into a GBM surface scanned out via DRM page-flips instead of a Wayland surface, for an embedded / headless box with no compositor. Behind a new `cuda-kms` feature (gbm with `default-features = false` so it stays on our drm 0.15, not gbm's drm-support 0.12; the DRM framebuffer is built from the bo's gem handle via a manual single-plane `Buffer`). Refactor: the shared NV12 GL render state (program + textures + per-frame CUDA upload + draw) moved to a new `glnv12` module used by both sinks, leaving each only its platform present (Wayland `eglSwapBuffers` vs GBM lock + page-flip); `CudaGlSink` re-validated unchanged on the RTX 3060 after the extraction (60 frames, p50 8.4 ms). The DRM discovery + flip-event draining mirror `KmsSink`. Authored + compiles + lints clean; the on-tty run is owed (KMS needs DRM master, which the dev session's compositor holds) so the GBM/EGL/DRM present spots are flagged `// VERIFY:`. New ignored `cudakms_smoke` test carries the on-tty recipe.
- M254: `CudaToWgpu` shared-image reuse pool. The bridge allocated a fresh exportable Vulkan image + CUDA import + `wgpu::Texture` every frame (M220 v1); now `CudaWgpuPool` (g2g-plugins `cudawgpu`) recycles them. New primitives split the per-frame work from the one-time setup: `import_image_into_cuda` does `cuImportExternalMemory` + map once (handles stored as integers so the mapping is `Send`, like `OwnedCudaBuffer`), and `cuda_copy_planes_into` is the per-frame device->device copy + sync (vs `cuda_copy_nv12_planes` which imported and tore down each call). The pool is a free list of `PoolEntry { mapping, texture }`; `CudaToWgpu` pops one (or builds a fresh one), copies this frame's planes into its persistent CUDA array, and emits a `WgpuNv12Texture` carrying a type-erased drop guard (`PoolReturn`) that returns the entry to the free list when the downstream frame's keep-alive is released. Cross-API hazard handled: a recycled entry's image may still be sampled by an in-flight wgpu submission, so the device is drained (`Device::poll(Wait)`) before its planes are overwritten; `WgpuNv12Texture` gained an opaque `Option<Box<dyn Any + Send + Sync>>` recycle slot so it stays decoupled from the pool (non-pooled `nv12_to_gpu_texture` unaffected). Measured on the RTX 3060 via `cuda_wgpu_e2e` (now times the bridge step alone, and `G2G_CUDAWGPU_NOPOOL=1` forces the old path for an A/B): at 1080p the bridge step is **~2.6x faster, p50 0.38 ms pooled vs 0.98 ms per-frame-allocated**, ~0.6 ms/frame saved; the chain still matches the CPU reference. A geometry change rebuilds the pool.
- M253: `CudaGlSink` vs `WaylandSink` A/B present-latency benchmark on the RTX 3060. New `cudagl_vs_wayland` test (ignored) hardware-decodes the same H.264 fixture two ways on NVIDIA and presents through each sink, so only the present path differs: A = `FfmpegVideoDec(NvdecCuda) -> CudaGlSink` (NV12 stays in CUDA device memory, GPU shader convert), B = `FfmpegVideoDec(NvdecCuvid) -> WaylandSink` (system-memory NV12, CPU NV12->XRGB convert + `wl_shm` upload). Arrival is stamped after decode and before the sink, so each histogram isolates the present cost. At **1080p the device-resident path is 10.7x faster**: CudaGlSink p50 ~8.4 ms (120 frames in 0.81 s) vs WaylandSink p50 ~89.8 ms (8.47 s), the per-frame CPU convert of ~3 MB being the work the GPU path elides. Closes the `CudaGlSink` benchmark item.
- M252: `CudaGlSink` first compile + on-display validation on the RTX 3060. The CUDA-GL zero-copy-ish display sink (keeps `NvdecCuda` NV12 in CUDA device memory, copies it device->GL-texture via CUDA-GL interop, NV12->RGB fragment shader, presents on a Wayland EGL surface) was authored off-Linux and never compiled. First compile on the host needed two adjustments only: `khronos-egl` 6's `get_display` is now `unsafe` (wrapped, with a SAFETY note), and `alloc::string::ToString` had to be imported for glow's `String` errors in the `no_std`+alloc baseline; the three crate-API spots flagged `// VERIFY:` all held. Added `cudagl_smoke` (ignored, file-driven so it needs no RTSP): `H.264 -> FfmpegVideoDec(NvdecCuda) -> CudaGlSink` on a live Wayland session, which **presents 60 frames** with glass-to-glass p50 ~8 ms. On this hybrid iGPU+NVIDIA laptop the GL context must be forced onto the NVIDIA GPU (`__NV_PRIME_RENDER_OFFLOAD=1` / `__EGL_VENDOR_LIBRARY_FILENAMES=.../10_nvidia.json`) or `cuGraphicsGLRegisterImage` fails. Also satisfied the workspace unsafe-doc lint (SAFETY comments on all six unsafe blocks) and the keep-alive `_egl_context` field. Owed: a head-to-head latency benchmark vs the `NvdecCuvid -> WaylandSink` baseline.
- M251: CUDA<->wgpu keep-on-GPU on-hardware validation (the GPU keep-on-GPU pillar, roadmap #4). The whole M220 chain was authored off-Linux and compile-only ("COMPILE/RUN-pending on the RTX 3060 host"); built + run for real on the RTX 3060. The `cudawgpu_spike` tests prove the Vulkan<->CUDA external-memory round-trip in both directions on the NVIDIA proprietary driver (CUDA fills a shared `VK_KHR_external_memory_fd` image and wgpu reads back the exact pattern, **0 mismatches**; and the inverse). The cross-crate `cuda_wgpu_e2e` test runs the full `H.264 -> FfmpegVideoDec(NvdecCuda) -> CudaToWgpu -> WgpuPreprocess -> WgpuInference` zero-copy chain: NVDEC decodes NV12 in CUDA device memory, `CudaToWgpu` shares it device->device into a Vulkan image, `WgpuPreprocess` samples it as a GPU texture, **all 30 frames match the CPU reference** with no PCIe download (p50 31 ms bridge+preprocess+infer; the Stage 0 `CudaDownload` reference path costs an extra 0.25 ms download). The matching CUDA round-trip also confirms adapter selection picks the NVIDIA device over the AMD RADV one on this host. No code changes (the chain worked first try); doc-only: the `cudawgpu.rs` caveat and DESIGN.md §5.1 "remaining piece" note now record it as validated, and the e2e tests document the ffmpeg fixture recipe. Owed: the per-frame shared-image reuse pool (currently allocates one per frame).
- M250: zero-copy tee. A tee broadcast no longer deep-copies CPU frames: the runner calls `MemoryDomain::make_shareable` once before fanning out, then each branch gets a refcount handle via `MemoryDomain::share`. New `SystemSliceInner::Shared(Arc<Box<[u8]>>)` / `SharedPooled(Arc<PooledBuffer>)` variants make owned/pooled CPU bytes shareable by *moving* the buffer into an `Arc` (a move, not the re-copy `Arc<[u8]>` would force; a pooled buffer returns to its pool once the last branch drops). The share is read-only: `SystemSlice::as_mut_slice` does copy-on-write (reclaims a uniquely-held `Arc` with no copy, else deep-copies), so siblings never alias a mutation.
